# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 16

## 5717

B"H, 3 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

We acknowledge receipt of your *pidyon nefesh*.

Some time ago, an alarming report was received here that you raised a hand against a Chabad *avreich* who is engaged in the *tzarchei tzibbur* of *chinuch* on the purity of holiness. As is explicitly stated in the *Acharonim*, such a matter must be nullified below in order to prevent a similar occurrence from above, *chas v'shalom*. And even though the hope is that you have already asked him for forgiveness—**as is commanded in our holy Torah**—we nevertheless explicitly urge you regarding this: that when asking for forgiveness, the matter must be made known to all those who were aware of the incident for which you are seeking forgiveness.

This letter is being sent as urgent and express, so that the matter may be resolved before the upcoming holy day, in accordance with the ruling of the *Mishnah* at the end of *Yoma*, and *kal v'chomer*.

You will surely acknowledge receipt of this letter immediately upon receiving it.

With blessings for a *chasimah v'gmar chatimah tovah* and for good tidings regarding the above.

The Secretary

#### ***5717***

Most of the letters are from the secretariat's copy, and some are from a photocopy of the letter. They are not marked with footnotes unless the source is different, or if they have already been printed in *Likkutei Sichos*.

**An alarming report:** See regarding this further on, letter 5783.

## 5718

B"H, 4 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter.

I am surprised that you are writing again regarding the question about which you have already written and to which I have already replied; namely, that there are differences of opinion between you and your wife, tichyeh, regarding the extent to which the matter of hachnosas orchim should be practiced in your home, as she says that it is difficult.

All such questions should be brought to a Rav, a moreh hora'ah b'Yisrael, and both of you should act according to his guidance...

Furthermore, just as it is written regarding the first one to practice hachnosas orchim [Avraham Avinu], that he did not only perform the act itself but subsequently spoke of the greatness of Hashem, so too, you should not be content with merely hosting your guests, but should also explain to them the greatness of Hashem as it is elucidated in pnimiyus haTorah, which in our generation has been revealed in Toras HaChassidus. And it goes without saying that in order to explain this to another, one must know it to a greater degree—*tofeach al menas lehatpiach* (to moisten so that one may moisten others). And since our Rebbeim have entrusted us with the matter of *hafatzas hama'ayanos*, it is certain that the *kochot* have been granted for this, and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With the blessing of *chasimah v'gmar chasimah tovah*.

## 5759

B"H, 4 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter with the enclosed *pidyon nefesh*, which will be read at an *eis ratzon* at the holy *tziyun* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

It is surprising that you write only a few words regarding the wedding, at a time that is the foundation for an eternal edifice (*binyan adei ad*) and an *eis ratzon*. According to the custom of Israel, one is inspired at such a time toward matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, and one speaks words of Torah and Chassidus. Although I rely on the presumption (*chazakah*) that in your case, this includes the repetition of a *maamar* of Chassidus and the *uvchein* that follows from it, nevertheless, there is a flaw in this *chazakah* due to the custom of interrupting in the middle, etc. To my astonishment, there are even *anash* who follow this practice! And even if one were to say, "When you go to a city, follow its customs," there is a specific instruction from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, who directed that one should complete [the *maamar*] and only afterwards begin a second time and interrupt.

Regarding what you wrote about Mr. [Name], may he live, who does not know how to combine letters, etc.: one should consult with a specialist physician in this field. It should also be clarified that often, in such cases—in many details and matters—these individuals are sufficiently developed, and perhaps even beyond the average measure. When they are organized in a way that they can utilize their **developed** talents, sometimes the matters that are currently not as they should be will develop little by little.

Surely the aforementioned person sets aside a few coins for *tzedakah* each day before the morning *tefillah*.

With the blessing of *chasimah v'gmar chatimah tovah*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

#### 5759

Part of this letter was printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 18, p. 208; part in *Igros Kodesh*, Vol. 21, p. 457; and it has been completed according to the secretariat’s copy.

**Due to the custom of interrupting:** See also below, letter 5882, and the references in the notes there.

## 5718

B"H, 4 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 27th of Elul and the 3rd, as well as the *pidyon nefesh* for Rosh Hashanah. It is astonishing that from time to time—and unfortunately, with not much of an interval—I receive a letter from you that is, at the very least, filled with despair or sorrow. What is even more distressing is that you draw conclusions from this that are the **opposite** of the desired conclusions. In this letter, too, you write that you lack patience, etc., and that because of this, there is a deficiency in your activities, etc., and from this you conclude that you have ceased [your efforts]... How great is the darkness of the *galus*, that one does not see the **startling** contradiction between the conclusions drawn from the reality itself and the conclusions you have arrived at.

I have already said to many young people and to *anash* that, in truth, it is incumbent upon each and every one to perform their work, and Hashem will do what is good in His eyes—whether one succeeds or, *chas v'shalom*, not. We have merited, specifically in our generation—this orphaned generation—to see with physical eyes how the decree of the Heavenly Beis Din is fulfilled, that *anash* are succeeding in their activities. Yet, in return, and as if to provoke, from time to time people find pretexts to diminish a certain activity or to minimize a certain matter, etc. It is a pity for their time that they write such justifications to me, since they are **not at all** accepted by me. If you were to receive such a letter from someone else, and you were not personally involved in the matter, you would see the startling contradiction and the invalidity of the conclusion from the outset...

May it be Hashem’s will that from here on, you and your colleagues—may they live—will bring tidings of tangible activities, and that the matter of complaints, lamentations, etc., will find no place within your four cubits. Then, ultimately, there will not be, within your four cubits, any of those reasons for complaints, etc. Surely, the merit of the many and the awakening of the *rachamei rachamim* (mercies of mercies) of our *Nesi'im*, our holy Rebbes, will assist you.

With the blessing of *chasimah v'gmar chasimah tovah*.

## 5718

B"H, 5 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

The Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, Montreal Branch
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 21 Elul, and thank you for the good news regarding the impression that the camp left even for the coming time. It is surely unnecessary to remind you that in all such matters, it is essential to utilize them while the impression is still fresh and warm. This is especially true now, as it is also the beginning of the study term and matters of chinuch, and any effort toward influence regarding chinuch is a matter that is "in its time." Not in all details can one rectify matters later if there is a deficiency in the efforts now.

At a time of favor, I will mention the counselors (may they live) for their aforementioned efforts at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Their reward is surely guaranteed by the Giver of the Torah and the Commander of the mitzvos, measure for measure—and even many times over. May it be the will of Hashem that the teaching of the Mishnah be fulfilled in them: "a mitzvah draws another mitzvah," that they should go from strength to strength in disseminating matters of Yiddishkeit and matters of Chassidus, specifically in every place their reach extends.

With blessings for good news and for a *chasimah v'gmar chasimah tovah*.

## 5782

5th of Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yedidya Alter
Greetings and blessings,

It is with pleasure that I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 17th of Elul, in which you write regarding your service in the army within the framework of the Military Rabbinate. Certainly—even though you do not mention it—you are utilizing your position not only for the classification of religious soldiers, but also to encourage and strengthen their spirits. This is vital for Ashkenazim, and all the more so for our Sephardic brethren, for whom their entire standing in life, in all its minute details, often depends on this.

I have taken an interest in those points of work that you are prepared to implement regarding religious soldiers. It would be very good if you were to discuss all of this with Mr. Leib Zalmanov (currently a shochet in Bnei Brak), who previously served in the IDF in the Military Rabbinate and is one of the active members of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad. It is said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation." I have strong hope that together, the two of you will be able to develop a detailed plan for the aforementioned, which is also suited to the current capabilities of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and which we may hope to expand over time. Once the details are known, it may be possible to create additional sources of income to finance this work in other branches. It is a pity that your letter was delayed in transit, as surely at the end of Elul and the month of Tishrei there are many special opportunities to initiate and establish these activities, and we do not cry over the past.

Since you have already touched upon this, it would be appropriate to print a summary of laws specifically for the life of a soldier, particularly under the conditions of Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established). It would be best in a pocket-sized format so that it is convenient to use. Although I have seen some laws printed in *Machanayim*, it is understood that since they are scattered across several booklets, this does not fulfill the requirement at all. Furthermore, in a summary such as this, there is no need for lengthy debate; at most, citing the sources is sufficient. Naturally, this is on the condition that there is no concern that such a summary of Shulchan Aruch would become a collection of leniencies on every side. However, we are not dealing with the wicked, G-d forbid, especially when the printing is done through the consultation of several rabbis together.

A special difficulty will be in connection with the differences in customs, but it is possible to suffice with a collection of laws that are accepted without distinction of community, which would also fulfill a vital requirement. Surely there will be a continuation to such a matter.

Not long ago, I had occasion in a *sicha* here to emphasize that although our Sages said regarding one who goes out to war that "the Torah speaks against the *yetzer hara"—which on the face of it implies that when one is in the army, one should be lenient in certain details—the truth is the opposite. That is to say, one who is in the army must increase in matters of caution and holiness, as it is written, "And your camp shall be holy." I emphasized that the source of holiness is the holy Torah, and I referred to establishing fixed times for its study. If this applies to all soldiers, it applies all the more so to members of the Rabbinate, who must be "moist enough to moisten others." My hope is that even though you conclude your letter by saying that when you are released from your position you will be able to study more, the emphasis is on the word "more," because your time will be more at your disposal. However, even now, you must have fixed times every day for Torah study. And surely, since you have been introduced to the teachings of Chassidus, you should also have a *shiur* in the teachings of Chassidus and influence your colleagues in this regard as well...

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and with the blessing of *Chasimah V'Gmar Chasimah Tovah*.

## 5718

B"H, 6 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn

To the Committee of Kfar Chabad, in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,
May Hashem keep them alive,

Peace and blessing!

In connection with the impure incident involving the raising of a hand, etc., I am compelled to write the following lines regarding the gravity of the matter:

It is **easy** for a person of understanding to see that throughout all the years of the village’s existence, it has been guarded and protected in a manner that transcends the natural order, thank Hashem. This is certainly due to the awakening of the infinite compassion of our Rebbes, and in particular my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the founder and director of the village. Indeed, from the day the village was founded in 5708, thank Hashem, not a single one of its residents has been harmed. The open miracle in this is understood. And since an awakening of compassion from Above requires a fitting vessel to receive it, and the vessel that holds Hashem’s blessing is peace—especially when we are speaking of the awakening of the infinite compassion of the Chabad Rebbes, who sacrificed themselves for the cause of ahavas Yisroel, as I have written several times—it is **obvious** that all residents of the village must be exceedingly careful regarding matters of peace and the drawing together of hearts...

May it be the will of the Creator of man, who fashions their hearts together and knows the great cunning of the animal soul and the yetzer hara, etc., and the difficulty and darkness of this double and redoubled galus, that He see our affliction speedily, and may the entire matter and its consequences be atoned for—an atonement in its fullness, in the language of the Alter Rebbe—so that it may be acceptable before Hashem and pleasing and beloved before Him, may He be blessed, etc. And may only goodness and kindness, in a revealed and manifest way, find every single one of the residents of Kfar Chabad, from now and forever.

May I receive good news regarding all that has been said, and may it be soon.

With the blessing of a good sealing and final sealing.

P.S.

According to the well-known instructions of our Sages regarding one who has caused a stumbling block for his fellow, and especially according to what is explained in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 25, even those who were insulted must take upon themselves increased care and beauty in the mitzvos of Hashem. It goes without saying that they must root out and eradicate any resentment from their hearts, chas v'shalom, chas v'shalom. As it is written in this week’s parsha, when the tribes of Israel are united—bringing together the heads of the people—they bring about that "He became King in Yeshurun," as is explained in Likutei Torah regarding the great virtue when Bnei Yisroel are in the state of "Yeshurun."

## 5718

B"H, 6 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Agudas Chabad, New Haven Branch
May Hashem keep them alive.

Greetings and Blessings,

I was pleased to receive your letter of 4 Tishrei along with its enclosure, in which you outline the main points of your activities over the past few weeks. Surely you are preparing a detailed plan regarding the upcoming days of joy for us and for all of Israel—the blessing of the Daled Minim, the farbrengens of Simchas Beis HaShoeivah, Shemini Atzeres, Simchas Torah, and so on.

Since this year there are three consecutive days of joy—two days of Yom Tov followed by Shabbos, during which we recite "They shall rejoice in Your kingdom" (even though it is understood that the essence of Shabbos is the matter of taanug, as explained at length in Chassidus)—may it be Hashem’s will that the number of your activities increases, as well as the number of those you influence. May you ascend higher and higher in the matter of spreading the wellsprings outward, until you transform the "outside" into the "inside," in accordance with the request of these days, beginning from Erev Rosh Chodesh Elul: "Your face, Hashem, I seek."

With blessings for good tidings and for a *Gmar Chasimah Tovah*.

## 5718

7 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and Blessings,

I acknowledge receipt of the newspaper clipping you sent, along with the few words you added.

The answer to this is also in your own style: What is being done in your circles so that there should be a youth born here who will (not only understand, but also) want to daven? And not only want to—in the sense of merely having the desire—but actually daven three times a day? And do you think that by printing a few lines in a journal, you are accomplishing much in that direction?

May it be Hashem’s will that instead of asking questions and coming with complaints against others, one should personally be a living example, fulfilling mitzvos in daily life, *v’al yevosh mipnei hamal’igim*—not being ashamed to do everything that depends only on him. Every person who has any influence should be close to the Jewish **way of life**, the intention of which is simple: putting on tefillin, eating kosher, keeping Shabbos, etc.

It is self-understood that since I do not know you, I do not know to what extent what has been said applies to you. But unfortunately, in this country, for most of those who write and ask questions about others, this serves as a justification for not practicing true Yiddishkeit, which simply means a daily conduct of life according to the Shulchan Aruch, *kifshuto*. Perhaps you are among the good minority.

With respect and blessings for a *Chasimah V’Gmar Chasimah Tovah*,

The Secretary

In any event, one question regarding the prayer itself:

*Ayefim l’horgim al Kiddush Hashem v’chevlei Mashiach.*

Why choose this phrasing? (It does not fit the rhythm of the prayer—the number of syllables is too high compared to the other rhymes. It is stylistically inappropriate—*horgim* [killers] *al Kiddush Hashem* is like David killing Goliath, whereas here the intent is the opposite—those who are *nehergim* [killed] *al Kiddush Hashem*. It is inappropriate in content—as it is superfluous—for a prayer for the end of suffering and the coming of the Geulah). And yet, it is precisely when it suggests itself to be written instead as:

*Nafshi (h)ayefah l’horgim b’chevlei Mashiach.*

*Titpallel...*

One also gains a "natural" continuation: *Nafshi tashiach... titpallel*, rather than as printed: *Nafshi el al tashiach...* (and afterwards it turns to the) *ayefim* etc. *nitpallel...*

Furthermore, *Nafshi ayefah l’horgim* is the language of the *Kesuvim*—which he strives for in the other rhymes.

***

The letter itself was written in the name of the Secretariat and corrected in the Rebbe’s holy handwriting. In the margin, there is an addition in the Rebbe’s holy handwriting.

**Newspaper clipping... added:** A poem he printed in a newspaper, upon which he remarked in writing: "How many of your students, born here, will understand this prayer?"

**In his prayer:** Regarding what follows later:

*Mishomrim laboker nafshi el al tashiach:* [5718]

...

*Ayefim l’horgim al "Kiddush Hashem" v’"chevlei Mashiach"*

*Nitpallel: Ha-ketz ha-ketz al "nachashei-bariach"?*

## 5780

B”H, 7 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write about the incident with Rabbi... regarding his sharp remarks concerning the study of *Pnimiyus HaTorah*, etc.

It would be appropriate to compile for him the words of Rav Chaim Vital (in his introduction to *Shaar HaHakdamos*, also printed in *Etz Chaim*, Warsaw edition, and in the supplement to the *Kuntres Etz Chaim* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe), as well as the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe Rashab, in that same *Kuntres*. Additionally, include the well-known passage from the holy letter of the Baal Shem Tov regarding "when your wellsprings spread outward, the Master will come." If the aforementioned individual also possesses the quality of being a "man of the world," you may also append the words of the Gra, that the Redemption depends on this. Send these materials to him with the request that he do one of two things: either state that he disagrees with these authorities and holds the opposite view, or retract the remarks he made in public—in which case, according to the law, he must announce his retraction publicly, just as he publicized his original remarks to the contrary.

Even if this does not achieve the desired result, it will certainly serve as a shield for the future.

I am sure you are preparing a plan to utilize the coming days of *segulah* to the fullest extent, and may it be Hashem’s will that it be successful.

With blessings for a *Chasimah V’Gmar Chasimah Tovah*.

#### ***5780***

**The words of the Gra:** See also above, Vol. 14, Letter 5093, and the references in the notes there.

## 5727

B"H, 8 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...And since we are currently in the days of *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah*, and our Sages of blessed memory have said that "everything follows the seal," may it be His will that your *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah* be for revealed and manifest good in all matters, both materially and spiritually. May you utilize the talents with which you have been gifted, with joy and goodness of heart, to raise the pride of *Yisrael Sava*, whose youthful strength is eternal, for he is connected and bound to the One of whom it is said, "The *Atik Yomin* sat." Through the commandment, "Cleave to His attributes; just as He is merciful, so too must you be merciful," the result follows as well, as it is written, "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today."

In the above, there is also an answer to the inner point contained in your letter—for all the causes for a lack of peace of mind, etc., are matters that exist within time. Most of them, if not all, are an extremely small fraction even in comparison to the span of a person’s life on earth, and they are of no true significance when compared to eternity and the actions of a person that are connected to eternity, and even more so when compared to that which is entirely beyond the bounds of time. As is well known, the saying of the Maggid that time, too, is a created thing.

With respect and blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and for a *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah*.

#### ***5727***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 19, p. 467.

**The saying of the Maggid:** See also above, Vol. 1, Letter 156; Vol. 2, p. 283.

## 5788

B"H, 8 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Avreich Shalom Dovber, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding your question concerning the wearing of a tallis and gartel for davening when praying in a shul that does not follow the customs of Anash.

It is understood that here, too, the rule of our Sages applies: "Dispute is hated." If it is possible to follow the customs of Anash there as well—and, of course, in a manner of peace and pleasantness—it is worthwhile to do so, while avoiding any dispute over this matter. It is also understood that this applies to the wearing of the tallis gadol, as the aforementioned [congregation] adds to the custom of Anash, and their shaliach tzibbur is accustomed to being wrapped in a tallis, unlike our custom. Since they are adding [to the practice], one should concede to fulfill their request, and the tallis gadol should be worn specifically draped over the shoulders. However, regarding the gartel, where they omit this, one should make every effort to daven specifically with a gartel. This is especially true as this relates to the matter of "Prepare to meet your G-d, O Israel."

Regarding the number of candles to light before the amud, it is understood that this depends on local custom. If the one leading the davening is an avel or observing a yahrtzeit, chas v’shalom, then during davening it is appropriate that five candles be lit, as per the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, that there are five names for the soul.

Regarding the text of the matzeivah, you should consult with the elders of Anash in your vicinity.

And approaching the coming year, may you all be blessed with a good sealing and final sealing.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***5788***

**Shalom Dovber, may he live:** Kievman, Tel Aviv.

## 5787

B"H, 8 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote about your son, *sheyichyeh*—throughout this entire time you have avoided mentioning the main point. The fact is that my agreement to his traveling here was on the explicit condition that during this year there would be a noticeable improvement in his conduct. Only this would serve as proof that his traveling here is worthwhile. If this improvement is not seen, it is understood that I remain of my original opinion: that it is better for him—as I told him at length when he was here—to continue to be in... in close proximity to his parents, *sheyichyeh*. It is simple that this is my opinion, because according to the aforementioned, this is truly for his benefit. Therefore, it is puzzling, if the aforementioned condition is not met, why there is such an effort that he specifically travel here.

...And since we are in the days of *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah*, and our Sages of blessed memory have said that "everything follows the seal," may it be the will [of Hashem] that the *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah* be for revealed and manifest good in all matters, both materially and spiritually. And may he, with joy and a glad heart, utilize the talents with which he has been gifted to raise the horn of *Yisrael Sava*, for the strength of his youth is eternal within him, since he is connected and bound to Him. Of Him it is said, "The Ancient of Days sits," and through fulfilling the commandment, "Cleave to His attributes; just as He is merciful, so too you be merciful, etc.," the result also follows, as it is written, "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today."

With the blessing of *chasimah v'gmar chasimah tovah*.

#### ***5787***

The final paragraph was written to several people.

## 5790

B"H, 8 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, along with the *pan* that will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in which you write that you are experiencing fear, etc.

In general, matters such as these have no actual existence (except for the fact that a person thinks about them and dwells upon them). *Hesech hada'as* (diverting one’s attention) nullifies them completely. It is well known regarding *hesech hada'as* that it is not a battle against a specific thought—for a battle is the opposite of *hesech hada'as*. Rather, the matter is simple: one should think about and focus on entirely different subjects. When such a thought enters your mind, do not pay it any attention. It goes without saying that you should not amplify it, nor should you fight against it; simply push it aside by occupying yourself with a different thought, especially a thought concerning matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, for even a little light pushes away much darkness.

It is understood that the above is easier to achieve when the body is strong and healthy. Therefore, it is advisable that you consult a doctor regarding this and follow his instructions in practice. However, as mentioned, do this without dwelling on whether or not you feel fear, etc. We are currently in the days of *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah tovah*, and Hashem, who is the essence of good, will bestow good down below to the Jewish person, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed.

With blessings for a *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah tovah*.

## 5791

B"H, 8 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the avreich Avraham Avish Mordechai, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding your question as to the source for the words of Rabbeinu HaZaken (in his Iggeres HaTeshuvah and also in Iggeres HaKodesh) that for a baal teshuvah who performs fasts and self-afflictions to redeem his soul, the rule of not spending more than a fifth [of one’s wealth] does not apply:

The matter is explained right there in the words of Rabbeinu HaZaken, for it is obvious that the healing of the soul is no less significant than the healing of the body; as it is written, "All that a man has, he will give for his soul." This simple logic is the most accurate source (see Kesuvos 22a, and elsewhere).

Regarding what you wrote about the order of study in the teachings of Chassidus, you should consult with the elders of anash in your vicinity, and they will guide you, as the matter depends on many details and nuances.

With the blessing of *Chasimah v'Gmar Chasimah Tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**Avraham Avish Mordechai:** Perush-Glickman, Jerusalem. Another letter to him — see above, Vol. 14, 4993.

**Sdei Chemed, Klalim:** Entry *Sevara* (Rule 63), whether it is considered *de'oraisa*.

## 5792

B"H, 11 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer HaKohen, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

On the eve of the Holy Day, before I traveled to the Holy Tziyun, I received your letter along with its enclosure, and I mentioned you at the Holy Tziyun in accordance with the contents of your letter.

Incidentally, because I returned from the Holy Tziyun later than anticipated, there was no time during the day for a telephone call. However, the very essence of the Holy Day is that the day itself accomplishes everything required. See also the Responsa Tzafnas Paneach by the Rogatchover Gaon, Part 1, Siman 101 and 102, regarding the laws of Erev Shabbos, Erev Yom HaNora, Motzaei Shabbos, and Motzaei Yom HaKippurim.

May it be the will of Hashem that all matters continue as explained in Chassidus during our upcoming days of joy, for ourselves and for all of Israel, for good—in a manner of absorption and the intake of all the "fatness," until the prophecy regarding the Kingdom is fulfilled shortly: "And one King shall be for them all." See the Hemshech of Rosh Hashanah 5748, which is now being published.

With blessings for a happy holiday.

#### ***5792***

**Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer:** Yalles. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 15, 5791, and in the references noted there. Below, 5798, 6:16, 6:42.

## 5718

By the Grace of Hashem, 11 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi, distinguished scholar, G-d-fearing, and engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Yosef Eliyahu, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 8th of Tishrei, in which you ask for my opinion regarding associating with various types of rabbis.

In general, it is not my practice to issue rulings on such questions. The reason I made my opinion public regarding participation in the New York Board of Rabbis and the Synagogue Council was that the situation compelled me to do so, as I saw that it was liable, G-d forbid, to cause [harm], etc.

However, since your question follows from the aforementioned, I am writing here what appears to be my clear opinion, which is as follows:

1) Is it proper to associate in matters of Halacha as a *beis din* with rabbis whose synagogues, while called "Orthodox," do not have a *bimah* in the center, and even if there is a *mechitza*, many women sit inside the synagogue proper? And similarly, with those whose synagogues have no *mechitza* at all, yet the majority of the members and the synagogue itself are called "Orthodox"?

I have already written in my letters regarding participation in the aforementioned organizations that in this matter, the *shita* (ideology) is more significant than the actual deed. That is to say: a rabbi who states that his *shita* is that the entire Torah was given to Moshe at Sinai, except for one verse, etc.—even if he personally observes all the *mitzvos* and their details in practice, his status has already been determined by the Torah as a *kofer* (denier). It is understood that "associating with him in matters of Halacha as a *beis din*," as you phrased it in your letter, is forbidden. On the other hand, a rabbi who says that Judaism consists of all 613 *mitzvos* and their details, and that the entire Torah is from Heaven, even if he stumbles in certain matters because his *yetzer* has overcome him with temptations and incitements (which relates to his livelihood, etc.)—he is a rabbi who commits a transgression, and not every act of transgression in and of itself forbids association in matters of Halacha, etc. From this, the instruction regarding the aforementioned is understood.

2) Since a synagogue and its affairs are a public matter, it is understood that the reaction of the synagogue members is of the utmost importance regarding the lack of a *bimah* in the center, as well as the fact that some women sit outside the *mechitza* or there is no *mechitza* at all. If they consider these matters to be entirely permissible—that is, even after it has been explained to them that according to the *Shulchan Aruch* this is forbidden, they say that "the United States is different," etc., and they brought the matter to a discussion in the synagogue board and the rabbi agreed to their view—then this is no longer a private transgression or a mere transgression; it is a fundamental change to the *Shulchan Aruch* and the Holy Torah. In that case, it is irrelevant whether he wants to call himself "Orthodox" or not. I am happy to add that many of the young rabbis I know, whose synagogues are in the situation described, actually announce publicly that a *mechitza* is mandatory according to the *Shulchan Aruch*, and from time to time they bring the matter back onto the agenda of the synagogue board.

3) Is it permitted to associate, etc.—as above—with a rabbi whose synagogue has a microphone and the rabbi uses it on Shabbos and Yom Tov, and the synagogue has no *mechitza*, etc.?

The use of a microphone on Shabbos and Yom Tov, for those who know a chapter in technology, is a clear prohibition [by Rabbinic decree, and possibly even by Torah law]. Since this is done in the synagogue—that is, in great public view, and furthermore with emphasis, in the manner of "to ravish the queen with me in the house"—the one who desecrates Shabbos in public has already had his status determined in the *Shulchan Aruch*. Especially when he calls himself a "rabbi," i.e., a spiritual leader of his congregation, it is understood that "associating with him in matters of Halacha as a *beis din*" is completely out of the question, and the best *mechitza* in the world changes nothing, obviously. It is also understood that there is no change in this even if the rabbi expresses his protest against the use of the microphone and says that he is being forced to do so, because he is the one desecrating Shabbos in public. Regardless of the manner in which he is being "forced," it is obvious that this does not constitute a case of *ones* (duress) that would permit such an egregious desecration of Shabbos.

May it be the will of Hashem that all those who are being tested in the aforementioned matters recognize the truth: that it is not as the mistaken logic suggests—that by making a "compromise," the synagogue members will be drawn closer to them, and their livelihood and honor will be more secure. Above all, they will not be called "old-fashioned" or "from the old world," etc. For in recent years in the United States, we see the opposite: even the laypeople are beginning to recognize the truth that one who makes compromises for a quarter has no restraint in his soul to increase the compromise to a third, to a half, and to the majority or the whole. Even if he is a good speaker and a capable communal activist and finds favor in the eyes of the synagogue members—the laypeople and their families—in their hearts they harbor contempt for him, knowing that everything depends on the salary they pay him, and today he says one thing, etc.—as per the well-known words of our Sages.

With blessings that Hashem should grant him success in strengthening authentic Judaism wherever his hand can reach—a pure, complete, and eternal Judaism, as the Torah given to all of Bnei Yisrael for all times and all places—and with good tidings regarding all the aforementioned.

## 5794

B"H, 11 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Regarding your question as to whether to put on Rabbeinu Tam tefillin:

Certainly, one should strive as much as possible for one’s davening to be in a state of purity, and as is known, the holiness of tefillin in general—and all the more so [the holiness of Rabbeinu Tam tefillin]—is greater than the holiness of the Tzitz, as our Sages of blessed memory have stated. Therefore, it is appropriate to wear them.

Regarding what you wrote, that one who does not wear Rabbeinu Tam tefillin should not write them: this has already been discussed at length. Even though the conclusion is that the statement of our Sages, "Whoever is not involved in the tying [of tefillin] is not involved in the writing [of tefillin]," does not refer to this (and certainly not to one who does so out of desire—see Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim 39), nevertheless, *lechatchilah*, it is certainly good and proper that they be written by one who wears these tefillin. (The various opinions on this are gathered in *Me'asef Lechol Hamachanos* and in the sefer *Shulchan Melachim* on *Kitzur Shulchan Aruch*.)

I trust you are keeping the three daily *shiurim*—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—in addition to the *shiurim* in the yeshiva curriculum. May Hashem grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

#### ***5794***

**This has already been discussed at length:** See above, Vol. 14, Letter 5223.

## 5795

B”H, 11 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R’ Moshe Yitzchak, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter bearing good news, informing me that on the upcoming Sunday of Chol Hamoed Sukkos, you will begin a public Gemara shiur. May it be the will of Hashem that the study be successful, both in quality and in quantity—that is, in increasing the number of participants—and surely the promise of our Sages will be fulfilled: "Great is study, for it leads to action."

Regarding your question as to which Masechta to begin and the manner of study:

Since the study is, for the time being, only one hour per week, it is appropriate that the study be in a Masechta where the sugyos are not overly long, and one of the smaller Masechtos, so that you might be able to complete it within a few months at least. Furthermore, since this is a new endeavor, it is also appropriate that it deal with topics that have relevance to practical halachos. Based on all the above, it would be good to suggest studying Masechta Megillah. While Masechta Rosh Hashanah is of a similar nature, we have already come from it. As for Masechta Beitzah, aside from the fact that it contains several complex sugyos, the laws therein are not as commonly encountered or as necessary in the practical daily life of people, unlike Masechta Megillah. Additionally, it contains several Aggadic passages that capture the heart, and one can find their interpretation in various ways in the commentaries of the Ein Yaakov, from which you can surely choose the approach most suitable for your audience.

May it be the will of Hashem that the beginning and completion of this Masechta be fulfilled [in the spirit of the verse] "on the eleventh... on the fifteenth." It is a known allusion brought by the early authorities that this constitutes the Name Havayah: its end is *Yud-Alef* (11) and its beginning is *Yud-Heh* (15), and the total sum from 11 to 15 is 65, the numerical value of *Adonai*, the Name Havayah as it is pronounced within its "shield" and "covering"—that is, as Elokus is drawn down and concealed within the garments of the world. It is the study of Torah—which declares "this is kosher," "this is pure," "this is permitted," etc.—that must reveal this. By doing so, one reveals, on every single day, the true content of that day. As is known, the conclusion [of the Gemara states] that Moshe ordained for Yisrael that they should inquire and expound **on the subject of the day**, and specifically in the manner of Rashi’s commentary there: to accept and fulfill [the Torah] upon themselves and their children, in this world and the next.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for a happy holiday.

## 5718

B"H, 27 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of [date], in which you write that despite having been in this country for 50 years and living in a small town, you have maintained Yiddishkeit and raised your children in that direction, and that your roots are from Lubavitch, and one of your brothers is named after the Rebbe Maharash, of blessed memory, of Lubavitch.

The conclusion to be drawn from the above gives me hope that when you write about maintaining Yiddishkeit, you do not mean what many mistakenly believe—that to maintain Yiddishkeit, it is sufficient to support Jewish institutions and attend a temple or synagogue a few times a year. Even if they demand more than that of themselves, they consider this the maximum for their children. Sadly, we have seen the destruction that such an attitude has brought to hundreds of families.

However, a Yid who emphasizes that he is of Chassidic descent and so on, certainly includes in the word "Yiddishkeit" its true content: daily life according to the guidance of our holy Torah—the Torah of Moshe, which he received at Har Sinai from the Hakadosh Baruch Hu. Since He, blessed be He, is the Master of all parts of the world—regardless of whether it was thousands of years ago, now, or years from now—it is therefore understood that the Torah which He, blessed be He, gave, also took into account how America would look in our times. Yet, He commanded us to perform all the mitzvos written in the Torah, as the verse states, even "in the end of days." Fortunately, we see here as well that those who truly desire to do so, succeed in carrying out authentic, non-falsified Yiddishkeit, not only for themselves but also for their children, may they live and be well.

What I find necessary to add, in accordance with the well-known saying of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: it is never too late. If, for whatever reason, yesterday was not as it should have been, teshuvah and a proper way of life from now on will help. I would be pleased to hear good news from you regarding the above.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
You also write thoughts regarding gilgulim! Seeing that you have been in the jewelry line for 50 years, you have surely studied that field for many years. It would interest me to know how many years you have studied the question of gilgulim, that you express an opinion on it with such firmness, at a time when the greatest sages of Yisrael—such as the Arizal, R. Chaim Vital, the Alter Rebbe, and also the Gaon of Vilna—substantiate the concept I spoke of, which you do not find favorable.

## 8800

B"H, 28 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and energetic activist,
Rabbi Moshe Yitzchak, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Sunday. Without waiting for my turn, I am responding as an expression of gratitude for the good news you convey. This is especially true as I wish for this response to be written while still in the month of Tishrei, which, as explained in many places—including the maamarim of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—is the general month for the entire year. That is to say, the conduct and matters that take place during this month have the unique quality of extending throughout all the months of the coming year.

Consequently, it is understood that every good action performed during this month possesses an added dimension, yielding fruits and the fruits of fruits in the months to follow. May it be His will that throughout the entire year, you will report only good, in a revealed and manifest way, both in general matters and in your personal affairs.

Based on the known principle that every person has a specific mitzvah that serves as the gateway to elevate all their affairs from below to above, and to draw down everything they require from above to below—which is usually recognized through the conduct of Divine Providence—you and your colleagues at Yeshivas Achei Tmimim in New Haven have surely realized that the eyes of this Yeshivah and its expansion are your specific mitzvah. In this, you must be **zehir taphei** (extra careful)—careful in the literal sense, and careful in the inner sense of the term, from the word *zohar* (radiance) and *ohr* (light). Since this is demanded of each one of you, and even more so from the administration, it is certain that from the outset, all the strengths and resources necessary to fulfill this role—and to fulfill it completely—have been granted, in accordance with the Baal Shem Tov’s instruction: "You shall surely help him" (*azov ta'azov imo*), with physical health, joy, and a glad heart.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all that has been mentioned, as well as for your personal matters. Please convey my regards to all who assist you in your holy work and to all who participate in the shiurim you teach in public.

## 882

B”H, 28 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Moshe, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, which seemingly crossed paths with my letter wishing you a happy New Year; I trust you received it in due time. My letter has been delayed due to the busyness of the Yomim Tovim.

Regarding what you write and emphasize—that despite communal affairs, my time is also dedicated to the needs of the individual—this surely does not surprise you, knowing that the entire system of Chassidus Chabad, like the system of Chassidus in general, is dedicated to the benefit of every individual. Furthermore, the mitzvah of Ahavas Yisrael, in light of the emphasis of the teachings of Chassidus, requires dedication and self-giving to the needs of every individual. As for the limitations of every created being in time and space, the statement of our Sages is well known: "A mitzvah leads to another mitzvah." One who strives as they ought for the benefit of the individual not only finds that it does not hinder their communal work, but on the contrary, it brings blessing to that as well.

Moreover, in the perspective of the teachings of Chassidus, the individual is also "many" in potential. Who can measure the abundance contained within the small? Every individual who strives to utilize their possibilities to the maximum extent in the correct direction and for the desired purpose connects thereby with the Source of good and holiness, which is Ein Sof, and consequently, the limitations fall away as well.

Incidentally, it is worth noting that one who observes what is occurring in the world of secular science from generation to generation sees how, in this regard too, the conclusions of secular science are moving and drawing closer to the conclusions of our Torah, the Torah of our ancestors. This is especially true in our generation, and particularly in recent years, where it has been revealed that even the most minute quantity contains immense powers, to the point that our entire era is named after the atom.

You do not mention your health in your letter... I see this as a good sign, that you have diverted your attention from it, for this is a sign of a healthy person who does not dwell on the limbs of his body.

I will conclude with the subject of the beginning of your letter regarding the purchase of the apartment: May Hashem grant that your decision in this matter—whatever it may be—brings the blessing of "a change of place, a change of fortune" for good and for blessing, in the traditional phrasing, in a manner that is good and revealed even to physical eyes.

With respect and blessing.

## 8303

B"H, 28 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Agudas Gemilas Chasadim,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and abundant blessing!

I have received with pleasure the report of your society’s activities over the past year. While it is understood that the turnover should have been much larger—for, unfortunately, the prayer that the Jewish people should not need one another’s assistance has not yet been fulfilled—my hope is strong that each of you will do what is incumbent upon you, and will also influence your friends and acquaintances to do all that is in their power to increase the capacity of the Gemach fund as much as possible, and as soon as possible.

This is especially true in light of the statement of our Sages that *tzedakah* is equivalent to all the *mitzvos* (a concept explained in many places, and in *Tanya*, chapters 34 and 37). Regarding the virtue of *tzedakah* itself, *gemilas chasadim* is the most exalted form, as per the ruling of the *Shulchan Aruch*. See also the *maamar* entitled *Kol HaMerachem Al HaBriyos*, printed in *Kuntres 61*.

In accordance with the verse, "I am a companion to all who fear You and to those who keep Your precepts," I am enclosing my check as a symbolic contribution to your Gemach fund.

Awaiting good news, and blessing each and every one of those who strive and labor in this, together with their families, with all that they require in both material and spiritual matters.

## 515

B.H., 28 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you outline the main events you have experienced, particularly recently regarding the bankruptcy of one of the firms, etc.

It is obvious that there is no room for despair, Heaven forbid—especially for the people of our generation, who remain as "brands plucked from the fire" through the manifest miracles of the Ribono shel Olam. This has strengthened in the mind of every individual, more and more, the absolute truth that nothing is impossible for Him—the Ribono shel Olam. Rather, the Creator of the world desires that we create vessels through the natural order, and then He sends His blessing and success, even beyond the natural order, as it is written: "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do." Based on this, my advice is that you should endeavor in business matters or a position, specifically one where you can utilize your talents or knowledge, and you should do this with a sense of strong bitachon.

Since, according to the above, this is merely a vessel, it is understood that you must increase your involvement in matters of Torah and mitzvos. The Ribono shel Olam, Giver of the Torah and the mitzvos, will then increase His blessings in whatever you require. In this regard, your decision to set aside a little more than a maaser from your profits for tzedakah is excellent. It is even better to give a certain amount immediately, on account of the profits that the Ribono shel Olam will provide you with soon; this serves as proof of your bitachon in the One who sustains and provides for all.

According to what is explained in many places, one of the auspicious times for giving tzedakah is every weekday before the morning davening.

I am sure you are aware of the three daily study portions for every person, established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and at the very least, you should observe them from now on.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

## 5807

B"H, 29 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Naftali Hertz, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

...It was a pleasure for me to read at the end of your letter that you are a descendant of the holy, chassidic, and scholarly Rabbi Pinchas of Koritz, as you write, a son following a son. This gives me the hope that you recognize the privilege and the responsibility of an heir. A son following a son is a form of inheritance that has no interruption. If, regarding material matters, a son inherits all of his father's assets, how much more so is this true regarding spiritual matters (though in those, it is like lighting one candle from another). See also Eduyos, end of Chapter 2, "The father merits the son, etc.," and the commentaries there explain that this is so even according to nature; how much more so in matters of Torah and mitzvos.

In particular, as a practical outcome of the above, you are surely also striving to spread the wellsprings of Chassidus wherever your hand can reach. There is nothing that can stand before the will, especially in our era, in which we see an awakening of the hearts of Israel in all circles, and so on. It would be a pleasure for me to hear good news regarding your activities in the aforementioned, and surely the merit of your ancestors will assist you.

On this occasion, I would like to encourage you regarding the three daily study cycles—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which, as we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, are accessible to every soul and are a segulah for many matters.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### 5807

R' Naftali Hertz: Shapiro, Antwerp.

## 8809

B"H, 29 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with satisfaction that I read your letter of 27 Tishrei, in which you write regarding the good resolution you and your partners, may they live, have made concerning matters of tzedakah. Since Hashem Yisbarach says, "Test Me now in this," which is also a form of request—that one should test Him—as He says earlier in the verse, "Bring all the tithes... and I will pour out for you a blessing until there is no end," and although there is a halachic ruling, "Do not test Hashem," tzedakah is an exception, where we are actually asked to test Him; one can therefore be very strong in bitachon that Hakadosh Baruch Hu will fulfill what has been said regarding this. I hope to be able to report good tidings regarding the sale of the houses, and also regarding the fact that you and your partners are fulfilling your resolution with joy and a glad heart.

## 5110

B"H, 29 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the end of Tishrei, in which you write that you wish to enter a yeshiva to study, specifically a Chabad yeshiva (as you previously studied in the Chabad yeshiva) in Lod, but that you are currently twenty-two years old.

Your reasoning is very correct indeed, for the years at your age are the years of preparation and the foundation for the entirety of a person’s life. For a Jewish person, one’s success—not only spiritual but also physical—is dependent upon and founded in Torah and mitzvos, and in their inner dimension. One draws closer to this, and in time also recognizes and feels it, through the study of Chassidus and by following its guidance. From this, it is understood that any matter of preparation is a gain, and a very significant gain at that, and not, Heaven forbid, time that was not utilized (as it should be, or at least to its fullest). As you conclude in your letter, there is nothing that stands before the will; when you study with *mesiras nefesh*, you will certainly succeed in this, and it will also assist you throughout your entire life in both spiritual and physical matters.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above, and for success in all of this.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5111

B"H, 29 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter, outlining the main points of your activities and your holy work since you were here. It is surprising that you do not mention how your matter of serving as *shaliach tzibbur* went, although I am firmly hopeful that it was in the best possible manner. Surely, the *Ribono shel Olam* fulfilled His promise, and based on what is understood from *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 1, your prayer was accepted within the collective of *Klal Yisrael* to draw down a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

Regarding what you wrote about having no money—this statement is surprising. Since the *Ribono shel Olam* says, "Mine is the silver and Mine is the gold," surely funds will not be lacking, *chas v'shalom*, for everything you and your family—may they live—require, both for general matters and for personal ones. The proof of this is the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that the past teaches us about the future. Just as you have seen the kindnesses of the *Ribono shel Olam* in the past, the promise of our Sages will surely be fulfilled, that all who do good for Him will be rewarded with long days and years. Certainly, on their part as well, they will maintain and strengthen the channels, and will continue to widen and enlarge them. It is obvious that I am referring to matters of Torah and *mitzvos*.

With blessings for good tidings and regards to all those you influence—may they live.

## 5812

B”H, 29 Tishrei, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your two letters from before the holiday season. Regarding your question as to what I mean when I say that the person in charge of the institution must have a Chabad character:

It is surprising that there is even any doubt about this, as the matters are quite simple. Even in an institution that has no other owners, if there is no person in charge who knows that he must bear the responsibility, the matter cannot exist as it should, and sometimes it cannot exist at all. Although I avoid causing pain to anyone, for the sake of the matter, I am compelled to bring evidence from within the four cubits of [the community]... where they tried and even founded a branch of Toras Emes in... where both he and [Rabbi...] were present. Not only did it not develop, but after a **very** short time, it was completely dissolved. And **all of Anash together** did not hold out in the aforementioned, and that is without even emphasizing the public disgrace!

It is understood that I remember all the reasons that he and Rabbi... wrote. But at that time, and even now, I am astonished that they do not recognize the situation as it is: that a branch of Toras Emes in... is to the credit of the Anash of... and first and foremost, it is the **obligation** of the Rabbonim of Anash, who are called *mara d’asra* according to Chassidus, that **they** should have immediately taken care to come and build the four cubits of the Torah of Chassidus in... And not only for themselves, but, and primarily, for the younger generation, who must build homes in Yisrael in the near future.

Many have heard that the *Temimim* must be candles that illuminate, specifically. And after many years passed and they did nothing, and after the members of the administration of... aroused the Anash of... regarding their aforementioned obligation—and not only that, but they also assisted with financial aid and by bringing students to establish...—he and his colleague, the Rabbi, interpreted the matter **the opposite** of what it is. That is to say, they think they are doing a **favor** to the administration of... by helping to establish the branch, and if the administration of... cannot sustain the finances, etc., their hands are washed of it, etc.—at a time when the matter is the exact opposite.

And can it be believed? Both of them serve in holiness in Rabbinical positions, dealing with the guarding of many "vineyards": kosher meat, kosher *gittin*, kosher *kiddushin*, etc.—and only "my vineyard," that is, the dissemination of the wellsprings of *Chassidus* (which in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily, can only be done through the establishment of an educational institution), they have **decided** is not their concern at all, and consequently, it seems to them that it is not within their capability either. And all the more so: if in a matter founded by the administration of..., he and the Rabbi could not hold out and continue, at a time when in the city of... they give much money for the maintenance of institutions and there are many students for such educational studies—I am highly "doubtful" that if an institution were founded by an active person, as is apparent from the above, the main activity of this institution would be carried out by this person, while he would merely utilize their names for the "Chabad" label. And it is obvious that they would not be diligent, and it is obvious that they would not consult on the development of the institution. From the first day of its founding, or at least within the first few weeks, the founding Rabbi will see that they are not eager for the development of the institution, he will leave them in peace, and the institution will have no connection to Chabad other than the name. And I am not eager for publicity without substance, but rather for the dissemination of the wellsprings, regarding which—as our Sages have informed us in this, as in all matters of our holy Torah—"If you have not labored and found, do not believe." And he will not delve into this, and the Rabbi... will also not labor in this, as experience has shown in the past. And the founding Rabbi sees no reason why, all of a sudden, he would be interested in a new matter for which he bears no responsibility.

I have written at length regarding all the above, and perhaps in sharp terms, and this is in response to the conclusion of his letter, which states: "In truth, we are also pained (regarding the manner of the management of Chabad institutions in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily, we wanted and desired to do something to fix it, etc., but as it appears, it is impossible for known reasons, etc.)." And as I have written already, reasons in the plural are unknown to me; there is only one reason, and that is the principle: "Sit and do nothing is better" and more comfortable.

And the pain, etc., both my pain and theirs—the saying we heard many times from the Rebbe is well known: "One action is better than a thousand sighs." And regarding what he wrote, that I should inform him what I want, what is missing, and what needs to be fixed—Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily, is full of educational institutions, *yeshivos*, *chadorim*, and *Talmud Torahs*. And not only those that were founded decades ago, but also new ones daily. If only they would emulate... etc., who in recent years have established many institutions, even though they did not merit even a **fraction** of the guidance of our Rebbeim, the *Nesi'im*, and the abundance of good that they poured out upon the *Temimim* and Anash from their Torah and their *mesiras nefesh*. And *k’lapi layah yatziva b’ara* (to the contrary, the truth is established on the ground), etc. It is understood that my words above are directed not only to him, but to all Anash who are in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily, except for a few people—a youth could write them down—who are striving to do what is dependent upon them...

## 5414

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Tishrei:

At an *eis ratzon*, I will mention all those you wrote about at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever they may need, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Regarding your question about the apartment: In general, according to what is explained in many places regarding housing, one should give great consideration to the opinion of the woman of the house for several reasons. Therefore, if you can, through pleasant ways, influence her to agree to the apartment where you are currently living—especially since, as you wrote, you have already been living there for about two years—that would be for the best.

However, if she will not agree to this under any circumstances, you should do as she wishes.

Regarding the situation of your daughter, may she live and be well, and her development—which is not satisfactory, etc.: You surely know that in recent years, several new types of treatment have been developed for such matters. Therefore, it is worthwhile to consult a doctor in this field, especially regarding these new treatments, to see if they are appropriate for this specific case.

May it be the will of Hashem that they provide the best advice for your daughter, may she live and be well, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed.

Since you conclude your letter by mentioning that you work as a professional teacher, etc.—which means that you have an influence on many of the children of Israel—even though you do not specify the subject you teach, it is tangibly evident that a teacher of any subject has a special influence on those who listen to his instruction, including in matters of religion and ethics. My hope is that you will utilize this opportunity to the best of your ability. In the measure of the Holy One, Blessed be He—which is "measure for measure," only many times over—may you and your wife, may she live and be well, be rewarded with an abundance of *nachas* from all your children, may they live and be well, which includes your aforementioned daughter, may she live and be well.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

P.S.
You surely know of the three daily *shiurim* in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, which, as we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, are appropriate for every soul. They are a *segulah* for many matters; in any case, you should keep them from now on.

## 8815

8815

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a very long interval, I received your letter from Monday, in which you write about the ups and downs you experienced over the past year, how this affected you, and that for various reasons you did not speak to anyone about this, etc.

It is understandable that the above is surprising, for surely you have studied the holy Tanya many times, from which it is understood—and it is also simple—that the concept of despair and the like is entirely refuted. See there, where it is explained well. Therefore, I will not dwell on this at length in my writing, due to the simplicity of the matter; there you will also find methods of rectification. It is also understood from there that the rectification is step-by-step, and not by jumping all at once.

The second matter mentioned above is also surprising, for the saying and message of the Mitteler Rebbe is well-known: that when two of the Jewish people speak together about matters of Torah and mitzvos (which, it is understood, applies both to the line of "doing good" and the line of "turning away from evil"), then they are two G-dly souls against one natural soul, and the resulting effect is understood. And since you have merited to enter to study in the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim—for which our holy Rebbes sacrificed themselves for its founding, its management, and its spirit, and the words of the tzaddikim endure forever—there is certainly Siyata Dishmaya to an even greater extent. This is on the condition that the student also does what is dependent upon him in the line of obligation, and rejects the matters that are in the line of negation (and in this, of course, is included the matter of despair, sadness, etc.). Then, the success will be even beyond what is expected. And the merit of your activities—whose inner point is the drawing of the hearts of the Jewish people to our Father in Heaven—will increase the aforementioned success, measure for measure, also regarding yourself.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary
