## 8816

8816

By the grace of G-d, 2 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Directorate of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
Tel Aviv Branch
May they live

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the report from the gathering of 27 Elul and the report on the activities of the months of Elul and Tishrei. I look forward to hearing more good news regarding your good work. It is surprising to read that you discussed where to obtain the Arba Minim needed for this mivtza, for surely all those involved in this have their own Arba Minim, or those of their fathers and relatives. It is already known that the conduct of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, was to allow many people to make a bracha on his esrog. It is told of one of the great Tzaddikim (I believe from Poland) that he acted this way consistently. When asked about the concern that handling the esrog might affect its hadar (beauty/integrity), he replied that there is no greater hadar than having many of the children of Israel fulfill this exalted mitzvah with it (and note the Gemara in Sukkah 35b, which states that one should not take an esrog of pure terumah only because it causes a loss to the owner. And look closely at this). It is a known principle of our Sages that a person is pleased to have a mitzvah performed with his money (and even if it is a minority, it is not otherwise, for in matters of money we do not follow the majority. See Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken, siman 269). If this is true for all mitzvos, how much more so for this mitzvah, whose essence is the unity of all Israel—which is the hint behind the Arba Minim—as is explained at length in many places and in the discourses of Chassidus.

It is understood that, as is my custom in other matters, I will, G-d willing, encourage anash to participate in this mivtza. You will surely inform me of your expenses, and I will encourage anash to participate in the special collection, covering approximately one-third of the actual expenses.

If the speeches from the 15 Elul gathering were recorded (at least their content), and surely there are also photographs from the gathering, it would be worthwhile to look into the possibility of publishing a booklet containing the above, along with some words of inspiration regarding Torah and mitzvos and the dissemination of the wellsprings. It would be appropriate for everything to be ready and published even before the celebration of 19 Kislev, upcoming. Since it requires time for editing, etc., it is worth looking into this as soon as possible. One should not limit the size of the booklet in advance; it depends on the material that will bring about a desired result, including regarding future activity and the Chabad institutions in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily.

You do not mention at all a farbrengen in Kfar Chabad itself, other than the farbrengen on Motzaei Simchas Torah. Surely the Kfar Chabad branch will provide information regarding this, for although the matter of disseminating the wellsprings outward is great, it is also said, "and do not hide yourself from your own flesh," in addition to the concept that even Ze'er Anpin is called "outward."

See also the Tzemach Tzedek’s notes to Eichah, p. 21.

With blessings for success, awaiting good news regarding all the above.

The reports from 29 Tammuz and 5 Elul were received in due course.

## 5817

B"H, 2nd of Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

Following the longest of interruptions, I received your letter from the 27th of Tishrei. Even in it, I did not find any reason or explanation for your silence throughout this entire time. This also raises the concern that during this period, you have not been printing materials regarding the *hafatzas hamaayanos* (as you surely would have sent the clippings here, as was your custom in the past), and likewise regarding your participation in the *farbrengens* of *anash* and the affairs of *anash* in general. Perhaps you will address this in your next letter.

It is my hope that, as you wrote in your letter, you will not delay the date of the wedding, in a good and auspicious hour, beyond the upcoming month of Kislev.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the expenses involved in arranging a "large wedding":

It is entirely unclear why you feel the need to pressure yourself with special expenses in order for it to be specifically a "large wedding," etc., at a time when what matters is that it be a wedding that is "large" in quality. This is especially true according to the words of our Sages on the verse "a great feast" (*Bereishis Rabbah*, ch. 43), that the "Great One of the worlds" should be present there. That is to say, it should be evident in all the details of the wedding—and primarily in all matters concerning the *chassan* and *kallah* in their preparation for the wedding and their resolutions for the future—that the "Great One of the worlds" agrees with them. This is what is meant by "the *Shechinah* dwells between them." It is understood that this is not tied to material expenses [aside from the allocations for *tzedakah*; these allocations are not an expense, since Hashem promises "tithe so that you will become wealthy," and "test Me now with this," etc.]. What is known in the eyes of the world (and in the language of *Chassidus*, *veltishe hanachos*) as a "large" wedding—with a *tararam* (commotion), etc.—is not worthwhile for several reasons.

I hope that just as you are making a plan regarding the material aspects of these matters, you are all the more so making preparations regarding the spiritual aspects. The matter of a wedding is established by the *Knesses Hagedolah* as a "building of eternity" (*binyan adei ad*). If, regarding a dwelling for a short time, one writes that one is so interested in the details, then how much more so is this true for a dwelling for decades, and how much more so for a dwelling for the entire duration of a person's life on earth, and how much more so for a "building of eternity," for the *neshamah* is eternal. And this is easy to understand.

I await good news regarding all of the above.

## 5118

B"H, 3rd of Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 27th of Tishrei, in which you write the main points of the past days of Tishrei. It is surprising that you are even more brief than a concise summary; may it be His will that at the next opportunity you fill this in, and from here on, that matters be detailed as necessary.

Regarding what you wrote—that you lack *chayus* in both *nigleh* and *Chassidus*—there are two points to consider:

1) It is known what is brought in the *sicha* of Simchas Torah 5690, section 21: "What do you want from me? Demand it of yourself." It is understood that this response is not intended to dismiss a request, *chas v'shalom*, nor to say "I have saved my own soul." Rather, it is a granting of strength. This is also known from the parable of the Baal Shem Tov regarding the townspeople who relied on the hero; through the fact that they subsequently realized they could not rely on the hero, tremendous and wondrous powers were awakened within them. The same applies in your case.

2) It is necessary to say this because of the second point (copied in *Hayom Yom*, 23rd of Sivan): that any *hisbonenus* which prevents good deeds does not originate from a pure place. From this, it is understood—and it is also simple—that the matter which nullifies this *hisbonenus* comes from true good, in the manner of "and one nation shall be stronger than the other nation." It is a pity to waste time on the aforementioned *hisbonenus*, in addition to the hindrance it causes in *hafotzas hamaayanos*. As is known from the saying of our Nasi, that "behold, He stands behind our wall," and in another moment the days will come—in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, "Then one will clutch his head, [wondering] why one let such a precious time pass when one could have accomplished so much," and *kal v'chomer*.

With blessings for good tidings, and regards to all those you influence, *shichyu*.

***

**5118**

**"What do you want from me":** See also above, Vol. 13, letter 4514, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

**"One will clutch his head":** See also above, Vol. 14, letter 5025, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 5819

B"H, 3rd of Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and refined,
R' Chaim Avraham Halevi, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter, bearing the good news of the improvement in your health and that you are already back at home. May it be Hashem’s will that your condition continue to improve, and that you return to your full strength—both in the literal sense and in the deeper sense, as explained in the *maamar* "Maskil L'Eisan" by our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, printed in *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*.

At an appropriate time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, each according to their specific needs as described in your letter. Based on the Sages' teaching that "whoever is granted a kindness, it is for long, good days and years," since you have begun with the good news of the success of the medical treatment for your health, may it be Hashem’s will that this statement be fulfilled for you as well, and that you bring good tidings regarding the other matters mentioned in your letter.

A sign of this is that this year, the beginning of the days of the year—following Rosh Hashanah—was Shabbos. On Shabbos, "there is no other dominion in all the worlds," and "the countenance is illuminated with a supernal light." This is the "light of the King’s countenance," which is life, from the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He. An analogy for this is found in earthly kingdoms: even the greatest criminal, when being led to the gallows, if he encounters the King, is pardoned from all punishment and sent home in peace. How much more so, and with greater force, when one encounters the *Shabbos Malketa* (the Sabbath Queen), and the Shabbos that is adjacent to the "long day" of Rosh Hashanah—for on Rosh Hashanah, too, "Hashem reigns, He has robed Himself in majesty," which is revealed. As brought in *Pirkei D'Rabbi Eliezer*, this is the statement of Adam HaRishon, who said to all the creatures of the world, even to the beasts and animals: "Come, let us bow down and kneel, for Hashem is King in a revealed manner," even to the eyes of flesh, animals, and beasts.

May it be Hashem’s will that in our immediate future, we merit the fulfillment of the prophecy, "And the glory of Hashem shall be revealed, and all flesh together shall see, etc.," as explained by the Mitteler Rebbe, son of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya*, that even the animals and beasts will recognize this—similar to the cows that carried the Ark in the days of David*, of which it is written, "And they went straight, etc."

With blessings for good tidings, as stated above.

## 8820

B"H, 3rd of Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished participants of the public Talmud Torah shiur,
May you all be blessed,

Peace and blessing!

I received your Pidyon Nefesh in due time, and on the eve of the past Rosh Hashanah, I read it at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, leader of Israel.

Regarding a leader of Israel, the well-known statement of our Sages applies: "Just as he stands and serves there, so too he stands and serves here," awakening Divine mercy for his flock for whatever they require, from soul to body.

May it be the will of Hashem, in His abundant mercies, to bless this year so that all the blessings with which the children of Israel blessed one another will be fulfilled in their entirety, from soul to body.

This applies especially to those who set fixed times for Torah study, which is the channel and vessel for receiving Hashem’s blessings for everything a person and their household requires. This should be a fixed commitment in accordance with the adage of our Alter Rebbe—the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah and the Shulchan Aruch, the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah—a commitment in time and a commitment in the soul, which is the essence.

It is well known that "that which is fixed does not cease." This means that this matter is powerful enough to overcome the concealments and hiddenness in our world, and to draw down the blessing written in our Torah, "If you walk in My statutes... you shall labor in Torah, and I will provide your rains in their time," and all the matters enumerated in that parsha.

May it be the will of Hashem that you all receive good tidings, each from the other, only good—both in material and in spiritual matters.

With respect and blessing,

#### ***8820***

**In the public Talmud Torah shiur:** By Rabbi Gluskin, Ramat HaSharon.

## 8821

8821

B"H, 3rd of Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 27th of Tishrei. May it be the will of Hashem, in His abundant mercies, that He bless this year so that all the blessings which the children of Israel have bestowed upon one another may be fulfilled in their entirety, from the soul down to the flesh.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the reasons for withdrawing from this proposal, and that the other matter is being neglected, etc.: I believe I have already written several times in my letters that the ruling of our holy Torah is well known—that even in a situation of complete *ones* (duress), we do not say "it is considered as if it were done." What good will all the reasons and justifications do, when there must be an actual, concrete action? Especially since human intellect—even that of a complete *tzaddik* who is not subject to any ulterior motive—is suspected of being subservient to desire. Therefore, the "bribe" of self-love can distort the words of *tzaddikim*. And indeed, the test is well known (copied in *Hayom Yom*, 23rd of Sivan) that if contemplation prevents a good action (and action in this case is the true good—good for Heaven and good for people, for "He created it to be inhabited"), it does not come from the true good...

May it be the will of Hashem that this be a year of success for you in general matters, in your personal affairs, and in the specific and primary matter that brings tranquility and wholeness, and as our Sages have said regarding this, a good *shidduch* in both material and spiritual respects together.

#### ***8821***

**From the proposal:** *Shidduch*.

\*) And the proof from *Sanhedrin* (18b) regarding the *Kohen Gadol* due to the cold is well known.

## 8222

B"H, 3rd of Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, a man of many accomplishments, R' Hillel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning a birthday: For the time being, I have found only one source regarding this, which is in the Yerushalmi, that on a person's birthday, their *mazal* is strengthened. However, this is also understood from the interpretation of the verse "And these days are remembered and kept" (Esther 9:28)—that on every anniversary of the year, the matters return to their original state. A known proof for this is from the law in the Mishnah (Gittin, end of chapter 3) that wine found in **barrels** changes at the turn of the year from the day of the "birth" of the grapes. In any case, it is known that a *maaseh* (an established practice) is great and powerful, even more so than a *sevara* (logical reasoning), and consequently even more so than a *mikra* (scriptural verse). Our Rebbeim, the *Nesi'im* holy ones, followed this custom, albeit privately.

With blessings.

## 8823

B"H, 4th of Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the avreich Binyamin Natan, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, along with the *pidyon nefesh* which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in which you write regarding your current affairs and your uncertainty concerning your future, etc.

In my opinion, since rumor has it that you are successful in the field of *chinuch*, and those who engage in this "work of Heaven"—namely, *chinuch* on the purity of holiness—are extremely few, while at the same time the demand for this is many times greater, to the point that it appears that in the near future in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, the livelihood of those engaged in this will also be secured—my opinion is that you should continue your work in the Chabad educational institutions, in a manner that will allow you to utilize your talents in this area as much as possible, and consequently, this will also develop more and more...

It is my hope that within the framework of the activities of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, you will utilize your influence on your friends who for the time being remain in the IDF, to influence them to connect more to matters of Yiddishkeit in general (the essence of which is, of course and simply, *mitzvos maasiyos*) and to matters of Chassidus in particular. As I have already written to someone else, all those who have been in the IDF have the merit and the obligation in this regard even more so, for several understandable reasons, and the main point is that they are in a position to influence more than those who were never in that framework.

I trust that you have *shiurim* in the study of *nigleh* and Chassidus, in addition to the three well-known *shiurim* in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*.

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 5824

5824

B.H., 5th of Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a most lengthy hiatus, your letter of the 26th of Tishrei was received. It is surprising that you do not mention how you utilized the *yimei haratzon* (days of favor) of the month of Tishrei. It is understood that I refer not only to your own person as an individual, but—and this is the main point—to your influence upon the many, for you have been gifted with this power of influence by *Hashgacha Elyona* (Divine Providence), and you must bring it into revelation and actuality. Surely you will make up for this at the next opportunity.

Regarding your question as to which chapters of *Tanya* and other *Chassidus* books to include in the program:

Surely you possess, or will find among *anash* in *Eretz Yisrael* (may it be rebuilt and established), the recent editions of *Tanya*, *Torah Or*, *Derech Mitzvosecha*, and *Shaarei Orah*. These books contain a subject index where you will find the answer to the above regarding the topics you write about, as well as regarding new topics should you wish to include them in the program.

Regarding what you wrote about the method of study: it is understood that this depends on the nature of the soul and the talents of each individual, as well as how much of his time is dedicated to study. Therefore, in this matter, one must consult specifically with those who are in his environment and know him, and he should detail all the aforementioned particulars to them.

A general point that applies to every soul is that both in *nigleh* (the revealed Torah) and in *nistar* (the hidden Torah), there must be study for the sake of *lemigras* (rote memorization/covering ground) and study for the sake of *leiyuna* (in-depth analysis). For the former is also of the utmost importance in order to acquire sufficiently broad knowledge, both in *nigleh* and in *nistar*, at least in a superficial manner.

As for what you wrote—that you become excited and experience *hispaalus*, but after a short while it passes, and consequently it interferes with your *avodah*—on the contrary, the excitement and *hispaalus* themselves should be utilized in holiness. Regarding your statement that it interferes with *hisbonenus* (contemplation), it is understood that one can restrain the excitement and *hispaalus* when studying from a text or in a group. In such a case, the letters of the text or the peers hold one back (*halten op*), not allowing one to fulfill his obligation in a superficial manner alone. The main thing in the above, as in all matters of holiness, is that it must be in a manner of "you have labored," for then we are promised "you have found."

It is also understood that your excuse regarding the delay until now in matters of *shidduch* is not "satisfactory" at all. Since it is a great *mitzvah* according to *Shulchan Aruch* and affects every aspect of a person’s activities—as is known from our Sages, "Whoever dwells without a wife..." and various matters are detailed there—the reasons you write are, in the vast majority of cases, merely coming to justify the lack of the energy required for such matters. In the language of our Sages, it should be "like a person searching for his lost object." It is obvious that these lines of mine are not intended as a moral rebuke, but rather to awaken and illuminate that one must act in this most exalted matter with the greatest energy, and focus on the essential rather than the peripheral; for then the *Ribono shel Olam* grants success, such that the peripheral also comes into reality.

Enclosed is a copy of my general letter for the past *Rosh Hashanah*, which I hope you will be able to utilize in your activities in general, and which is appropriate to the points mentioned above in particular.

Awaiting good news.

## 5825

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter with the enclosed *pidyon nefesh*, in which you write regarding the matter of secular studies and asking me to write to the administrator about this, etc.

It is understood that this is not the way, as this is the concern of each individual and not the concern of the institution, which has a charter regarding this. The matter is the concern of each of the parents who desire the true well-being of their children—that they should live—in that they must fulfill the instruction of our Sages, of blessed memory, to "feed him like an ox." And if they have informed us that "where one would feed vegetables, one should feed meat," then how much more so in the present case, where it is not even "vegetables." Furthermore, it is the opposite, as is explained in the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of the Alter Rebbe, in *Tanya*, and elsewhere.

Regarding what you wrote that they told you, that "one must know how to ask," etc.—it is true that one should not ask about this, because as stated above, the matter is simple in *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, in *Tanya*, and in many other places.

Regarding your informing me of the condition of your wife, *tichyeh*, may the *Ribono shel Olam* fulfill the days of her pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child at its proper time, properly and with ease.

With blessings for good tidings.

Regarding your question: since you have finished *Torah Ohr* and *Likutei Torah*, as a replacement for that study, you should study the aforementioned works again, and you will surely see an increase in understanding, etc.

## 8,830

8,830

B"H, 6th of Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Tuesday: I hope that, even though you did not mention it, upon returning to New Haven you indeed shared the content of the farbrengen here—the relevant points—with those whom you influence, and which are truly appropriate for them. After all, we spoke of matters of Torah and mitzvos, which were given to **all** Jews until the end of all generations. As is well known, this is why the language at the giving of the Torah, "Anochi Hashem Elokecha" (I am Hashem your G-d), is in the singular—because it was addressed to every single one of the six hundred thousand who were present at the time, as well as to all the souls of all generations who were also present at the standing at Har Sinai, as stated in Pirkei DeRebbi Eliezer.

In accordance with your request, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. When you write the name of your wife, may she live and be well, along with her mother's name—their names in Lashon HaKodesh—she will also be mentioned, as is the custom of Israel to mention someone by their name and their mother's name. May Hashem Yisbarach help that you should soon be able to report good tidings regarding all the details you wrote about, and also regarding the matter of the "cruse of oil" that you mentioned. Literally speaking, we are always drawing closer to Chanukah, when the miracle was revealed. The preparation for that was the mesiras nefesh of Jews in those days. Mesiras nefesh does not necessarily mean that a gentile comes to wage war; it also includes mesiras nefesh in the war against the nefesh habahamis, which, unfortunately, one must do quite often. Since one is compelled to do so, it is certain that Hashem gives the strength to be victorious, and with joy and a good heart.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 8430

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Wednesday, in which you write regarding the doctor’s opinion concerning the condition of your left eye, and you ask for my opinion on this matter.

It is already well-known that the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life, is what grants permission in this matter, and it is this that also provides the power for the doctor to heal. Regarding a surgery such as the one you describe, it is also understood that it must be performed by the most expert doctor, who surely has more experience (*praktike*) in this, as experience in such matters is more relevant than theoretical knowledge. May it be the will of the Healer of all flesh, who performs wonders, that He heal you through this person and this treatment at a good and auspicious time.

It is understood that since the matters of the human body are dependent upon the matters of the human soul, and the matters of a Jewish person are dependent upon the Torah—and consequently, everything that the Holy One, blessed be He, created in the body has its parallel and source in the soul, and everything that exists in a Jewish person is found in the Torah—from this it is understood that when a repair is needed in the body, there must be a repair in the corresponding matter of the soul. And when a repair and improvement is needed in the matter of a Jewish person, there must be a repair and improvement in the corresponding matter in the Torah. As our Sages of blessed memory said: "If one feels pain in his head, he should engage in Torah; if he feels pain in his entire body, he should engage in Torah," etc. In the present case, it is essential that you resolve to increase, from now on, your study of that part of the Torah called the "light of the Torah," which is the inner dimension of the Torah (which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus). Through this, success will be added to the light of the matters of the soul and the light of the matters of the body. This is understood based on all of the above.

With blessings for good tidings in all that has been mentioned.

The conclusion from the above is that if there are any details regarding the young woman that are not clear to you, they should be clarified through friends or the like, and this is sufficient and adequate.

## 8832

8832

B"H, 7 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc.,
Rabbi Nissan Nemanov, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter regarding the arrival of the new class of avreichim students from Morocco. May it be the will of Hashem that He increase their borders, both in quality and in quantity—that is, in the number of students, in their knowledge, and in the caliber of their conduct.

Since additional benches have been added to the beis medrash, it is imperative that the situation of the school for soferim finally be strengthened and established as it should be, or at least to a degree comparable to the mikveh. As I discussed here with the esteemed Chassid, etc., Rabbi Tzvi Leib Levin, may he live, it is understood that the students of the school for soferus are also students of Tomchei Temimim. This means that they must study the regular shiurim in nigleh and Chassidus, etc., and also engage in the avodah of tefillah. It is only that for a portion of the day—when the other students are studying in the yeshivah—these students study this melaches hakodesh, namely the writing of STa"M. However, before and after these hours, they bear all the responsibilities of a student of Tomchei Temimim. Consequently, it is understood that there is no reason for anyone among them to feel discouraged, chas v'shalom.

On the other hand, they must receive instructions regarding their studies in nigleh and Chassidus from the mashpi'im and roshei yeshivah of Tomchei Temimim, except for those hours dedicated to the study of soferus STa"M and the relevant halachos, in which they receive instruction from the esteemed Chassid, etc., Rabbi Tzvi Leib Levin, may he live.

In order for the study to align with our teachings regarding *dibuk chaveirim* (the bonding of peers), it is necessary that, in addition to those two who have already completed the training—and as you wrote to me, have already begun writing parshiyos and making batim—there be at least five students studying soferus. It would be even better if there were six or more, provided this is possible without disrupting a class in Tomchei Temimim.

Based on the above, I am confident that the administration of Tomchei Temimim will select suitable students for this—meaning, after they are tested in the craft and it is seen that they are capable of it. And so that there should not be any grievances or wasted time later, it is understood that it is more appropriate to conduct the testing and selection as close to the beginning of the zman as possible. I will await good news soon.

Please convey to those students who are selected that fortunate is their lot to be engaged in this melaches hakodesh. For although the responsibility of a sofer STa"M is great, as is explained in several places, the very fact that others have determined they are worthy of learning this melaches hakodesh shows that from Above they have been given the strength to bear this responsibility and fulfill it. In all times, and certainly now, by enabling the many to perform the mitzvah with kosher tefillin and kosher mezuzos, their reward is beyond description. This is especially so given that the entire Torah is compared to tefillin, and in Chassidus it is brought that a mezuzah is equivalent to all the mitzvos.

Even according to nigleh, this is understood based on the kavanah cited in the Shulchan Aruch as a halachic ruling: that tefillin is a matter of the subjugation of the heart and the brain—that is, the entirety of the person—and the mezuzah is the seal of the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, upon all the possessions and matters within that house.

I will await good news regarding all of the above. To expedite the matter, this letter is being sent via express mail. With blessings for success in your holy work.

**M. Schneerson**

## 5833

Brooklyn.

To the partners of the Independent Tinware Co., may they be well,

Peace and blessing!

I received your *pidyon nefesh* note in due time, requesting success for the business.

This is done by resolving with your whole heart to give between ten and twenty percent of the profits to *tzedakah*. Just as any partner does everything in their power to ensure the success of the business, so too will Hashem, as a partner, certainly grant His blessing and success in the aforementioned endeavor.

It goes without saying that one must ensure the vessel remains a *keli tahorah* (a pure vessel) according to the instructions of our holy Torah. This applies not only to *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*, but also to *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*, and regarding matters such as *hasagas gevul* (encroachment on another's livelihood), and so on. Although there is a *chazakah* (presumption) that the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov fulfill what Hashem has commanded, the above is mentioned to encourage diligence, preference, and increase. May Hashem help that this diligence, preference, and increase on your part should also increase the blessings from Hashem, which will come with diligence—that is, very soon—and with preference and increase beyond what one could expect through the ordinary course of nature.

Looking forward to hearing good news.

## 8,833

B”H, 9 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the 2nd of MarCheshvan, in which you write regarding the debts that have accumulated over the last few years, and that seemingly you do not see a way at present to settle them, and therefore it has occurred to you that perhaps it would be worthwhile to travel abroad for a few years to earn an income there in a manner that would not only cover current expenses but also suffice to settle the debts.

Now, it is understood that first and foremost, the travel expenses for the round trip will be added, which are not insignificant. Furthermore, moving from one place to another is generally associated with special expenses. It is also understood that there is no absolute certainty that in the country to which you would go, you would earn enough to cover all expenses and debts, for those who make promises can only guarantee them for a year or two—and this, too, only if conditions do not change significantly, among other uncertainties. In addition to all the above, there are also the difficulties of adjusting to a new place, especially regarding young children. For all these reasons, the aforementioned idea does not seem advisable to me.

Rather, you should look into opportunities for additional income locally, beyond your permanent position, just as you have seen the kindness of Hashem regarding your shidduch, children, apartment, etc. (And surely you remember that in those matters, too, you were, G-d forbid, in despair). My hope is that in this matter as well, the future will be better than you anticipate, provided that you increase your efforts **and apply yourself personally** to the channel and vessel for what is needed for you and your household, may they live...

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned—and since everything follows the conclusion—may you do your part to increase courage in your holy work, and as a result of the cause, may you also bring good news regarding your personal matters.

## 8834

B"H, 9 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos.

At an opportune time, I will mention your wife, may she live and be well, at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. This is appropriate, as you were privileged to hear from him the well-known maamar regarding the verse, "Therefore those who speak in parables say, 'Come, let us calculate,'" and it is understood that as you increase in Torah and mitzvos—in accordance with what our Sages of blessed memory explained regarding the verse, "Come and let us calculate the reckoning of the world"—you will receive an increase in the blessings of Hashem in all that is needed, both materially and spiritually.

It is obvious that what you write in your letter—that you are unworthy of writing because you lack the strength to stand in the battle against the yetzer, etc.—is incorrect. Surely you remember, or at the very least you should now study in the holy Tanya, how even those for whom the battle against the yetzer is difficult within their own four cubits have been given the full ability not only to stand in the battle, but also to be victorious (see the places indicated in the index of subjects in the appendix to the Tanya). This is especially true for those who were privileged to see the face of a tzaddik and hear his words, for the words of the tzaddikim are alive and enduring and continue to exert their influence. This is all the more so regarding spiritual matters; after all, everyone agrees, even non-Jews, that it is impossible to create something from nothing (only to change a form), so how much more so is this true regarding spiritual matters, and even more so regarding matters of Torah and mitzvos.

According to the adage of our Rebbes, "One action is better than a thousand sighs." Therefore, instead of sighing over yourself, etc.—even though that is sometimes necessary—it is certainly better to begin taking action to increase in Torah and mitzvos beyond what you have done until now. Those who occupy themselves with this are promised an increase in the blessings of Hashem in all that is needed.

May it be the will of Hashem that in His abundant mercies, He will continue to bestow an increase of blessing and success for the future as well, and may you bring good tidings regarding all of the above.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 8,335

8,335

B"H, 9 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write about two possibilities for how to construct the internal road.

It is simple that in such matters, the committee on-site must make the decision. If it is a difficult matter for any reason, the spiritual committee and, in general, the elders of Anash in your camp should be included. The general point in this is that the ways of Chassidim and Chassidus are only ways of pleasantness and peace. However, at the same time, it is simple that the benefit of the many overrides the benefit of the individual, and ultimately, since the individual is part of the many, he will certainly recognize that his own benefit is also contained within the benefit of the many.

It is understood that in this case, one must also discuss the detail you mention regarding the fruit trees, where in one of the options they would need to be uprooted. This is a question of Din, and they will surely clarify it before making a decision on the matter.

Based on the above, it is understood that everything written here is unofficial, and only in the nature of a suggestion to discuss all of the above in accordance with the conditions on-site.

I take this opportunity to urge you, as well as your colleagues on the committee and, in general, the activists and the finest of Anash in Kfar Chabad, that it is imperative that you take a much greater interest in the **general** affairs of the village. For to my regret, until now, in the vast majority of cases, the attitude of most of the village residents toward the affairs of the village has been that of an individual interested only in his own welfare and private matters—except that this also included utilizing the group of village residents to improve his private situation, and the necessary interest in the shared affairs of the village residents as a whole was not evident.

In other words, they viewed themselves as a certain number of Jews who happened to be in one lodging within the four cubits of the village, but each one stands in his own reality and will not concede his private interest at all, unless he will also gain more in his own private matter. Based on the above, the phenomenon is also understood whereby most, if not all, of the general, shared affairs of the village **are neglected**, and elaboration for those who are on-site and see the state of affairs is surely superfluous.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

#### ***8,335***

From a copy.

**The internal road:** In Kfar Chabad.

## 8,836

B"H, 10th of Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos, in which you ask—following what the Alter Rebbe writes in Iggeres HaTeshuvah regarding giving tzedakah in place of a taanit—whether a "taanit dibbur" (a fast of speech) also serves as a substitute.

It is understood from the entire presentation in Iggeres HaTeshuvah that in this case, it does not. See also Iggeres HaTeshuvah there, Chapter 3, and certainly the authorities who rule to give [the value of the meal] for every day of fasting, etc. The matter of a taanit dibbur and the like is a separate concept, applicable in certain cases (see also Sefer HaToldot Maharash, page 72, at the end), but it does not replace the fasts **mentioned** [in the Alter Rebbe's discussion].

Regarding your question about the custom of giving coins, etc.—it requires study as to what practical difference this makes for your own affairs. It is well known that our Sages said that Hashem did not create a single thing in His world in vain. This is also a directive for a person’s own affairs: that all of his thoughts, speech, and actions must not be in vain, but rather for a purpose and a goal. That purpose and goal is as the Mishnah rules: "I was created to serve my Maker." This is also understood from the Rambam, the Tur, and the Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chayim, Siman 231, that one must "know Him in **all** your ways." Regarding the explanation of the specific question you raised—what the effect of this [custom] is, and whether it is done so that people will not say, etc.—it is possible to say that it is an explicit Gemara (Bava Basra 15b, end of the page).

I hope that you are increasing from time to time not only in the study of the revealed Torah, but also in the teachings of Chassidus, for this is an explicit law: "We elevate in matters of holiness."

#### ***8,836***

**That they would give coins:** Polish Rebbes—for protection and the like. What is the concept behind this? See also Igros Kodesh of the Rebbe Rayatz, Vol. 7, Letter 1,873, and the references noted in the footnotes there.

## 8,838

B"H, 11 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and industrious, involved in communal needs, R' Moshe Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 4 MarCheshvan.

You have surely already received the response regarding the questionnaire via telephone, due to the time constraints.

Regarding what you wrote about instituting the recitation of the monthly Tehillim shiur in the various classes of the school: although it is well-known, and we have heard many times about the greatness of this Tehillim shiur, one must still take into account for each individual class how much time the recitation of the entire shiur will take. After all, this time will be subtracted from their holy studies, which are already limited as it is. Therefore, while in the higher grades, where their reading of Lashon HaKodesh is fluent, this should be instituted, in the lower grades one must consider the aforementioned. In the very youngest classes, one should suffice with reciting one chapter from the daily monthly shiur.

May Hashem grant you success in raising students who study pure Torah with fear of Heaven.

With blessings for good tidings,

## 8339

8339

B"H, 12 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Alter, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 2nd of MarCheshvan, regarding your notes on what was printed in *Kovetz Lubavitch*, Year 5, Issue 1, in the section of *Teshuvos U'Biurim*, concerning what is written in *Tanya*, Chapter 24, regarding the matter of *pikuach nefesh*.

Your letter does not sufficiently clarify whether, by wanting to interpret *pikuach nefesh* as referring to the matter of suffering, you intend to include suffering that leads to death, or if you do not necessarily mean that. In any event, beyond the fact that the very expression *pikuach nefesh* signifies only the preservation or loss of life, this is explicitly proven in several *sugyos* in the *Gemara*. The *binyan av* (foundational principle) for all of them is in *Yoma* 85a, **at both** extremes: that in a case of doubt regarding death, one overrides the Shabbos, even if there is no suffering involved. And in a case of suffering without death, it is not discussed at all in that *sugya*, as it concludes: "Violate one Shabbos for his sake, so that he may observe many Shabbosot." The same applies in other places in the *Gemara*.

2) In that same *kovetz*, in the section *Mahani Milei Me'ali'ata*, regarding what I noted in *Rambam*, *Hilchos De'os*, beginning of Chapter 4—that seemingly it should say "ways of **avodas** Hashem" rather than "ways of Hashem." It seems you wish to interpret my intention as meaning that I am explaining the *Rambam* as referring to the commandment, "And you shall guard yourselves very carefully."

But it is simple that this was not my intention. Rather, I meant to say that these words of the *Rambam* follow the conclusion of Chapter 3, as is also implied by the beginning of the chapter, "Since..."—for he is speaking about the matter explained at the end of Chapter 3: "And he will not be able to **avod** Hashem while he is ill; thus, his sleep is an **avodah** to the Omnipresent, blessed be He, etc." That is to say, that the state of health—meaning physical well-being—is the path through which he can **avod** Hashem. The language of the *Rambam* is not similar to the saying of our Sages, "Cleave to His ways; just as He is merciful, etc.," because that is appropriate to say regarding being "gracious and merciful," but it is not appropriate to say regarding the matter of physical health, as is understood.

With blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding your question on *Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken*, 271:23, concerning the word "the first" (*ha-rishonah*)—Rabbi Naeh has already noted in *Kuntres HaShulchan* that it should be corrected to "the last" (*ha-acharonah*). This is also proven by the fact that the language of *Admur HaZaken* here is the language of the *Rema* in that place.

## 8840

8840

B"H, 12 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Chol HaMoed Sukkos, in which you ask for the reason behind the custom of many among Bnei Yisrael to use an esrog from the land of Calabria.

I am surprised by your question, given that much has already been written on this subject in the Shailos U'Teshuvos, the Poskim, and so on. See Shailos U'Teshuvos Chasam Sofer, Orach Chaim, Siman 207; Shailos U'Teshuvos Bikurei Shlomo, Siman 28; and many others.

Regarding what you mention in your letter—that there are Rabbonim who use esrogim from other places—I am also surprised by this query. There are many matters where communities differ from one another according to the rulings of their respective Gedolim, even though all accept the Torah of Moshe and its mitzvos to the fullest extent (it is understood that we are speaking here of true Gedolim and leaders of Yisrael, not those whose authority is based on money or similar motives). However, in specific halachic details—just as it was in the time of the Mishnah and Gemara with the disputes between Beis Shammai and Beis Hillel—it is possible for such differences to exist in later generations as well. This, of course, does not apply to those laws that have been accepted in the Shulchan Aruch by the entire collective of Yisrael.

I must add that I am surprised more than anything else, upon reading your letter, that you connect your question to the matter of helping Eretz Yisrael, even though it has **no connection** or relevance. An esrog must be taken because that is what Hashem Yisborach commanded, and it must be an esrog that the Torah defines as such. For those Gedolim who have accepted that an *esrog hamurkach* (a grafted esrog) is *pasul* according to Torah law, it makes no difference in which country it grows. The fact that it grows in Eretz Yisrael adds nothing that would fulfill the mitzvah of esrog for those who hold the ruling that an *esrog hamurkach* is *pasul*; it would be a *bracha l'vatalah*. Furthermore, one cannot help a land—especially a land that is called *Eretz HaKodesh*, which literally means that it is a land where all its affairs must be **holy**, and as the Torah expresses it, "a land which Hashem your G-d cares for; the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year"—through such means. The absolute truth is that **only** by walking in the path of Torah and Mitzvos can Yidden be helped and the Geulah brought closer. Just as the Galus came **only** because of our sins, as we say in davening, "And because of our sins...," so too, the Geulah will come through **teshuvah** for those sins and transgressions, as is the **pask** of the Gemara and Poskim in many places. At that time, Hashem Yisborach will send us Mashiach Tzidkeinu, who will gather our exiles and bring us to the true and complete Geulah. Therefore, every Yid who **truly** wants to do what is necessary to bring the Geulah closer and shorten the Galus must first do everything in their power to ensure that the observance of Torah and Mitzvos among Yidden becomes ever greater, and must fight against all things that are contrary to this with all possible means. May Hashem Yisborach help you to do your part in this to the fullest extent.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

#### 8840

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 26, p. 591.

## 8841

B"H, 13 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 5 Cheshvan, in which you write regarding the relations in your home and the influence this has on your situation regarding Torah and mitzvos, which is not as it should be.

Now, while the ways of our Torah—Toras Chaim—are known to be ways of pleasantness and peace, we have simultaneously been commanded, "You shall surely rebuke your neighbor." This means that the ways of pleasantness and peace are the *form* of all matters, all suggestions, and the manner in which one should influence others, but the *content* must be directed toward the instructions of our Torah, Toras Chaim. If this is the case regarding others, then regarding one’s wife, it is all the more so that the command is to conduct oneself in ways of pleasantness and peace. However, this does not permit **at all**, Heaven forbid—as you phrased it in your letter—to travel on Shabbos, G-d forbid, or anything of the sort. For all the commands of our holy Torah stand in their place, as mentioned above, and this is certainly true regarding the matters of Shabbos, which is equal to all the mitzvos.

It is also clear that the expression in your letter about "abandoning" your wife, G-d forbid, is not to be considered at all. Rather, both matters—"Love your neighbor as yourself" and "You shall surely rebuke your neighbor and not bear sin because of him"—were commanded to us together by the Creator of the world and its Guide, who fashions the hearts of all the Jewish people together and knows the best way to influence them. However, since a person is biased toward himself and can tilt the judgment in all matters in which he is interested, you should present the situation to your G-d-fearing friends, and they will instruct you.

Regarding what you wrote at the end of your letter, as to the meaning of the dreams you saw, etc., the statement of our Sages is well known: "All dreams follow the mouth." Therefore, interpret them for good—for the true good, which is Torah and mitzvos, encouragement of spirit, and a directive to go from strength to strength in our Torah and its mitzvos. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 8842

8842

B"H, 13 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Mr. Avraham Moshe, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 5th of Cheshvan, in which you raise the question regarding what is written in Chapter 11 of Iggeres HaTeshuvah by our Alter Rebbe: how is it possible that one returns and sins between the blessing of "Forgive us" (*Selach Lanu*) and "Redeemer of Israel" (*Goel Yisrael*)?

However, you do not explain what compels you to interpret the words of our Alter Rebbe in this way—that the words "returns and sins" refer to that specific time frame. For even though regarding the request for pardon and forgiveness, "He is abundant in forgiveness" (*Rav Lislioach*) is immediate when we ask *Selach Lanu*—as what could delay it? —nevertheless, regarding the Redemption, even though the expression used is "redeemed immediately," it does not mean "immediately" in the same sense as mentioned above. After all, there is a specific order to the Redemption: the coming of Eliyahu HaNavi and several matters that precede and follow it, as explained in many of the teachings of our Sages.

Incidentally, the concept of Redemption immediately following Teshuvah is also the language used by the Rambam in Hilchos Teshuvah, Chapter 7, Halacha 5.

I am certain you are aware of the three daily portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya; in any event, you should maintain them from here on.

With blessing.

## 8445

B"H, 16 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter from Thursday, in which you write of the suggestion that you study as a student in the slaughterhouse, and that the administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Montreal, where you study, has agreed to grant permission for this.

However, you do not mention a primary point in your letter: whether you have already acquired sufficiently important knowledge of our holy Torah. For matters of parnassah, whatever they may be, a person has an inclination to occupy himself with them until seventy years, or by reason of strength, eighty years. This is not the case with the aforementioned, where, due to our many sins and the darkness of the golus, the desire [for Torah study] diminishes from time to time—especially once the proposal of "a millstone around one's neck" arrives. And those who are meticulous in this regard [claim] that as preparation for the "millstone around one's neck," one must neglect Torah study for several years beforehand, even though this is the complete opposite of the law of the Torah (see Hilchos Talmud Torah by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 3, end of section 1).

Therefore, you should present all of the above before the administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Montreal. If they find that you possess the knowledge or the aptitude that makes it appropriate for you to study the craft of shechitah for several hours during the week, and you take upon yourself to set aside ample time for shiurim in both Nigleh and Chassidus, then it is possible to take an interest in the aforementioned proposal.

With blessings,

## 5846

5846

B"H, 16 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos, in which you request a blessing for success in your studies, etc., and mention that although you have the desire, etc., you lack the *cheshek* (enthusiasm), and it feels as though it is being taken away from you, etc.

Now, it is impossible for this *cheshek* to be taken away, *chas v'shalom*, since it is the command of the Creator and Guide of the world that every single Jew must have complete *cheshek* and desire for the fulfillment of everything stated in His holy Torah—and the matter of *talmud Torah* is equivalent to them all. Rather, the aforementioned feeling is also one of the stratagems of the *yetzer hara*, which invents various and strange ploys in order to weaken a person in his *avodah* to his Creator. It does not even shy away from matters of falsehood and deceit. This itself should awaken in a person additional strength to fight against it—a battle through the approach of *da'as* (intellect/resolve), which means not entering into any pilpulim or debate with it at all. Instead, respond with a short phrase: "There is no time for pilpulim, for I am a servant to the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, and I am occupied with fulfilling the command of my Master, the Holy One, Blessed be He." See also the Tanya in many places for the advice given regarding this. May the statement of Chazal, "If you have labored and not found, do not believe," be engraved upon your heart.

With blessings for *talmud Torah* with *hasmadah* and *shekidah*, and for the fulfillment of *mitzvos* with *hiddur*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

8847

Upon this depends the existence of our people, who have endured much yet emerged in peace solely thanks to their adherence to the living G-d and the Torah of life. From this, there is absolute proof that the traditional Torah and mitzvos are the very essence of the life of our people, the Children of Israel, in every place and in every generation, and therein lies the secret of our survival. Fortunate is the person who utilizes all their possibilities and abilities to uphold and disseminate this light of life.

## 8848

8848

By the Grace of G-d
16 Marcheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter from the previous Motzaei Shabbos and Monday, along with the enclosed material.

It is well known what is explained in many places in Chassidus: that from the perspective of the *binah* within the intellect, it is possible to arrive at opposite conclusions regarding a single matter—whether to lean toward *chesed* or *gevurah*. Only a strong *da'as* determines the matter. This is also the case regarding the information about which you write. Following the excerpt from the newspaper you attached to your letter, my own takeaway is the exact opposite of yours. As is evident from your letter, this has caused you a sense of discouragement, regarding how others are competing with them, etc. In my opinion, the conclusion to be drawn from this is that the residents of... recognize the necessity of a Torah education, even if, for the time being, they cannot distinguish between *techeiles* and *kala ilan*, or even between *kala ilan* and something of even lesser value. Consequently, the campaign in this area is now easier.

The second point of the conclusion is how precious time is in matters of education. This is not only from the perspective of the students—for if one day is lost, who knows if the child or their parents will listen to words explaining the education of our holy Torah—but also regarding the teachers and the *askanim*. For now, it is clearly evident that if they had increased their involvement in... even more, they would have captured more and more territory, and the "empty space" would have diminished accordingly. Since one does not cry over the past, it is understood that my intention here concerns the future. This is especially true regarding the competing institution mentioned in the press, which operates only twice a week; this gives them the greatest possible opportunity to spread further and further. After all, everyone admits the fundamental difference: a visit to a school once a week is not comparable to five times a week. This is especially true since the Chabad *anash* have the matter of the camp, the *mivtza* of the past *Chag HaSukkos*, etc. Indeed, even the *farbrengens* of *Yud-Tes Kislev* and *Yud Shevat* should be utilized in the aforementioned direction, just as our *Raboseinu Nesi'einu* explained that even in these, there is a benefit in actual practice. In such *farbrengens*, our *Raboseinu Nesi'einu* spoke regarding the strengthening of the institutions, etc. As I have written many times, since the above is the demand of the hour in..., it is simple that they have been given the strengths and the possibility to fulfill this demand completely.

From this, it is also understood that the complaint that some of the teachers are not so expert in the profession of education, etc.—while it is understood that one must work to correct and improve this—it is obvious that one must not become discouraged. Furthermore, in addition to the fact that surely those on the other side are not ministering angels but rather human beings fashioned from clay, it is also simple that they do not possess the same *mesiras nefesh* and dedication that we do. And furthermore—and this is the main point—they do not have the *hisorerus* of the *ruach* of our holy *Raboseinu Nesi'einu*, and *kal v'chomer*.

In continuation of all the above, I will await good news that you are increasing your efforts even more regarding the upcoming camp, and in a manner that will utilize it also for the days and months that follow—all the more so and *kal v'chomer* compared to last year. The same applies to the celebration of *Yud-Tes Kislev* and its utilization, as well as the days of *Chanukah* in the aforementioned direction. May Hashem bless you with outstanding success in all of this, with proper health and with joy and a glad heart.

With blessings,

## 5849

5849

B"H, 16 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 9th of MarCheshvan, in which you write regarding your strained financial situation and your intention to travel to the United States, apparently as a shadar or in a similar capacity.

I have seen several of those who came here who, unfortunately, were burned by such a move. They traveled here without investigating and inquiring into the conditions involved, and upon arriving, they saw that many of the details were such that a refined person could hardly tolerate them. They were unwilling—and some, even if they were willing, were unable—to humble themselves to such a degree, and I doubt they even earned enough to cover their travel expenses.

It is understood that opinions are not all the same, and possibilities are not all the same, especially since you do not specify in your letter the prospects for earning a living here or the connections you have. I have only come to urge you that you must conduct **detailed** investigation and inquiry and engage in **thorough** deliberation before taking such a step, for several reasons.

Regarding what you wrote—that you do not know how to emerge from your current distress—in the case of many of those who have already traveled here, had they exerted the same intensity of effort—to the point of self-sacrifice and dedication—to improve their situation on the spot, they would not only have earned their travel expenses, but would surely have found various means of livelihood and profit in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, and with more dignity than the matters they are engaged in here.

I am certain you are preparing in good time for the upcoming days of Kislev in general, and in particular for the holidays and special days within it. May it be His will that it be with success in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5850

5850

16 MarCheshvan, 5718

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday, regarding what I said that it would be appropriate for you to engage in agriculture in the village... the point is not desirable in the entire matter, as it appears from your letter that you have no desire whatsoever for the entire aforementioned matter in all its branches. Prolonged work cannot be performed in an orderly fashion if it is based solely on *kabalas ol* (accepting the yoke). This is in accordance with what is explained in many places in *Chassidus*—that the power of *ratzon* (will) and *taanug* (pleasure) are what activate all the faculties in their establishment and expansion. You should consult once more with your friends in Kfar Chabad, and Hashem, who oversees each and every person with *hashgacha pratis* (divine providence), will guide you in the best way for you, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings.

## 8551

8551

B"H, 17 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the end of Tishrei, in which you write that in certain instances you fall into a state of extreme despondency, feeling broken and crushed, and find it difficult to learn, even though you are careful regarding several matters explained in the sefarim in connection with this.

It seems I have already written to you that one of the points to rectify this situation is the matter of *hesech hada'as* (diverting one's attention). It is explained, and understood even by simple logic, that *hesech hada'as* does not mean fighting against the matter, nor even debating it—even to negate it—for that is the **opposite** of the concept of *hesech hada'as*. Its meaning is, quite literally, to divert one's mind entirely from the matter, even from the attempt to fix it or from thinking about how bad the matter is, etc. However, since the mind is always wandering, *hesech hada'as* is only possible by immersing one's thoughts in matters of an entirely different nature—and what is better than matters of Torah? If a little light pushes away much darkness, how much more so does much light, especially when studying the *ma'or shebaTorah* (the light within the Torah), which is the source of light—namely, the *pnimiyus haTorah* (inner dimension of Torah), as is explained in many places. The necessity for *hesech hada'as* is explained in many places and is also based on the well-known responsum of the Tzemach Tzedek (printed in his *Responsa*, *Sha'ar HaMiluim*, section 62).

Regarding what you wrote—that it is difficult for you to participate in Chassidishe farbrengens because you have no "sense" for *nigunim*—this is along the lines of the statement of our Sages: "He who has eaten garlic..." [should eat more garlic, etc.]. Furthermore, your conclusion from the above—that "it has no influence on me at all"—is incorrect, for that is impossible. A person is generally influenced [by his environment], especially during an *eis ratzon* (time of favor), as is known regarding the *petka d'min shemaya* (the note from Heaven) that descends with the magnitude of the influence that a farbrengen generates.

Regarding your question as to whether a person is obligated to sacrifice his own spirituality in order to save the spirituality of another: the statement of Rabbi Akiva is already well-known, "Love your fellow as yourself—a great principle in the Torah." See also the words of our Sages in *Sotah* 21b regarding the "foolish pious one," and several other statements of our Sages that testify to this. The main point here is what is known regarding the interpretation of the verse, "And charity shall exalt a nation"—that one's mind and heart become refined a thousand times over. Certainly, spiritual charity—that which touches the soul—is no less significant than material charity. It is understood that there are boundaries to this: just as one is obligated to involve himself in the welfare of others, a *ben yeshiva* should not cancel all his yeshiva studies to involve himself only in matters of material or spiritual charity. This is similar to the well-known story of our Sages regarding "Is it not enough..." (*Yerushalmi, Pesachim* ch. 3, halacha 7; see also *Moed Katan* 9, end of side a). Rather, as with all matters of our *Toras Chayim* (Torah of life), one must find the middle path, as explained at length by the Rambam at the beginning of *Hilchos De'os*. However, since a person is biased toward himself, you should present the matter and its details to your friends, and they will guide you. May it be His will that in all the above, you will bring good tidings regarding your own personal growth and your influence upon others.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

 See also *Iggeres HaKodesh*, section 16.
 *Torah Or*, at the beginning.

## 8454

8454

B"H, 18 MarCheshvan, 5718

Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Tzvi, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

Following the recent interval, I received your letter of the 10th of MarCheshvan, in which you write about your activities over the past weeks. It is understood that it is **most** appropriate to organize matters in such a way that... other anash, and even those who may become anash in the future, will be drawn into the sphere of Chabad activities. For the entire land of Brazil lies before them; my intent is that it is **incumbent** upon them to spread the wellsprings, not only within their own limited four cubits, but in circles that expand further and further until they reach throughout the entire country. This is in accordance with the letter of the Rebbe Rashab (printed in the introduction to *Kuntres U'Maayan*), that in this time, the manner of *birurim* is without order, in the sense that one should not wait to first conquer one's own palace. That is to say, even those who are still lacking within their own limited four cubits must also work in the palaces of others. Since this is the demand of the hour, surely the ability has been granted to fulfill this demand.

Special attention is required, and it is worth the effort and great exertion, regarding the summer camp, etc. For as experience has shown in every place where this has been done in the United States, and subsequently in Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established—and Canada: when the matter is organized properly, and the results are subsequently utilized properly, it is possible to acquire great assets through a summer camp. This means, quite literally, to draw in (*arayntziehen*) a large number of youth, and through them, a large number of parents and homes in Yisrael. Furthermore, many of them will reach the level of *tofeach al menat lehatpiach*—being moistened in order to moisten others, and influencing them as well.

I believe I have already written regarding a structured plan well in advance concerning the utilization of the days of Kislev, and especially the upcoming 19th of Kislev, the Rosh Hashanah for Chassidus, to promote the ways of Chassidus in the most effective manner possible. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 8555

8555

B.H., 18 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, learned, and energetic, etc.,
Rabbi Chananya Yom Tov Lipa, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday regarding the mikveh in Albany.

I spoke about this matter the day before yesterday with the esteemed Rabbi Aharon, may he live, a shochet and bodek, to urge them to improve the situation as much as possible. Once again, they promised that they would place the question on the agenda and discuss it again. May it be the will of Hashem that the matter finally reaches a practical conclusion, and in the manner required for matters of mikvaos—that it be with all possible hiddur. Surely, when it nears fruition, they will be in touch with you.

The matter of the construction—and as is apparent from your letter, the lack of communication regarding it—is understandably distressing and even alarming. After all, there is a deficiency in such a place and in such a matter. Even if we were to say that it was due to circumstances beyond their control (*ones*), we do not say "it is as if it were done." It is understood that my intention is not, G-d forbid, to offer mere moral rebuke; it is only necessary to draw **special** attention to the fact that since you have become aware of the aforementioned, it is certainly an instruction that it is in the hands of all those who know of it to do what they can to rectify and improve the situation. From this, it is understood that with appropriate contemplation, the ways and means for this will be found. The above is based on the adage of the Baal Shem Tov that we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that everything a Jewish person sees or hears contains an instruction for him in his avodah to his Creator, and this is well understood.

Regarding what you wrote about comments for the recent and future parts of your books: what can I do when my time is not my own due to the multitude of preoccupations? Even as I wrote some time ago, I have not despaired, G-d forbid, that I will eventually be able to go through them—at least in haste. But to the extent that there will be room for some comments, even if only in haste*, I do not know for now when such a situation will arise. To Hashem belongs the salvation.

May the Almighty grant you success in strengthening purity and spreading it wherever your hand can reach. May it be His will that the inwardness of this also be revealed, which is the matter of the inwardness of the Torah, as is hinted at by the words of our Sages, of blessed memory: **Da’as** (knowledge)** is the Order of Taharos (Purity). This is explained even further in the Rambam at the end of Hilchos Mikvaos, how the matter of purity in its inwardness is Da’as—to know Hashem, "as the waters cover the sea." Although in its fullness this will be with the coming and revelation of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, a semblance of this and a beginning of this must exist during the days of the galus. This is the matter brought also in Sifrei Mussar, that the Geulah began at the very moment of the Churban. It is also hinted at in the well-known story in Eichah Rabbah, that the cow lowed the first time for the Churban, and immediately a second time for the birth of the righteous redeemer. In the words of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya: "The ultimate perfection of the days of Mashiach and the resurrection of the dead depends on our deeds and our avodah throughout the duration of the galus" (see there, Chapter 37).

With respect and blessing.

## 8860

B"H, 20 Marcheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter of 14 Marcheshvan, in which you write that you have begun the study schedules at the yeshiva, but you do not feel any inner vitality, etc.

It is a well-known statement of our Sages: "If one says, 'I have labored and not found,' do not believe him." It is understood that the question is not about whether one feels a sense of vitality—that is not the "labor" being spoken of. Furthermore, labor is primarily a matter of *kabbalas ol* (accepting the yoke), and not necessarily dependent on the presence of inner vitality.

The conclusion from the above is that you should study with *hasmadah* (diligence) and *shekidah* (application) as required during the yeshiva study sessions, and also during the hours between the sessions, without searching and demanding that there must first be vitality and only then will the study begin. For the order is the exact opposite. When you conduct yourself in the manner described, my hope is that the promise of our Sages will be fulfilled in you: "You have labored and you have found."

I trust that you know and keep the three daily study portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—that are appropriate for every soul, and that you also influence your fellow students to do the same.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 8861

B"H, 20 Marcheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

I have received news that has caused me distress: that at times you are not careful regarding the consumption of mashke, to the point of exceeding the measure such that it is evident to all that you are intoxicated, and at times this even occurs in public during a farbrengen or the like.

The words of our holy Rebbes, of blessed memory, are already well-known **against** such matters—that is, against the drinking of mashke in general, except during a time of simcha, and even then, in a limited measure, and for each person in a manner appropriate to him. This means that if there is any concern or fear that one might become intoxicated even from a small amount of mashke, then even that amount of drinking is forbidden. And if they demanded this even regarding matters not done in public, how much more so during a farbrengen in public... Our Rebbes have demanded this for decades and across several generations, and in these days of ours, this demand is even more forceful and severe. For on one hand, the obligation is placed upon each and every one to "spread the wellsprings outward," and therefore one must be extremely careful regarding any matter that could cause damage in this regard. On the other hand, precisely in these "footsteps of Moshiach," the darkness of the galus—and consequently the materiality of the body—is intensified. Therefore, the aforementioned matter (not only the measure of becoming intoxicated, but the drinking in general) is liable to strengthen the materiality and thereby lead to several negative and forbidden outcomes.

My hope is strong that immediately upon receiving this letter of mine, you will restrict yourself in the aforementioned matter as much as is necessary. And in a place of doubt—the rule is to be stringent. I will await good news from you regarding all that has been said, and as soon as possible.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**
