## 8863

B"H, 21 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 MarCheshvan, regarding your question concerning the blessing for Hallel, which is printed differently in *Hayom Yom* than in the *Siddur*—the rule in such matters is known: we follow the later version. It is understood and obvious that at the time *Hayom Yom* was compiled, they knew of and considered what was written in the *Siddur*. There is no reason to be surprised that the practice is actually different, as there are many such instances, and there are certainly various reasons for such changes. Our Sages of blessed memory have already informed us regarding such variations (*Bava Basra* 166b) that it must be specifically in action; see there. Regarding this specific matter, see *Shaar HaKollel* there, and the beginning of *Piskei HaSiddur* by Rabbi Naeh.

Regarding what you wrote about a *tikkun* for shaming a fellow, after the friend has forgiven: it is true that this matter involves both *bein adam l’chavero* (between man and his fellow) and *bein adam l’Makom* (between man and Hashem), and for this, a *tikkun* is required. Like all *tikkunim*, it must be in the specific area where the damage occurred—that is, to increase in *kavod habrios* (respect for people) in general, and respect for friends in particular. Since in the vast majority of cases the cause of shaming a fellow is connected to the trait of anger or pride, in this area as well, one must conduct oneself with the opposite extreme, as is understood from what is written in the Rambam, *Hilchos Deios*, Chapter 2.

Regarding what you wrote about studying *Tanya* with a friend who does not understand the *peshat* (literal meaning): it is astonishing that you would write such a thing, as it is certainly entirely out of place and inappropriate. This is true even though the words of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, navgam, zya*, are known regarding the difficulty of understanding the depth and essence of the words of *Tanya*. Together with this, it is brought in the aforementioned *reshima* (record) that even the simplest person understands something there; see the *reshima* there (printed at the end of *Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya*). This is all the more so when the person in question is a *yungerman* who has been in *yeshivah* for several years, and the merit of the public assists him in spreading the *maayanos* (wellsprings) until they reach even further outward. However, even in this, the *avodah* must be with joy and a good heart, and then one will succeed.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

Regarding what was written in *Tosafos, s.v. Rabbanan* (*Gittin* 3, bottom of side b and there), see the commentaries there, *Maharam Schiff* and others.

***

8863

*In Hayom Yom:* 1 Teves.

*Regarding what was written in Tosafos, s.v. Rabbanan:* That witnesses of delivery are required for a *shaliach* for *holachah* (transporting a get), even though witnesses are not required for the appointment of a *shaliach* for *kabbalah* (receiving a get).

## 8864

B"H, 22 Menachem Av, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 18 Cheshvan, in which you outline the main points of what you have experienced until now, noting that there was a change from one extreme to the other, but that you have since set your heart to return to the path of our Torah—the Torah of life—and its mitzvos, and have become integrated into this path.

May it be Hashem’s will that you not be discouraged by the fact that it sometimes seems to you that there are certain difficulties in walking this path. For in the vast majority of cases, this is nothing more than an illusion. Even in the small number of instances where there is some reality to the concealment, it is less and fewer in obstacles than any other path. This is because it is impossible for a Jewish person to succeed on a path that is not the path of Hashem’s Torah (which includes, as well, psychological satisfaction), since that is the opposite of his true nature. Even if, at times, the bribe of **fleeting** pleasure blinds the eyes of the wise—making it seem as though one is satisfied—its end is bitter as wormwood, as is explained in many places. Furthermore, we see this tangibly. Fortunate is he who now walks in the path of Torah and mitzvos. May it be His will that you go from strength to strength and from level to level, and may it be good for you, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 8866

B"H, 22 Marcheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 17th of Marcheshvan, along with the enclosure, at an auspicious time I will read the *pan* at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be His will that you bring good tidings among us.

Thank you very much for the precious gift—a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—in addition to the matter regarding the well-known saying of our Sages, "A matter that is worn is precious."

Regarding what you wrote about your son, *sheyichyeh*: Beyond the fact that every individual has a specific *mitzvah* in which they must be especially careful—and Divine Providence shows what that is—in his case, this is education within the framework of *Torah U’Melachah*. Another, primary point here is that "measure for measure" is the way of the Holy One, Blessed be He; increasing one’s efforts in the education of the children of the Omnipresent adds to the success of the education of the educator’s own children. This is simple to understand. This "addition" in education refers not only to the students currently in the classrooms, but also to the effort to increase their numbers, to bring in more students even to the classes of others, etc., and not as you wrote in one of your previous letters, that this does not apply to you.

Regarding what you wrote about the appointment for collecting *Maamad*: In general, this is a matter that *Anash* in that location must decide, since it depends on local details. However, in the vast majority of cases, the person whom they wish to appoint is biased toward himself, and consequently, the matter sometimes leans to the right or to the left. Therefore, he should not rely on his own judgment, but rather lean on the opinion of *Anash* in his vicinity and act according to their instruction.

Regarding what you wrote in your discussion about whether one must be careful not to speak about, etc.: You do not add what the benefit is in speaking about even the lowest of the low. As for the example you bring that there was someone who acted in such a way, the rule in *piskei dinim* is already known: if the reason for a matter is not known, one should not issue a ruling. This is especially true regarding a matter where the negative side is clear and certain, and it would require deep contemplation to find a positive side that could not be reached in any other way except through this crooked path. Furthermore, in our generation and in your environment, the mission of these days is the spreading of the *maayanos chutzah* (the wellsprings outward), and such speech not only fails to assist, but on the contrary, it hinders—and hinders forcefully.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

The report from the 27th of Nissan through the 10th of Elul was received in due time.

***

**Appointment for collecting Maamad:** Whether to accept the appointment.

**Not to speak about:** Opponents.

## 8867

8867

B"H, 22 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 17th of MarCheshvan and the one preceding it, it is understood that I am not at all pleased with what is implied by your letter—that due to a lack of necessary attention to your business affairs, there is some defect in your merchandise. Aside from the issue of *bal tashchis* (wanton destruction), which is an injunction from the Ribono shel Olam just like all other *mitzvos*, there is the additional point that for those who set aside significant sums from their profits for *tzedakah*, the aforementioned negligence also affects the matter of *tzedakah*.

It is indeed a true and accurate precision of the teachings of Chassidus that "when you eat the labor of your hands, you are fortunate and it is good for you"—referring to the labor of your hands, not the labor of your mind. The power of deep *hisbonenus* should be directed toward spiritual matters, not toward the aforementioned [business concerns]. However, it is simple that an action in business matters—regarding which it is said, "and Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do"—cannot be performed with closed eyes and with the palm of your hand alone. It requires, at the very least, practical intellect; that is, the action must be performed in a manner that is appropriate for the goal of the action.

My hope is that, at the very least, from now on you will follow the path of Torah in this as well—meaning that in matters of livelihood, you will act in a way that you will succeed even according to the natural order. Then, the Ribono shel Olam grants His blessing even above the natural order. May it be His will that you bring good tidings regarding the above.

With blessings for good news in the aforementioned.

## 8868

8868

B"H, 24 Marcheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos: Based on the well-known teaching of our Sages that whatever is done for someone’s benefit is for long, good days and years, may it be Hashem’s will that you continue to share good news in general, and specifically regarding the matter of arranging the papers. Although it is also understood that one must make an effort in this through natural means, as it is written, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you do"—meaning that when one acts through natural means, the Ribono shel Olam bestows His blessing even beyond the natural way.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the cutting of hair in the front for married women: In general, there are several approaches to this and various customs even among the Chareidim themselves. As our Sages said regarding such matters, "Both are completely righteous," meaning that I am referring to customs whose purpose is greater yiras shamayim. Therefore, one should clarify what is the best approach in this specific case and conduct oneself accordingly.

May it be Hashem’s will that, in accordance with the words of our Sages, "If they are worthy, the Shechinah dwells between them," your home will be built upon the foundations of Torah and its inwardness—which is the Torah of Chassidus and its guidance. It is obvious that any influence they have on their surroundings in this regard, by each of them, adds to the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam and His success in what they need for this very matter, for the attribute of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is "measure for measure," only many times over.

With blessings for good news in all that was mentioned.

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 18, p. 446, and completed based on the secretariat’s copy.

## 8869

B"H, 22 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Dovid Meir, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your *pidyon nefesh* dated 23 MarCheshvan. G-d willing, when I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, at the end of this week, I will mention you and your wife, may she live, for whatever you need, in accordance with the content of your letter.

Yom Kippur Katan is approaching, and Rosh Chodesh Kislev is the month of redemption—the redemption of all those who have merited to taste of the teachings of Chassidus and its matters. As is well known, the saying of our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*, is that 19 Kislev is the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus. One of the ways of Chassidus is "you shall surely help him" (*azov ta'azov imo*)—as interpreted by the Baal Shem Tov, to help [the soul] with the body, and not through self-affliction and fasting.

Regarding *Rosh Chodesh*: Our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, and his son, the Mitteler Rebbe, explained the precision of the term *Rosh* (head) rather than *techilah* (beginning). Just as the head contains the vitality of all the limbs of the body, so too does Rosh Chodesh contain within it all the days of the month. From this, it is understood that on the Shabbos of **mevorchim**, these matters begin, and on Yom Kippur Katan—which is the preparation—the preparation begins for that upon which the *hemshech* (drawing down of light) depends. As our Sages of blessed memory have taught, even an opening the size of the eye of a needle opens the "entrance to the hall" (*pischu shel ulam*)—specifically the *ulam* (hall), which, in addition to its greatness, is always open, for it has no doors to be closed, *chas v'shalom*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and in the phrasing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: "A healthy winter."

## 8870

B"H, 22 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Saadya, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 18th of MarCheshvan, in which you write that during your travels you conveyed regards to Anash, may they live, in the places you passed through, and also mentioned some of the matters that were discussed. May it be the will of Hashem that these words have their intended effect. For if it is said regarding the entire Torah that "study is great because it leads to action," and all the more so regarding one who learns with the intent not to act [which is better than not learning at all], then this is certainly true regarding the teachings of Chassidus and its matters. As is well known, the demand of our holy Rebbeim, our leaders, is that **from every** aspect of these teachings, there must be actual action.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of teaching French or Arabic, etc. — it is to be hoped that the matter will be extended (*fartziehen*), and "a court ruling nullifies a previous ruling." In any case, it is understood that they must coordinate among themselves—I refer to all the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok institutions currently in your country—so that not only will there be no contradiction between the words of one and those of another, but rather, there will be added assistance. It is understood that in such a case, it is said that "it ascends with him and does not descend, G-d forbid"—meaning:

That even if in some place there must be a concession out of necessity, one must continue (*fartziehen*) the matter in the other places from week to week and from month to month, etc., and specifically in a diplomatic manner.

...With blessings for success in your holy avodah, the inner point of which—like the inner point of our entire generation—is the spreading of the wellsprings outward. For this is the generation of the footsteps of Moshiach, which is also the generation of the beginning of the Geulah, speedily in our days through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

You surely conveyed (or will convey) my regards specifically to the esteemed Rabbi, etc., etc., Ovadia, may he live, along with my thanks for his help and assistance in the matters of Oholei Yosef Yitzchok in Morocco in general, and regarding his book in particular.

## 8771

B"H, 25 Marcheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, man of action and integrity, involved in communal affairs,
R' Avraham Chanoch, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters: I have received the copy of the *mahaduras* of the *sichos* from Tishrei 5717, material for the upcoming publication (the *Omer* booklet, which I believe has already been approved), and a segment from the *kuntres*. It is understood that the month of Tishrei and the days preceding and following it do not allow the time to review the aforementioned copy of the *sichos*, nor even the material for the publication. At the earliest opportunity, this will be done, and any necessary corrections will be sent to you.

Regarding your question concerning what was explained: that during the *Ketziras HaOmer* the publicity was less than during *Simchas Beis HaShoeivah* because the former is the period of the *avodah* of *tzaddikim*, whereas the month of Tishrei is the *avodah* of *baalei teshuvah*. You ask: what is the practical difference, given that the publicity is done to refute the position of the *Tzedukim*?

Now, there was indeed publicity during the *Ketziras HaOmer*—which is why they performed and recited the entire procedure three times, etc. (see *Menachos* 65a). However, the difference lies in the joy of those engaged in it. It is understood that the joy of a king’s son who has returned from captivity is greater than the joy of a king’s son who was never in captivity (if there is even a concept of such joy there at all). For a constant *taanug* is not a *taanug*. Furthermore, even regarding the *Tzedukim*—they have a smaller and much slighter foothold within the *daled amos* of *Tzedukim* who never sinned, than they do within the *daled amos* of *baalei teshuvah*.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of *bechirah* (free choice) among the nations of the world: based on what is explained in many places in *Chassidus*, including *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Emor* (35b), and the *maamar* "Kavod Malchuso" of 5700 from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *n'e*: there is no such thing as free choice—in the absolute sense—except in the *Atzmus* and *Mahus* (Essence) which has no cause or reason, *chas v'shalom*, etc. Consequently, this also applies to the Jewish people, who are like a son, coming from the *Mahus* and *Atzmus* of the father.

The matter of reward and punishment among the nations of the world should be explained in two ways: 
1) Reward and punishment in their case is merely a term borrowed from the reward and punishment of Israel. In truth, however, it is a matter of cause and effect, similar to a small child who puts his finger into boiling water (and see the difficulty raised by the *Rambam*, *Hilchos Teshuvah*, end of chapter 5). 
2) That in those matters regarding which they were commanded—i.e., the *mitzvos* of the *Bnei Noach*—the command itself provides the possibility for both paths. That is to say, it elevates them above their nature and places them in a state where there is room for *bechirah*. This is understood from the statement of the *Mishnah* that "the reward of a *mitzvah* is the *mitzvah* itself." For the very fact that a great sage commands a simple person in some matter connects him with the great sage, and any connection brings about a common point between those who are connected, and *kal v'chomer*.

Certainly, as is your custom, and especially after your last letter, you have prepared and are sending to the *kuntres* material for printing for the days of the month of Kislev, and especially for 19 Kislev, the *Rosh Hashanah* for the teachings of *Chassidus* and the ways of *Chassidus*.

With blessings for success in all matters and for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned.

## 8872

B"H, 26 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Shmuel Elazar, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your two letters, in which you write in detail about your activities in the most exalted matter of *hafatza maayanos chutzah* (spreading the wellsprings outward), in addition to your activities in the *mechina* (preparatory division) of Yeshiva Toras Emes.

May it be His will that you continue to increase in holiness in all of this. As the well-known expression goes, "we ascend in matters of holiness," and since there are levels even within this, may it be to the greatest possible extent. As is known from the *derashos* (expositions) of our Sages—it is not merely the act itself, but that the act must be performed as it ought to be. The very demand itself proves that the ability to fulfill it has been granted, and the matter depends solely on one's *ratzon* (will).

We are approaching the month of Kislev, the month of *geulah* (redemption)—the redemption of all those who have merited to taste of the *Toras HaChassidus* and its matters. As is known from the saying of our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im* of holiness, that the 19th of Kislev is the *Rosh Hashanah* for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus. Our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, and his son, the Mitteler Rebbe, explained the precision of the term *Rosh* (head) rather than *techilah* (beginning): just as the head contains the vitality of all the limbs of the body, so too does *Rosh Hashanah* contain within it all the days of the year. The days preceding it are days of preparation, upon which the *hemshechos* (drawings down of light) depend. As our Sages have taught, even an opening the size of the eye of a needle opens the "opening of the hall"—the *hall* specifically, which, in addition to its greatness, is always open, for it has no doors to be closed.

With blessing for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding what you wrote about the custom to interrupt a *chassan* or the like during the recitation of a *chiddush* or *maamar* (it has been said that this custom began so as not to embarrass those who do not have one)—the response of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding such matters is known: that after he finishes saying the entire *maamar*, he should begin it again, and then they may interrupt him.

Regarding what you wrote about the time for *chinuch* (education)—see the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of the Alter Rebbe (1:6), where he rules from age 15 to 24!

## 8873

8873

B"H, 26 Mar-Cheshvan, 5718

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 24th of Mar-Cheshvan, in which you write of the differences of opinion among the doctors you have consulted.

It is not entirely clear from your letter whether the doctors’ opinions differ because they examined you at different times—in which case it is possible that your condition has changed in the interim—or if even those who saw you at the same time do not agree in their assessment. In any event, you should first try wearing a belt [support] to see its effect; it is possible that this will suffice and no further treatment will be necessary.

On this occasion, I must remark upon the wonder and astonishment regarding the several instances during your time here where matters were not in order, and consequently, were not desirable: at one point you traveled here without the permission of the administration of Tomchei Temimim of [city name]; at another time you did not appear for an examination at all, neither in Nigleh nor in Nistar (which is conducted by the local Tomchei Temimim administration **at my request**); and at another time you took the examination and it did not go well, etc. It is understood that **all** of the above is not at all desirable, especially in our generation, and particularly regarding a student of Tomchei Temimim, whose purpose is to be a "lamp to illuminate"—that is, to influence others. This influence is primarily achieved through conducting oneself as is fitting. From the positive you can infer the negative, and this is well understood.

May it be Hashem’s will that from here on out, everything will be corrected in all details, and in the manner explained in the letter of our Alter Rebbe, in Iggeres HaTeshuvah, end of Chapter 9: "He who was accustomed to read one page should read two pages," etc.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 5874

B”H, 26 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, a man of many accomplishments,
R’ Shlomo, may he live, known as Dr. Ehrman,

Surely there is room to utilize it or its content to explain the significance of this day to circles that, for whatever reason, have not been aware of it until now. And if in all times it was required to utilize every form of outreach to strengthen and disseminate Yiddishkeit, how much more so in our generation—an orphaned generation—where, at the same time, there is a palpable sense of great disappointment in the various idols of idealism prevalent in the street. This disappointment has led to the realization that one must find the true goal and purpose in life—the life of a Yid. And whoever is the first to show those who are searching the true path that leads to this goal—which is Torah and mitzvos—is effectively sustaining a soul of Yisrael. Very often, the sustaining of this one soul sustains an entire household, and sometimes even the circle in which he is found. The merit of the many assists all those who strive in this with success in their efforts.

With a blessing for success in your work to raise the banner of the Yisrael of old, which surely also brings an increase in the blessings of Hashem in your personal matters, as promised by the Giver of the Torah in His Torah.

With respect, and awaiting good tidings,

## 5875

B"H, 26 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of November 17, in which you write regarding your studies and the difficulties you are facing concerning Shabbos, as there are those who demand that you attend school on this day as well.

It would be appropriate for you to turn to the Rav of your community and ask him to do everything in his power, together with the community activists, regarding this matter. He should explain to the school administration the great importance of keeping Shabbos, and what our Sages of blessed memory said, that Shabbos is equivalent to all the mitzvos, and so on and so forth.

Even if you succeed in arranging the Shabbos matter in the best possible way, it is understood and simple that even then, it would be far better for you to study at the seminary in Tangier. I believe that secular subjects are also taught there, so you will be able to continue those studies while you are there. You should explain to your parents—may they live and be well—that Hashem, blessed and exalted be He, oversees each and every person with Hashgacha Pratis, and He sustains and provides for everyone with His goodness, grace, kindness, and mercy. By allowing you to study at the aforementioned seminary, where holy studies are taught, and by doing so promptly, it is clear that all of this will assist you in your future life. Therefore, it is surprising that they wish to delay this for any length of time. May it be His will that this effort also succeeds.

I am sure that you make a practice of saying some prayer every day in the morning and also at night before going to sleep. May Hashem, blessed be He, grant you success and bring you good tidings regarding all of the above.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 8796

8796

B"H, 26 Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn

To the administration of the Nusach Ari Anshei Lubavitch Synagogue,
Dorchester, led by Mr. Menashe Vinakur, President,
And its members,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the custom for a shaliach tzibbur to daven Mincha and Maariv while wearing a tallis:

1) As is well known, the Lubavitch customs, which have been practiced for generations, dictate that even on Rosh Hashanah for Maariv or Mincha—and certainly on Shabbos and Yom Tov for Mincha and Maariv—the davening of the shaliach tzibbur should be without a tallis. The reasons for this are explained in the holy seforim, and some express themselves in even stronger terms regarding this. It is also known that there are other synagogues that conduct themselves differently, just as there are various differences in customs between Chassidim and non-Chassidim, and among Chassidim in general, and between Chassidei Chabad Nusach Ari and other prayer customs, etc.

2) According to the name of your shul, "Nusach Ari Anshei Lubavitch," it is evident that you have always conducted yourselves according to the customs of Lubavitch and the Ari. Added to this is the instruction of Chazal: "Do not alter the custom of your ancestors."

3) It goes without saying that machlokes, Heaven forbid, must not exist at all among Yidden, and certainly not in a holy place, even when it concerns upholding a custom such as the one mentioned above, which has been practiced for many generations. However, I hope that when you explain to the mispallelim the basis for the shaliach tzibbur not davening with a tallis at Mincha and Maariv—that this is how it has been handed down by the Rebbes from generation to generation—I believe that no one will want to go against this mesorah.

4) The above applies only to Mincha and Maariv, but **not** to Selichos. For Selichos, it is the custom everywhere that the shaliach tzibbur recites Selichos at the amud while wearing a tallis.

May the Ribono shel Olam help that, in accordance with the instruction of the Mishnah, "Hashem did not find a vessel that holds blessing for Yisrael other than peace," there should be peace in your synagogue in an ever-increasing measure. As we say in davening, "Talmidei chachamim increase peace in the world," and surely everyone will do what depends on them in this direction. May the Ribono shel Olam accept the tefillos of everyone and fulfill the requests that one asks of Him, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

With blessings for good tidings, and that your synagogue should **grow** regarding tefillah, regarding shiurei limud Torah, and regarding maaseh hatzedakah.

With the blessing of all the best.

## 8776

8776

B"H, 26 Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Shmuel Pinchas, may he live:

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to the administration of the Nusach Ari Anshei Lubavitch shul.

If it is not possible, through ways of pleasantness and peace, to maintain our custom as explained in *Hayom Yom* (19 Kislev 5703)—that the *shaliach tzibbur* does not wrap himself in a *tallis* for *Mincha*—you will surely be able to arrange for the *shaliach tzibbur* to wear the *tallis* over his shoulders rather than over his head. In any case, considering that you are dealing with the *gabbaim* and people who are older than you, you should ask for their forgiveness in a way that leaves them satisfied. Especially since, in this manner, you will accomplish much more than you would through sharpness or the like.

## 8879

B"H, 27 Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 23rd of Mar-Cheshvan.

May it be Hashem’s will that just as you bring good news that several of the undesirable neighbors have vacated their apartments and have been replaced by good tenants, so too may you bring good news regarding the other matters about which you write.

Regarding what you write—that about a year ago you purchased a house in a different neighborhood, and you are constantly having troubles, etc.:

It very often happens in such cases that one is not careful about separating maaser—at the very least, maaser for tzedakah—from the profits of that house. If this is the case in your situation as well—meaning that until now you have not separated maaser (and the statement of our Sages is well known, that one should not be overly precise with tzedakah—and therefore one should add at least a little more than the maaser)—it is understood that first and foremost this must be rectified. It would be best to make up for what you lacked in maaser for tzedakah during the past months. Since the Ribono shel Olam says regarding tzedakah, "Test Me now with this," and the exposition of our Sages is well known, "Give maaser so that you will become wealthy," this promise will surely be fulfilled in your case as well.

It is my hope that, at the very least, from now on you will observe the three well-known daily study portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, which we heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that they are appropriate for every soul and are a segulah for many matters. Your wife, may she live and be well, should observe the custom of kosher daughters of Israel to set aside tzedakah before lighting the candles every Erev Shabbos Kodesh and Erev Yom Tov.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 8880

B”H, 27 Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 23 Cheshvan, in which you write regarding the difficulties you have encountered concerning shidduchim, and that you have seen in many seforim and masechtos that one must seek a wife from a distinguished family, etc., and also one who is kosher, etc.

It is well known that our Sages stated that all daughters of Yisrael are beautiful, and it is understood that the true beauty referred to by our Sages is beauty in spirituality. It is also known that our Sages stated (Yevamos 63a) that a chassan should descend a step to choose a wife. While it is obvious that all the qualities you enumerate in your letter are worth seeking, it is also understood that not every search is the same; a search must be conducted with an "ayin yafah" (a generous eye). Based on what you have written, my advice is that you entrust the matter of the search to the administration of the Tomchei Temimim where you study. It is obvious that a student of Beis Rivkah is most appropriate, since her very presence in that institution is proof of her integrity and yiras shamayim. Furthermore, she comes there with the agreement of her parents, which is also proof of the parents' yiras shamayim. We see tangibly that when one does not become overly particular about secondary matters—and certainly when one does not become particular about the secondary of the secondary—but rather demands matters of yiras shamayim, tzniyus, and the like, then Hashem grants success, so that together with the aforementioned essential qualities, one also finds the secondary ones. It is understood and simple that if in every matter one must do everything in one’s human power to increase Siyatta Dishmaya, then all the more so in an essential matter such as a shidduch, regarding which it is said, "And from Hashem comes an intelligent wife." The actions to increase Siyatta Dishmaya are to increase one’s involvement in Torah and mitzvos—the study of Nigleh and the study of Chassidus—and to fulfill the mitzvos with hiddur, and to influence one’s friends in such matters.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 8881

B"H, 27 Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the pious and G-d-fearing man, who occupies himself with the needs of the community, a man of many accomplishments, etc.,
R' Yehoshua, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 13 Mar-Cheshvan, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

In it, you share the news of your grandson Dovid’s entry into the yoke of *mitzvos* this past Shemini Atzeres, as well as the upcoming entry of your grandson Nach into the yoke of *mitzvos* on the holy Shabbos of *Parshas Vayishlach*. The wondrous words of our Sages regarding Bar Mitzvah are already well-known. They state:

"On that day, it is an obligation upon the *tzaddik* to make a celebration of the heart, like the day he ascends to the *chuppah*. And because of that merit, the Holy One, blessed be He, will awaken them in the future and proclaim before them with joy, 'Go forth and see, O daughters of Tzion'" (*Zohar Chadash, Bereishis 15d*; see also *ibid. 10c*, and *Zohar Vol. II, 98a*). Regarding the day of Bar Mitzvah, it is said—referencing the statement of King David—that Hashem says to him, "You are My son; this day have I begotten you" (and this matter is explained in the *Reshimot* of the Tzemach Tzedek on *Tehillim* there).

May it be the will of Hashem that for long, good years, you see true *nachas*—specifically *Chassidishe nachas*—from all your descendants, may they live. May this further grant you, in your honor, renewed strength to work for the strengthening of Yiddishkeit and its dissemination—true Yiddishkeit, without compromise, the Yiddishkeit of our ancestors.

Especially as we are approaching the month of Kislev, the month of miracles and redemption, the victory of "Your Torah and the statutes of Your will." As the precision of this phrasing is explained: "Your Torah" specifically, not merely wisdom in general, and "the statutes of Your will"—"I have issued a decree, I have enacted a statute, and you have no permission to question it."

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 8882

B"H, 27 MarCheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
R' Eliezer, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 9th of MarCheshvan and the one preceding it.

It is my prayer that, in accordance with the content of your letter, there will be an improvement—a tangible shift—in the matters about which you write, and in all matters of Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established. And since the matter is similar, it should be in the manner of what is written in Iggeres HaKodesh by our Alter Rebbe, at the end of Chapter 9: "He who is accustomed to reading one page should read two pages," etc.

This is especially relevant as we are approaching the month of Kislev, the month of redemption and victory—a redemption for all those who have merited to taste of the teachings of Chassidus and its matters. As is known, the saying of our holy Rebbes is that 19 Kislev is the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus. Regarding the term "Rosh Chodesh," our Alter Rebbe and his son, the Mitteler Rebbe, explained the precision of the word *Rosh* (head), rather than *techilah* (beginning); for the head contains the vitality of all the limbs of the body. Likewise, Rosh Chodesh contains within it the days of the month. From this, it is understood that on Shabbos Mevarchim we begin these matters, and today, Erev Rosh Chodesh—which is Yom Kippur Katan—is the preparation for Rosh Chodesh, and the preparation begins for that upon which the *hemshech* (drawing down of light) depends. As our Sages of blessed memory have stated, even an opening the size of the eye of a needle opens the entrance to the *Ulam* (the Hall)—specifically the *Ulam*, which, in addition to its greatness, is always open, for it has no doors to be closed, Heaven forbid.

With blessings for good tidings in good health,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8883

B"H, 28 Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Cheshvan and the one preceding it.

1) What are the rules for determining one’s path in life when there are several options?

You have asked this question before, and I believe I answered then that, as with all matters of a person’s life, here too one must find guidance in the source of instruction for all Bnei Yisrael: our Torah, which is *Toras Chaim* (a Torah of life), the word *Torah* itself stemming from the word *hora'ah* (instruction). Since *talmud Torah* is a constant, unceasing obligation, so too is the concept that "study leads to action" a constant matter—meaning that all the actions of every moment of a Jewish person’s life must come as a result of that study, and this is well understood.

2) Since Hashem knows everything that will happen in advance, how is the concept of *bechirah* (free choice) possible?

This has already been written, printed, and spoken about **extensively** by the greatest of our people, from the earliest authorities to the very latest. The simplest explanation, as with many such matters, is through a living analogy: consider a person who knows the future and sees that after some time, a certain individual will perform a certain act. Even so, the choice of the one performing the act remains entirely free from the knowledge of the observer.

3) Regarding *tefillah* and *hisbonenus*, you write that you do not know how to engage in *hisbonenus*.

*Hisbonenus* in general, and before *tefillah* in particular, is a fundamental matter. "One should not stand to pray except with a heavy head" (seriousness of mind)—see the commentaries there. As for how and in what to engage in *hisbonenus*, this is explained in many places, among them in the *Tanya Kadisha*, the *Kuntres HaTefillah* of the Rebbe (Rashab) *n.e.*, and many others.

You should certainly participate in the *farbrengens* of *anash*, and especially the *farbrengen* of 19 Kislev. May it be the will that its impression be felt throughout the entire year.

With blessings.

## 8884

8884

By the Grace of G-d
28 Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal affairs, R' Yitzchok [Ginzburg]
Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 6th, 10th, and 12th of Cheshvan, and the one following them. It gave me pleasure to read that you have approached your holy work in the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch in the Holy Land (may it be rebuilt speedily) with added energy and renewed vitality. It is my firm hope that, contrary to the norm in worldly matters—where vitality and energy diminish over time—in this endeavor, which is one of the foundations of the mitzvah of the holy Torah, "And you shall teach them to your children" (these students), it will be as the Torah commands: "increasing in holiness." This is a matter that depends solely on one's will, as we have discussed regarding the concept of *mozhes da niye khotches* (you can, but you do not wish to).

It is simple, as I have written and also stated orally, that all regular expenses of the Reshet will be paid in full; this is merely a matter of timing. On the other hand, regarding the phrasing in your letter about "not restricting," experience has shown that this immediately leads to staggering expenses, in such a way that after some time, no one can explain how the sum became so large, as we have discussed orally.

It is understood that I stand by my position that the separation of boys and girls is mandatory, and it is impossible to compromise on this. However, regarding the combining of classes, this should be evaluated in each school according to its specific conditions and in accordance with the assessment of how the relevant offices will react to the merging of these classes.

Regarding your question in your letter, where you say that I mentioned the need to concentrate a staff of expert teachers and ask how this is possible, given that Anash have not been involved in this until now:

Expertise does not necessarily require many years of work. If there is talent for this and a strong will to specialize in the field of education for its own sake, it is to be hoped that within a few months one will become an expert. During these months, one is not obligated to be a principal or a teacher in difficult classes or the like; they can be employed in classes where the work is easier, and so on.

You do not mention in your letter my request to convey regards to those of Anash who are in the army. I hope this is merely an omission in your letter, and that you will do so upon your return to the Holy Land, so that they feel they are not forgotten, G-d forbid. Surely R' Y.L. Zalmanov and the others whose work is within the framework of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad—who are most closely connected with them—will help and assist you in arranging this in the most effective manner.

Since one of the primary tasks of a school principal is the negotiation with various offices, and the impression one makes there, it is understood that in a case of doubt, one should prioritize the person known for his good relations and the positive impression he makes.

Regarding what you wrote about opening a teachers' seminary, you do not write any plan for this, only that the matter is connected with great difficulties.

One must inquire about the seminaries that already exist and have been operating for some time, whose methods are therefore known, and choose from them those that are most suitable. Certainly, through negotiations with them well in advance, it will be possible to demand several additional improvements to refine them.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and primarily regarding this—that he has thrown himself into his holy work to develop all the affairs of the Reshet and sees the success of the Almighty in this.

#### ***8884***

**R' Yitzchok [Ginzburg]:** Tel Aviv. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 10, p. 218, and in the references noted there. Below, Vol. 6, p. 44.

## 885

885

B"H, 28 Mar-Cheshvan, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Committee of Kfar Chabad,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

...It is a simple matter that the farbrengen of Kfar Chabad for 19 Kislev is a matter for anash in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily, and it is obvious that it concerns the entire village and **touches upon** all its affairs. This is especially true since among the participants are several people of influence in various offices, and through the acquaintance made at the farbrengen, their activities are enhanced. Therefore, not only is this farbrengen necessary in a public manner, but a pre-planned program is also necessary...

From this, it is also understood that even if there are seemingly extra expenses for the aforementioned farbrengen, it is reasonable to say that they are worthwhile for the sake of the expected benefit — both material, and even more so, spiritual. (It goes without saying that "extra" does not mean without limit, but rather extra in a measured way, according to reason and good judgment.) Due to the great value of this farbrengen, I will, bezras Hashem, encourage anash to participate in it through a special collection to cover one-third of the expenses.

Regarding what was written concerning the meal: in general, it is appropriate that it consist primarily of *mezonos*, except that more than a *minyan* should wash their hands for a meal so that they can recite *Birkas Hamazon* with a *minyan*. Similarly, for the residents of the village, if they wash their hands, there is no concern. This is not the case for guests, who do not always remain until the end of the farbrengen, and there are several details regarding *Birkas Hamazon*, etc., in addition to the difficulty of washing hands properly. Therefore, for such a farbrengen, it is worthwhile to have *mezonos*, fruits, and, of course, *mashkeh*, and this is clear. It is our custom here that close to the conclusion of the farbrengen, it is announced that all those who ate the required amount should certainly recite the blessing they are obligated in, etc., and I believe it is brought in the *sefarim* that the Rema and the great leaders of Yisrael were accustomed to announce such things...

On this occasion, I will raise another point, about which I have been prompted from several sides, and it also has a connection to the above: namely, that there are no benches near the station in the village, nor along the path from the station to the village, for the rest of the guests who arrive or visitors. They also write that there are no trees or sources of shade there, even though this is sorely lacking during the hot summer days. Along with this, they write that the expense for this is very minimal, but during the nine years that the village has existed, there has been no interest in such matters...

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and in this regard, for outstanding success in your holy work, and for the establishment and development of Kfar Chabad in all directions.

## 8,880

B"H, 1 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write about the difficulties you are facing and the demands being made of you, etc.

It is simple that wherever one finds oneself, one must study Torah with consistency and diligence. It is also understood that the *yetzer hara* fights against this with various strange tactics and various strange explanations. It is not at all impressed if one travels from one country to another, for even in the new country, it invents reasons and excuses suited to the conditions there. Ignoring its enticements does not depend on the validity of its reasons, but rather on the will of the person—whether he truly desires to fight the *yetzer hara* or whether he does not.

It is understood that all of the above applies to your situation as well. The reasons you write regarding why it is impossible to study in your current location are among the tactics of the *yetzer hara*, which, in your present situation, has found a way to entice you using this specific formulation. If, *chas v'shalom*, you listen to it, or at the very least spend your time debating and arguing with it, this is proof that even if you were to go to a new place, it would be the same as mentioned above.

The statement of the Mishnah, "Go into exile to a place of Torah," is correct, but it is clear that this does not apply to your case, as your claim is not that you lack comfort or that you are not in a place of Torah.

If you will listen to my opinion, you will see in the demands being made of you regarding consistency and diligence a hint from *Hashgacha Elyona*—that you have been given the ability to fulfill these demands, and the matter depends solely on your will, since you possess the ability.

May it be His will that you contemplate the above deeply, and that you increase your study of Torah, both in *nigleh* and in *Chassidus*, as much as is required, and may Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 8887

B"H, 2 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs,
R' Menachem Zev, may he live, Halevi

Greetings and blessings!

...It is surprising that it seems the collection of Chabad customs was compiled with such great difficulty, etc.

Regarding what you wrote about those who were present at the farbrengen — I have already said many times, to many of anash, that the entire concept of a farbrengen is one of plowing and sowing. It is obvious that afterward there must be absorption and harvesting, and usually, between the sowing and the harvesting, there are many twists and turns. Therefore, it is incumbent upon the friends who are present at the farbrengen to do something about this, especially regarding those who are present at a farbrengen for the first time, or those whom one must protect from undesirable influence.

And lastly, regarding your announcement of the entry of your son, Avraham Yechiel, may he live, into cheder — may it be G-d’s will that it be in a good and auspicious hour. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "Let the pure come and engage in the pure." May the prophecy be fulfilled in his days and in our days, and in the language of the Sefardim, "The Kohen shall see in Tzion." This is especially relevant to him in particular, as written in the writings of the Arizal, that then the Leviim will be Kohanim (Likutei Torah of the Arizal — cited in Tanya, Chapter 50).

With blessings for good tidings.

## 8888

B"H, 2 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs,
R' Efraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Mar-Cheshvan, and primarily regarding the conclusion of your letter concerning the explanation in the Maamar entitled *Be'etzem HaYom HaZeh*, 5741, regarding the matter of *tzava* (army/service), etc.

You should also examine the *Hemshech* of *Basi LeGani*, section 11 and onwards, where my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on 10 Shevat 5710, provides three interpretations of *tzava* and their implications.

It is puzzling that you wish to interpret this at a low level, in the depths below, at a time when it is possible to interpret it in the heights above. Even according to the language in your letter, "their end is embedded in their beginning," the *Hemshech* of this Maamar continues, "and their beginning is in their end"—meaning that one must search in the end, and when one searches with *yegiah* (toil), one eventually finds the beginning, the heights above.

It could be said that this is along the lines of *kavua* (fixed) and *me'ushar* (enriched), which is the beginning of *avodah* and also its ultimate purpose, and this is the concept of *tzava*.

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to someone regarding this, which is relevant to the aforementioned matter.

With blessings.

## 8890

B"H, 2 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and distinguished man of many accomplishments,
R' Yisrael Yitzchak Halevi, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’vrachah!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 24 MarCheshvan. Although the state of the relevant funds here is difficult, and at the same time the needs of your people are many and increasing from time to time, since you have turned to me in this matter—and for the honor of Torah—I am enclosing a check. Since this fund was established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, surely you will fulfill through this the teaching of our Torah: "Whoever takes... from Iyov is blessed."

And since I have come to the subject of *hachnasas kallah* (providing for a bride) from the fund of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who sacrificed his life for the dissemination of Yiddishkeit in general, and the dissemination of the teachings of Chassidus and its matters in particular, one should expound upon the well-known ruling: "One moves the dead before the bride, and this [the bride] before the King of Yisrael" (Kesuvos 62a), which contains a deep allusion.

For, in general, the matters of Torah and mitzvos—which are the purpose of man’s creation, as the Mishnah states, "I was created to serve my Maker"—are comprised of two lines: *sur meira* (turning away from evil) and *aseh tov* (doing good). The matter of "evil" is, in the language of the verse, "death and evil," while the matter of "good" is, as mentioned above, making the things of the world a vessel and instrument for Elokus, a "bride" that receives the indwelling of the Shechinah, just as our Sages said, "Who is a worthy woman? One who does the will of her husband."

The instruction is given that when two paths are before a person—the avodah of *sur meira* and the avodah of *aseh tov*—one moves the "dead" (the negative) before the "bride" (the positive). For even a little light pushes away much darkness. This is brought as a halachic ruling that a positive commandment overrides a negative commandment (and note also the *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* of our Alter Rebbe, beginning of Chapter 1: "That regarding the fulfillment of a positive commandment which overrides a negative commandment, this is because through fulfilling a positive commandment, one draws down light and abundance into the upper worlds from the illumination of the Ohr Ein Sof, and also upon one's own neshamah elokis").

And in this same vein, this is also one of the fundamental differences between the teachings of Chassidus and the teachings of Mussar: the former emphasizes and is primarily concerned with *aseh tov*, while the latter emphasizes and strives to explain the matters of *sur meira*.

However, in both matters—both *sur meira* and *aseh tov*—the ultimate intent is as it is said, "And Hashem commanded us to do... to fear Hashem our G-d." This is also the beginning and foundation of avodah, as the Mishnah states, "Why does the Shema precede [the paragraph of] 'And it shall be if you listen'...? So that one may accept upon himself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven first." And similarly in the Mechilta regarding the Ten Commandments: "Accept My Kingship, and afterwards accept My decrees." In this way, the avodah is aligned with its purpose and is performed with *hiddur* (beauty/excellence). Therefore, the main thing—and the one that is moved before the other—is before the King of Yisrael, who is the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He.

With blessings.

## 8,892

B"H, 3 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote in general about whether to think about "lofty matters" for your son, may he live: In this and similar matters, as well as with others, one should not confuse the son or daughter until there is a specific proposal that is practically relevant. For what benefit is there in them knowing that you are thinking about it? It is impossible that it will not cause at least some confusion, and afterwards, there is no detailed proposal, especially since it is connected in any case to the question of the arrangement.

Regarding what you wrote as the reason concerning the wedding of your son, may he live—that you wish to delay it because you are pressed by debts, etc., even though the in-laws say that from their side there is no obstacle, and you do not know what to do about this:

This is a matter of wonder and astonishment. For it is known from our Sages, and explained in *Likutei Torah* at the end of *Parshas Berachah*, that a person is given *parnassah* for the sake of his wife. If so, it is possible that the reason you are pressed is precisely because he has not yet married. The argument that "the clothes are not suitable," etc., is understandable as to how ridiculous it is regarding such a fundamental matter as marriage, which affects one's entire life. Even if it were clear that there were those who would mock, the beginning of all four parts of the *Shulchan Aruch* is that one should not be ashamed, etc. Especially since this is an imagined concern; there is no mockery regarding this, even in the United States, where—more than anywhere else in the world—money occupies a significant place. Many of *anash* here, and even those who were not educated in a Chassidic home or as *temimim*, marry with the intention of afterwards learning in a *kollel* for several years with the agreement of both the *chassan* and the *kallah*, even while living a life of hardship. How much more so when we are speaking of the son of *temimim*, etc. It is a wonder that even regarding such a simple matter one needs to ask across the sea, and when one answers, it is doubtful whether the words will be of use and whether they will have their intended effect. It is even more of a wonder that, apparently, for the **parents**, these reasons carry no less weight than they do for the son. Is it possible to recount such a thing? And regarding what you wrote—that you ask "why the rush"—the wonderment of this argument is understandable, and even more so than the above, for "a person knows his own soul," as is known from the statements of our Sages regarding this, and *kal v'chomer*.

May it be the will of Hashem that you bring good news regarding all that has been mentioned, and that the news be in the spirit of Chassidus.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8,893

B"H, 3 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, a man of noble character, a scion of noble ancestors, etc., R' Sh.Z. Shlita,

Shalom u'Bracha!

I was informed that you are undergoing medical examinations, and although I do not have the details, my hope is that everything is peaceful and in order.

Moving from one subject to another: It is a known fact that among our people, the treasured nation, and especially in the Lashon HaKodesh, even matters that seemingly pertain to the body are connected to the soul. As is well known, our Sages of blessed memory used the expression "he examined his soul" (*badak nafsho*). And is there anything more physical than eating? Yet even regarding this, the expression is used: "A righteous man eats to satisfy his soul" (*tzaddik ochel l'sova nafsho*).

It is surely unnecessary for me to write to you that I have a strong hope that this year, too, in accordance with your good path and custom, you will visit Kfar Chabad on the bright day of 19 Kislev, which is, in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, "the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus." The explanation of the Alter Rebbe regarding the precise use of the word "Rosh" (head) rather than "techilah" (beginning) is well known: the head contains the vitality of all the limbs. So it is regarding the cycle of the year and the month, and in this manner, the Rosh Hashanah of Chassidus draws down Chassidic vitality into all the days of the year. May it be the will of Hashem that the *hisorerus* of this Rosh Hashanah in Kfar Chabad will draw down an awakening of warmth and light throughout the entire year.

I requested of the guests who were here from Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) and have returned, to convey to you my regards orally, and it is a certainty that a *shaliach* performs his mission.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding the aforementioned.

With respect and blessing, and with many thanks for your most important gift, the manuscript of the Siddur of the Arizal which reached me, and the commentary of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe on this (Likutei Torah, beginning of Parshas Shemini).

#### ***8,893***

## 8894

B"H, 3 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the avreich engaged in his holy work,
David Tzvi, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 27th of MarCheshvan,

It gave me pleasure to read that your borders have expanded with students, and among them are those who are outstanding not only in Torah but also in yirah and character traits. It is certainly superfluous to emphasize the necessity of this matter, and it is therefore understood that every effort and exertion in this regard is worthwhile.

Regarding what you wrote about a guide for this, it is appropriate to say that the search should be conducted by the activists, who are familiar with the yeshiva students and those who have recently left the yeshiva and are capable of the aforementioned work.

You do not mention in your letter whether you have a curriculum of the halachos required for daily life. Perhaps this is merely an omission in your writing; in any case, the necessity of this study is understood and self-evident, especially in our times. In previous generations, daily conduct was known to everyone from their parents' home, and even from the street, and certainly from the beis medrash, to which they would go two or three times a day. This is not the case in this orphaned generation, where all of this must be provided by the educational institution in which the boy or girl is found, starting from aleph-beis and the halachos required for the simplest matters. If only they would institute this study even in the large yeshivos, for unfortunately, the knowledge of the laws of Orach Chaim—which are the most common and frequent—is extremely weak, and "an error in study is considered intentional".

As we have entered the month of Kislev, the month of redemption and victory, and especially the bright day of 19 Kislev, the Rosh Hashanah of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidim, may it be the will of Hashem that you engage in spreading the wellsprings wherever your hand can reach, and may Hashem grant you success in all of the above with good tidings.

With blessing.

Enclosed is the Birkas HaShanah that was returned from Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, as I did not know your address.

***

8894
David Tzvi: Merzbach, Be'er Sheva. Additional letters to him: Vol. 14, 4859; Vol. 15, 5448.

## 8,896

B"H, 4 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the avreich Yosef, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Rosh Chodesh Kislev, regarding your question about participating in a party, etc.

Since this depends on several details (the nature of the party and the nature of the participation), you should present the matter to a *moreh hora'ah* in your vicinity, and he will instruct you.

Surely you are aware of what is brought in the *sefarim* regarding the ways in which children can bring *nachas ruach* to the souls of their parents. Among the essentials in this regard is involvement in the dissemination of Torah and its *mitzvos* (and one may also note the *Zohar*, Vol. 3, end of *Parshas Bechukosai*). You surely know how much your father, of blessed memory, *masar nefesh* for the matters of Chassidus in general, and for its dissemination in particular. Therefore, my hope is that you are doing everything possible to exert yourself in this, both generally and specifically during the year of mourning. Your merit—and also your responsibility—in this is many times greater, since your position is such that you can influence a specific circle, and especially your class. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

You surely know of the three daily *shiurim*—in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—which we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which are appropriate for every soul and are a *segulah* for many matters. In any event, you should keep them from now on.

With blessings.

## 8,897

B"H, 4 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in the work of Heaven with communal needs, etc., Moreinu HaRav Yehuda Zev, may he live, HaLevi.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Monday.

At a time of favor, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, each according to their specific needs, as befits the content of your letter.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the request of so-and-so, may he live, regarding the addition of a name: since this is his desire, his request should be fulfilled. May it be the will of Hashem that this change brings about a positive effect, in a good, revealed, and manifest way, both materially and spiritually.

You will surely also hold a farbrengen in your camp on the bright day of 19 Kislev, the upcoming day of redemption and victory of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch. May it be the will of Hashem that the words of inspiration and Torah spoken there achieve their effect, in accordance with the statement of our Sages that "great is study, for it leads to action." This is in addition to the fact that speech itself is considered an action—at the very least, a minor action through the movement of the lips (see Chiddushei HaRashba, Shevuos 21a). This is especially true when the subject matter concerns those of whom it is written, "And your people are all righteous," and our Sages have said, "The righteous are like their Creator." The speech of the Holy One, blessed be He, is considered an action, and does not even require the movement of the lips; a slight sign is sufficient (see Rif, Sanhedrin, end of chapter 7). This is particularly true when the speech subsequently leads to action, which is analogous to the prohibition of *machmer* (driving an animal with a voice), where it is considered an action, and a sound without an articulated letter is also sufficient (see Tosafos and Shittah Mekubetzes, Bava Metzia 90b; Responsa Noda B'Yehuda, Second Edition, Orach Chaim, sec. 76. See also Tanya, beginning of chapter 32; Likutei Torah, Shir HaShirim, discourse beginning *Mayim Rabim* [54d]).

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above, and with regards to all the participants, may they live, in the aforementioned farbrengen.

***

**8,897**

**Moreinu HaRav Yehuda Zev:** Segal, Manchester. Additional letters to him appear above, Vol. 12, p. 266, and in the references noted there.

**See Chiddushei HaRashba:** See also below, letter 6,012.

## 8897*

B"H, 4 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After a long interruption, I was pleased to receive your letter of 2 Kislev, in which you write of the improvement in your material situation and also of the shiurim you have in Torah—which, unfortunately, are not yet to the fullest extent that they should be, though you hope to rectify this.

However, it is explained at length in many sefarim that the matter of Talmud Torah cannot be "made up" in the future. Since every day, no matter how much one learns, it is only sufficient for that day itself, there is consequently no spare moment with which one could compensate for the deficiency of the past. Furthermore, the interpretation of our Sages, which Rashi brings on the verse "If you walk in My statutes" (*Vayikra 26:3*)—that you should be **toiling** in Torah, etc., and "I will give your rains in their time," etc.—is well known. From this, it is clearly understood that there is no place to say, "When my parnassah improves, I will set a fixed shiur for Torah." On the contrary, the improvement of parnassah can come and be hastened precisely through shiurim in Torah. The fact that your parnassah is not yet as it should be is all the more reason to increase in Torah and mitzvos. And even if **the** study might contain an element of *lo lishmah*, it is well known what our Sages said: "A person should always engage in Torah... for from *lo lishmah* one comes to *lishmah*."

Regarding what you write—that you only have a chavrusa once a week—I hope that with effort, a solution can be found for this as well. Until then, you must at least learn in solitude, and "there is nothing that can stand before the will."

In connection with the approach of the bright day, the Chag HaGeulah of Yud-Tes Kislev, I have enclosed a booklet regarding the significance of the festival of Yud-Tes Kislev. You will surely share its content with all those with whom you come in contact.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 8898

8898

By the Grace of Hashem, 4 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...You write regarding your travel to America, and ask about traveling on a Jewish ship, which is also underway on Shabbos.

As explained in detail in several of my letters regarding this matter, based on how ships are operated in our time, there is no doubt that traveling on such a ship—a Jewish ship that is moving on Shabbos—is a definite prohibition of *chilul Shabbos*. Furthermore, since many people are traveling on it, this constitutes *chilul Shabbos b'farhesya* (public desecration of the Shabbos). This is the ruling even if the ship departs at the beginning of the week.

It is certainly unnecessary to emphasize the greatness of *shmiras Shabbos* and the severity of *chilul Shabbos* in general, and *chilul Shabbos b'farhesya* in particular. I would like to add that, unfortunately, there are those who seek to justify this *chilul Shabbos b'farhesya* by traveling on such ships, arguing that by doing so, Jews—the owners of the ships—will profit, and especially since the owners are from Eretz Yisrael, this will bring profit to Eretz Yisrael.

Incidentally, this is the same argument used by those who demand that all factories in Eretz Yisrael should operate on Shabbos, and that the fields should be worked on Shabbos, because through Shabbos the income of Eretz Yisrael will be increased, and this income will help the Jews there. And this would be true to an even greater extent than the *chilul Shabbos* of the ships, for the income would be far, far greater.

In all this, they forget that the Ribono shel Olam has warned in His holy Torah that from business conducted through *chilul Shabbos*, not only can no benefit come to Eretz Yisrael, but, according to the statement of our Sages (Shabbos 119b), "Jerusalem was destroyed only because they desecrated the Shabbos therein." Those who wish to help Eretz Yisrael through money derived from *chilul Shabbos* are like one who tries to extinguish a fire with kerosene or gasoline, *rachmana litzlan*.

Great is the darkness of *galus* and the confusion of minds, that there are those who call themselves "lovers of Israel," even though the Creator of the world and its Guide states that they are harming Eretz Yisrael. Meanwhile, those who hold fast to our Torah, *Toras Chaim*—which is the only thing that sustains, gives life, and holiness to Eretz Yisrael—are maligned: "Why do they not want the factories to operate on Shabbos? Why do they not want the fields to be worked on Shabbos? And why do they not want the ships of Jewish owners to desecrate the Shabbos *b'farhesya* before the eyes of all the nations?"

If under all circumstances a Jew must fulfill Torah and *mitzvos* to the fullest extent, this is even more necessary when one is in need of a special blessing from Hashem. Therefore, I am certain that regarding your health, about which you write, the fact that your travel will be conducted in a manner of *shmiras Shabbos* according to *halacha*—and not, *chas v'shalom*, through *chilul Shabbos b'farhesya*, *rachmana litzlan*—will serve as a merit for you. Since Shabbos is equivalent to **all** the *mitzvos*, this merit will assist you toward a speedy improvement in your health, for a near and complete recovery.

With blessings for good tidings,

## 8900

B"H, 5 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Mordechai Sorkis, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter acknowledging receipt of my letter from this year. May Hashem fulfill in their entirety all the blessings that our fellow Jews extend to one another.

Regarding what you write—that you do not know what merit you have that I should remember you—on the contrary, it would be a wonder if I did not remember you. You are the head of the place where many Jewish boys and girls are located, *kein yirbu*, each of whom is an entire world. Divine Providence has granted me the merit of being able to do something regarding their education, with your assistance regarding the buildings, support, and the like. Indeed, all the hundreds of children who have been educated until now, and those currently being educated in this school, bring you to mind—not only regarding themselves, but also regarding all those who assist in their education in the spirit of our ancestors. It is my hope that your efforts and assistance will be in a manner of "increasing and continuing," so that through this, not only will any lack of remembrance be ruled out, but on the contrary, the closeness of our relationship will grow in general, and regarding the school in particular. Since you have been privileged with influence in your surroundings, and according to the well-known statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that there is nothing in creation that is in vain, my hope is strong, and I am confident, that you will utilize your influence to its fullest in the aforementioned direction. My warm thanks are given in advance, in addition to the fact that the matter itself expresses its own gratitude.

I trust that, following your good custom from last year and the years prior, you will also visit Kfar Chabad this year on the auspicious day of the upcoming 19th of Kislev—days of *hisorerus* and remembrance of the victory of Chassidus, and the motto that love of a fellow Jew, love of Torah, and love of Hashem are all one.

With respect and blessing,

## 8901

B"H, 6 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Avraham Zalman, may he live and be well,

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter of 3 Kislev with the good news regarding the establishment of a regular shiur in the study of Chassidus: May it be His will that you not only succeed in this, but that you also increase your study. We have the assurance of our Sages that "great is study, for it leads to action," and consequently, it leads to an increase in following the paths and customs of the teachings of Chassidus. There is nothing that can stand before willpower and firm resolve.

These days are especially conducive to this—the 10th and 19th of Kislev, the days in between, and the days of Chanukah, even more so than other days of the year. For on the 10th and 19th of Kislev was the redemption of the Alter Rebbe and his son and successor, the Mitteler Rebbe; this redemption below was proof of the additional strength granted from Above for the dissemination of this Torah, as is understood. Furthermore, the matter of the days of Chanukah: the victory was not merely against opposition to Torah and mitzvos in general, but rather—as is precise in the language established in the prayers of Yisrael—"to remove them from the laws of Your will." That is to say, one performs a mitzvah because it is the will of the Creator (and it makes no difference whether one understands it with his intellect or not). And [the Greeks sought] "to make them forget Your Torah" specifically; for they did not mind the study of Torah in general, as it is a wondrous wisdom, as it is written, "for it is your wisdom and your understanding in the eyes of the nations." Rather, they did not want the study to be according to the holiness of the Torah and the inwardness of the Torah—"Your Torah" specifically. See also the discussion at length regarding this in the Bach to Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, siman 47, s.v. "U'mah she'katav d'amar R' Yehuda," that it is a mitzvah to publicize them, in general and in particular, among those who sit in the tents of Torah and study it.

Although you do not mention your wife, may she live, it is my hope that she is also engaged in matters of disseminating Yiddishkeit.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 8812

B"H, 6 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, R' Betzalel, Shochet u'Bodek, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After a very long interval, your letter from Rosh Chodesh Kislev was received, along with the *pidyon nefesh*, which will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be His will that you bring us good tidings.
