And [the goal is] to do this in accordance with the precise phrasing: "spreading the wellsprings outward"—*spreading* specifically, *wellsprings* specifically, and *outward* specifically, as explained, at least briefly, elsewhere. There is nothing that can stand before the will, and experience from previous years has shown that the more detailed and clarified the plan is in advance, the greater the room for success.

It is altogether surprising that it seems the *anash* in Melbourne are not interested at all in the Jewish people in other parts of Australia. It is understood that this surprise is even greater regarding those who are called "candles to illuminate." For those who called them by this name are certainly correct; however, it is incumbent upon the candles to bring this from potential into actual. When they do not do so, it is a betrayal of their mission, *chas v'shalom*. There are many settlements in the country that are certainly no further away than the definition of "outward," and if so, the obligation of "spreading the wellsprings" applies to them. Furthermore, this [inaction] delays the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu, and the sitting of each person under his vine and his fig tree, even if the vine and fig tree are in a spiritual sense (see *Likutei Torah* for the three *parshios* of *Bereishis* 23b: *pnei nifla'ah*, *birur levushim*).

And this does not replace, in any way, shape, or form, his obligation regarding the aforementioned spreading.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 8903

## 8505

B"H, 6 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal needs, R' A. Friedman, shlita,

Shalom u'Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Shabbos, and thank you for the good news regarding Anash there. At an auspicious time, I will mention them at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, zy"a, who will surely arouse Heavenly mercy for this, among the rest of the Jewish people.

Thank you for what you wrote regarding the Zohar with the annotations of my father, zlal"h.

Regarding what you wrote about the portrait of the Gaon R' Moshe Chefetz, it seems to me that it was printed in books long ago, and perhaps that is what you are referring to.

As for the reasoning you write—that some say that for a prayer for a sick person, the essential name is the one given at the cradle—it is a great wonder how one can say this. It is the opposite of the laws and statements of our Sages regarding the changing of a name for a sick person, which is replete throughout the Gemara and Poskim. Surely it is not for nothing that the law was ruled that the [original] name is uprooted, to the extent that a Get would be invalid according to Torah law—*atmah*! Furthermore: in the case of a sick person, the change of name alters the Heavenly decree—and in the prayer for him, one would mention the name upon which the decree was originally issued!

You will surely participate in the farbrengen of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, the Rosh Hashanah of Chassidus, and may it be His will that its impression be evident throughout all the days of the coming year.

With blessings for good news.

## 8806

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal needs,
R' Avraham Chanoch, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of the 2nd and 3rd of Kislev, in which you also write as a representative of the meeting of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad regarding the proposal to conduct a widespread campaign for the recitation of Tehillim as divided by the days of the month.

While the greatness of this matter requires no length or explanation—as is also understood from the letters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on this subject—on the other hand, this is not the specific mission of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad. That is to say, their primary avodah is *hafatzas hamaayanos*—I refer to the study of the teachings of Chassidus and living according to its guidance. Although the aforementioned [Tehillim campaign] is one of the *takanos* and forms of guidance, there is reason to fear that through engaging in this campaign, there will be a significant lack in their avodah regarding other primary matters. Furthermore, such a campaign has no limit... Therefore, in my opinion, they must gird themselves with all strength to solidify all those activities they have already begun, and in addition to them, to assist the Chabad institutions in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, in whatever capacity depends on them. For the time being, they should not think about new activities on a broad scale, unless there are matters that are currently pressing and the time demands it.

It is understood and simple that all of the above concerns a specialized effort to implement this *takanah*. However, it is obvious that at every opportunity, one should mention and arouse others regarding this *takanah*, as well as regarding the daily *shiur* of Chumash and Tanya.

I was pleased with the proposal you wrote regarding a gathering of youth in Kfar Chabad. It is my hope that the preparations will be made according to a plan, and all the more so, it goes without saying that the gathering itself should be conducted according to a detailed plan prepared in advance, and with the necessary energy. This is especially true after the experience of the previous youth gathering, where you saw the deficiencies caused by the lack of a detailed plan and the lack of coordination among those active in it, and the wise will understand.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

P.S.
Since this gathering is almost the first attempt of its kind, I will, G-d willing, encourage Anash to participate in this through a special collection to cover one-third of the expenses.

## 9807

B"H, 8 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent worker in the work of Heaven,
R' Dovid Avrohom, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

After a very long hiatus, your letter of 27 Cheshvan was received, and I was pleased to read therein a summary of your activities during the past month of Tishrei.

Since, according to your letter, you meet from time to time with Mr. Zerubavel, may he live—who, as you surely know, possesses the power of influence within a certain fairly broad circle—you should utilize **every** meeting for words of *hiso'rerus*. Since the activities of the aforementioned are in an undesirable direction, it is primarily because he has become accustomed to it, and not because he is **currently** contemplating and has arrived at a decision that this is how one must act. Therefore, if he is awakened from time to time, incessantly, regarding the magnitude of the damage and destruction he causes thereby—instead of utilizing his talents to increase goodness in the world in general, and especially regarding *Bnei Yisrael*—then, ultimately, these words will have their effect, for the truth must prevail, even if at times the process is prolonged.

It is understood that in this matter, and others like it, the greatest obstacle for the aforementioned will be, according to what is discussed at the beginning of **all** four parts of *Shulchan Aruch*, "Do not be ashamed before those who mock." It is understood the uproar that will be created within those circles if the aforementioned contemplates his approach until now, and upon arriving at an opposing decision, publishes it without embellishment or pretense. But according to what is heard, he has not been so impressed by the opinion of the majority in his activities until now. And if this is the case regarding matters of destruction, how much more so must he utilize his courage, in a much greater measure of goodness, and say: "The things I have said before you until now were a mistake on my part." And according to what is stated—if regarding the side of destruction they said, "Do not believe in yourself," how much more so regarding a change for the better.

May it be His will that he also not be ashamed, and that he speak of all that has been said, *aliba d'emes* (according to the truth). For we have already been promised that words which emerge from the heart enter the heart. It is understood that he has the authority to mention in a conversation that he is doing this based on what I have written to him, if in his opinion there will be some benefit in the essence of the matter.

And then he also has the authority to add that surely, for some time now, doubts have arisen within the aforementioned, but he strives to silence them himself, and as soon as they fall into his mind, he pushes them away—as is the nature of people, who are afraid to examine the correctness of their way of life once more, for this requires special courage of heart. But precisely because the aforementioned has influence over many, meaning that a rectification in himself will be multiplied many times over in those he influences, he must not retreat and must not fear conducting an accounting of his soul once more, and yet again.

And as per the instruction of *Chazal*, that although one who injures himself is exempt—at least in the hands of man—one who injures others, etc. And as a sign and a wonder to his aforementioned relative, that the time has come for a critique once more of his approach in the past, he will have the dream that is close to your conversation with him.

Regarding what you wrote about their residence in *Kfar Chabad* and the drawbacks therein, the contradiction is understood when these words appear in the letter in which you write about the visits of your relatives to you, and the results thereof. And if, as the well-known adage brought many times in the *sichos* of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the *Admur*, states: that a *neshamah* descends below for seventy or eighty years even just to do one good deed for a Jew, whether in spiritual or physical matters, how much more so is their residence in *Kfar Chabad*, where "Hashem commanded the blessing," which is in any case a lofty matter, and especially when one *mitzvah* leads to another, and matters such as the aforementioned occur.

Regarding what you wrote about the housing—one should have found out what type of candidates they are. And surely, if only the appropriate type, they will be among the candidates...

## 9808

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Tzvi, may he live.

Shalom u'Bracha!

In response to your letter of 2 Kislev, it is surprising that you again make no mention of printing matters of Toras HaChassidus and the environment of Chassidus in the newspapers read by the Bnei Yisrael in your country. This is especially so, as I recall that some years ago you wrote that you had spoken and befriended the editor of a newspaper published there; the benefit of such an endeavor surely requires no explanation or elaboration.

I hope, even though you do not write about this, that regarding your mention of the preparations for 19 Kislev, you are preparing a **detailed** plan on how to utilize this day for the dissemination of the wellsprings (*hafatzas hamaayanos*), in a manner that its impression will be evident throughout the weeks and months that follow. Since it is called the Rosh Hashanah for Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, surely there is the precision here of "a head (*rosh*) and not a beginning (*techilah*)," just as the head contains the vitality of the limbs, as is explained in many places. And there is nothing that can stand before the will, for the ability to do so has been granted.

With blessings for good tidings and regards to those participating in the work of *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*.

## 8509

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, R' Eliezer, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

After a very long interval, I received your letter of 5 Kislev, with good tidings that you have seen good fruit from your labor in the field of pure, holy education—that the students continue in the tradition of their fathers even after completing their education at the institution where you serve.

May it be Hashem’s will that this success will awaken in you additional strengths—that is to say, not only to activate the revealed powers of the soul, but also to draw and extract from the wellspring of hidden powers, in order to add courage, and what is even more relevant, vitality and light to your activities in the aforementioned field. For if in all matters success depends on the measure of vitality and light within the action, how much more so in matters connected to the younger generation, which yearns and thirsts for a word that is alive, warm, and saturated with an internal light that breaks forth and illuminates everything around it.

In connection with the above, I was particularly pleased to read in your letter, at its conclusion, that you recognize the benefit of delivering Chassidic sichos to your students. I am sending you, under separate cover, the Kehot Publication Society catalog, in which you will see what has been published here in various areas, so that you may choose what is appropriate for the character and level of knowledge of the students. Since time is a loss that cannot be recovered, it is worthwhile that even before receiving the catalog, you should endeavor to find it among anash in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established (among them, Mr. Z. Vilimovsky, P.O. Box 4595, Tel Aviv, or Rabbi Avraham Pariz, 16 Bar Kochva St., Petach Tikvah), and from them you can also purchase the books you choose.

Surely you are aware of the significance of the upcoming auspicious day, 19 Kislev. A booklet is being sent separately (written at the time by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory), and the content of the booklet will surely interest those you influence as well.

With blessings for success in your holy work to raise the horn of the Israel of old, and for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 5810

B"H, 9 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from 3 Kislev.

At an auspicious time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, each according to their specific needs as described in your letter. To the extent that you increase your study of our holy Torah—both in Nigleh and Chassidus—with consistency and diligence, and beautify your observance of the mitzvos, you will see an increase in the blessings of Hashem, both in what you require and in the fulfillment of your aforementioned request.

Since we are approaching the days of Chanukah, it is surely unnecessary to emphasize the lesson of Chanukah: that in matters of Torah and mitzvos, one must act in a manner of "increasing and continuing" specifically—even when, to the physical eye, the situation does not appear so favorable. This is the law of Chanukah, where we light the candle after the sun has set, yet we increase the light from day to day. Regarding the concept of light and the candle, the verse already states, "A mitzvah is a candle and Torah is light," especially for a young man who is a ben yeshiva.

I trust you are keeping the three daily study portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—as is well known, and in any event, you should keep them from this point forward.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.

## 8511

By the Grace of Hashem, 10 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, a man of noble character, a scion of a noble family, etc., R’ Sh. Z. [Shazar], may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received the good news that the representatives of Kfar Chabad and the representatives of the relevant offices have met, and a meeting was held under your chairmanship regarding the construction of the housing project in Kfar Chabad. It is my hope that this meeting will surely bring about practical results in the near future, commensurate with the great importance of the matter.

We bring about merit on a meritorious day; today is the day of the redemption and victory of the Mitteler Rebbe, successor to his father, the Alter Rebbe. As stated in a letter from the Rebbe, my father-in-law, printed at the end of *Kitzurim VeHe'aros LeTanya* (end of page 122): "Because of this *mesiras nefesh* (of the Alter Rebbe) for the teachings of Chassidus, it was decreed in the Heavenly Beis Din that in every matter of Torah, *yiras shamayim*, and good character traits, the hand of those who are connected to him and follow in his footsteps shall be uppermost." This strengthens my confidence that even if there are any obstacles, they will be overcome, and the matter will not only be brought to fruition, but will be done to the maximum extent and as soon as possible.

Since my hope is strong, and in accordance with what I wrote to you in my previous letter—that you will participate in the *farbrengen* of Kfar Chabad on the Day of Redemption, the "Festival of Festivals," 19 Kislev, the day of the redemption and victory of the Alter Rebbe, and with him, the teachings of Chassidus and its affairs—this is an opportune time to announce the housing project during the *farbrengen*. A Chassidishe *farbrengen* has the power to break through barriers and remove partitions, and this includes the partition between the "desired and good" and the "possible," so that there will be full possibility, and they will bring it to fruition, fulfilling the desired and good in their entirety.

As you write to me, the discussion at the aforementioned meeting concerned a housing project of limited dimensions. While the Rebbe, my father-in-law, was accustomed to mentioning the Baal Shem Tov’s emphasis on the intent of the verse, "Though your beginning was small, **(and through this)** your end will greatly increase," one should fulfill the obligation of "your beginning was small" in speech, but in practice, one should act on a broad scale. If there is any possibility, my heartfelt request is for a housing project, in the first stage, of at least twenty-four units. A further request: that the homes for the professionals also have their construction completed, and those that have not yet begun should begin and also be completed. I wish to hope that through your efforts, and based on the aforementioned ruling of the Heavenly Beis Din, all the construction and the aforementioned first stage will be completed by the Day of Redemption of the Rebbe, my father-in-law—12-13 Tammuz, may it come upon us for good.

I will take the liberty of making you a *shaliach* for a *mitzvah* regarding another point in the aforementioned: I am enclosing a check from the London campaign for the benefit of the Village Committee, representing their contribution to the construction of the housing project, and a second check—my own private contribution to the construction of this housing (which is also, of course, on account of the sum that the Village Committee committed to provide). Thank you for the trouble of delivering the checks to their intended purpose.

Our Sages of blessed memory said, "Anyone who engages in building becomes impoverished," and in that same passage, it is understood that "any person who has no building is not a person" (*Yevamos* 63a). I have explained the seemingly contradictory nature of this: in order to establish a building—a true building that includes, encompasses, and unifies a person with all his assets, until they are all elevated to their highest level, which is the level of *Adam* (man), so called because he is "like the Most High" (*Adamah L'Elyon*)—the assets that are in the open, the revealed powers of the soul, are not sufficient. For a building of eternal endurance is not built in such a way. Only when one "becomes impoverished"—meaning, one invests all of one’s revealed powers and, furthermore, draws from the hidden, essential powers—does one lay the foundation, build the walls, and up to the roof, and including it. And then it becomes—**"the glory of man"** (because he performed his *avodah*, labored, and achieved) to dwell in the house. This is understood from matters in spirituality, and especially according to what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus in the *maamar* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, *D"H Mizmor Shir Chanukas HaBayis*, printed in *Likutei Torah*, end of *Parshas Berachah*.

With this approach to this problem, the housing project will surely be built in the aforementioned dimensions (even though, to me, this too is in the category of "your beginning was small"). I hope that here, too, the following will be fulfilled: "He who has one hundred wants two hundred; he who has two hundred wants four hundred." When you and those you influence see the success in the construction of the aforementioned housing, you will want double and double-double (with the help of Hashem), and ultimately, this desire, too, will be realized.

With respect and blessing for good news regarding the above, and for a joyous and active *farbrengen*.

## 8813

8813

B"H, 10 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brothers, the Children of Israel, who love and cherish Torah and mitzvos,
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

The annual celebration of the Merkaz Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, which will take place, G-d willing, on the 20th of Teves 5718, marks this year the sixtieth jubilee since the founding of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lubavitch.

The Lubavitcher yeshivos have traversed a long path, a path filled with great upheavals and experiences. Throughout these sixty stormy years of upheaval and galus, its founders and leaders—the Rebbe (Rashab) and the Rebbe Rayatz, of blessed memory—along with the administration, mashpi'im, roshei yeshivos, and talmidim, have carried the "ner mitzvah v'Torah ohr" and the "maor shebaTorah" with the greatest mesiras nefesh, spreading the light of Torah and mitzvos in all the roads, cities, and countries to which Divine Providence has led them.

This year, the central Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim celebrates, in addition to the sixtieth jubilee of its founding in Lubavitch, its eighteenth jubilee here in this country—a golden chain of uninterrupted activity for Torah and yiras shamayim.

A jubilee is not merely a way to mark a date. It is a challenge to take stock of the achievements of the time that has passed—with the goal of increasing those achievements in the years to come.

If, during an era of world-altering events, with extraordinary difficulties and obstacles, the Lubavitcher yeshivos were not only able to exist but also to expand, spread, and branch out, in both quantity and quality, one can imagine what will be possible to achieve under better circumstances.

This is precisely the challenge and the cheshbon hanefesh that everyone to whom Torah and Yiddishkeit are dear must undertake in connection with this year’s celebration and double jubilee.

True, over the course of the last eighteen years, the central Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch has, B"H, flourished greatly and left its mark on American Jewish life. However, there must be "ma'alin bakodesh," **increasing and continuing**. One must not be satisfied with the achievements of the past years. One must ascend and add, and add yet again, and expand. This, however, is dependent upon and requires the broad participation of everyone, who must also be **"ma'aleh bakodesh," increasing and continuing**. One must increase their support—in funds and in cooperation for the Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim in general.

And the Ribono shel Olam promises: "Whoever adds, they add to him"—in whatever one is in need of, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

With blessings for all the best in revealed good,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8,915

[10 Kislev, 5718]

I am responding to your letter from the night of Sunday, and subsequently the information received via telephone through Rabbi Chadakov, that the business is closing in the shortest possible time, and only the proposal regarding the poultry shochet remains.

I accept that in the matter you write about, there is **no issue of *hasagas gevul*** (encroachment upon another’s livelihood). If this is the case, may it be done in a *sha’ah tovah umutzlachas*. It would be a proper thing for you to contribute a certain sum from the upcoming earnings to a *kupah shel tzedakah*. This will establish the new venture from the very beginning according to the will of *Hashem*, *aser te’aser* (tithe), and as it is written, "And test Me now herewith, etc."

At a *eis ratzon*, may you mention all those you write about at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h*, *nvg"m*, *zy"a*, each according to their needs, and may *Hashem* help that you bring good news regarding this as well.

Certainly, in your camp as well, you are making preparations for the *yom habahir* 19 Kislev, the *Yom HaGeulah* of *Rabbeinu HaZaken*, the teachings of *Chassidus*, its matters, and its guidance. May the merit of the *baal hasimcha*, *Rabbeinu HaZaken*, stand for each and every one of you, in all that you need, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for good tidings and for a joyous and active *farbrengen*.

## 8916

B"H, 10 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Friday... May it be the will of the Creator and Guide of the world that your endeavors meet with success, bringing tidings of **only** good—in the expression of our Sages, "good to Heaven and good to people." When one observes what is happening around us, especially in our times—a period in which all foundations have been shaken—one sees that these two are interdependent. One who does not acknowledge the obligation to be "good to Heaven," that is, in matters between man and Hashem, is suspect of also being dismissive of being "good to people," in matters between man and his fellow. This dismissal eventually leads to undesirable actions that are harmful to the mutual relationships between man and his fellow.

You have surely heard at least the main points regarding the upcoming day of 19 Kislev. Since your letter arrived in proximity to this day, I am enclosing a booklet that explains the significance of the festival, which will surely be of interest to you.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

in Montreal

## 8,818

B"H, 11 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from 27 Cheshvan, which has just arrived. It is surprising that until now you have not written regarding your work in the field of education, especially since it appears that you are seeing the fruits of your labor.

Regarding what you wrote—that when your students reach a certain age they move to another kindergarten that is secular—it would be appropriate for you to draw the attention of the directors of the institution where you serve to this matter. By allowing this to happen, not only are the children lost, but the influence upon the parents is also lost to a significant degree. This is detrimental even from a communal-organizational perspective, in addition to the primary concern: the religious aspect. Surely, it is easy to arrange for your institution to accommodate children up to age five, and generally until the age they enter regular school. A year at such a tender age is a significant achievement for the child, and furthermore, it allows for influencing the parents for one additional year.

Surely the N'shei Chabad in your area will utilize the days of the month of Kislev in general, and the days of 10 and 19 Kislev in particular, for the development of their work. It is my hope that you are also among those active in this, and the more one increases, the more praiseworthy it is, especially in a matter that concerns the many.

With blessings for good tidings in all that was mentioned, and also in your personal matters.

## 5819

B"H, 12 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the avreich, Avraham Baruch, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

I received your letter in due time regarding your move to Chicago, and subsequently the updates via the esteemed Chossid, etc., etc., Rabbi M.A. Hodakov, may he live, as well as via Rabbi Ben-Zion Altheiz, may he live, who organized a group of students, which gave me much satisfaction. Surely, in this too, you are fulfilling the principle of "ascending in holiness," by increasing the group in both quantity—the number of students—and in the quality of the studies. It is not always necessary for the two to be dependent on one another; my intention is that one should not set a condition that all participants must immediately be at the appropriate level of quality, as that would limit the avodah. It is well known that even the simplest person in Yisrael is obligated in Talmud Torah. Rather, my intention is that on one hand, one must strive to increase the number of participants, even if they have not yet reached the appropriate level, and on the other hand, for those who are suited for it, one must strive to increase their quality.

May Hashem grant you success in your avodah for the benefit of others, which is a great principle in the Torah, as Rabbi Akiva said regarding the verse, "And you shall love your neighbor as yourself." May this avodah bring success in your personal matters as well, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you regarding the preparations for the auspicious day of Yud-Tes Kislev, and you will certainly convey this to those you influence as well.

With blessings.

#### ***5819***

**Avraham Baruch:** Gabai.

## 8921

B"H, 13 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the participants in the farbrengen of the Day of Redemption and victory of the Mitteler Rebbe, may Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

I received with pleasure your letter dated the aforementioned day, sent from the midst of your farbrengen.

May it be the will of Hashem that the blessings of each and every one of the Jewish people for one another be fulfilled in a revealed and manifest good. It is already known what the verdict from Above is, as related by the Alter Rebbe: "What a Chassidishe farbrengen can accomplish, the angel Michael cannot accomplish."

And one mitzvah leads to another; surely anash in Toronto will gather on the bright day of 19 Kislev, the Rosh Hashanah for Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus. Regarding the word "Rosh" (head), the Alter Rebbe and his son, the Mitteler Rebbe, explained the precision of the terminology—"Rosh" (head) and not "techilah" (beginning)—for the head contains the vitality of all the limbs of the body; likewise, Rosh Hashanah contains all the days of the year. May it be the will of Hashem that this hisorerus be drawn down and its impression be evident throughout all the days of the coming year.

With blessings for a joyous and impactful farbrengen.

## 5922

B"H, 13 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

...Regarding what you wrote at the end of your letter, that you are prepared to do whatever you are told: it is truly surprising to ask such a question, after so many years that I have been "raining down" instructions, requests, and even orders regarding the avodah of each and every person—which is a *chovas gavra* (a personal obligation) in this generation of ours, with no exceptions. The point is the *hafatzas hamaayanos* (spreading the wellsprings) and all the activities that can assist in this. And *hafatzas* means exactly that: spreading the teachings of Chassidus in a way that is suited to the understanding of the listeners. Repeating *maamarim* of *Da"Ch* (Divrei Elokus Chassidus) from time to time, and so much more.

To my great regret, I have not yet been informed of good news regarding the aforementioned, except for a brief report on rare occasions that *maamarim* were repeated in such-and-such a place, and they write about this as if it were a completely exceptional event—and I fear that this is indeed the case. For it happens very rarely, at a time when your father and his sons, *shichyu*, could have—and consequently are also **obligated** to—make [the location] a Chabad place. Instead of reports about the activities of Chassidim, the *olam’she* (the worldly ones) are conquering territory after territory and establishing institution after institution, while *anash*—with them at the head—wait for an exceptional day, hold a *farbrengen*, and then go back to being idle regarding any activity until a few months pass and another holiday arrives.

It is obvious that my intention is not to preach morality, but that, finally, they should be aroused to take concrete action. Behold, the King Moshiach is standing behind our wall, the time is extremely short, and the work is extremely great.

Certainly, the *farbrengen* of the upcoming 19 Kislev will be to the necessary extent—that is, with great expansion—and may it be G-d’s will that this be a good beginning to fulfilling their role in the aforementioned.

It is understood that all the above words are directed not only to you, but also to your father and your brothers, *shichyu*. May it be G-d’s will that you find the appropriate words to explain what has been said, so that your own actions will arouse them and compel them to do what is incumbent upon them. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for good news in all the aforementioned, and for a joyous and active *farbrengen*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9823

B"H, 13 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn

To the Administration of the Lubavitch Beis Medrash
And Agudas Chabad in...
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter of 11 Kislev, in which you write regarding the proposal to purchase a plot of land for a cemetery, etc., and the positive aspects of this.

It is surprising that you do not mention whether there is any downside to this. It is brought in many places—including the sicha of 19 Kislev 5694 by my father-in-law, the Rebbe—that there is nothing in the world that does not contain a mixture of good and evil. What interests me is whether this does not provide grounds for grievances from the administration of the Chareidi cemetery, who, it seems, have already proposed and even requested that you participate in the purchase of their cemetery, etc. It is not my intention to magnify the concern, for the proposal you write about is inherently correct, and therefore one should not be overly stringent about this; on the contrary. My approach regarding all matters of anash in every place they reside is already well-known, and regarding them, as I have written many times to anash in your camp, you have a great possibility to increase activities in all areas, yet for reasons that are **utterly** strange, you do not do so. It is understood that every action by Chassidim is not only desirable, but good and even necessary. Would that through this, the teaching of the Mishnah, "one mitzvah leads to another," be fulfilled—that one achievement will cause, even if against one's will, an expansion in all other matters, until knowledge increases and they come to the realization that expansion in all areas is not only possible but also necessary, and that it will not only fail to infringe upon existing matters but will actually assist in their stabilization and development.

The conclusion from the above is that if there are no clear negative sides, you should endeavor to make the aforementioned land purchase. In their days and in our days, the complete and true Redemption will come, and the prophecy will be fulfilled: "And I will remove the spirit of impurity from the land," and "Hashem will wipe away tears, etc." He will revive us after two days, and on the third day He will raise us up, and we will live before Him—the soul united with the body in this world. And above all—that there will be eternal life.

You will surely gather for a farbrengen on the upcoming bright day of 19 Kislev in the desired manner, and the impression of the farbrengen will be evident throughout all the days of this year, in both spiritual and material matters, and in daily life as well.

With blessings for good tidings and for a joyous and active farbrengen.

## 5924

B"H, 15 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh.

In general, the rectification of an undesirable act must first and foremost be in that very area. Since the transgression concerned Shabbos, you must resolve with firm determination to be meticulous from here on in the observance of Shabbos and its related matters in the most complete manner. In order to know its halachos, it is understood that you must become proficient in the halachos of Shabbos that are relevant in practice, at the very least. Therefore, you should choose the chapters in the Kitzur Shulchan Aruch regarding the halachos of Shabbos that apply in practice, and study them several times until you are proficient in them.

And since for everything one requires Siyata Dishmaya—especially for one who has sinned and desires a complete teshuvah—you must increase your study of our holy Torah with diligence and persistence, for through this, one receives additional assistance from the Giver of the Torah and the Mitzvos.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 8925

B"H, 15 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of December 1, I acknowledge receipt of your letter of New Year’s greetings, and I ask whether perhaps the letter was intended for another person who shares your name, as you have not previously been in correspondence with us.

However, even though you were correct in your remarks, nonetheless, since everything occurs through *Hashgacha Pratis*, may it be His will that these blessings be fulfilled, along with the blessings that all other members of *Bnei Yisrael* wish upon one another. As is known from the story of our *Rabbeinu HaZaken*, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, when our Father in Heaven sees the good relationship and the good blessings that *Bnei Yisrael* wish upon one another, He adds His own blessings over and above the fulfillment of those stated blessings. This is analogous to a father with his children among human beings, where the closeness of mind between the children causes the greatest *nachas ruach*, and the father adds to his gifts for those children.

It is my hope that, since you wrote in your letter, "I ascended to the *Eretz* ten years ago," you are surely striving with all your ability and everything that depends on you to ensure that this be a true *aliyah*—that is, an *aliyah* of the *neshamah*—by drawing closer and closer to the purpose of the *aliyah*, which is the *Hashem Yisbarach*, Giver of the *Torah* and the *mitzvah*, who is *Ein Sof* and without limit. Through a lifestyle that conforms to His instruction in His *Torah* (the word *Torah* implying *hora'ah*, instruction), one ascends on the path that leads to Him. After all, even in the mouths of all the nations of the earth, this land is called the *Eretz HaKodesh*, named for the *Beis HaMikdash*, the holy sites, and the holy events that occurred within it; and it is holy, as explained in the *Torah*, through living a life of *Torah* within it.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the *Rebbe* shlita,

Secretary

## 9926

B"H, 16 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...I read with interest what you wrote regarding the minyan. It is surprising that you conclude your letter by stating that while you are on good terms with the people, they are "simple" and "opponents," and that it is impossible to study with them. This is surprising, for the importance of simple people and their stature is well-known, as is understood from what is explained in the Kuntres Limud HaChassidus of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. Furthermore, regarding what you wrote about "opponents," there are no such people among the House of Israel; even those who oppose in speech do so only out of a lack of knowledge. When the matters are explained to them as they truly are, not only do they cease their opposition, but they become friends, supporters, and helpers. This depends entirely on the one who is doing the inspiring—that his words should be filled with vitality and come from the heart, for then they will surely have their effect.

You will surely participate in the farbrengen of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, in a manner that its impression will be evident in the days that follow.

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above.

## 8927

8927

B"H, 17 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I confirm receipt of your letter from the 2nd of Kislev, in which you write about the status of the shiurim being taught in your beis medrash, and that this is by the grace of Hashem Yisbarach, and that perhaps someone else could have done the same, etc.

Now, in general, everything a person does is by the grace of Hashem, but when Hashem says that one does it himself, He then grants success through His abundant mercies, and therefore it is credited to the account of the person.

Regarding what you write, that perhaps someone else would have accomplished more:

The only result of such a thought should be that, since someone else could accomplish more—and he, too, is a descendant of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov—he must also be able to do so. Consequently, one must simply do more, and in the end, there will be success for him as well.

And regarding what you write about the shiurim, that for the time being it has not been possible to establish them:

I hope that you are not, chas v’shalom, despairing of this, and that you will continue to make an effort for it in the future. After all, one cannot know when the eis ratzon is above and when the eis ratzon is below. It is possible that it could happen soon, whereas a lack of hishtadlus will certainly bring about nothing, and from a lack of hishtadlus, no shiur will ever come to be.

Especially since the days of the month of Kislev, the month of miracles and redemption, are auspicious for this.

I am certain that you know the significance of 19 Kislev; nevertheless, enclosed is a booklet on 19 Kislev which was written in its time by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, regarding the parsha of Chag HaGeulah and the moral lesson to be derived from it. I am sure you will utilize it in an appropriate manner.

With blessings for good tidings, with joy and a glad heart.

## 9928

B"H, 17 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, engaged in communal needs,
R' Yitzchak, may he live, HaKohen

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter regarding the Bar Mitzvah celebration of your son, may he live.

You should examine the Zohar Chadash, Bereishis 15d, regarding the reason for this celebration, from which it is simple to understand when it should take place. If someone wishes to hold some sort of celebration prior to that for any reason whatsoever, then why not? If it results in an increase in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos, why should this path for strengthening Yiddishkeit be any less valid than other paths?

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 9829

B"H, 17 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, your letter was received, in which you write about the events that have occurred during the months and weeks since your last letter.

Regarding all of this, in my opinion, you should make a greater and greater effort to complete your studies so that you can become a certified teacher or a certified kindergarten teacher. Beyond the benefit of the matter in and of itself, it is also understood regarding parnassah that one gains more by completing one's studies and subsequently earning a salary as a teacher or kindergarten teacher than by stopping one's studies midway and beginning to earn an income somewhat earlier, but for much less and for a period of several years. When you truly make an effort in this, you will surely succeed. However, as I have written to you previously, it is worthwhile that you consult about this with friends on the spot, for it is said, "In the multitude of counselors there is salvation."

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 8950

B"H, 17 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 15 Kislev, in which you write regarding suggestions for shidduchim.

As much as I know the talmidei hatmimim, and as I also said to your father shlita, there are **many** among the students about whom one can think and take an interest. Therefore, I do not understand why one needs to go looking elsewhere.

It is understood that just as all people are not perfect, for the only one who is perfect is the Holy One, blessed be He, so too among the students, people can find things that lack perfection. But as I said—**all** people are like that, and yet people marry and are subsequently happy with true happiness. And if in all matters one looks first at the essential and then at the secondary, I do not believe that in a matter of a shidduch, which affects your entire life, one should overlook the essential and begin the examination (test) of the secondary, or perhaps even something less than that.

Regarding the thought of traveling this year to Eretz HaKodesh tichyeh—without going into the essence of the idea, specifically in this year, when the secularists want to make such a trip a matter of "my strength and the might of my hand have gained me this wealth," if one has not traveled until now, I do not believe that one should add strength to this by traveling precisely now.

And for your birthday, this coming Shabbos Kodesh, may Hashem help you to have a year of success in all matters, and with a truly good shidduch at the appropriate time.

I hope that the N'shei U'Bnos Chabad of... will also utilize the yom habahir 19 Kislev in an appropriate manner, on that same day or in the coming days, and may Hashem grant them success.

With blessings.

As is recounted and explained in many places, with wonder upon wonder, to the point that they stated that "Love your fellow as yourself" is the vessel for, and one with, "Love Hashem your G-d." And in the Iggeres HaKodesh of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, in Epistle 9, [it is explained] how this is the entire essence of the service of Hashem in these times, in the footsteps of Moshiach.

## 8932

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Kislev, regarding your work as a sofer and whether you should continue in this profession or not.

It is appropriate that from the salary you earn in this field, you should give more than a maaser—close to a chomesh—to tzedakah. This will draw down blessing upon the remainder of your earnings, as expressed by our Alter Rebbe in the holy Tanya, chapter 34: even if one gives only a chomesh, that chomesh elevates the other four parts to Hashem, to be a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the matter of forgetfulness—the advice for this is known: be careful with tevilas Ezra, be fluent by heart in several chapters of Mishnayos and, at the very least, one chapter of the holy Tanya, and minimize idle talk and idle thoughts.

Regarding what you wrote about success in your learning and your endeavors: you must set fixed times for study. It is best to dedicate at least a short time each day to the study of pnimiyus haTorah, which is called in the holy Zohar the "Tree of Life," where there is no place for forgetfulness, etc., and no foothold for any undesirable matters, as explained by Moshe Rabbeinu, the Ra'aya Mehemna, in Zohar Vol. 3, 124b, and as explained in the Iggeres HaKodesh of our Alter Rebbe, section 26. And our Sages of blessed memory have already informed us: "You have labored and you have found."

With blessings for good tidings in all the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 8,834

8,834

By the grace of Hashem, 18 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in the study of Torah,
Rabbi Refael Chaim, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I have seen the galley proofs of the sefer *Tiferes Tzion*, a commentary on *Midrash Rabbah*, which you are preparing for publication.

May it be the will of Hashem that you increase your strength in Torah study with breadth, especially in the *Aggadah* of Torah. As is well known, the instruction of Chazal is: "If you wish to recognize the One who spoke and the world came into being, study *Aggadah*" (*Sifrei, Eikev* 6:6). This is particularly true in our generation, the *ikvesa d'Meshicha*, a time of double and redoubled darkness, where the study of this part of Torah is required more than ever, as per the well-known parable of Chazal regarding this (*Sotah* 40a; see Rashi there).

As a token of affection, although time does not permit me to study the aforementioned proofs as thoroughly as is required, I have reviewed them as much as time allowed. I have noted two or three comments in the margins of the beginning of this commentary. These points are based on the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and the teachings of Admur HaZaken, the author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*. The timing is appropriate, for on 19 Kislev, Admur HaZaken was released to freedom, marking the beginning of the dissemination of the wellsprings of his Torah—which is the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov—in a manner of constant progress, "increasing and growing." The dissemination and publicizing of this Torah is itself the greatest proof that it is the obligation of the time and the obligation of the individual to sanctify one's time to the study of this part of Torah. This is as is known from the words of the Arizal, that in our generation it is a mitzvah to reveal this wisdom, followed by his great student, R. Chaim Vital, as explained at length in his introduction to the sefer *Shaar HaHakdamos*, based on the words of the holy *Zohar*.

May it be the will of Hashem that through this, the end of our exile will be hastened, and we will merit, in our days, the fulfillment of the prophecy that knowledge, wisdom, and truth will increase, to attain the knowledge of their Creator according to the capacity of man, as it is said: "For the earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem as the waters cover the sea."

With respect and blessing.

P.S.

Comments: **1. 1,** and based on the saying of Chazal, "There are seventy faces to the Torah."

Questions: Regarding the connection between the first explanation of *Rabbah* and the second explanation: "Another explanation, etc." (Based on what is written in *Tiferes Tzion*, it should have only brought the second explanation). What is the reason for their order? Seemingly, the second explanation is simpler and should have been presented first. How can one say "pedagogue" (tutor), which implies a state of smallness—which was "with Him" (and according to *Tiferes Tzion*, "with Him" is only covered and hidden)—what is the matter of *rabbah* (greatness) as a separate category? For the pedagogue who is covered and hidden is himself *rabbah* (great); rather, this is the *Torah Shebe'al Peh* (as in *Midrash Rabbah*, *Parshas* 17:1, which is brought in *Tiferes Tzion*, and according to the *Rabbah* of the heavens). And more.

And the explanation of the above: *Pedagogue*—the education of the infant and the small child, which is only in simple and easy matters. *Covered*—here the entire matter is present, but it is covered in the garment of another matter, like the human body, "the worm that is trusted upon me." *Hidden*—the matter is in another place, like Mordechai who hid Hadassah. *Rabbah* means **great** and not **many**, like *Alexandria Rabbah*, one city but **great**. *Rabbah* explains the verse, "And I was with Him," in that it hints at all parts of the Torah: **Pshat**—revealed and simple; **Covered**—*Drush*; **Hidden**—*Remez* (only, and not the matter itself); **Sod**—which is the only thing that is **great**, and as Chazal inform us (*Sukkah* 28a), and therefore it comes in a separate category. And the Torah says that all its parts were with Him, and from this evolves: "Another explanation, etc."—He looks into the Torah and creates the entire world, worlds that are revealed and worlds that are hidden and not revealed, and its entirety also corresponds to the four: *Asiyah, Yetzirah, Beriah, Atzilus* (which correspond to the *Pardes* of Torah).

**1, 2.** The explanation of the *Midrash Rabbah*: *Bereishis* **with** the Torah, which is called *Reishis* (beginning), or—**for the sake of** the Torah—they are opposites. The first explanation explains the detail that the world (the creations) is primary, as per the saying of Chazal (*Bereishis Rabbah* 44:1), "The mitzvos were only given to refine the creations," and here further on—"The thought of Yisrael preceded the Torah." The second explanation explains the detail that the Torah is primary.

***

Regarding what was discussed about *zerizus* (diligence) beginning not before morning—this is also explicitly stated in Rashi and Tosafos there (*Pesachim* 4a).

#### ***8,834***

**R. Refael Chaim:** Goldman.

**Tiferes Tzion:** By the esteemed Rabbi Yitzchak Zev Yadler.

## 9,361

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and man of many accomplishments, R' Shlomo, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 24 Mar-Cheshvan and 10 Kislev, and the enclosures therein; I trust that in the meantime you have received my response to your previous letter.

It is a pity that you are feeling discouraged because so-and-so has raised a complaint or because so-and-so is behaving in an undesirable manner. This has been the way of our world for years and generations past—perhaps even to a greater extent than now. And who is greater than the first public activist after the Giving of the Torah, Moshe Rabbeinu, the first recipient of our holy Torah, and yet [he faced] all this, etc. On the contrary, in these days the avodah is easier, for the actions of the fathers are a sign for the children, as they have already paved the way. Furthermore, the concealments and hesterim are lighter in comparison to the aforementioned. And although—who is he and which is he whose heart prompts him to approach and compare himself, etc. (similar to what our Alter Rebbe writes in Tanya, Chapter 44)—nevertheless, one can draw strength and encouragement from this **a fortiori**, and it is easy to understand.

Especially in these days, as we have entered the month of Kislev, the month of redemption, miracles, and the instruction that within it, one **continues to increase**.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and that you utilize the days of this month with outstanding success.

P.S.
I trust that this year, too, you will distribute Chanukah gelt in my name—as you did last year.

## 8,937

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Shlomo Chaim, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter; in the meantime, your daughter's letter was received, and I have already replied to her.

You will surely gather in Tomchei Temimim on this bright day of 19 Kislev and the day following it, and you should make every possible effort to bring in students from other yeshivos as well. After all, they are closer than those who are "outside" in the literal sense. This is especially true after contemplating the efforts of Rabbeinu HaZaken (in addition to the efforts of the other students of the Maggid) to acquire Torah scholars and talented individuals for the study of Chassidus. Furthermore, the very name "Chabad" indicates this specifically, as explained in several sichos of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. From this, it is understood that extra effort is required in this point of acquiring Torah scholars. Surely, in this, too, the heavenly decree will be fulfilled: that because of this mesiras nefesh (of Rabbeinu HaZaken) for the study of Chassidus, it was decreed in the Heavenly Beis Din that in every matter of Torah, yiras shamayim, and good character traits, the hand of his followers and those who walk in his footsteps shall be uppermost.

With blessings for an active and joyous farbrengen and for good tidings regarding the above.

## 9,938

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc., R' Shlomo, may he live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

Following a long hiatus, your letter, which you began writing on 27 Mar-Cheshvan, has been received. Fortunate is your portion for organizing *farbrengens*. Regarding what you wrote—that you do not always see results or fruits, etc.—surely, during the *farbrengen* itself, words of Torah and *hisorerus* are spoken, and it is impossible for *Chassidus* not to have its effect. It is a well-known declaration of our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im* holy ones, that the *neshamah* hears, even regarding a person who is entirely simple. This is also understood from the *sicha* of Yud-Tes Kislev 5693; see *Likutei Dibburim* Vol. 2, section 17. This is especially true in your case, where those involved are people of Torah, etc.

Regarding what you wrote about the Rav, may he live, from Makov, and that he is a student of R' Sh. Greenfield, author of *Shu"t Maharashag*: surely, at an appropriate opportunity, convey my regards to him, even though I do not know him. My hope is strong that he will certainly do everything in his power for the dissemination of the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov in general, and as it was revealed in the Torah of Chabad by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe. This hope of mine is strengthened by the attitude toward our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe held by the teacher of the aforementioned Rav, as is understood from the fact that he takes the trouble to reconcile the words of the Alter Rebbe; see *Shu"t Maharashag*, Part Two, Siman 34 and Siman 75 (I do not have Part One of the aforementioned *Shu"t* in my possession, and it is possible that there, too, there is a similar matter).

You mention in your letter Rav Safra, may he live. Indeed, I have also met a Rav Safra, may he live, who told me that his father lives in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and perhaps this is the one.

My confidence is strong that you also did everything in your power to arrange the *farbrengen* for Yud-Tes Kislev as is fitting. Regarding what you wrote—that you do not feel you have sufficient strength, etc.—our Sages of blessed memory have already taught us in our holy Torah, the *Toras Chaim* which is **eternal**, through the stories regarding R' Chanina ben Dosa: they demanded of him only to lend his hand, and from Heaven they assisted him in bringing a stone to Jerusalem (*Shir HaShirim Rabbah* at the beginning, and *Koheles Rabbah* at the beginning; see there). There is a wonderful allusion in this to what is explained regarding the matter of the "heart of stone" and "Jerusalem, the city that is built as one." Great is the merit of your involvement in the aforementioned and similar matters, and may you and all your household, may they live, succeed in all your affairs.

Regarding what you wrote at the end of your letter, that one of the participants in the *shiur* stated as a conclusion from what he studied in *Kuntres U’Maayan* that in the future, the body will influence the *neshamah*—this is indeed so, as is explained at length in the *maamarim* of the Rebbe (Rashab), *L’Chol Tichlah* 5659, and it is also brought in *Kovetz Lubavitch*, Issue 3.

With blessings for good tidings and for a joyous and active *farbrengen*.

## 8999

B"H, 18 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, whose work is the work of Heaven,
Engaged in communal needs,
R' Yaakov Yosef, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 15 Kislev and those preceding it: It is understood that there is no place or basis for discouragement, etc., due to the delay in receiving a response to your letters from here. The reason is the abundance of preoccupations. For this reason, responses are sent to those whose matters are most urgent, such as those who are conducting themselves in crooked ways and the like. As is known, the Sages’ interpretation regarding the prayer of King Solomon is that regarding Bnei Yisrael, conditions were stipulated, whereas otherwise, etc. This applies in a subtle way to our current matter as well.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the Talmud Torah: While there is certainly room for several of the improvements you detailed, it is my hope that everyone agrees that it is impossible to cast doubt upon the necessity of the Talmud Torah matter itself. Given its obviousness, there is no need to elaborate on this...

I await good news from the farbrengen of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev. Surely you will also utilize the days of Chanukah—for matters of Yiddishkeit in general, and the dissemination of the wellsprings in particular—and may Hashem grant you success.

With blessings for Chag HaGeulah,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**R' Yaakov Yosef, may he live:** Gurkow, London. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 14, 5132, and in the notes indicated there.

**As is known:** See also below, letter 6131.

## 8940

B"H, 20 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rav, G-d-fearing, man of many deeds and full of energy,
Engaged in communal needs,
Et cetera, et cetera, R' Zev, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your regards through the avreichim, shlit”a. Although they did not provide me with details, my hope is strong that you are increasing from time to time in your holy avodah to bring the hearts of the Bnei Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven, for we are commanded to "increase in holiness."

These days are especially auspicious for making good resolutions in this regard, for we have just come from the bright day of 19 Kislev, which, in the words of our holy Rebbes, is the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus. As the Rebbe (Rashab), father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, zt”l, nishmaso eden, stated: on this day, a revelation of the inner light of the holy Torah is drawn down in a general sense for the entire year.

And the inner dimension of the Torah is the "Tree of Life," where there is no "other side," the spirit of impurity, etc., and through it, the Bnei Yisrael will emerge from galus with mercy, as stated by Moshe Rabbeinu, the faithful shepherd, in Zohar Chadash, Vol. 3, 124b, and explained by our Alter Rebbe in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 26.

Fortunate is his portion that from Heaven they have merited and appointed him to influence many of the Bnei Yisrael. May it be the will of Hashem that He grant him success, and that he merit to utilize this influence to its fullest, and the merit of the many will assist him.

Regarding the aforementioned avreichim and their study of the craft of shechitah—based on the halachic ruling that a shochet must be "a kosher person whose ways are upright and the fear of Hashem is upon his face, and he must also know how to study and understand for himself in the Gemara and Rashi, etc., be exceedingly G-d-fearing, and tremble at the word of Hashem, and not be hasty or impulsive in his mind, etc." (see Shulchan Aruch of our Alter Rebbe, Yoreh Deah 1:2; his Responsa 69; Responsa of the Tzemach Tzedek, Yoreh Deah 12, and others)—it has been the custom for many years that as a prerequisite to studying the laws of shechitah, there must be a period of preparation to acquire the aforementioned necessary qualities. This preparation is, of course, through the study of the holy Torah without any ulterior motives—even motives of holiness—good conduct in general, and the performance of mitzvos with hiddur in particular, and more.

My hope is strong that you, in your letters to them, will awaken them to this again and again, and that for the time being, they will not be preoccupied at all with thoughts regarding the study of the craft of shechitah, etc., but rather their desire will be in the Torah of Hashem, and in His Torah they will meditate day and night with diligence and with the vitality of "all my bones shall say." Surely you will find the appropriate words for them, and you will succeed.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all that is mentioned, and for a Chanukah that illuminates and follows the school of Hillel—increasing and going forward.

## 9442

B"H, 22 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 15 Kislev, in which you outline the main events you have experienced and mention your concerns regarding sorcery, witchcraft, and the like:

You should dismiss this from your mind entirely, once and for all. Strengthen your trust in Hashem, may He be blessed, who oversees each and every individual with *hashgacha pratis*. However, you should have your *tefillin* and the *mezuzos* in your home checked. Every weekday morning before *davening*, set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*. After *davening* each morning, and also on *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*, recite the daily portion of *Tehillim*—as the *Tehillim* is divided for the days of the month.

Regarding what you wrote about a *tikkun*: First and foremost, you must engage energetically in the matter of a *shidduch* with a *kosher* woman. Furthermore, ensure that words of Torah are engraved in your memory—meaning, know them by heart. This should include some chapters of *Mishnayos* and, at the very least, one chapter of the *Tanya Kadisha* (as per what is written in *Likutei Torah* by the Alter Rebbe, at the end of *Parshas Kedoshim*). You may also conduct yourself with *taanis dibbur* (fasting from speech) and the like. However, fasting from food and drink is absolutely ruled out, as that is the opposite of the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and *Chassidus*. My reference to *taanis dibbur* is based on what is written in *Sefer Toldos Maharash* (end of page 72), but it goes without saying that this must be done without any outward display or fanfare, so that onlookers do not notice. In a manner appropriate to your situation, you should also strive with the greatest energy in the matters of educating the sons and daughters of Yisrael in accordance with the purity of holiness.

You are surely participating in *chassidishe farbrengens* that are held from time to time. By participation, I mean—of course—not regarding the physical aspects, but regarding hearing the words of *hisorerus* (inspiration) spoken during the *farbrengen*, and primarily, the resulting change for the better. It is well known—*petka d'shmaya nachis*—the words of the Alter Rebbe: "What a *chassidishe farbrengen* can accomplish, even the Angel Michael cannot accomplish."

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

***

**The words of the Alter Rebbe:** See also above, Letter 9439, and the references in the notes there.

## 8943

B"H, 23 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Kfar Chabad Committee,
May Hashem preserve them and let them live.

Peace and blessing!

Disturbing rumors have reached here regarding the lack of order (or lack of willingness) prevailing concerning the payment of taxes by the residents of the village, and that due to the non-payment, various communal matters of the village are suffering—meaning, everyone is suffering. It is understood that order must be brought to this. And although it is surely difficult to settle all the debts at once, in an expanded meeting, times and methods of payment must be established, appropriate to the status and situation of each individual and in accordance with the size of their debt.

It must be explained again and again, based on the point in my previous letters, that it is essential in Kfar Chabad—and all the more so, *kal v'chomer*, that this is essential in all places where Bnei Yisrael reside—that each person understand that the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life, [that] "the individual and the many, the halacha follows the many," is the benefit of the **individual** and the benefit of the many. Furthermore, this is the true benefit of the individual, not only in spirituality but also, quite simply, in physicality: for by setting aside his private benefit for the **moment**, the general benefit—of which he is a part—is increased. Moreover, by doing so, he is in a position to demand for tomorrow and the day after that others also do the same and set aside their private benefit for the benefit of the many—this is a great gain, even in the simplest sense. Further elaboration is unnecessary regarding the most basic matter, which is standard in all communal affairs and even in matters of partnership...

I am certain you will report with the necessary detail regarding the farbrengen for Yud-Tes Kislev, the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, and the days preceding and following it. Most importantly, [report] regarding the *uvchen* (the resolution) and the action for the benefit of all the affairs of Kfar Chabad, for "there Hashem commanded the blessing, life forever."

With blessings for success and for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and for an illuminating and joyous Chanukah to all the residents of the village—may Hashem preserve them and let them live.
