## 9945

B"H, 23 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After a very long interval, I received your letter dated the 15th of the month of Redemption. Regarding what you wrote—that your situation has unfortunately not changed, that you see no progress, and that your state is, G-d forbid, entirely poor—my opinion is clear that all of the above is inaccurate.

That is to say, the fact that your situation has not changed is not, as you conclude, a cause for sorrow. It is simply because the verse states, "And Hashem your G-d will bless you in all that you **do**." "Do" means genuine action, not merely going through the motions to fulfill an obligation so that one can say they have done something. Consequently, there is no cause for sorrow that the situation has not changed, as this is the way of our world as revealed by the Torah. This is explained in many places, including the *Kuntres U’Maayan* (Maamar 23), that blessing must come specifically through the action of man.

This is all the more true, and certainly applies, to matters of *shidduch*. Regarding this, our Sages of blessed memory said that one must be like someone searching for their lost object. Therefore, it is strange that you have decided for yourself that it is difficult for you to find a *shidduch* in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) and that it must be abroad—this is the opposite of reality. If you will listen to my opinion, you will uproot this entire decision of yours and make an effort in a manner appropriate for one who fears Hashem regarding a good *shidduch*. The Holy One, Blessed be He, Who pairs couples, will provide you with your *zivug* at a good and auspicious time. May it be His will that you decide as stated above, promptly and completely, and that you become engaged soon as well.

Regarding all that has been said, the same applies to your settling down. Although in matters of settling down, one does not require as much exertion as in the aforementioned matter—as per the words of our Sages of blessed memory cited above—this, too, requires "the labor of your hands" and personal action to settle in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), both regarding a *shidduch* and regarding settling down in general. Then, you will share good news regarding all of the above, soon.

With blessings.

## 8946

B"H, 24 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

After the longest of intervals, your letter of 22 Kislev was received. It is surprising that you do not mention whether you participated in the farbrengen of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, from which we have just emerged; I trust that you are aware of the significance of this day and its themes.

Regarding what you wrote about your personal situation—that despite all your efforts, nothing has come to fruition, etc.:

Since we follow the majority, in most cases of this nature, the reason is that one is overly particular about proposals regarding matters that are not essential at all. Consequently, one pays no attention to proposals that are appropriate in the essential matters—and even in the secondary matters—(except that in the most trivial details, there are some points that are not to one's liking). When one contemplates the absolute truth—that there is no perfection in the world, and the only One who is perfect in the ultimate sense is the Ribono shel Olam—it is understood that both the chassan and the kallah lack perfection. Indeed, it is for this reason that our Torah, the Torah of life, was given: to ascend from level to level on the path that leads to the perfection of the human being.

It is understood that my intention in the above is not to preach, but rather to awaken you to the possibility that perhaps this is the situation in your case as well. If so, it is no wonder that for the time being, the matter has not been concluded. On the other hand, the matter depends on you; for if, from here on, you focus on the proposals as mentioned—that is, on what concerns Torah and mitzvos, etc.—and you daven to the One who pairs couples, as our Sages of blessed memory said, and as it is written, "A prudent wife is from Hashem," the Ribono shel Olam will provide you with your suitable match, both materially and spiritually.

Since Divine Providence has placed you in the role of educating the children of Yisrael, it is understood that the more you increase your efforts in this holy work with faithfulness, the more Hashem’s blessing will hasten in what you need in general, and in the aforementioned matter in particular. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all of the above, soon.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 8947

B"H, 24 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Since all matters of a person, and especially the matters of a Jewish person, are by Divine Providence, and since, together with this, the purpose of all matters of a Jewish person is as the Mishnah states: "I was created to serve my Maker."

I am taking this opportunity in my letter to arouse you regarding the words of the Arizal, brought in Iggeres HaKodesh by our Alter Rebbe, Siman 26, that in these generations of ours, it is a mitzvah to reveal this wisdom (Pnimiyus HaTorah). In the Kuntres Eitz Chaim by my father-in-law, the Rebbe—the son of the Rebbe Rashab—it is explained at length how this is relevant, and how it adds even to the study of the Nigleh of Torah, and to the fulfillment of mitzvos and the avodah of a person in general. And one who studies the words of R' Chaim Vital, the foremost disciple of the Arizal, in his introduction to Shaar HaHakdamos regarding the necessity of this study, will find that the hair on his head will stand on end. One should also examine the halachic ruling—which is also a matter of Mishnah—in Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim, Siman 98 and the Rema there. For we see tangibly that only through the study of Pnimiyus HaTorah and following its paths does a person in this orphaned era of ours have the ability to fulfill what is stated there three times a day. And if this applies to every person, how much more so to one who is engaged in the chinuch of the children of Israel, where every addition in his own matters is multiplied many times over in those whom he educates. And this is clear.

With respect and blessings.

## 8948

B"H, 24 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 18 Kislev, the eve of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev—the Rosh Hashanah of the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, as proclaimed by our Rebbes, the Nesi'im—I hope that you participated in the farbrengen of that day. It is a time of favor for awakening and making resolutions regarding Torah and mitzvos, for wherever ten are gathered, the Shechinah rests, and consequently, there is an added measure of assistance at that time.

Regarding what you wrote: that when you reach Kabbalistic terminology in your study of Chassidus, you are overcome by doubt, thinking, "Who am I, and what am I?" etc.

It is obvious that ever since Hashem said, "And Hashem descended upon Mount Sinai..." and spoke, "Anochi" (I), and our Sages explained this as an acronym for "I Myself wrote and gave [My soul]," the essence of which is that Hashem inscribed Himself into His Torah—in any matter of Torah study, one is taking Him—the same applies to the performance of mitzvos. As is explicitly stated in the holy Zohar, cited in the holy Tanya, Chapter 47, not only has the ability been given to nullify the argument of "Who am I," but one is actually obligated to nullify it. Even though in earlier generations the study of the inner dimensions of Torah was a matter for the select few, our generations are not like those generations. This is explained at length in Igeres HaKodesh by the Alter Rebbe, Epistle 26, and explained even more extensively in Kuntres Eitz Chaim by the Rebbe (Rashab), the father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. This is understood even more powerfully through the parable of the Alter Rebbe told to the great Gaon, Chassid, and Tzaddik, Rabbi Pinchas of Koritz (printed in *HaTamim*), the parable of the precious stone in the crown of a great king. See all of the above, and I hope that through all this, you will increase your persistence and diligence in the study of Chassidus and in following its guidance.

Regarding what you wrote, that you "steal" time for the aforementioned study: here, too, one can apply the teaching regarding the verse "Do not steal" (*Lo Tignov*), where there is a *taam mafsik* (a disjunctive cantillation mark) under the word *Lo* (No). Thus, a "theft" that is *d'oraisa* (a Torah-level necessity) is permitted (Zohar, Yisro 93b).

When you provide the names of your children along with their mother's name, may they be well, they will be mentioned at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for whatever they may need.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, and for a bright and joyous Chanukah,

On behalf of the Rebbe,
Secretary

Postscript: Tosefta Bava Kamma 7:3; Shach, Choshen Mishpat 292, subsection 35; *Mei'am Loez* on Mishlei.

## 5949

B"H, 25 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which was delayed in transit—in which you write about the relationships at home and how, to a certain extent, they interfere with your studies in a way that is apparent to you, and you ask how you might manage in order to study properly and in the appropriate manner.

Since you write... it would be appropriate to look into the possibility of arranging for yourself a place in the school for girls or in a Bais Yaakov school where there is a dormitory. In any event, it is understood that one must not become discouraged, G-d forbid, by the fact that there are obstacles in the path of life. Not everything is ready-made; rather, one requires effort and exertion, and often, extra exertion. For such is the order of this world of ours, as everyone knows regarding their own situation. It is only because one does not know the details of what is happening with others that one sometimes mistakenly thinks they are the exception to the rule, in that their path in life is not entirely comfortable. Yet, we see that it is precisely these trials and hindrances that fortify a person and prepare them to walk more securely on their path in life...

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 8550

8550

B"H, 25 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and industrious, active in communal affairs,
R' Moshe Yitzchak, may he live, and his wife, the Rabbanit Rivka, may she live,

Greetings and blessings!

I received with pleasure your letter from the first night of Chanukah, along with the enclosure.

May it be the will of Hashem that for many more years you continue to engage in matters of Torah and mitzvos with expansion, and in a manner of expansion, as it is written, "And I will walk in a broad place" (*Tehillim* 119:45). This is also the instruction of these days of Chanukah: to increase and continue from day to day.

For even when the sun has set on the outside, not only did the Children of Israel have light in their dwellings, but they were also given the strength and ability to kindle a light at the entrance of their homes **on the outside**, and to increase in this as well, until they reach the goal. This is hinted at in the teachings of Chassidus, based on the words of our Sages regarding the duration of the Chanukah light: "until the foot of the Tarmodites has ceased" (*Shabbos* 23b). This means that a Jewish man and woman, through the conduct mentioned above, cause the "foot" (even the lowest levels) of the Tarmodites—the letters of which spell *moredes* (rebellious)—to cease, in relation to Hashem, His Moshiach, His Torah, and His mitzvos. This was also the nature of Tarmod at that time, when their hand was strong, as brought in the words of our Sages.

And if, regarding every individual, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, said that "an individual is a multitude"—meaning that he can influence many to elevate them from level to level and from strength to strength—then how much more so is this true for those whom Divine Providence has placed in the field of education in purity and holiness. Many are in need of them, and they are worthy of special success in their general and personal affairs. This is as the verse teaches for the bright day of 19 Kislev: "He has redeemed my soul in peace from the battle against me, for there were many with me" (*Tehillim* 55:19). The redemption in their affairs, since many are in need of them, will be in a manner of true peace—that is, peace in material matters and peace in spiritual matters.

With blessings for success in all the above, and for good news regarding all the above.

**R' Moshe Yitzchak, may he live:** Hecht, New Haven. Additional letters to him appear above, 8595, and in the notes referenced there.

**An individual is a multitude:** See also above, letter 8508, and the notes referenced there.

## 8951

8951

By the Grace of Hashem, First Night of Chanukah, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Anash in the Holy Land (may it be rebuilt and established), and to the youth—especially the students—may they live:

Greetings and blessings!

On this Festival of Lights, it is surely unnecessary to explain and emphasize the content of the matter for which our Rebbes, the leaders of our generations (may their merits protect us), called their students—the students of Tomchei Temimim—by the name "candles to illuminate." As is explained at length in other places, the precision in this title is that it is incumbent upon each and every one to illuminate their surroundings as well, with the "candle of mitzvah and the Torah of light" and the inner light of Torah. The act of naming is a matter of revelation—drawing something down from the root, the source, and the state of concealment into practical affairs. As is explained in Chassidic discourse in many places, the concept of naming is to connect the soul with the body, and so on.

Based on this, one can also explain the dispute regarding whether Adam gave names to the fish as well; for they are, by their nature, creatures of the "hidden world" (*alma d’itkasi*), the opposite of the concept of revelation. However, this "hidden world"—relative to the world above it—is also called a revelation, which is the secret of the opinion that the fish were also given names. See Tosafot, Chullin 66b; Chizkuni and Radak on Bereishis 2:19; Midrash Chaser V’Yatir, and elsewhere.

Now, although this title was bestowed upon the students of the Temimim, it is certainly understood that it applies to the students of their students as well. For this is the goal of education—that a good educator produces students like himself. This is especially true since the exile of Tomchei Temimim from its original location in Lubavitch, as the title and the role of "candles to illuminate" must be fulfilled wherever any one of them has been exiled, and certainly in a place where many of them, their children, and their children’s children are found.

It is understood that there are many ways and methods to fulfill the task of illuminating—some are primary, some secondary, and some are for times of emergency. But the primary, direct, and simple way is through education, and by exerting effort regarding the desired type of education—exerting effort with one’s body, one’s money, and one’s soul. This is similar to the three ways of fulfilling the mitzvah of tzedakah and gemilas chasadim, of which education is a part.

It is also understood that this task is many times more important in this time and place, where every single moment is extremely precious in the field of education. For the opportunity has been given to elevate many of the sons and daughters of Israel from strength to strength, and a lack of action in this area endangers their future.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate on the fact that in the Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu—this situation is currently at its peak. Since many are immigrating with their families, their children’s future depends entirely on how they settle in—both in their general affairs and, in particular, in matters of education—during this initial period.

Based on the above, my call and request to all Anash, and especially to the youth (may they live), is that each one of them should examine themselves: if they are capable of working in the education of the sons and daughters of Israel. And since a person is close to himself and can err in his assessment, he should consult with experts in this field. Those who have the talent for it should strive, as much as necessary, to arrange their lives so they can be involved in education with their very bodies—that is, as teachers, counselors, school administrators, and the like.

Certainly, in order to fulfill this role, one needs knowledge in various subjects. Many already possess this knowledge and only need to supplement it, while some already possess it in full. Regarding the rest, there is surely an opportunity to acquire this knowledge in an accelerated manner and to complete it later while engaged in the work of education. Indeed, the work of education itself teaches and instructs the person engaged in it how to perfect themselves.

Those for whom it is clear that they have no talent in the aforementioned field should enlist to strengthen and establish educational institutions—on the foundation of pure holiness. The main point here is advocacy among parents: that if they truly desire the happiness of their children—and their happiness not only in the World to Come but also in this world, not only in spirituality but also in physicality—they must educate their children on the foundation of pure holiness, in the spirit of the Israel of old. Every effort and exertion in this is worthwhile, as it concerns the entire future of their children.

The conclusion from all the above is that anyone who has reason to believe they are capable of being a teacher is requested to begin immediately to search for a way and a method to utilize their talent in this field, to the greatest extent possible, as this is the demand and the necessity of the hour.

May it be the will of Hashem that these days of Chanukah—which add and increase light at the entrance of one’s home from the outside—will also add to the "candles to illuminate." May those who are already illuminating have their light increased to reach far distances, in accordance with the precision of the expression, "Your springs shall spread outward." And those who, for whatever reason, are not yet illuminating, should raise their flame until the flame rises by itself, and in the manner described in *Iggeres HaTeshuvah* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (end of Chapter 9), that it should be "double the wisdom," in order to make up for the deficiencies of the years that passed without utilizing the strengths that were given to them.

And since our Sages have said regarding the verse, "He tells His words to Yaakov..."—that what He commands Israel, He does Himself—may the Holy One, Blessed be He, fulfill "And you shall teach them to your children"—the sons and daughters of Israel—by educating them in wisdom, understanding, and knowledge in both general and specific matters. And with expansiveness, joy, and a good heart, may they illuminate their entire surroundings with the "candle of mitzvah and the Torah of light" and the inner light of Torah.

Awaiting good tidings regarding all the above,

And signing with a blessing for immense success for all who participate according to the above, both they and all their households (may they live)—

—They shall stand upon the blessing, in both physicality and spirituality together.

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 8553

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn

To the holy Yeshiva in the holy community of Buenos Aires,
The students, the Roshei Yeshiva, the Mashpia, and the administration,
May Hashem keep them and may they live,

Peace and blessing!

It was with great pleasure that I learned some time ago of the founding of the holy Yeshiva. The news that it has developed since its inception—both in quantity, that is, in the number of students, and in quality, the caliber of the learning—has given me additional taanug.

Surely this development will provide each and every one of them with strength and encouragement to do even more, each in his own area, for the development of the Yeshiva, as mentioned, both in quantity and in quality.

For it is within the ability of each one to act in both these areas, since every Jew possesses both a body and a soul, both a nefesh elokis and a nefesh habahamish.

And in all these parts, one is commanded to serve his Creator and Master, the Giver of the Torah and the Commander of the mitzvos, as the Mishnah states: "I was created to serve my Creator."

These days are auspicious for making good resolutions and for taking action in all the aforementioned, for we have just come from the bright day, the 19th of Kislev. In the words of the Nasi of Israel, my father-in-law, the Rebbe—tzaddik livracha, nishmaso b'eden—in his letter to his son, my father-in-law, the Rebbe—tzaddik livracha, nishmaso b'eden: "The festival on which our soul was redeemed in peace, and the light and vitality of our soul was given to us... to draw down the revelation of the light of the pnimiyus of our holy Torah... so that it should shine within the pnimiyus of our soul... to banish from us every bad and despicable trait among our natural traits, so that all our deeds and affairs (both in avodah—meaning tefillah and the performance of mitzvos—and in worldly matters necessary for the sustenance of the body) will be with true kavanah for the sake of Heaven, which is what Hashem desires..."

And we have entered the days of Chanukah, the concept of which is that even when the sun has set outside, one must kindle the "lamp of Hashem, the soul of man," and the "lamp of mitzvah, the Torah of light," in a manner of "increasing and adding" from day to day. And one should not be satisfied with what concerns only oneself, but rather [kindle it] specifically at the entrance of one's house, facing the outside. The hint is understood. And as our Sages have taught, Hashem does not deal tyrannically with His creatures; surely, to each one have been given the necessary kochos to fulfill this holy task, and as the Creator commands, specifically with joy and a glad heart, as the words of the great teacher, our Rabbi the Rambam, in his Yad Hachazakah, at the end of Hilchos Lulav.

Enclosed is a contribution as a symbolic participation in the expenses of the holy Yeshiva.

With blessings for success in your holy work and for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 8954

B"H, 26 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yaakov, may he live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter. May it be the will of Hashem that, since we have just emerged from the luminous day of 19 Kislev—the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus—and given the well-known precision of the Alter Rebbe and his son, the Mitteler Rebbe, in using the term "Rosh" (head) rather than "techilah" (beginning), that it implies the head **includes** and draws vitality into **all** the limbs—that is, into all the days of the year; and since we are now in the days of Chanukah, whose essence is "increasing and continuing," and specifically at the entrance of one's house from the outside, even after the sun has set—may each one of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, fulfill the inner content of the above through actions in our surroundings, illuminating them with the "mitzvah candle," "Torah is light," and the "light of Torah," which is the teachings of Chassidus that brings one back to the proper path.

Indeed, this is also a lesson from the days of Chanukah: one should not be discouraged if the quantity of oil (which permeates the whole—Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah 105:5) appears, on the face of it, to be enough for only one day. For a person must do everything that is incumbent upon them, and Hashem will do what is good in His eyes. And if one acts according to one’s own capacity, the oil will suffice until new oil is prepared. And this is well understood.

With blessings for good tidings.

You also make no mention of the well-known dictum of our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*, that every Rosh Hashanah, a Jewish person must take upon themselves some increase in positive *mitzvos*, in the avoidance of negative *mitzvos*, and in Jewish custom. This applies all the more so regarding the matters of 19 Kislev, the Rosh Hashanah for Chassidus. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all of the above, and may I hear good tidings in a revealed and manifest way.

With blessings,

## 8990

B”H, 29 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Chanukah, in which you write regarding the proposal under consideration and that the proposal meets with your approval, and you see in this a double mitzvah: saving a Jewish soul by returning him to his source (a lifestyle according to Torah and mitzvos) and the mitzvah of marriage.

Regarding such mitzvos in general, Chazal have said that one should not perform mitzvos in "bundles" [i.e., one should not combine unrelated matters]. Furthermore, it is the common practice that marriage is not intended as a goal for educating one another, and certainly not for changing the most fundamental aspects of the other person’s life. This is especially true since, as is apparent from your letter, this would involve a change in the lifestyle that the person in question has followed for many years. Suddenly and abruptly, he would be required to take upon himself the yoke of Torah and mitzvos in his daily life—meaning, to change his habits several times a day. This is particularly relevant because even when people do take such a change upon themselves, they do not always anticipate the difficulty of the matter for someone who has for a long time conducted himself in the opposite manner.

You do not mention in your letter what the response of the person in question was to the condition you set, and most importantly, the nature of that response. I mean to ask whether he is agreeing to it because he has no other choice, or whether he is doing so willingly, or even with joy and a good heart.

In any event, even if the response were in the best possible terms, since you did not set a date in your letter, it would be appropriate for the person in question to begin conducting himself immediately in the lifestyle that you require of him. The coming weeks should serve as a sort of trial period for him and for you.

May Hashem, who oversees each and every one with Hashgacha Pratis, guide you on the path of good, in a way that is good and revealed.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 8957

8957

B"H, 29 Kislev, 5718
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter of 16/12, in which you write that you have been offered several shidduchim, but when the matter nears completion, nothing comes of it, and you ask for the reason for this and what you should do.

In most cases, this is because there is no true resolve to build a Jewish home after the wedding on the foundations of Torah and mitzvos. Therefore, Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, waits for more time, perhaps in the interim you will recognize the absolute truth: that it is essential that the marriage and the life thereafter be based on the foundations of our Torah, the Torah of life. It is understood that the primary elements of this are the observance of the laws of taharas hamishpacha, Shabbos, and the kashrus of food, etc. When you resolve this truly and with the necessary strength—that even if there are difficulties, you will conduct yourself as is fitting for a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah—Hashem will provide you with your suitable match before you.

Furthermore, in order to hasten the blessing, set aside every weekday morning a small amount of money for hachnasas kallah (helping poor brides), and also recite a prayer, Shema Yisrael, and the like. If you are unable to recite the prayer in Lashon HaKodesh, you may recite it in a language you understand.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

P.S.
In my secretariat, we do not write in French, which is why this response is in Lashon HaKodesh. However, you may continue to write in French in the future, as I am able to read that language.

## 8959

B"H, 1 Teves, 5718.
Brooklyn.

N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in the city of Cleveland, Kinsman branch,
May Hashem grant them life.

Blessings and peace!

Your contribution for the *magbis* of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, the liberation day of our Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, for the benefit of the Shikun Chabad in our Holy Land—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu—has been received, and the receipt is enclosed.

May Hashem Yisbarach help that for many years to come, you should be able to engage in matters of *mitzvos* in an ever-increasing manner. This is indeed the instruction of the days of Chanukah: that each day, one must add more light.

This is to be done without regard for what is happening "in the street," which is also a lesson from Chanukah: that we kindle the lights specifically *mishtashkeiah hachamah* (when the sun has set) and *b'chutz* (outside)—meaning, when the sun has already set and it is already dark in the street.

Furthermore, just as in those first days of the original Chanukah miracle, it was seen that according to the natural order, the light could last no more than one day—as there was only enough oil for that long—yet through the strong *bitachon* that the Yidden of that time had in Hashem Yisbarach, the light from that small amount of oil lasted for eight full days, until new oil was prepared to continue illuminating further and further.

So too in our time, through a strong sense of *emunah* and firm *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach—who is the Creator of the world and directs the world—Yidden can accomplish that it should be bright for them and around them, both *b'gashmius* and *b'ruchnius*, even more and far more than what the calculation according to the natural order would suggest.

And just as it was then, may you do this in good health and with joy.

With blessings to all the members of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad and their families, may they be blessed, for a bright Chanukah and to draw that light throughout the entire year, *b'soch k'lal Yisrael*.

## 8960

B"H, 1 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the first night of Chanukah, in which you write regarding a surgery to remove a gland, etc.

Regarding all matters of surgery—that is, an action that cannot be reversed—one must consult with experts in the field, at least two, and preferably three. I am certain that your father-in-law, may he live and be well, will not object to this; indeed, according to the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life, the opinion of two or three carries weight that is incomparable to the opinion of a single individual. Human reason also agrees with this, for a person, whoever he may be, is but a limited creature, and consulting with two or three together brings "salvation through many counselors." Since you wrote your letter and it was received and this response is being sent during the days of Chanukah—whose theme is "increasing and continuing" in light—may it be Hashem’s will that your fortune be illuminated with the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 8962

8962

B"H, Seventh Night of Chanukah, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
R' Yosef, may he live, known as Dr. Burg

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your letter confirming my letter of New Year’s blessings.

I am writing now to express my regret regarding the news I received: that you traveled to Kfar Chabad for the farbrengen of the auspicious day of Yud-Tes Kislev, but due to the crowding—and perhaps also due to a lack of order—you were unable to make your way through the crowd. Subsequently, the chairman of the village committee went to clear a path for you so that you could ascend the stage, but for some reason, you did not wish to do so. It is understandable that this causes me distress from two perspectives: first, on behalf of the crowd gathered there, who surely would have benefited from your words of hisorerus had you not declined; and—if you will forgive me for adding—also on your own account. For if our Sages have said that the Shechinah rests among every ten Jews—as explained by the master of the celebration of Yud-Tes Kislev, our Alter Rebbe, even when they are not speaking words of Torah at that moment (see Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 23, for wondrous words on this)—how much more so in a gathering of many tens of Jews where, certainly, words of Torah were heard, especially when they are permeated with light and warmth. And words that come from the heart enter the heart. There are many levels within the heart itself: the external, the internal, and the essence of the internal (in the language of the Alter Rebbe: the illumination of the point of the heart and the essence of the point of the heart—*Likutei Torah, Tetzaveh 36a, column 1*). This is all the more true for a Chassidishe farbrengen, where the participants strive for the deepest possible level of inwardness, and often succeed in this. This is especially true in light of what you mentioned in our conversation, that you have joined the family of the Rav through your wife, may she live, which adds further weight to all of the above.

Although one does not cry over the past, this naturally does not exempt me from expressing my reaction, and the main point is to negate, or at least weaken, the background from which the aforementioned situation grew. I am referring to your reaction to the lack of order, or whatever one might call it. This is relevant for the future as well, since all Jews are responsible for one another, and the action of one individual affects all other Jews—in the manner of the witticism of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that a person sneezing at the North Pole affects all the inhabitants of the world.

Events are orchestrated to coincide with similar days. I received this news during the days of Chanukah, the mitzvah of which is to increase light—and there can be no light without warmth—in a manner that is "increasing and continuing" and spreading, and such warmth precludes even the possibility of the aforementioned reaction.

With respect and blessings for Chanukah.

It appears from snippets of news that the time is approaching for discussion regarding... a "united front," but one does not mix "one joy with another," and there is still time for that. Despite the disappointment regarding the effectiveness of my letters on this matter in the past, the Chassidishe adage is well known: one must try again and again; and in truth, it is a law in the Torah, in the language of our Sages, "even up to a hundred times."

## 5863

B"H, 2 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It has been a very long time since we have received any letters from you. This is especially concerning, as your last letter from 9 Tammuz was written in what appeared to be an undesirable state of mind—and I must permit myself to say, not at all in a Chassidishe spirit. As is explained at length in Chassidus, sadness is fundamentally rejected, and even bitterness is only appropriate at specific, temporary times, and so on. May it be the will of Hashem that the influence of these days be drawn down upon the entire year, from the "secret of secrets" down to the revealed Torah, and the action that comes from this study, in accordance with the ruling of our Torah that the oil permeates everywhere, to fulfill that which is written, "You shall be wholehearted," with the revealed, the hidden, and the action all together.

With blessings for good tidings and for success in your holy avodah,

**M. Schneerson**

## 5866

5866

By the grace of G-d, 2 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi Shalom Yechezkel Shraga, Shlita

Greetings and blessings,

I was pleased to receive your letter, though it arrived during days of burdens added to the usual burdens—which, unfortunately, are not all burdens of joy. Although even a burden of joy prevents the necessary study, I have nevertheless, due to your request, stolen time to review the matter cursorily, as noted below.

May it be the will of G-d that the bright day of 19 Kislev—the day of victory and redemption for the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and the teachings of Chabad—continue to influence the entire year. As the Rebbe Rashab, father of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote in his famous *Iggeres HaKodesh* regarding 19 Kislev being the Rosh Hashanah for Chassidus, which our holy ancestors bequeathed to us, and which is the very teaching of the Baal Shem Tov; and in proximity to the days of Chanukah, which are eight (see the responsa of the Rashba, siman 9, regarding the virtue of specifically eight days, and this is well understood based on the *maamar* of Chanukah by the Baal HaTanya printed in *Torah Or* 34:3), where the candle and the mitzvah are in the oil, the "secret of secrets" of the Torah as explained in the holy Zohar—may this influence the entire year, from the "secret of secrets" down to the revealed Torah and the practical action that comes from this study. And as our Torah rules, the oil permeates everywhere, to fulfill what is written: "You shall be wholehearted," [uniting] the revealed, the hidden, and the action, all together.

With respect and blessing,

P.S. As requested, the *kuntres* is returned herewith.

**Notes regarding the matter itself:**
To read the *Parshah* of the *Nesi’im* (at the beginning of Nissan) from a Torah scroll—my father-in-law, the Rebbe, did not follow this custom, nor did he follow the custom of *Shnayim Mikra V’Echad Targum* (even though it is brought in the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe (285:4) that it is good to read *Shnayim Mikra* from a kosher Torah scroll). It is known that the customs of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, were like the customs of his father, and even higher in holiness. And our Sages have already said: "Every river has its own course."

**Regarding the question itself:**
For those who do read the *Parshah* of the *Nesi’im* from a Torah scroll—is it correct to attach this reading to the public Torah reading on Shabbos, using the same scroll—meaning, to scroll it to *Parshas Nasso*—in order to minimize the carrying of a Torah scroll? Even though you did not mention this, it is understood that the doubt applies also to Rosh Chodesh Nissan and to Mondays and Thursdays.

For the aforementioned reason, in my humble opinion, this should not be done:
1) It appears as an addition to the public Torah reading. Although we do add [extra] people to be called up, we do not find anywhere that one may add to the reading itself. Even though there is a sign (even for those entering in the middle) that it is not a mandatory reading because one does not recite a blessing (afterward), we find instances even in mandatory readings where one does not recite a blessing (*Shaarei Ephraim* 8:27).
2) One does not scroll a Torah scroll in public unless there is no other choice (*Orach Chaim* 144).

However, perhaps one could attempt to find a basis for leniency:
1) After all, what prohibition is there to add to a mandatory reading? In the Priestly Blessing, a specific teaching is required to state that one may not add (*Rosh Hashanah* 28b). Just as there is a rationale there to add [blessings] because it is a requirement to recite them, here too it is a matter of Torah study. (It is understood that this is only if one does not add blessings and does not burden the congregation.)

A sort of proof that we do add is that for the public Torah reading, it is sufficient to complete the Torah in three and a half years (as in the West (*Yam Shel Shlomo*, end of *Bava Kamma*)), yet the simple custom is to complete it in one year. However, there is a counter-proof from the fact that on Simchas Torah we repeat the same *parshah* several times, but we do not add from the previous *parshah*.

See the responsa of my father-in-law, the Tzemach Tzedek, *Choshen Mishpat* (at the end), that it is preferable to read something new, etc. (This can be refuted, as the intention may be that the reading must be in the context of blessings). There is also proof to prohibit this from the discussions and conditions regarding completing the public Torah reading, where the congregation was stringent (the opinions are collected in *Shaarei Ephraim* 7:16). They did not say that in any case one should read without a blessing, as one completes *Shnayim Mikra* until Simchas Torah. This requires further study. I will not elaborate.

2) In the responsa *Nehar Afarsimon* (cited in *Shaarei Rachamim* on *Shaarei Ephraim* 7:23), it says that one may scroll a Torah scroll in public to avoid carrying it. But this can be refuted: that is only when the congregation itself benefits from avoiding the carrying of the Torah—similar to what the *Magen Avraham* writes in 144:7. This is not the case here.

If there were a benefit—but regarding the concern of carrying the Torah in the aforementioned manner—i.e., within the synagogue itself—for those who do carry a Torah scroll for the reading of the *Parshah* of the *Nesi’im*, one must conclude that the concern does not exist at all, since they are carrying the Torah for a reading that is merely a custom, and a custom not brought in the *Shulchan Aruch* or *Rema*.

Therefore, for them, it is only from house to house that one does not carry it. See *Zohar* Vol. III 71b: from the synagogue, and certainly to the street.

In *Shaarei Rachamim* there (22), he cites the opinion that from room to room there is not even much concern regarding carrying.

3) And the main point, in my humble opinion: In general, one should not read the *Parshah* of the *Nesi’im* before *Mussaf*, for the reading is a remembrance and a stimulus to offer their sacrifices, and the *Mussaf* sacrifice, which is constant and holy, precedes the sacrifices of the *Nesi’im*.

To attach the reading of the *Parshah* of the *Nesi’im* to the *Mincha* reading is questionable—aside from the above—also regarding the *Kaddish*.

**Some notes on your *kuntres*:**
Page 1: You explain the reason for reading the *Parshah* of the *Nesi’im* from a Torah scroll is because we read *Shnayim Mikra* from a Torah scroll. It is understood that they are different, for the reading of *Shnayim Mikra* is a requirement of the Gemara, unlike the *Parshah* of the *Nesi’im*.

There is also a fundamental difference—for the reading of *Shnayim Mikra* has a connection to the public Torah reading, as the Rambam says, copied in the *Shulchan Aruch* 285:1: "Even though a person hears the entire Torah every Shabbos in public, he is obligated to read *Shnayim Mikra*..." (and according to the Ra’avan, he is only obligated if he did not hear it in public)—and therefore it is appropriate to equate it also regarding the matter of reading from a Torah scroll. See also the *Taz* 285:1.

Page 9: That one should not read before *Mussaf* because of the burden on the congregation. It is questionable whether this reason applies here, since the congregation praying in this synagogue already follows the custom of reading the *Parshah* of the *Nesi’im*. What additional burden is there? And those who separate themselves from the congregation in this—it is questionable if one should encourage and strengthen them in this separation by delaying the aforementioned reading.

Similarly, what you wrote to delay it until after *Mussaf*, as they delayed [the reading of the Megillah] on *V’Hayah Lachem* (see *Shulchan Aruch* 692)—for this reason, one should delay the reading of the *Parshah* of the *Nesi’im* until after the meal or even until *Mincha*. Just as regarding *V’Hayah Lachem*.

And for its reasons.

Pages 9-11: I see again that you mention the matter that it appears as an addition to the mandatory public Torah reading, and also that one does not scroll in public—and I wrote about this above.

Regarding a "new decree"—note also the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, *Orach Chaim* 661:10 (based on the *Magen Avraham* there). [One must conclude from what is written in 662:8: "A decree lest..." See the *Beis Yosef* there]. In any case, what is written in *Beis Shlomo* is the opposite of what is written in the early and later authorities. See also *Ikarei HaDat* for *Orach Chaim* 1, cited in *Sdei Chemed*, *Ma’areches Rosh Hashanah*.

- Due to a reason, the sending of this letter was delayed, and I ask for your forgiveness.

## 8867

[3 Teves, 5718]

It was with great pleasure that I received your letter in which you write about the farbrengen of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, the day of the redemption of Rabbeinu HaZaken. As our Nesi’im, our holy Rebbes, call this day the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, and on Rosh Hashanah we say "May you be inscribed and sealed for a good year," so too regarding 19 Kislev in relation to the aforementioned matters. For one of the ways of Chassidus is the avodah of Hashem Yisbarach with simcha and a good heart, and as per the exalted teaching of the Baal Shem Tov, which we heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, [the goal is] to serve Hashem Yisbarach with the body together, and not to push Him away through fasts and self-afflictions.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you should always report good tidings, in good health and with avodas Hashem in simcha and a good heart.

## 8968

8968

B"H, 6 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Committee for the Support of the Construction of the Mikveh in Kfar Chabad
In the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established speedily
May Hashem protect them and grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

I was pleased to learn of your efforts to support the construction of the mikveh in Kfar Chabad, which was founded and directed by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, so that they may be able to build and complete the structure as required, and to hasten its completion as soon as possible.

Certainly, all those who cherish Torah and mitzvos do not require an explanation of the magnitude and importance of this matter; what greater proof do we need than the well-known halachic ruling that one may sell a Sefer Torah to provide for the construction of a mikveh taharah.

Nothing is needed now but prioritization and alacrity in providing the aforementioned assistance, especially in light of what is explained in Iggeres HaKodesh by our Alter Rebbe, Epistle 21, regarding the great virtue of alacrity in all mitzvos. This applies particularly to this mitzvah, which also contains an aspect of tzedakah and acts of chesed, as explained in Iggeres HaKodesh there. It is well known how much our Sages of blessed memory praised this quality, even when it involves advancing the matter by a single day (Eruvin 63b). This is especially true in our generation, the *ikvesa d'Meshicha*, as the end of our exile draws near (as is well known from the explanations of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on many occasions). For purity brings about, etc., Eliyahu HaNavi, who heralds our redemption, and through *is'arusa d'lesata* comes *is'arusa d'le'eila*, and the fulfillment of the promise: "And I will take you... and I will sprinkle clean water upon you, and you shall be purified... and you shall dwell in the land... and you shall be My people, and I will be your G-d."

With blessings for success in your holy work, with abundance,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9965

B"H, 7 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Mr. Hillel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 5 Teves, in which you ask why, regarding the number of the ten Sefiros, there are two ways of counting them: Chabad (Chochma, Binah, Da’as) or Chacham-Binah-Da’as, Chesed-Gevurah-Tiferes, Netzach-Hod-Yesod-Malchus.

The crux of the matter is the well-known concept in Kabbalah: when Keter is counted, Da’as is not counted. This matter is explained in various places in the teachings of Chassidus, among them in Likutei Torah by the Alter Rebbe, Parshas Shelach, page 49c.

2) Regarding your question as to what is the essence of the Chabad Chassidic approach, etc. — it is understood that such questions cannot be answered in a letter, especially since these matters are already explained in printed works. You should refer to *Kuntres Toras HaChassidus* and *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus* by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

You are surely aware of the three daily study cycles—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which are incumbent upon every soul. In any event, you should observe them from this point forward.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

#### ***9965***

**Hillel:** David, Baltimore.

## 9872

B"H, 7 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

I received with pleasure your letter of 1 Teves, regarding the arrangements for the farbrengens of the Chag HaGeulah, 19 Kislev, and those preceding and following it. I was very pleased to see that you have apparently begun to bring students from other yeshivos to these farbrengens, in a manner of "increasing and continuing." For this is the very essence of "every candle is to illuminate," and all the more so for an institution that produces students who are "candles to illuminate," with the intent of lighting the candles at the entrance of one's home—the content of which is the drawing down of light to the outside—and furthermore, specifically in a manner of "increasing and continuing." And if in times past, when there was opposition in certain circles, this was the case, then certainly now, in place of opposition, there has begun a search, an investigation, and a demand for the inner dimension of Torah and its matters (even if many of those searching do not yet know that it is this which they are seeking, similar to the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that when the body is hungry for bread, the inner reality is that it is because the soul is hungry for the Divine spark, for the "utterance of Hashem" that is within the bread).

It is understood that in addition to the above, there is also the greatest benefit in the participation of various baalei batim in a farbrengen in such an atmosphere, the value of which is also exceedingly great. But the primary focus remains on the first point—as this is a fundamental task of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, and this is simple to understand. And since the merit of the many assists them, they will certainly succeed in this as well, provided only that it is done in a manner of "you have labored"—for this is the requirement in all matters of holiness.

With a blessing for success in your holy work and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 8973

B"H, 7 Teves, 5718

May it be the will of Hashem that just as you have emerged into the expanse through the kindness of the Ribono shel Olam, the promise of our Sages—that all who do good for Him will be rewarded with long days and years—be fulfilled for you and your wife, in goodness that is visible and revealed.

At a time of favor, I will mention you and all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzkllh"h, nbg"m, zy"a, for whatever each one requires, in accordance with the content of your letter. May Hashem redeem all those who were or are still in distress, speedily in our days, with kindness and mercy and with an abundance of joy, taking a leading part in all that they require. For their preservation of Yiddishkeit and Chassidus was under terrifying conditions and in a state of extreme distress and constriction. Yet, it is only through the inwardness of Torah—which connects the inner and essential soul with the innerness of the Ein Sof, His essence and being, which is beyond time and place, even in the most sublime levels—that even in the deepest depths, the *Eisan* is drawn down, with all three aspects of the *Eisan*: *yashan*, *hart*, *shtark* (as explained at length in the maamar *Maskil L'Eisan HaEzrachi* by our Alter Rebbe and its commentaries). And ultimately, their side is victorious, leading to a revealed victory in goodness that is visible and revealed.

As is known, the Baal Shem Tov’s interpretation of the verse, "My soul thirsts for You... in a dry and weary land without water—so I have beheld You in the Sanctuary."

With blessings for a successful settlement, both physically and spiritually, with proper health and with good tidings.

## 8974

B”H, 7 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 7 Chanukah, and in accordance with your request, the reply is being sent without waiting for its turn.

You ask regarding the fact that good and even excellent proposals are coming up concerning shidduchim, and whether one should take into account what is found in certain seforim regarding the calculation of names, etc.

Behold, we have only the words of our Sages in such matters, which are based on what is stated: "You shall be wholehearted with Hashem your G-d." In matters of shidduchim in particular—of which it is said, **"And from Hashem** is an intelligent wife"—one must increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos and evaluate the proposal based on the observance of the faith and its matters, so that she will be an intelligent, G-d-fearing woman. And as for one who is not particular about everything mentioned in the sefer you cite, it is **obvious and self-evident** that we do not concern ourselves with it. Especially since, regarding books like those you mention in your letter, there is great doubt whether they are authoritative; it is possible that they were said only for their specific place and community, etc., etc. This is all the more so given the warnings of Rabbi Yehuda HeChassid, regarding which many of the clauses are said to be as mentioned above—that they were said only for his descendants, even though the masters of Kabbalah have relied upon Rabbi Yehuda HeChassid. And if all the above was said even in earlier times, how much more so now, when there are many concealments and hidden matters regarding shidduchim—that apart from the **specific** injunctions of Rabbi Yehuda HeChassid and the like, one should not be particular at all*. If the proposal is good and excellent according to Torah and yiras shamayim, he should conclude it, and may it be at a good and successful hour.

With blessings.

#### ***8974***

Printed in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 461.

*) And one should be particular about the matter of the Mishnah, "At eighteen for the chuppah," and the well-known words of our Sages (Kiddushin 29b, Pesachim 113a, and elsewhere), which are certainly authoritative and were said for all communities, etc.

## 9975

B"H, 8 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from 5 Kislev, which was received recently (having apparently been sent via regular mail), in which you write about your desire for hiskashrus, at the very least by way of correspondence, etc.

It is well known that the connection between two of Bnei Yisrael increases their capacity more than twofold, as is known from our Sages on this (Sotah 34a). The true hiskashrus is that of the neshamah, as explained in what our Rabbeinu HaZaken wrote in his Tanya, Chapter 32. Regarding matters of Torah and mitzvos—since our Torah is one Torah, and the essence of it and the essence of the mitzvos is to draw down that "Hashem is One and His Name is One," even here on earth, in earthly matters (see Iggeres HaKodesh of Rabbeinu HaZaken, Epistle 9)—in this, physical location is no barrier. My intention is that when this hiskashrus is expressed through an increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos in general, and specifically in the "light" within them that has been revealed in our generations through the teachings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs, this is a true hiskashrus. It goes without saying that an increase in Torah and mitzvos increases the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam in whatever a person and his household require, both materially and spiritually. This is especially true for one who serves in holy work, such as the profession of a shochet, which requires an extraordinary degree of yiras shamayim, as explained in many places, including by the Alter Rebbe and the Tzemach Tzedek, as detailed in their Shulchan Aruch and responsa. And there is nothing that can stand before the will.

You are surely aware of the three daily study cycles—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which we heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that they are appropriate for every person and are a segulah for many matters.

## 5976

B"H, 8 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh with the enclosure, in which you write about the discussions and the back-and-forth... We have been given an absolute promise, as recorded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of the Mitteler Rebbe (regarding the Alter Rebbe), that because of his mesiras nefesh for the teachings of Chassidus, it was decreed in the Heavenly Beis Din that in every matter of Torah, yiras shamayim, and good character traits, the hand of those who are his followers and walk in his footsteps will be uppermost. It is obvious that there is no room at all for the spirit of fear, chas v'shalom, in which the lines in your letter are written. You have already seen in the past that there were many concealments and obstructions no less significant than these—and, on the contrary, even greater—yet "ours was victorious," because this is the necessity of the time: to spread the wellsprings outward. This is especially true among our Sephardic brethren, may they live, who a few generations ago were renowned for praise and glory. Due to the pressures of the times, the situation changed significantly for the worse, which only further increases the merit of all those who restore the crown to its former glory. This is especially true regarding the light and the inner dimension of Torah that has been revealed in our generation through the teachings of Chassidus, which several generations ago was the heritage of the Sephardim—the study of the Zohar and matters of Kabbalah. There is no need to elaborate on such a simple matter.

It gave me special pleasure to read about the farbrengen of the auspicious day of Yud-Tes Kislev and the completion of the Shas that followed during Chanukah. The connection between these two matters is understood in its simplest sense, for the miracle of Chanukah was with oil—the "secret of secrets"—and specifically at the entrance of one’s house, on the outside; that is, the "secret of secrets" within the intellect that is found on the outside, the intellect of the nefesh habehamis.

May it be the will of Hashem that the matters of Yud-Tes Kislev, which is the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus—and as the precise wording indicates, "Rosh" (head) and not "techilah" (beginning), for the head contains within it and draws vitality to all the limbs of the body, i.e., the days of the year—should be drawn into them in a revealed and manifest good.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 9777

B"H, 8 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

The point of this is that in all their goings and comings, it should be evident that these are the goings and comings of one for whom the inner dimension of Torah—the Torah of Chassidus—permeates every place, just like oil. My hope is strong that they are elevating themselves through this, for this is holy work. **And certainly**, if there are others who are qualified for this, they should be added to the previous ones... ## 5979

B"H, 9 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

After the longest of intervals, your letter of 27 Kislev—the month of redemption—was received, in which you write regarding the activities in connection with the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, the festival of victory and redemption of our Alter Rebbe and all those who are connected and bound to him. May it be the will of Hashem that this should effect an *hisorerus* for the entire year, in thought, speech, and action, in your daily life.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you, and all those who are involved in this, to remain in connection with the participants of the *farbrengen* even afterwards. As is explained in other places, a *farbrengen* is akin to plowing and sowing, and at most, the beginning of the harvest—but the main harvest must come afterwards, and *kal v'chomer* (it is understood).

Regarding what you wrote about setting the date for your sister’s wedding (may she live and be well) for the month of Menachem Av, the length of time is surprising, especially since the *chassan* and *kallah* are in the same city. Furthermore, regarding the actual matter of setting it for Menachem Av: even in months such as these, it is better to have it at the beginning of Tammuz than on any day in the month of Av.

[One may note the *Tosafos* at the end of *Megillah* and the *Shu"t Chasam Sofer*, *Orach Chaim* siman 160; and even though others have questioned him on this, nevertheless, what concern is it of ours, etc.] Regarding a case such as this, the earlier it is, the more praiseworthy, and *kal v'chomer*.

Regarding what you wrote about the couple’s place of residence after the wedding, *b'sha'ah tovah u'mutzlach* (in a good and successful hour), the matter is correct—in a place and city where the cost of housing is inexpensive, or at least relatively inexpensive.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

A. Quint
Secretary

## 9880

B”H, 11 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 6 Teves, along with the enclosure, in which you write regarding your older brother-in-law, may he live, concerning what occurred after the purchase of the second car.

Now, I do not know the customs of the circle to which he belongs according to your letter, but it seems to me, from what I have heard, that in that place the matter of a woman driving a car is **strongly** discouraged. Although in other observant circles there is a different perspective on this, it is a well-known principle of Torah that in the place of a Rav, one must conduct oneself according to the ruling of that Rav, and in the place of Shmuel, according to Shmuel. From this it is understandable that the publicity surrounding this matter—that the car belongs to the woman—and as it appears, efforts were made to publicize this for the reason you wrote, has only exacerbated the situation of not conducting oneself according to the custom of the circle to which he belongs, both in the past and in the present. And this is possibly the cause of the incident.

If so, the *tikkun* is to publicize the opposite (and this is easy, since the fact is indeed that she does not use the car). However, in matters of *tikkun*, one must add beyond what was previously done. As explained in the letter of our Alter Rebbe, *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, Chapter 9, it is appropriate that he give approximately a fifth of what he paid and will pay for the car to *tzedakah* that is specifically connected with *yiras shamayim*. May Hashem grant him success.

With blessings for good tidings.

P.S.

Since every matter is by *hashgachah pratis*, and the aforementioned person turned to me through you, it is simple that while I understand less about car matters than about matters of Torah and *yiras shamayim*, yet he asks me about this, so I also answer regarding matters of Torah: that he should have taken upon himself to observe—*bli neder*—the *shiurim* of *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya* that we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzuklalah”h, nbg”m, zy”a*, that they are appropriate for every soul. Consequently, it is irrelevant to which *chug* (circle) he may belong, and this is obvious. Surely you will find the appropriate words to explain this to him, although it does not require much explanation.

## 8981

B"H, 11 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, man of action, etc.,
R' Elchanan, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Erev Chanukah, which reached me the day before yesterday, along with the complete book *Marganita D'Rabbanan*. Many thanks for this response and for your thoughtfulness in sending the book to me. May it be the will of Hashem that you gather strength for the sake of Torah, to increase and glorify it. This encompasses the study of Torah from the most basic level up to the ultimate perfection—the study of young children (see Rambam, *Hilchos Talmud Torah*, end of chapter 2). In the words of our Alter Rebbe, this applies even if it is not yet *lishmah*, but rather from the "fear of the strap in the hand of the teacher" (*Tanya*, 155a). This is in line with the teaching that study is superior because it leads to action (*Chullin* 66b). In our generation, this is the essential point of the aforementioned commandment and necessity: to bring together the two "woods" in the Torah—the Tree of Life and the Tree of Knowledge—to bring them close, one to the other, etc., "and they shall become one in your hand" (see *Zohar*, Vol. III, 126b and 157a). This is explained according to the teachings of Chabad Chassidus in the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of our Alter Rebbe, Epistle 26, and in his *Likkutei Torah*, *Parshas Shelach* 42b and onwards, until "the wellsprings spread outward," and the prophecy is fulfilled: "As I am written, so am I read"—the unity of the revealed and the hidden of the Ribono shel Olam.

With respect and blessings,

P.S.
As is my custom, out of affection for the matter, although time does not permit, I looked through the book in haste and glanced at the notes in the margins.

1) At the beginning of the book, on the verse "And there was light":
Seemingly, the novelty in the explanation of the matter requires study, as this is the very point of our Sages in *Bereishis Rabbah* 42:4, which is noted at the beginning of the commentary.
Likewise, regarding what is written that the light that was hidden is the light of the sun, etc.—which is brought in many places—the light created on the first day and the light of the sun are two separate matters. This is also proven by the fact that the light of the sun was "hidden in its sheath" (and in the future, Hashem will take the sun out of its sheath), whereas the "hidden light" is that which is said to have been hidden for the future (though, of course, this precision has its resolution).

2) At the end of the book, regarding the "Eighteen" [curses], etc., and based on the teaching of the "seventy faces of Torah":
This is based on the teaching of our Sages that "Israel will perform teshuvah, and then King Moshiach will come" (though they differ as to the manner in which they perform teshuvah—*Sanhedrin* 97b). Through the first seventeen curses, the performance of teshuvah is extremely difficult, because even those who do perform teshuvah for their own matters are, by virtue of the concept of *arvus* (mutual responsibility), guarantors for all of Israel, for they had the power to protest. And even those who did protest, our Sages said, were only heard to the extent of a rebuke, a reprimand, or a curse. And even though it is revealed and known before Him that if they had protested, the others would not have accepted it from them, it must be "revealed" to them—as in the story of our Sages (*Shabbos* 55a). To rectify this, Yeshayahu the Prophet **publicized** "The youth shall act insolently against the elder," so that it would be revealed to them as well that they would not be accepted, and thus this claim is nullified. Based on the above, his mind was put at ease, since this matter rectifies the consequences of **all seventeen** that preceded it. Through this, one can also understand the precision of our Sages, that when they perform teshuvah, they are redeemed **immediately**, as stated by the Rambam in *Hilchos Teshuvah*, chapter 7, halacha 5, and in the words of our Alter Rebbe in his *Iggeres HaTeshuvah*, chapter 11.

***

**R' Elchanan:** Heilperin, London.

**This encompasses:** See also above, Vol. 13, Epistle 4328, and the references noted there.

**Eighteen:** "Yeshayahu cursed them with eighteen curses, and his mind was not put at ease until he said to them this verse: 'The youth shall act insolently against the elder,' etc." (*Chagigah* 14a).

## 8984

Recently, I learned that in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established), a *Treasury of Parables and Aphorisms from Medieval Literature* by Prof. Davidson was published by Mossad Harav Kook, containing more than three thousand aphorisms (along with their histories—that is, various versions with similar content). Since, in my opinion, the aforementioned number is quite small, there is certainly room for someone who merits it to distinguish himself in this field. I would be interested to know if you are working on the aforementioned project; if so, you should certainly first examine the published book by Prof. Davidson for the purpose of comparison and supplementation.

With blessings,

P.S. Enclosed is a check for the shipping expenses.

## 989

B"H, 14 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Following the long silence, your letter was received. It is understood that regarding what you write about the "evil of the decree" and so forth, it is simple that one must uproot such thoughts and the like: a) because they have no basis; b) as is known from the adage taught by our Rebbes, the Nesi'im, generation after generation: "Think good and it will be good"; c) according to the known litmus test for a person’s conduct in a place of doubt—whether a thing is desirable or not—is to observe the influence of the matter on one's actions and deeds. We see tangibly that thoughts such as these (regarding the "evil of the decree") lead to a weakening in good deeds, to sadness, despair, and so on—things that are forbidden and rejected, not only from the perspective of holy intellect but even from the perspective of human intellect.

Instead of this, in my opinion, it is a holy **obligation** upon all members of the family to strive and strive again so that the descendants of the deceased... may they rest in peace, will walk in the path of Torah and mitzvos in their **daily lives**... It is understood that **this is** the great essential. And this is not only regarding themselves, but also regarding the deceased; it is incomparably more important than printed eulogies or speeches at public gatherings. Certainly, there is no need for proof of such a simple matter, nor for its explanation...

## 8990

B"H, 14 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote about the trip to Teveria and the positive and negative aspects involved.

With all due respect, it is like a merchant calculating the accounts of opening a business: he must invest in renting the premises and purchasing the merchandise—let us say, one hundred zuz—but if he does not open the business, there is no possibility of earning a hundred times that amount. For in our world, there is no endeavor that does not require an investment—whether of soul-powers, physical strength, or money—and this is the very capacity to earn many times over. Such a calculation applies as well to this trip; that is, the temporary discomfort involved in traveling to the hot springs of Teveria is negligible compared to the potential to earn many times over, and to gain long, good years that will come about as a result of this trip. If only you had traveled last year! But one does not cry over the past; I mention this only as proof that this trip is not merely permissible and outweighs the negative aspects you mention, but is actually desirable—even for the sake of those who might suffer for a short while due to this trip.

With blessings for good news and a healthy winter in every respect.

## 9990

16 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Pinchas Steinwaks
Shalom u’Bracha,

In connection with what Rabbi Hodakov conveyed to me regarding his conversation with you, I am writing this letter now, despite the many letters preceding this matter that are awaiting a response. I begin with thanks.

Acknowledgment of receipt and thanks for your book, *Yidden Tzum Gedenken*. May it be His will that, in accordance with the purpose of the concept of remembrance—which must connect a person to the matters he brings to mind, a connection that should lead to an influence upon him—the memory of these individuals about whom you write will also influence the readers of the book to continue in the same path that these *Yidden tzum gedenken* walked: a path of life in the spirit of our ancestors.

***

Regarding your question and comment in the conversation with Rabbi Hodakov:

1) The position regarding the problem of the **name**—*Eretz Yisrael* or *Medinat Yisrael*—is well known. I emphasize the **problem of the name**, for we are not discussing anything other than the establishment of the name.

It is this:
There is no room for doubt, once the name was established from of old by the G-d of Israel, as stated in the Torah in the prophecy of Yechezkel: "In the visions of G-d, He brought me to the land of Israel" (40:2), and elsewhere.

Our Sages of blessed memory in their Mishnah, Gemara, and Midrash likewise call this holy land by this name (or by the name **HaAretz**—the special land, as in the expression of the verse, "When you come to the land"). It is understood and simple that, like all matters established by the Creator of the world and its Guide—the matters of Torah and its *mitzvos*—this name, too, is not in the hands of man to change or replace with the name *Medinat Yisrael*, even if the majority were to agree to it, for this is not a matter for a vote.

The rejection of a vote on a matter of Torah is a fundamental principle, and this is not merely a *pilpul* about a word or expression. There is also a point regarding the **practical** aspect that highlights the difference between the two names: the Kingdom of the Khazars (after they converted) was a *medinah* (state) of Israel, but it was not *Eretz Yisrael*.

I am precise in every place where the matter is mentioned in my name that the name used should be the one called by the Torah—this traditional name of some three thousand years.

2) The concept of *yishuv Eretz Yisrael* (settling the Land of Israel) and the concept of *shivat Tzion* (the return to Zion) are, it is understood, separate. The fact that some confuse them and exchange one for the other has brought, and continues to bring, many confusions, incorrect conclusions, and more.

*Yishuv Eretz Yisrael* is a matter in the Torah; some say it applies during the time of the Beis Hamikdash and when Israel is on its land, and some say it applies even during the time of *galus*. *Shivat Tzion*—as it literally means—is a matter connected with the *geulah* from *galus*. It is understood that this applies only after the destruction, for it is the matter of the "return."

For this concept, too, is not new, nor did we acquire it from the ownerless. It was established long ago in the Torah (Tehillim 126:1).

These are the words of the great teacher, our Rambam, in his *Mishneh Torah* regarding *shivat Tzion* (*Hilchos Melachim*, Chapter 11): "The King Moshiach will arise and restore the kingdom of David to its former state, to its original sovereignty; he will build the Beis Hamikdash and gather the dispersed of Israel, etc. The Torah testified about him, as it is said: 'And Hashem your G-d will return your captivity and have mercy on you, and He will return and gather you, etc.'" And at the end of the chapter: "He will arise, a king from the house of David, meditating on the Torah and occupied with *mitzvos* like David his father, according to the Written Torah and the Oral Torah, and he will compel all of Israel to walk in it and strengthen its breaches, etc., and he will build the Beis Hamikdash in its place and gather the dispersed of Israel, etc."

The precision of the Rambam in every single word in his *Mishneh Torah* is well known, as is the **order** of the matters in terms of priority and sequence. As stated, the order according to the ruling of the Torah is that first, King Moshiach will arise and restore the kingdom; afterwards, he will build the Beis Hamikdash; and afterwards, he will gather the dispersed of Israel. This is the promise in the Torah: "And He will return and gather you, etc., if your outcasts are at the ends of the heavens, etc., and Hashem will bring you." As mentioned in the previous section, a ruling in the Torah is not a matter for a vote or for a decision based on the opinion of the majority.

There are many statements of our Sages that substantiate and expand upon what is said above, but I have chosen the ruling in the book of *halacha* that is accepted by all our people, the Children of Israel, and which, as stated, is extremely precise in its expression and order.

It is surely unnecessary to emphasize the common denominator in what was said above and in what we have spoken of since regarding the Transjordan (and the borders of *Eretz Yisrael* in general): that it is a part of *Eretz Yisrael* and a part of the *geulah* of the people of Israel.

For it is forbidden—and also impossible—to relinquish the name *Eretz Yisrael*, even if they propose to replace it with the name *Medinat Yisrael*. It is forbidden—and also impossible—to relinquish the concept of *shivat Tzion*, even if they propose to replace it with the concept of *yishuv Eretz Yisrael*, even when the settlement is by thousands upon thousands. It is forbidden—and also impossible—to relinquish any part of *Eretz Yisrael* whatsoever, even if the majority were to agree to it.

We have been promised that it is precisely the refusal to relinquish that brings closer the end of the *galus*—the *galus* of the body and the *galus* of the soul—and will bring, finally, the *geulah*, our redemption and the salvation of our souls.

With respect and blessing.

## 9994

[17 Teves, 5718]

... It is surprising that you do not mention the farbrengen of the auspicious day of Yud-Tes Kislev.
