## 9995

18 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual United States celebration of the Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch Yeshiva network, may they live:

Peace and blessing!

On the occasion of this year’s celebration, which marks the sixtieth anniversary of the founding of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lubavitch and the eighteenth anniversary of its relocation to America, I extend my heartfelt greetings to the distinguished activists, guests of honor, and all those gathered, as well as to all friends of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim wherever they may be. I wish them abundant success in their work for the yeshiva, which in turn brings abundant success to their own personal affairs.

This year’s celebration takes place during the week leading up to the *histalkus* (24 Teves) of the Alter Rebbe, *Baal HaTanya v’HaShulchan Aruch*, the founder of the Chabad *shita* that animates the Lubavitcher yeshivos, their administration, *roshei yeshivos*, *mashpi'im*, and *talmidim*—may they live.

It is therefore timely to recall the famous teaching of the Alter Rebbe: "Jewish *gashmius* is *ruchnius*; Hashem gives us *gashmius* so that we may transform it into *ruchnius*."

This is the very concept of Zevulun and Yissachar, of those who study Torah and those who support Torah—that those who support the students of Torah have a share in the study of Torah itself. In fact, both aspects are encompassed in the name of the Lubavitcher yeshiva—**Tomchei Temimim**: it contains the ***talmidim temimim***, the students of Torah, and the ***tomchei*** *temimim*, those who sustain the yeshiva with their bodies and their means.

When Hashem gives a Yid *gashmius* (livelihood) and he utilizes it for the sake of *mitzvos* in general, and for *limud haTorah* in particular—for *talmud Torah* is equivalent to them all—by contributing and giving *tzedakah* to institutions of Torah—for *tzedakah* is also equivalent to all the *mitzvos*—he transforms *gashmius* into *ruchnius*.

And since all matters of *kedusha* must go "from strength to strength" (*meichayil el chayil*) and we must always ascend in holiness, one must create as much *ruchnius* as possible from one's *gashmius*. Consequently, the blessing "Give a tithe so that you may become wealthy" (*aser bishvil shetis'asher*) is fulfilled: Hashem gives ever more *gashmius*, and then one can create even more *ruchnius*, and thus one proceeds constantly from strength to strength—not only in quantity, but also in quality. Through this, one also gives the yeshiva the ability to advance more rapidly from strength to strength, to accept more and more *talmidim*, and to constantly improve the physical and spiritual state of all its details.

I hope that all friends of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch will be inspired in the aforementioned spirit; those who have already contributed will increase their support, and those who will contribute under the impression of this celebration will do so in the greatest measure. In this way, they will draw down upon themselves and their households, may they live, the blessings of Hashem, in a manner of "increasing and continuing" from strength to strength, in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius*.

With respect and blessing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 9996

9996

B"H, 18 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 4th and 14th of Teves and those preceding them, I was pleased to read in your latest letter that you are very satisfied to have merited being among the donors, etc. May it be the will of Hashem that in this, too, you will fulfill the teaching of our Sages, "We increase in holiness." Surely, Hashem will fulfill His promise, as our Sages taught, "Whoever adds, they add to him," for we have been informed that whatever Hashem commands Yisrael to do, He does Himself. May it be His will that in this, too, you will be a *Chassid*, and consequently, you will act in accordance with the *Mishnah* (Avos, Chapter 5, Mishnah 13), "There are four traits among those who give charity: He who wishes to give and wishes that others should give—is a *Chassid*."

In this regard, I would like to point out that regarding your concluding remark on the aforementioned matter—"If only I could fulfill through this, 'And break your sins with charity'"—while this hope is appropriate for those who focus on *mussar*, our Rebbes, our leaders, have taught us something greater: that one should not be satisfied with the aforementioned. For ultimately, this is only in the aspect of "turn from evil" (*sur meira*). Rather, one must pray and request, and with intensity, also in the aspect of "do good" (*asei tov*), to draw down through this light, vitality, and strength, both in physicality and in spirituality, and this is understood...

## 9898

B"H, 20 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and industrious,
R' Yisroel Sussman, may he live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

After a long interval, I received your letter of 15 Teves, in which you write with the utmost brevity regarding the farbrengens and the shiurim being studied. It is surprising to be so brief about something that can cause *nachas ruach*; as I have already written to several of *anash*, this too is included in the mitzvah of "Love your fellow as yourself."

Regarding what you wrote about the *nigun* of *Arba Bavos*, the times when it was customary to sing it are well known, as explained in various places and, I believe, in the introduction to *Sefer HaNigunim*. That is to say, at these times during Chassidic farbrengens, it is certainly sung.

As for your question whether there was a place to sing it at the specific farbrengen you mention, this depends on the *hergesh* of the heart of those gathered: whether they felt at this farbrengen something akin to the feeling of the farbrengens at the established times mentioned in the aforementioned *sichos*. For example, the custom to sing it at the conclusion of the 12 Tammuz farbrengen, as it is a continuation of the *geulah* of 19 Kislev and the like. However, regarding the *hergesh* of the heart, it is difficult to bring proof from one instance to another, especially from elders to the youth and vice versa, etc. There is room to say that the decision regarding this depends on the "touchstone" about which the Rebbe, my father-in-law, told a story (based on the well-known story regarding the righteous R' Menachem Nachum of Chernobyl, transcribed in *Hayom Yom*).

Regarding your question about the *Kaddishim* after *Uva L'Tzion*: if ten men did not remain, is it not brought in the *pask* (*Shulchan Aruch*, 56) and is it not the custom that we say *Kaddish* even if ten did not remain, when the *Kaddish* is a continuation of what preceded it, at which time there were ten in the *beis medrash*?

With blessings for good tidings in general and specific matters—for one is dependent upon the other—and with proper health.

## 8999

B”H, 22 Teves, 5718

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos.

It is regrettable that you are experiencing such difficulty adjusting to the temporary situation regarding your livelihood. We see tangibly what is explained in many holy seforim: that the more a person is strong in their bitachon in the Creator of the world and His guidance through hashgacha pratis, the sooner the improvement comes, and in greater measure. Surely it will be the same in your situation...

Although you do not mention it, I hope that you are taking part in the work of N’shei U’Bnos Chabad in the place where you are now. This surely gives you the opportunity to utilize your talents for the benefit of the many, and the merit of the many will assist you.

In addition to the above, it would be appropriate to inquire about teaching Lashon HaKodesh to the children of Anash, may they live. Strengthening your bitachon and rejecting despair, chas v’shalom, will add success in all your personal and general matters.

With blessings.

## 5100

B”H, 21 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter—though it lacks the date of writing—along with the enclosure.

Regarding what you wrote, “Ribono shel Olam, until when, etc.,” it is already well-known from the holy sefarim that it is not worthwhile to engage in questions and challenges regarding the Holy One, blessed be He. For it is not worthwhile [es loyent nit] to have one’s own account examined regarding one’s conduct toward the Makom. It is far, far better to ask Hashem for blessings and salvations through His kindness—a kindness of grace—and in the familiar language of prayer used by all Bnei Yisrael: “To You, Hashem, is the righteousness, and to us, etc.; not because of kindness and not because of deeds have we come before You; like the poor and the destitute, we have knocked on Your doors, etc.” (And then one is assured that) “from before You, our King, do not turn us away empty-handed.” Elaborating on a matter that is explained in so many places is certainly superfluous, especially since it is apparent from your letters that you have read and studied [these concepts].

May it be His will that you bring good news regarding all those you wrote about, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed. And since you are also included in this, it is understood that regarding yourself, you will bring good news that you are increasing in the study of Torah and in the beauty of performing mitzvos, going from strength to strength, and that the blessings of Hashem are increasing from day to day.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

## 61

B"H, 21 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

It was with pleasure that I heard from your parents, may they live, regarding your studies in our holy Torah—the *Torah-Chayim* (Torah of Life), Torah from the word *hora'ah* (instruction), for it is an instruction for life in this world, in our day-to-day existence. My hope is that the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, will be fulfilled in you: "Great is study, for it leads to action."

Knowing your parents, may they live, and knowing the stock from which you are hewn—both on your father’s side and your mother’s side—you have the merit of your ancestors to assist you. The matter depends only on your own will. It is my hope that you will increase your Torah study with consistency and diligence. In all times, and especially in this era of ours, which is full of events and changes, the necessity for a strong and firm foundation in life—one that will withstand all types of changes and trials—is even greater. This foundation is the Torah and *mitzvos* in our daily lives; it is only through them that the people of *Bnei Yisrael* have remained alive and enduring despite the crises and wanderings of thousands of years. It is this that stood for our ancestors and for us. As is known to anyone familiar with a chapter of our people’s history, it was not language, nor land, nor other values that ensured our existence throughout all the generations, but solely our holy Torah and its *mitzvos*, which are our life and the length of our days in all times, in all places, and under all conditions.

It would please me to hear from you directly regarding your progress in the above, and that you are continuing to increase in your studies and finding success in them.

With blessings,

## 62

B"H, 21 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rav, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, a man of many accomplishments,
R' Shmuel Abba, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

After a very long hiatus, your letter was received—though it lacked the date of writing—in which you write, albeit very briefly, about the farbrengen of Chag HaGeulah, the 19th of Kislev, and that a larger crowd participated in it than in previous years.

It is understood based on the well-known teaching of our Sages that when ten people sit together, the Shechinah rests among them, even if they are not speaking words of Torah, as per the language of Rabbeinu HaZaken in Iggeres HaKodesh, section 23. How much more so when there is a large crowd, many times ten, and they are speaking words of Torah and Yiras Shamayim. May it be His will that these matters exert their influence throughout the entire coming year. This is also based on what our Rebbeim, the Nesi'im, revealed to us: that this day, the 19th of Kislev, is the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus. It is well known that the precision of the term "Rosh" (head) rather than "techilah" (beginning) implies that the head contains the vitality of all the limbs and draws vitality down to them—meaning, throughout the days of the entire coming year.

It was pleasant for me to read in your letter about the reciting of Tehillim before davening on Shabbos Mevarchim. May it be His will that the prayers of the "Sweet Singer of Israel" draw down an increase of blessing and success in everything necessary for each and every one, from the soul to the body.

With blessings for good tidings, may we be written and sealed in general matters, and through this, there will certainly be an increase in private matters as well, for the one is dependent upon the other, and may you bring good news regarding them as well.

#### ***62***

**R' Shmuel Abba:** Snieg, Munich. Additional letters to him appear in Vol. 12, p. 474.

## 63

B"H, 22 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 Teves:

It goes without saying that I was deeply shocked by its content, and especially by the conclusion of the letter, from which it appears that you wish to fast for forty days.

Such conduct is contrary to what Rabbeinu HaZaken [the Baal HaTanya—who is the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah, and the Shulchan Aruch—the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah] writes in his Iggeres HaTeshuvah. Therefore, I am rushing to write to you and am sending this letter express. May Hashem Yisbarach help that it should have the intended effect—namely, that even if you have already taken this upon yourself in a manner that requires a *hataras nedarim* (annulment of vows) by three people, you should do so. Tell them that you were unaware of what is written in Iggeres HaTeshuvah [see there, Chapter 3 (page 92b)]. Furthermore, this is against the famous teaching of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse, "When you see the donkey of your enemy lying under its burden... you shall surely help **with him**" (see Hayom Yom, 28 Shevas (page 23)).

You can replace the forty-day fasts by doing two things:

a) Give *tzedakah* in a way that the sum of approximately 27 dollars is paid by Purim or the upcoming Pesach.

b) Exchange them for *taanis sha'os* (fasting for partial days). That is to say, over the course of several years, divide them into fasts until midday; you can spread this over nine years.

It is also understood that your writing regarding *perishus* (abstinence) from your wife, *tichyeh*, is entirely against my opinion. You must conduct yourself in accordance with the laws of our holy Torah, following the statutes and laws of *taharas hamishpachah*, but not through *perishus*. This is especially true since this involves causing pain to another person, which occupies a significant place in the Shulchan Aruch.

Regarding your question about what to do for *tikkun* (rectification): You should ensure that you know several chapters of Mishnayos and at least one chapter of Tanya by heart (it can also be one of the shorter chapters). Every weekday before *davening*, give *tzedakah*, and keep the daily *shiurim* of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya. It is understood that all of this must be done *bli neder* (without a vow).

Awaiting good news regarding the above, as soon as possible.

With blessings.

***

**27 dollars approximately:** Two-thirds of a dollar for each fast. See above, Vol. 18, Letter 6334, and the references in the notes there.

**Nine (9) years:** See Iggeres HaTeshuvah there, "over nine years or more."

6.4

B”H, 22 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and dedicated shaliach whose work is the work of Heaven,
Rabbi Tzvi Dov, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

After a very long hiatus, I received your letter dated Thursday, in which you describe your current daily routine and ask for my opinion on whether you should continue as you are, or if you should endeavor to move to a large city where there are many G-d-fearing people.

Regarding this, based on the instructions I heard many times on such matters from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, since Divine Providence has granted you the merit that your voice is heard and your influence is felt in the place where you are, and since there are not many people there who are observant of Torah and mitzvos, it is not only the case that you should not move from there; on the contrary, you should become even more deeply rooted there. You should seek out strategies, methods, and ways to fully utilize the influence you possess. As it appears from your letter and your daily routine, you are currently utilizing it to a small degree, which is not sufficient at all. Even though it is evident from your letter that you are using your spare time to study yourself—and indeed, Torah study is great, etc.—in our times and in our generation, especially in the United States, the dissemination of Yiddishkeit on the **greatest** scale is a matter of *pikuach nefesh* in the literal sense. It is not only a salvation for the life of the World to Come, but also a salvation for the life of this world. This is tangibly visible in the lives of the youth, where a non-religious education, or one that is religious only to a very small degree, places their conduct in danger, even to the lowest extreme, and the wise will understand. A mitzvah that cannot be performed by others, and certainly the mitzvah of *pikuach nefesh*, is greater even than Torah study, as ruled by our Sages in many places.

Especially since you have merited to be in such a place and in this period of the recent years, where an awakening toward *teshuvah*, religion, and religious life is felt even among those in whom this matter was not felt at all until now—**one who contemplates** the concept of "Love your fellow as yourself," and especially according to the well-known saying of our Rebbes in the name of the Alter Rebbe that "Love your fellow as yourself" is one with "Love Hashem your G-d," which is the root of all the mitzvos, and as is known from our Sages that one who serves out of love is not comparable to one who serves out of fear—surely there would be no room for the question you raised. My hope is strong that these few lines in quantity will suffice to guide you. Furthermore, may you also find the appropriate words to explain and illuminate this matter to your wife, may she live and be well, so that she will not only agree with the above—that is, with engaging in the strengthening of Yiddishkeit in your current camp with *mesiras nefesh*—but that she will also cooperate in this. May the efforts of both of you be in a manner of "increasing and adding light," as required by our holy Torah: "We increase in matters of holiness."

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above.

P.S.
At the end of your letter, you ask if you should be satisfied with your service of Hashem as you are doing now. Based on the above, it is forbidden to be satisfied with this at all, for you must increase your efforts in strengthening Yiddishkeit many times over. There is nothing that can stand before the will, especially since in our times we see with our own eyes the success in this work.

## 65

B"H, 22 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Teves, in which you write regarding the two paths before you concerning your future arrangements, and ask my opinion on the matter.

Often in such cases, the decision and its determination come about through prior decisions regarding other points—points that are more important than the specific question at hand, which is merely a consequence of them. In my opinion, this is also the case regarding your situation. You should arrange your life in such a way that: a) You will be able to marry and build a home in Yisrael in the very near future; b) You will be able to set times for the study of Torah. And it would be best—since until now you have studied in a mixed fashion, i.e., studies of holiness alongside, lehavdil, secular studies—that you dedicate at least one year to the study of holiness alone. Your decision regarding the question you wrote about should be in accordance with these two points. Based on this, my opinion is clear: the logic of pursuing studies that would prevent you from marrying for four years is rejected, provided it is possible to become proficient in your profession through one or two years of study, and no more. It would be even better if you were to marry in the middle of this period; it is worth looking into this.

Regarding the detail of whether to be in a religious kibbutz or to live in a city, this is not important in comparison to what has been said, since your residence for the next year or two does not at all determine your permanent place of residence, not even during the months when you are free from studies. Therefore, your temporary residence should not influence your question regarding your life arrangements.

Furthermore, since it appears that you have influence in a certain circle, and there is certainly a possibility to utilize your influence to strengthen Yiddishkeit—and the main point is the deed, i.e., daily life according to our Torah, the Torah of life—it is necessary that you arrange yourself in such a way that you can utilize this possibility. It is understood that this is easier in a kibbutz than in a large city.

Since every matter is through Hashgacha Pratis coming from the Ribbono shel Olam, who is without limits, there are certainly several benefits in every situation. I am taking this opportunity, aside from expressing my opinion on the question you asked, to also awaken you to the necessity of studying Pnimiyus HaTorah, which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. This is not merely an additional matter of Torah knowledge, but something that touches upon a person’s entire life, including their daily life. A Chassidishe way of life is distinguished in a fundamental point from a way of life devoid of the light of Chassidus. Naturally, a letter is not the appropriate medium for an extensive explanation of this, but the saying is well known: "That which is famous requires no proof." It is obvious that in saying these things, my intention is not, chas v'shalom, to touch upon the honor of anyone, and certainly not to touch upon the way of life of those who fear Hashem and keep His mitzvos. I only wish to emphasize that even within true goodness there are many levels, one above the other, and furthermore, that in our event-filled era, the necessity for Chassidishe warmth, light, and vitality is emphasized more and more.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

With blessings for success in spreading true Yiddishkeit—that is, through mitzvos maasiyos—in your surroundings and in every place your reach extends, with an expanded mind and with good news.

## 68

B”H, 23 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from 23 Kislev, which has just arrived, in which you ask regarding the continuation of your studies from now on.

It is understood that since you are in a yeshiva, you must conform to the yeshiva’s schedules and conduct as mentioned. Therefore, you should turn to the administration of the yeshiva where you are studying, and they will instruct you.

Regarding what you write about acquiring personal *da’as*, you do not specify or explain your intent in this. It seems you are referring to the negation of the trait of despair that you experience, as you write. You should study in the *Sefer Tanya Kadisha* in the places where it explains how a person’s heart should not fall within him, and where it negates sadness, etc., with all strength. You will find these places in the subject index printed at the end of the *Tanya* (Kehot edition), which is surely available in the yeshiva library or in your possession.

In the inner dimension of these matters, the negation of despair is founded upon a fundamental principle in our Torah: the absolute *emunah* that the *Ribono shel Olam* oversees each and every person with *hashgacha pratis*. Since He is the essence of good, it is certain that "everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good."

It is my hope that you have fixed times for studying *Toras HaChassidus*, and that you are also aware of the three daily *shiurim* in *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*. You should observe them, at the very least, from this point forward.

With blessings for success in Torah study with *yiras shamayim*,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 619

B"H, 24 Teves, Hilula of the Alter Rebbe, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Eliezer Steinman,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I am writing to thank you for your thoughtfulness and for the books you sent to my library. It is my hope that you will continue to do so in the future, for "one cannot study without a new insight." May it be Hashem’s will that you go from strength to strength in your work, especially in disseminating the ideas of Toras HaChassidus, in accordance with the demand placed upon each of us to be in a state of "increasing and growing." This is especially true given that you have been granted the ability to bring these ideas to, and instill them within, the various circles over which you have personal influence.

As is explained in many places, and in the language of Chassidus, everything must be "in truth" (*b’chen*). Surely this also emphasizes that despite the declaration that "the Merciful One desires the heart," the actual deed is essential. Furthermore, the deed and the action are the proof of the heart’s sincerity and integrity. As is known, the explanation of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding the adage "there is no wise man like one with experience"—which is brought in several places in the teachings of Chassidus (and for now, I have found it in *Akeidah*, Shaar 14, and *Maavar Yabok*, Shaar 2)—is that experience and action are the proof that one is truly wise.

Regarding the present matter, I am writing to inform you that in a separate package, I have sent you the Chassidic books that we have published recently. Among them are two volumes of Maamarim by the Alter Rebbe, printed from manuscripts for the first time. In these two books, there are several Maamarim from the early period, in the style usually referred to as "pre-Petersburg," when the Maamarim were, for the most part, brief. In the words of the Rebbe (Rashab) n’e: "The Maamarim from before Petersburg set the world on fire; they were flashes from Above" (*Sichas* Yom Kippur 5663, printed in *Toras Shalom*).

With appreciation, honor, and blessing.

## 610

B"H, 24 Teves, the Hilula of Rabbeinu HaZaken, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent worker for the sake of the community, etc.,
R' Moshe, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter of 29 Kislev, I was pleased to read that you have aroused several of those you influence regarding the alarming matter of the public and wholesale desecration of Shabbos caused by travel on ships (between Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and the USA) on Shabbos Kodesh, where, as is known, the crew—and all services provided—are performed by Bnei Yisrael. May it be the will of Hashem that this matter finally be rectified at its root; it is a disgrace even in the eyes of the nations of the world, in addition to the gravity of the matter itself. How ridiculous it is—if not for the alarming issue of public Shabbos desecration—that many who are fearful of Hashem’s word, who wish to ascend to Eretz Yisrael because it is the Holy Land and the palace of the King, the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, schedule this travel for the Yamim Nora’im or Yom Kippur and the like. They are meticulous that it should be specifically in accordance with the teaching of our Sages, "acquire or sell from your fellow," yet they pay no heed to the declaration of our Sages that "Jerusalem was destroyed only because they desecrated the Shabbos therein." They travel to the Holy Land for the holy days by means of desecrating the Shabbos, which is equivalent to all the mitzvos, and no one opens their mouth or chirps a protest. Furthermore, in response to what I told those who asked my opinion on this, they immediately began to exert pressure on me (naturally, not by bringing proof from Shas or Poskim), and to the wise, a word is sufficient.

One can learn a *binyan av* (a foundational principle) from the experience regarding the paper mill in Haifa: when a firm stance was taken, it is heard that the matter was finally rectified. This will surely add courage to the hope that one should not despair of rectifying the matter of the ships as well, provided that the *Daas Torah* on this is made known publicly with one voice...

With respect and with blessings for success in your holy work of raising the horn of the elder Israel through the dissemination of true Judaism, going from strength to strength, increasing in light.

## 611

B”H, 24 Teves, the Hilula of Rabbeinu HaZaken, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, engaged in communal affairs, possessor of excellent character traits, branch of a noble tree, etc., R’ Sh.Z. [Shazar]—may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive the telegram confirming that you have received the two volumes of Rabbeinu HaZaken’s works. For several reasons, this letter was delayed until today, the day of his Hilula.

It is similar to what I wrote in my previous letter regarding physical construction: that no matter how much one estimates the investment required for a building, when it comes to the actual work, one finds oneself in a difficult position, requiring hidden strengths—and even one’s own essential strengths. This is all the more true regarding spiritual construction. As our Sages said, "I am a wall"—this refers to Torah; and this is true even when the matter at hand is merely the publication and revelation of a structure that already existed.

This was confirmed for me personally. When I approached the editing of the aforementioned manuscripts, I estimated how much attention, depth, etc., the matter would require. Initially, I estimated a rather limited measure. Yet, when the matter came to fruition, I realized that the time and attention I had estimated were not sufficient at all. Furthermore, the very engagement and preparation for print—and even the proofreading after the arrangement of these maamarim—transports one to an "other world," a supernal world. This is especially true since several of the maamarim in these two volumes are from before the period of Petersburg, regarding which the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is known: "The maamarim from before Petersburg burned the world; they are literally from Above." (Yud-Tes Kislev, 5703).

People usually say in such cases that if they had estimated in advance all the toil and labor involved in such work—especially if it also involves mesiras nefesh—who knows if they would have entered into the matter at all. But in our case, even though, as mentioned, I did not even estimate the extent of what would be required, and especially the point that this engagement places one in "four other cubits," I would still have done it—though perhaps with longer preparation. And since you were one of the factors in this, you also have a share in all the good that is in it, along with my thanks for bringing me to this point.

Regarding the matter of the housing project, I was pleased to hear in the recording of your speech on Yud-Tes Kislev that you publicized this publicly. According to the letters I receive from the Kfar Chabad committee, the matter is still proceeding with difficulty. While there are surely several reasons for this, they must certainly be overcome with the appropriate effort.

I am certain that you do not need to be urged or encouraged in this, for the matter itself is the catalyst. The main reason I am writing about the housing project here is that if there is any possibility, in my opinion, the time has come not only for housing for Kfar Chabad, but also for the founding of a second Kfar Chabad, planned in a better way. The hope is strong that then, they will not require such difficult and long birth pangs as in this Kfar Chabad. By this, I also mean physical matters in the literal sense—that the issue of livelihood should not be so difficult and so limited, and that it should be somewhat further from the border, etc. With the founding of a second Kfar, several matters in this Kfar could also be arranged better. This also applies to schools for older youth, such as a seminary for girls, a teachers' school, or the Yeshiva—the goal being that both should be in Kfar Chabad. It is appropriate, of course, that they should not be in the same Kfar Chabad, which is also one of the reasons I am not in such a rush to move the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva to Kfar Chabad at this time.

It is understood that the above is only a general point, as I am not familiar with the locations that might be considered for the founding of a second Kfar Chabad. I will await your reaction to the aforementioned idea, and you will surely also inform me regarding the most suitable locations.

I do not know exactly the methods and labor of construction in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt speedily—but it is possible that the project of building a new Kfar would also solve the question of the Shemitah year for a significant portion of the current residents of Kfar Chabad.

And since I have already permitted myself to write about a somewhat broad plan, I will add one more point: my hope is that the aforementioned housing project and the founding of a second Kfar will certainly not detract from the plan for the Chabad housing project in Jerusalem—the Holy City, may it be rebuilt speedily.

After the farbrengen where we spoke regarding the housing and the second Kfar, I mentioned what I heard a few times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the saying of his grandfather, the Rebbe Maharash: "The world says that if you cannot go under, you must go over; but I say that from the outset, one must go over." In many matters, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, conducted himself according to this line, and he was accustomed to saying that through this, success is added. May it be the will of Hashem that in the matter of the housing project as well, the conduct will be in the aforementioned manner, "I will walk in a broad place," and may success be added—an extraordinary success.

With respect and blessing, looking forward to hearing good news.

## 612

612

B”H, 25 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent in communal affairs, etc., etc.,
Rabbi Sh. Y. Zevin, may he live and be well.

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to our friend, Mr. Shazar, may he live, so that you may be fully apprised of the matters. Should an opportunity arise, please utilize your influence upon him with words that come from the heart, in order to hasten the realization of these matters in their entirety and in the best possible way. May it be the will of the Almighty that the desire of Hashem succeeds in the hands of each of the individuals involved in these matters, within the broader context of all the efforts of *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*.

From the copy of my letter enclosed herewith, the reason for the delay in confirming and responding to your letter will also be understood. During the time spent preparing the manuscripts for print, all schedules were disrupted (cf. *Pesachim 113a*, *Rashi ad loc.*). That is to say, all the time that could be dedicated to the aforementioned matter was strictly allotted to it. Even during the time when it was impossible to change the focus of the work, my thoughts were occupied with the manuscript matters. However, after all the aforementioned interruptions, it was not only a *tirdah* of a *mitzvah*, but a pleasant *tirdah* of a pleasant *mitzvah*. May it be the will of the Almighty that the difficulties that cropped up after the printing will also be resolved quickly and easily, at least relatively speaking. You are already familiar with the details from the letter of the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal affairs, Rabbi Ch. A. Hodakov, may he live.

And last but not least, the eighth volume of the *Entziklopedia Talmudit* has been received. As with the previous volumes, so it is with this one: full of matters and enlightening notes. Even regarding topics that seemingly had been dealt with for some time, it is impossible to review them without finding something new. It is understood that in such a monumental work, omissions are inevitable. Surely you receive letters such as this, and you collect them; eventually, it will be possible to fill in the omissions slowly but surely in a booklet of additions or the like.

Incidentally, at the *farbrengen* of Yud-Tes Kislev this past year, we spoke about the concept of speech (in connection with the conclusion of *Tanya*, and the emphasis there on the times of heaven and earth—the physical realms—even though there is a distinction in terminology: the first, *me'asos*, and the second, *mi'yud maamaros*). I addressed the concept that speech is considered an act (*dibur chashiv kemaaseh*), which is also mentioned in *D'ch* (Chassidic discourse). It is surprising that the distinction found in *Chiddushei HaRashba* to *Shevuos 21a*, in the name of *R' Y. Migash*, was not mentioned in its entry. See *Likutei Torah* for the three *parshios*, *Parshas Noach*, end of the *maamar* beginning *Mayim Rabim* (54d).

May it be the will of the Almighty that you succeed in this holy work with proper health, peace of mind, and for long, good years, and that it be done with *zerizus*—or in other words, that there be success in time, as is known from the story of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding this. Surely this depends in part on you as well, by abstaining from other matters that are not essential. After all, the aforementioned work contains two elements: the matter of *Talmud Torah* and also a *mitzvah* that cannot be performed by others (*Moed Katan 9b*).

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above, and for success.

P.S.

Regarding your question as to where it is brought in his book concerning the Tzaddik, etc., R' Sh. Karliner: it is in *Sippurei Chassidim L'moadim*, entry 246. Incidentally, this was omitted from the index of names there.

## 613

B"H, 25 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 21 Teves, in which you write that you are experiencing difficulties in your livelihood, to the point that you feel compelled (in your opinion) to work even on Shabbos and Yomim Tovim (Heaven forbid), and despite all this, you and your family still lack the bare necessities.

Surely you understand that Hashem, blessed and exalted, is the Creator of the world and its Guide, and you also understand that Hashem, blessed and exalted, is the Giver of the Torah. Based on this, it is impossible in any way that the One who guides the world would guide it in such a manner that someone would be forced to transgress the command of that Guide. Further proof of this is that you yourself see that you are lacking the bare necessities. Rather, since man was created in perfection so that good would come through his free choice, one is not coerced in this matter. Ultimately, one will see the good before him—the true good, not only in spiritual matters but in physical ones as well. And since He wishes to grant him a great reward—and "according to the effort is the reward"—He sometimes places him before a test, the purpose of which is as it is said, "for He is testing you," etc. When one stands firm in the test, one is rewarded not only in the World to Come but also in this world. One then realizes that it was nothing more than a test, intended to increase the reward through improved livelihood, physical health, and—most importantly—true *nachas* from one’s children, may they live.

It is my hope that these few lines, though brief in quantity, will suffice for you to immediately begin conducting yourself in accordance with the command of our Torah, the Torah of life. Even if the difficulties do not pass at the very beginning, I am confident that in a short time you will see that you have chosen the good, and you will be increased in the blessings of the Creator of the world, who is the Giver of the Torah, in all that you and your household, may they live, require.

Awaiting good news regarding all of the above,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

#### ***613***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 9, p. 286.

## 14

[25 Teves 5718]

In response to your letter of 20 Teves: It is a great wonder to me that my previous response apparently caused you to feel discouraged. This is certainly surprising, as you are surely aware of the Baal Shem Tov’s directive regarding ahavas Yisrael, and the saying of the Alter Rebbe that "Love your fellow as yourself" is the vessel for "Love Hashem your G-d"—and you are familiar with the answer to the question of which comes first. Surely there is no area in which one can exercise ahavas Yisrael more than in the field of chinuch al taharas hakodesh. This is especially true regarding those who, for whatever reason, were in the army; the special approach required toward them, as opposed to children, is evident to the senses.

My hope is strong that you will recognize that this discouragement comes from the "clever one" [the yetzer hara] and not from the matter itself, chas v’shalom. Consequently, you must fight this with all your might, since this is the very "doren marke" whose entire purpose is to create "svarke" [discord], as in the well-known nigun of the Chassidim.

Regarding what you wrote about visiting here: It is certainly not impossible, chas v’shalom. However, it would be appropriate for you to come here with "assets" (and in truth, this would be a great asset): that is, at a time when there is already activity in the aforementioned chinuch, through your involvement in it for some time. Furthermore, at that point, your travel and visit here would not only concern yourself, since you would be taking the children with you—even if not in body, then in spirit. And it is obvious that upon your return, you will influence them in body as well. This is not the case when there is not yet any connection between you and the future students. If only all those who traveled here in the past, and all those who wish to travel now, recognized the truth and the vast difference between traveling in these two aforementioned ways. It goes without saying that you have my permission to publicize this matter, even in my name, although sometimes even simple matters require explanation and clarification, and even then, one is not always certain that the explanation and the conclusion will be grasped.

#### ***14***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 22, p. 367.

**And the saying:** See also above, Letter 4, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 615

B"H, 26 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning your state of mind and the reasons for it, etc., it is obvious that there is no need to apologize for writing about this, as such writing is necessary. However, what you should indeed apologize for is the state of mind itself. While it is certain that the teaching of the Mishnah, "Do not judge your fellow..." has not escaped you, nevertheless, for every one of the Bnei Yisrael—and especially those who have merited that Divine Providence has given them the opportunity to bring the hearts of the Bnei Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven, and furthermore, that despite obstacles and delays they are engaged in this (though I must add that it is not to the appropriate degree at all, and that the state of mind mentioned is certainly one of the reasons for this)—one must know that the difficulties, concealments, and hiddenness are in the manner of what is written, "For Hashem your G-d is testing you..." to know, etc. There is a wonderful explanation of this in Chassidus: it is not only *menaseh* in the sense of a test (*nisayon*), but also in the sense of elevation (*haga'ah*), as in "raise (*nes*) a banner on the mountains." The moral lesson in your specific case is understood...

With blessings for success in your holy work, and for good tidings in your personal matters as well.

Regarding the boy... *sheyichyeh*—you must endeavor to have him divert his attention from the world of machshavah (thought) in general, and from the content of what he writes in particular. Among the suggestions for this is to pair him with a cheerful *chavrusa*, or to make him a leader of a group (Shabbos parties and the like), so that he will be required to prepare a practical program and the like. And, of course, one should not enter into a long *shakla v'tarya* (debate) with him regarding the content of his writing, but rather dismiss it in passing or by diverting the conversation to other matters.

## 6116

6116

B"H, 28 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs,
R' Ephraim Eliezer HaKohen, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters from the eve of 24 Teves—the day of the Hilula of Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch—along with the enclosures, and from the day following.

Many thanks for the good news regarding your health... and may it be His will that regarding the other matters you write about, you will also share good news, in a way that is visibly and revealedly good. This corresponds to the words of our Sages regarding the tenth month, the month of Teves, for which the "contribution of the year" is that "the body derives pleasure from the body." This must also be explained according to the Midrash (cited in *Meorei Or*): "Ahasuerus—this is the Holy One, Blessed be He, whose is the end and the beginning." From this it is understood that the "body," the essence and being, derives pleasure from the "body" of the Jewish person (see *Tanya Kaddisha*, Chapter 49, and regarding "You have **chosen** us from among all peoples and tongues," this refers to the material body, etc. The matter of **true** choice exists only in that which is not subject to any boundary or limitation, and as a result—this applies also to the Jewish people, for they are the true subject of this matter. See Rambam, *Hilchos Teshuvah*, Chapter 5; *Likutei Torah* by the author of the Hilula, *Emor* 38b). The pleasure is specifically from the body—according to what is explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 36—and it is specifically through the matters of the body that the desire of the Holy One, Blessed be He, is fulfilled, etc. All of the above requires the prerequisite that the body be healthy and whole, as explained in Rambam, *Hilchos Deios*, beginning of Chapter 3 and Chapter 4.

With respect and blessings for good news in all the aforementioned—and in connection with your birthday—and for a year of success in both material and spiritual matters.

Regarding your wonderment, "Natural love on Shabbos Kodesh?!"—it may be explained that the essence of Shabbos Kodesh is *taanug* (pleasure) in all its details (even in sleep).

Like oil that permeates everywhere. This is the opposite of the "natural," whose point is something constant, for a constant *taanug* is not *taanug*. See *Tanya*, Chapter 44: "**And like** nature, etc., nevertheless they are not called, etc." And in the letters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the supplement to *Kuntres HaAvodah*.

***

**R' Ephraim Eliezer:** Yalles, Philadelphia. Additional letters to him—above 5792, and in the references in the notes there.

**That the body derives pleasure:** See also above, Vol. 14, Letter 5041, and in the references in the notes there.

**The wonderment, "Natural love on Shabbos Kodesh?!":** In his letter: "I remember that on Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh *Emor* 5704, when I entered into the inner sanctum, during the drinking of tea (presumably this was a *yechidus*), I recounted with excitement (as was my way then, in my youth) our sitting together on Shabbos Kodesh, during the *seudah*, and what we spoke about, and it slipped from my mouth: 'I felt natural love.' Immediately, our holy master replied to me with a tone of wonder: 'Natural love on Shabbos Kodesh?!—[it is] hidden love.'"

## 6117

6117

B.H., 28 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal affairs, R' Shalom, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 22 Teves.

At an *eis ratzon*, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. It is understood that since you are the one writing on their behalf, the Sages have already stated that one who prays for his friend is answered first. This is the main point—the fulfillment of your heart’s desires to raise your tender son, Ben Tzion, may he live, together with your wife and daughter, may she live, for Torah, for the *chuppah*, and for good deeds.

Regarding what you wrote about the youth who wishes to convert, etc.: both according to the *nigleh* and, even more so, according to the *pnimiyus* of these matters, since you have not been involved in this until now, it is appropriate that you connect them with rabbis who are *chareidim* to the word of Hashem. They will take an interest in the matter and act according to the instructions of our Torah.

Regarding what you wrote about the *avreich*... The point I made to him regarding *chalav akum* is based on the well-known story of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (and I believe it is also in print), that *chalav akum* arouses doubts in *emunah*. These are the things I said to him, and if in all times it was necessary to be cautious regarding the above—as is simple and obvious—how much more so for the youth in the United States, especially those studying in institutions where there is a mixture of good and evil, and "nation shall be stronger than nation," and the wise will understand. Regarding what you wrote about the health of the aforementioned: I believe I spoke clearly—that he is located in... and only comes home rarely. In any case, it is not in my hands to change what was stated explicitly. It is obvious that no one can take upon themselves the responsibility to conceal a matter from which, as mentioned, doubts in *emunah* are aroused. As for the fact that he refrains from using the dishes of his parents, may they live—this is not understood, for there are separate dishes for dairy foods, and consequently, this does not affect all the dishes, and thus not all foods.

Regarding the question of whether he should change his place of study to a different *yeshiva*: the *yeshiva* you write about is known for teaching in a spirit of *yiras shamayim*, and in several other matters of *kashrus* that are properly maintained.

And certainly, this is also true regarding the matter of *chalav Yisrael*. Regarding what his father, may he live, says—that the tuition will be difficult for him—they can certainly make an effort in this regard, as surely there are several acquaintances in their city who know the administrators of the aforementioned *yeshiva*.

I will mention you at an *eis ratzon* at the holy *tziyun* that your efforts regarding the *mechitza* should be successful. May it be the will of Hashem, in accordance with the foundation of all four parts of the *Shulchan Aruch* (which is why this comes first), that one should not be ashamed before those who mock; and furthermore, that one should be "moist enough to moisten others," and consequently, you will influence every place your hand can reach so that they, too, will not be ashamed before those who mock, and then your efforts will succeed.

With blessings for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding what you wrote about the *Sefer Torah*—there is testimony that it is *kosher* according to the Torah, as it is a *gezeiras hakasuv*, as is known. Since nothing happened, as a thanksgiving for the kindness of Hashem that nothing happened, it is appropriate that you set aside four dollars for the *tzedakah* of *chinuch* for the holy Torah.

618

B”H, 28 Teves, 5718

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Yitzchak Koren,

Shalom u’Bracha!

After a hiatus, I received with pleasure your letter of 17 Teves. It gave me satisfaction to read about your efforts regarding the advancement of agricultural matters in Kfar Chabad, and the consultations regarding this with the Village Committee, etc. It is my hope that these matters will reach the practical stage, and soon.

Especially since the time has already arrived to implement the matter of establishing a second Kfar Chabad. Based on my recollection of the content of our conversation during your visit here, I hope for your broad assistance in this. Therefore, I will take the liberty of writing to the Kfar Chabad Committee regarding the content of my letter to you. May it be the will [of Hashem] that it be with great success.

Immediately after the Yud-Tes Kislev farbrengen in Kfar Chabad, I was pleased to receive the news from there regarding your participation in the celebration. Now, I was happy to read in your letter about your deep impression from this celebration. Despite the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe — (said during such a celebration where there was extreme crowding and there was concern for his health) “A Yid does not crush me” — I agree with you regarding the need to arrange a spacious venue in Kfar Chabad, suitable for accommodating the large crowd, *kein yirbu*, who come to participate in the celebrations. I am writing to the Kfar regarding this. My hope is that this, too, will increase the number of participants, and thus it will spread and thus it will break through.

With respect and blessing and for good tidings regarding the above.

## 619

B"H, 28 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
R' Moshe A. (may he live and be well),

Shalom u'Bracha!

Following a long silence, I was pleased to receive your letter of 27 Teves.

Regarding your question about the possibility of my visiting Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) at the beginning of the summer: as it appears for the time being, my work schedule will compel me to remain here—at the very least, throughout the entire summer.

Although you do not mention it in your letter, I hope that you participated in the farbrengen of 19 Kislev (in Kfar Chabad?), for as you surely know, this is a bright day—a day which our Rebbes, our Nasi'im, called the "Rosh Hashanah" of Chassidus. The concept of a Rosh Hashanah is a general awakening for the entire year, and so it is regarding 19 Kislev: its purpose is to awaken and draw down a Chassidishe awakening and warmth into all the affairs of a Yid, and especially in the strengthening of Torah and its dissemination.

With respect and blessing.

## 620

B"H, 28 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 24 Teves, the day of the Hilula of our Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, in which you write regarding your situation, and primarily concerning matters of shidduchim.

Regarding what you wrote—that on your part you have done everything, and that secondary matters did not hinder you—it is based on the statement of Chazal, "One does not cry out over the past." What has been, has been. From here on, you should focus on ensuring that your wife will be a G-d-fearing woman, and you should pursue this as one who searches for his lost property, naturally following the ways of the Torah, and then you will succeed.

As for what you wrote, that you rejected a certain proposal because they wanted you to abandon the field of *hora'ah* (teaching/rabbinic instruction), it is understood that this matter is not an absolute impediment. If the proposal is suitable in all other details, it is not strictly necessary that you be a teacher by profession; you can be of service in the field of *chinuch* as a teacher not for the sake of receiving a reward, and certainly by being among the supporters of Torah—and indeed, Scripture places Zevulun before Yissachar.

Regarding your comment on the apparent contradiction in the words of Chazal concerning whether a shidduch depends on a person’s choice or if it is a decree that cannot be changed: in general, there is no decree that cannot be changed (see Rosh Hashanah 16a, and elsewhere). Regarding the aforementioned, this question has already been addressed in many places, including the Gemara and the Zohar. They explain that *rachamim* (mercy/prayer) are effective (Moed Katan 18b), or that the decree is fulfilled in another *gilgul* (reincarnation) (Zohar Vol. I, 91b; Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 14; Sefer Chassidim 383). And this is not the place to elaborate further.

Surely you are increasing your strength in your holy work of drawing the hearts of Bnei Yisrael to our Father in Heaven. Great is the merit to increase the blessings of Hashem in general, and specifically in this great mitzvah, which is the first mitzvah in the order of the Torah.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

***

**And they explain that *rachamim* are effective:** See also above, Vol. II, Letter 264.

## 621

B"H, 29 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 25 Teves, requesting a blessing.

At an opportune time, I will mention you at the holy resting place of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever you and those you wrote about may need. Regarding the stumbling block that occurred—even though it was unintentional—it is understood that the rectification must be in that very area. That is to say: care and **precision** in matters of eating and drinking, ensuring they are as they should be. Since one requires *siyatta d'shmaya* for everything, each weekday before the morning *tefillah*, you should set aside a few coins for *tzedakah*. Furthermore, after *tefillah* each day—including Shabbos and *Yom Tov*—you should recite at least one *kapitel* of *Tehillim*.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

Secretary

## 622

B"H, 29 Teves, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 21 Teves, in which you write that several of your friends have purchased land, etc., and you ask whether you should do the same.

If the conditions are equal in your estimation, and the information that several of your friends have done so is accurate, it is appropriate that you do so as well. However, this should be done in a way that you do not invest all of your available cash into it. If your available funds are insufficient for this, you may borrow a certain amount to complete the sum, but you must not leave your coffers empty, Heaven forbid.

It is surprising that for a long time you have not written at all regarding general matters, and especially regarding the central point of *hafatzas hama'ayanos*, particularly since the matter of organizing the recitation of *D'chassidus* in the *batei knesiyos*, etc., was upon your shoulders. Perhaps you will make up for this at the next opportunity.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 623

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, Branch:
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, in which you write regarding your activities in the holy work, the inner and central point of which is the spreading of the wellsprings outward (*hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*).

Surely you will not be satisfied with what has been done until now, for "we elevate in matters of holiness" is a command and a decree. This is especially true regarding the wellsprings of Chassidus, its guidance, and its customs, which are life-giving for all three pillars—Torah, Avodah, and Gemilas Chasadim—upon which the world (the great world, and also the small world—which is man) stands.

And we bring about the merit of this call to action on this day—the day of Rosh Chodesh Shevat, the head that includes and gives life to all the limbs—the days, and among them the tenth day, which is the day of the Hillula of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi Yisrael.

On this day, his soul ascends each and every year from level to level, and the body—these are his Chassidim, those connected to him, and those who belong to him—follows the head (*basar reisha azil*).

And there is an allusion in the language of the verse: "In the eleventh month, on the first of the month... Moses (the faithful shepherd) began to explain this Torah (and this instruction) saying (to all generations after him)—"

For every year, at the turn of the year, the matters of this day—like other such matters—when they are remembered, they are also enacted.

And the beginning of the explanation and the instruction is: "You have stayed long enough at this mountain" (even though this is the standing and the place of the Giving of the Torah. For a person must be one who "goes from strength to strength," and also—not to be satisfied with his own activities and his own self-refinement, but rather to influence others, even those who are found "outside, on the outside." And therefore),

"Turn and journey" (and a mere journey or passing through is not enough, but rather) "and come" (inwardly.

And the school of Rabbi Yishmael taught—inheritance (of the sparks that have fallen from their level and are considered dead) and settling specifically, and in this place that is before you, "and your people are all righteous" (it seems to them), "the mountain of the Emorite" (which includes and is the essence of the "opposite side"—Torah Or, Additions 102c) "and to all its neighbors," etc.,

(And through this you will merit the fulfillment of the promise, "Hashem your G-d will expand your border") "to the great river, the river Euphrates" (for they will also inherit the Kenite, the Kenizzite, and the Kadmonite—Rambam, Laws of Murderer 8:4; Likkutei Torah of the Arizal, Parshas Lech Lecha; Maamar beginning "Hinei Anochi," 5654).

And thus, the lesson is understood. And the merit of the many will assist you.

With blessings for success.

## 624

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter. May it be the will of Hashem that His desire succeeds in your hands to remove all obstacles and delays regarding the matters mentioned therein, to nullify the concealments and obstructions, and for all of you to cooperate together to fulfill His will—may He be blessed—in spreading Torah and education in the purity of holiness, increasing both in quantity and in quality. For the merit of the many—the students, both male and female, who yearn in their inner souls with deep desire and longing for the word of Hashem, which is Torah—will assist you.

This is especially true regarding the children of the house of the Rebbe (tishbar), as explained regarding the greatness of the breath of their mouths, even according to the question of our Sages: "Mine and yours, whose is it?" and the answer given there (Shabbos 119b). There are wonderful words on this in the Kuntres Acharon of our Alter Rebbe (155a) regarding this breath that ascends on high, even if it is not entirely *lishmah* (for its own sake), but rather from fear of the rod. Together with this, the breath of the *tishbar* ascends all the way to Atzilus. The magnitude of this wonder is understood from what is written in the Tanya in several places, among them Chapter 39 and 40. This provides an explanation and illumination of the law in our Torah that one does not interrupt the study of *tishbar*, not even for the building of the Beis Hamikdash.

And merit is brought about... and therefore, the lesson to be learned is understood, and the merit of the many will assist you, as mentioned above.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

## 626

B"H, 1 Shevat, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs,
R' Zev Dov Alter, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter dated 23 Teves, the eve of the yom hilula of Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch, in which you write regarding your current situation.

Surely you have heard the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, quoting his grandfather, the Rebbe Maharash: "The world says that if one cannot go under, one must go over; but I say that one should go over from the outset." The same applies in this instance: even though, on the face of it, one might think to wait for open joy until one’s health actually improves, there is room to say—following the aforementioned approach—that one should precede the improvement of health with joy, even if that improvement is not yet manifest. This will hasten the matter. This is similar to the saying heard many times from the Nesi'im of Chabad: "Think good and it will be good." It is obvious that when one brings this into speech of joy and action of joy—especially regarding your honor, who, through your pen, the pen of a ready writer, has the ability to influence the masses with the aforementioned—it is well known what the reward is for those who bring joy to others (Taanis 22a).

With blessings for a good month, the day on which the Ra'aya Mehemna began to explain the Torah, as the verse states: "In the eleventh month, on the first of the month... Moses (Ra'aya Mehemna) began to explain this Torah (and this instruction) to say (to all generations after him)..." The lesson and the moral are understood, especially since the merit of the many who read your articles will assist you.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 627

B"H, 1 Shevat, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, pious, and learned, engaged in communal needs,
R' Yehuda Zarchia Mordechai Leib Chaim, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

After a very long interval, your letter of 22 Teves was received, along with the request for a blessing and a *pidyon nefesh*, which will be read at an *eis ratzon* at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be the will of Hashem that you bring us good tidings.

I was pleased to read at the end of your letter about the students who have increased their Torah study. Surely, they will not only be satisfied with this, but it will awaken a yearning and thirst in this area, as is known from the statement of our Sages: "He who has a *maneh* (feels the lack and) wants two hundred; he who has two hundred (feels the lack even more and) wants four hundred," and so on. If this holy *avodah* is incumbent upon everyone, it is all the more so for the youth who have only recently entered the battle of life, and especially for those who have been gifted with the power to influence their surroundings. And if "the head of the well is appointed from Heaven," then certainly this applies to a Rabbi and teacher of instruction in a holy congregation.

Although it is understood that in order to influence others one must first be "moist enough to moisten" (*tofeach al menas hatpiah*), in our current era—where the entire world has been confused, and the paths in this *avodah* have been confused yet again—this is explained at length in the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rashab), printed in the introduction to *Kuntres Uma'ayon*, page 22, regarding the matter that there is an order and gradation in leadership; see there.

Regarding what you wrote about the connection between the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and the teachings of Chabad, see the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, printed in *HaTamim*, issue 2. Also known is the response of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch*, to the righteous Rabbi R' Boruch of Mezhibuzh, the grandson of the Baal Shem Tov, regarding his claim that he was the grandson of the Baal Shem Tov.

With blessings for good tidings.

***

**R' Yehuda Zarchia Mordechai Leib Chaim:** Segal, Tel Aviv. Additional letters to him appear in Vol. 15, 5712, and in the notes referenced there.

## 628

B"H, 1 Shevat, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Kfar Chabad in our Holy Land,
May it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu,
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letters and the *pidyon kesafim* :

1) It is absolutely understood and simple that there is no room for the notion of a village or cooperative housing project [affiliated] with a political party—even the best one. This is in complete and absolute contradiction to the leadership of our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*. The essence of Chabad is supra-partisan, and its inner mission is the dissemination of the *ma'ayanos* until they reach the "outside"—and certainly to those who are not on the "outside." It is obvious that a political party, whichever it may be, interferes with the core of the *avodah* and its branches. It is a source of great astonishment, even regarding the mere thought of such a strange concept.

2) It seems there has been some misunderstanding of my opinion regarding the new housing project in Kfar Chabad. Apparently, it was interpreted as referring only to housing, whereas my intention was that this is an expansion of Kfar Chabad in its essence, where the primary point is agriculture. Consequently, the settlers of this housing project should have priority given to farmers, etc., as I wrote in my previous letter. From this, it is understood that the matter is also connected to the allocation of plots of land, whether for agriculture in its simple sense, or at the very least for a vegetable garden or a chicken coop.

3) Regarding the *mikveh*, this too is puzzling: why do completely unforeseen difficulties arise so frequently? After all, many *mikvaos* have been built in Eretz Yisrael, may it be built and established, and surely there are experts in this field—experts not only in theoretical knowledge, but also regarding practical implementation. Why are they not being consulted? After all, this would eliminate the aforementioned surprises. Especially since I began writing to urge this matter several years ago, and until now, I have not merited seeing this improved *mikveh* in reality.

In order to preclude further steps regarding a partnership with a political party, this letter is being sent as an urgent express.

With blessings for success in the establishment and development of Kfar Chabad in accordance with the will of its founder and director, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and for good tidings in all matters.

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to Mr. Koren, *sheyichyeh*, and I am certain you will discuss what I emphasized in this copy.

Thank you in advance for delivering the enclosed letter to the *Tzeirei Agudas Chabad* in Kfar Chabad as soon as possible.

***

**628**

**My letter to Mr. Koren:** See above, 618.

*) Dates: 3, 15, 24, 29 Kislev, 8 Teves, letter from 10 Teves with the enclosure. For some reason, the *pidyon kesafim* from 7 and 11 Elul have not yet been acknowledged.

The intention here is, quite simply, in the manner of our Sages' teaching that "great is study, for it leads to action." As is well known, the demand of our Rebbes is that every concept in *Chassidus* must lead to "thus"—and since they demand this, it is certain that the ability and the strength are granted to fulfill this demand in its entirety. I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above.

## 632

632

B”H, 2 Shevat, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was greatly astonished to receive the news that, to this day, there is no monument or marker of any kind on the grave of his father, a”h. Furthermore, even the construction intended to prevent the grave from sinking has not been done, and as a result, the grave is sinking and neglected.

It is possible, given the magnitude of my astonishment, that this information is not accurate. But it is obvious that if this is indeed the case, he will certainly do everything in his power to rectify the matter as soon as possible. The wondrous words in the Zohar, Vol. 3, at the end of Parshas Bechukosai, are well known regarding this, in addition to the halachic ruling in the Shulchan Aruch. Even if there are some who argue for the custom of waiting until after twelve months to erect a monument, this is all the more reason to do so after twelve months have passed. Elaborating on such a simple matter is superfluous, and I look forward to hearing good news from him regarding all matters as soon as possible, and thank you in advance.

With blessings.

## 633

B"H, 3 Shevat, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Motzaei Shabbos:

1) How to merit success in studies and receive great assistance from Hashem in this.

It is a well-known statement of our Sages: "If you have labored and not found, do not believe it"—meaning that if one labors in the study of the holy Torah, it is certain that one will find and succeed, and the matter depends only on one's strong desire for it. In order to increase the assistance of Hashem in this, which will in turn increase success and diminish difficulties, one should set aside money for tzedakah every weekday before the morning davening, and recite the monthly Tehillim shiur every day, including Shabbos and Yom Tov, after the morning davening. It is also very good to keep the known daily shiurim of Chumash and Tanya, which we have heard many times from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, are appropriate for every soul and a segulah for many matters.

2) Since we are commanded to "serve Hashem with joy," what should one do when one begins to feel a bit of sadness?

One should study the Rambam at the end of Hilchos Lulav, from which it is understood how every person, in every standing and situation, can be in a state of joy while serving their Creator. And not only is it possible, but it is a great avodah—it is essential and fundamental. The advice on how to rid oneself of sadness and negate it is explained in the holy Tanya in many places (as noted there in the index). May it be the will [of Hashem] that you bring good tidings regarding all that has been said, and that you increase your study of the holy Torah and the "light" within it—which is the pnimiyus haTorah that has been revealed in our generation through the teachings of Chassidus.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 634

B"H, 3 Shevat, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished, etc.,
R' Schneur Zalman, may he live,

Shalom u'Bracha!

Following the long silence, I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated Erev Shabbos. It is surprising that you write that until now you have not received confirmation of the receipt of the *bichlach* (booklets) that you sent via the esteemed R' Dober, may he live, to the Admur, as they were acknowledged long ago. It is understood that when they print from the *bichlach* you sent, they will cite the *bicheal* along with the name of its author—that is, your father, *a"h*—and that it was received by the Rebbe, *shlita*; this is the custom of Yisrael.

In this regard, I would like to note that you mention in your letter that this was the first *aliyah* of Chabad Chassidim sent by the Alter Rebbe. I am interested to know if this was a slip of the pen and should instead say the Mitteler Rebbe, for it seems to me that the first *aliyah* of Chabad Chassidim occurred in his time, not in the time of the Alter Rebbe (as the *aliyah* of Chassidim in the year 5537 was an *aliyah* of Chassidim in general, immediately following the passing of the holy Rav, the Malach, at which time Chabad Chassidus had not yet been publicized as an independent entity, until the Alter Rebbe assumed the leadership publicly some years later).

At a time of favor, please mention him and his household, may they live, at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzuklalleh, nishmaso b'eden, zechuso yagen aleinu*, for whatever they may need.

With thanks once again for sending the *bichlach*.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 635

B"H, 5 Shevat, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished,
R' Dovid, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the proposal to strike the head of the animal immediately after shechitah to hasten the animal's death, in order to allow the workers to begin processing it.

We see tangibly with all such proposals, whether before shechitah or even after shechitah, that if one agrees to any of them, it establishes a precedent and leads from "one leniency to another," in addition to the concerns that exist regarding this matter **in and of itself**, and there is no need to elaborate here. Since the benefit in this matter is slight—as the difference is only a matter of moments—the damage is not worth it, even according to those who would wish to "permit" it, and the matter is understood.

It is my hope, even though you do not mention it, that you participated in the farbrengen of the auspicious day of 19 Kislev, and may it be G-d's will that the hisorerus leave a recognizable impression throughout the entire year.

With respect and blessings for health, both literally and in its full meaning, and for good tidings.

#### ***635***
