## 683

[Rosh Chodesh Adar 5718]

In response to your letter of the 22nd of Shevat, in which you write that "the head says there could be no better proposal, but the heart says no." However, you do not state the reason why (the heart says no).

Regarding the practical application, in matters of shidduchim, the heart generally occupies a place that is more than secondary.

Therefore, one must have at least the beginning of an attraction to the matter, or at the very least, an anticipation that this will come. If, however, this is lacking, and the heart says no, one must take that into account.

What is not clear to me in your letter is what you write, that if the heart is not secondary, etc., "I will have to wait longer." Whether your intention is to wait for a different proposal, or for a change in this proposal itself—and depending on what your opinion is regarding this—you must decide what to do next.

May it be the will of the Ribono shel Olam, who oversees each and every person with Hashgacha Pratis, that He lead you on a path that is truly good, and in a way that is good in a revealed and apparent manner.

684

By the Grace of Hashem
Erev Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, distinguished in Torah and fear of Heaven, of noble lineage, etc.,
Rabbi Yosef Dovid, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, together with the "Kuntres Tikkun Eiruvin" authored by your honor, shlita. The Kuntres is returned herewith.

Regarding your request for an approbation: It is well known that this is not the custom of the Rebbe’s house. We hold fast to the customs of our forefathers.

Furthermore, the time does not at all permit a study of the book as is required. Moreover—and this is the primary point for me—in every place, *ana b’asrei d’Rav ana* (I am in the domain of the Rav), namely my grandfather, our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya and the Shulchan Aruch. We conduct ourselves specifically according to the Rav. Included in this, of course, is what is written in his Shulchan Aruch (Section 363, Paragraph 36) that the sea does not rise to serve as a partition.

As for your honor’s attempt to stretch and interpret this ruling—specifically in a case where there is a concern that the refuse heap might also be removed, leaving only one partition—with all due respect, there is no room for this at all. For he explicitly wrote his ruling in the Shulchan Aruch there regarding a refuse heap of the public that is not intended to be cleared. And when the sea washes up a sandbank, two partitions will remain adjacent to one another, like a doorpost and a *lechi* or a beam on the side of a wall.

***

Now, although, notwithstanding the above, I was pleased to read at the conclusion of the Kuntres that he who hires it [the labor] and he who gathers it, etc.,

(Though surely without a *bracha*, and not as the superficial reading of the language might imply, for one cannot escape several doubts. And *brachos* are not an impediment.)

And in my opinion, it is a great and wonderful merit for your honor, even if we were to say that according to several opinions there is room to debate various details and doubts.

Nevertheless, it is my absolute and firm opinion that it should not be printed, nor published in any other manner, that the matter is concluded and the *eiruv* is fixed (at least according to his opinion).

Regarding what you wrote at the end of the Kuntres about the benefit of publication—in order to save even those who intend to violate the law, as per the Gemara (Nazir 23a),

Surely your honor can also estimate how many of these willful violators study, or even just know about, such books and Kuntresim.

This is not the case regarding those who are observant of Torah and mitzvos, of whom our Sages specifically said that they "teach themselves leniency" (if they can find any basis or pretext whatsoever), and the publication of this matter is liable to lead them to breaches, etc. And after the publication, the matter will be beyond repair, even if one were to desire it.

- The great warning at the beginning of the Kuntres—we have already seen tangibly that this is of no avail in something that is printed and published, since, unfortunately, the attitude that "it is comfortable to be lenient" is prevalent. Especially in this country, where the "Rabbis" stand at their post—a post against Hashem and against His Torah—to breach the wall of religion and Yiddishkeit.

May it be the will of Hashem that in his days and in our days, the statement of our Sages (Yerushalmi, Taanis, Chapter 1, end of Halacha 4) will be fulfilled in practice: "If Israel would observe one Shabbos as it should be, immediately the son of Dovid would come."

- In the Bavli (Shabbos 118b) it says "two Shabbosos as they should be." This does not contradict the statement in the Yerushalmi of Taanis mentioned above, as explained by our Rebbe in his book Likkutei Torah, Parshas Behar, in the discourse entitled *Es Shabbosai Tishmoru*. See there. -

And in addition, in Shemos Rabbah (end of Chapter 25): Why? Because it is equivalent to all the mitzvos.

With respect and blessing.

P.S.
As is my way, for the love of the "chatter" of Torah, I have included some notes in the margins between the pages:

**At the beginning of the Kuntres. Section 1 (by).** Are the mitzvos of the Rabbis considered *asei* (positive commandments) or *lo saasei* (negative commandments)? One may note from Shabbos (23a): Where did He command us? Rabbi Ivya said: "Do not turn aside." Rabbi Nechemiah said: "Ask your father and he will tell you, etc." — regarding which the above-mentioned authorities disagree.

Indeed, seemingly, this is how this dispute is explained in the *Drushei HaRan* of *Doresh HaShem*. But we do not find among the enumerators of the mitzvos that they count "Ask your father, etc." in the count of the 248 positive commandments. If so, he is singular in his interpretation. (And no one has remarked upon this innovation!)

But for all the enumerators of the mitzvos, it must be that "Ask your father, etc." is a command, but it is not a positive commandment from the Torah among the 248 positive commandments. And according to them, there is no opinion that the mitzvos of the Rabbis are **only** positive commandments.

- This is also the case according to what is explained regarding the inner dimension of the matter in the teachings of Chassidus in the discourse *Mai Mevarech* (of the year 5680, and of the year 5691) by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. -

The opinion of the Rambam on the above—he wrote it explicitly, which is that they are included in the negative commandment of "do not turn aside" **and also** in the positive commandment of "according to all that they instruct you, you shall do" (*Sefer HaMitzvos*, First Root (and see the Ramban’s glosses there), end of the count of the mitzvos at the beginning of *Sefer HaYad*. *Hilchos Mamrim*, beginning of Chapter 1). According to this interpretation, one can say that the reason Rabbi Ivya brought the end of the verse, "do not turn aside," is because a negative commandment is more severe than a positive one. And the reason the Rambam in *Hilchos Brachos* (11:3) brought the first part of the verse, "according to all that they instruct you," is because one does not recite a *bracha* over a negative commandment, as is also written in *Bnei Binyamin* on the *Yad* there, and in *Torah Temimah* to Devarim (17:11). It requires study why, in *Hilchos Brachos* (6:2), the Rambam brought only the first part of the first part of the verse—"according to the Torah which they instruct you"—and similarly at the beginning of *Hilchos Mamrim*. In the *Sefer HaMitzvos* published by Rabbi Chaim Heller, shlita, the publisher noted the omission of the word "etc." after the word "instruct you." And there is some indication of this in *Sefer HaChinuch*, Mitzvah 495—which, as is known, follows the language of the Rambam in every place—that he copies the entire verse.

Regarding the count of the Rabbinic mitzvos and which ones are counted—what I wrote about this long ago is copied here:

Seven from the Midrash: And their mnemonic is *Na'ah B'Simcha* (Pleasant in Joy): *Netilas Yadayim*, *Eiruvin*, *Brachos*, (Ner) *Shabbos*, *Megillah*, *Chanukah*, *Hallel* (*Megaleh Amukos*, *Ofan* 75. Cited in *Yalkut Chadash*, entry *Mitzvos*, subsection 75). And they are also counted this way in *Sefer HaChinuch* at the end of the indices. And the reason these specific mitzvos were counted and no others is explained in *Sefer Mitzvos HaShem*: that only those that the Sages instituted to recite a *bracha* over, and which have no basis in the Torah, enter the count. See in *Torah Or*—by our Rebbe—(in the discourse *Vayomer, etc., Mi Sam Peh*) and in *Likkutei Torah* (explanation to the discourse *Eileh Pekudei*, Chapter 3; end of the explanation to the discourse *Shechorah Ani*), that all of them are specifically in the category of "arise and do" (active).* — That the number of Rabbinic mitzvos is seven is also brought in the *Shelah* (Parshas Yisro, *Chelek Torah Or*, at the beginning) in the name of the **ancients**, in *Me'orei Ohr*, letter *Zayin*, subsection 13, and others. — And seemingly it requires study, for the *Sefer Mitzvos Gadol* (at the end of the section of positive commandments) counts only five positive commandments from the words of the Scribes (*Eiruvin*, *Aveilut*, *Tisha B'Av*, *Megillah*, *Chanukah*) and concludes that he already explained the mitzvah of *Netilas Yadayim* as being from the words of the Scribes—(one could say he does not count *Brachos* because it belongs to the positive commandment of *Birkas HaMazon*, and also not *Hallel* because he includes it in the mitzvah of *Chanukah*, or that he holds it is from the Torah, like the opinions of the *poskim* cited in *Nitzotzei Ohr* on the Rambam’s *Sefer HaMitzvos*, Root 2, and in the commentary of the *Ridbaz* Perla on the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the *Rav Saadia Gaon*, positive commandment 90). And it is even more difficult that in *Shaarei Kedushah* by Rabbi Chaim Vital, Part 1, Gate 4, he counts several Rabbinic mitzvos. And so as not to disagree with the above, one can say simply that the *Sefer Mitzvos Gadol* and Rabbi Chaim Vital in *Shaarei Kedushah* did not come to count the **number** of Rabbinic mitzvos, but to inform us of all the enactments of the Sages and to explain their laws. But they also hold that there are seven Rabbinic mitzvos that complete the number 620 "pillars of light." And those who hold that *Hallel* is from the Torah, one can say that they include another Rabbinic mitzvah in its place to complete the count of seven Rabbinic mitzvos, just as we find several opinions as to which mitzvos enter the count of the 613 mitzvos from the Torah.

And even though regarding the number 620 letters in the Ten Commandments—several hints have been stated regarding the number of the seven letters added to 613 (which they explained as corresponding to the 613 mitzvos from the Torah)—and not just the simple hint that they correspond to the seven Rabbinic mitzvos,

- (And it is even more difficult from *Bamidbar Rabbah* 14:16: they correspond to the seven days of Creation. And from *Matnos Kehunah* to *Bamidbar Rabbah* 18:21—that the Kabbalists wrote that they hint to the seven *Sefiros*) -

One can say that they do not disagree on the actual number of Rabbinic mitzvos that enter the count, as above, but rather that there are seventy faces to the Torah.

By the way: The *Rashei Teivos* of *Ashir* (wealthy) are *Einayim* (eyes), *Shinayim* (teeth), *Yadayim* (hands), *Raglayim* (feet), cited in *Midrash Shmuel* on *Avos*, beginning of Chapter 4.

*) To note the opinion of the *Ravad* (*Hilchos Mamrim*, end of Chapter 2) that "arise and do" specifically applies to "do not turn aside."

## 685

B"H, 3 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Vaad of Kfar Chabad, in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In response to the telegram in which you write that there is a rumor regarding the opening of a meat cannery, and asking whether it is worthwhile to make an effort to have it opened in Kfar Chabad, although for the time being no details are known.

In any event, it is my opinion that the aforementioned would be a matter under the control of others regarding kashrus, etc., and furthermore, as you write, this is a factory—meaning, production on a large scale—and certainly they will not conduct themselves with extra stringency. The very announcement that it is in Kfar Chabad will serve as a certification of kashrus (especially if someone from Kfar Chabad is among the workers there, etc.). And protests will **not** be effective at every single moment (even **if** the details regarding this were known, etc.). For the reasons mentioned, the matter is not worthwhile at all, even if there were **no other** matters of concern. Regarding the future as well, in such cases, one should know that the village must maintain its independence as much as possible. Opening a factory by someone else within the area of Kfar Chabad will certainly serve as a conduit for influences, etc., and the wise will understand.

By the way, regarding the aforementioned proposal, it is surely known to you that in most cases it also concerns matters of **health**, due to the remains of the meat, etc.

On this occasion, I wish to awaken you once again, and yet again, regarding what I have written many times to individuals and to many of anash: that it is most necessary to organize and form an *artel* (cooperative) from the people of the village themselves. There are many benefits in this, both material and spiritual, even though it is understood that this requires wholehearted cooperation; yet, for this reason alone, it is worth doing.

The importance of this matter increases many times over in connection with the fact that we are in the sixth year, on the eve of the Shmittah year. It is most surprising that in the minutes of the village committee, it does not appear that this issue is being discussed.

In continuation of the above, I do not know the custom in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, during the Shmittah year regarding bread, etc. Perhaps there is room for baking matzah in a way that it will be *shemurah* for the entire year, although, of course, this requires special machinery and packaging methods, etc.

With blessings for good tidings.

P.S.
The minutes from the 14th and 22nd of Shevat were received.

#### ***685***

**The matter is not worthwhile at all:** See something similar to this also above, Vol. 5, Letter 1800.

## 686

B"H, 3 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi Ephraim, may he live, Shochet and Bodek,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 26 Shevat:

1) Regarding how one should conduct oneself in the beis medrash concerning the silent Amidah and the Chazzan’s repetition when only six people have not yet davened:

The custom follows what is written in the Magen Avraham, Orach Chaim 69:4, which is brought as a halachic ruling in the Shulchan Aruch of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya—who is the authority on the hidden aspects of Torah—and in the Shulchan Aruch—the authority on the revealed aspects of Torah. They rule that one davens the silent Amidah and afterwards the Chazzan’s repetition is recited aloud. Regarding your reference to the Shaarei Teshuvah, siman 55, subsection 9, which copies the words of the Magen Avraham and writes "ten" instead of "six," it appears that a printing error occurred in the early editions: where a *vav* (6) was intended, a *yud* (10) was written. This is evident because many others who copy the words of the Magen Avraham all write "six," and they explain the reason: because it constitutes a majority of a minyan.

2) Regarding how one should conduct oneself during the reading of "Vayechal" on the four fast days: Below is a copy of what is printed in one of the kuntreisim.

On this occasion, I would like to encourage you regarding the observance of the three daily shiurim—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which are well known. We have heard many times from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that they are appropriate for every soul and are a segulah for many matters.

With blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
In the Kuntres Reshimot on Megillas Eichah, Likutei Minhagim, it states:

The reading of "Vayechal"—on the four fast days—is permitted even if there are only three people fasting in the beis medrash (Responsa Tzemach Tzedek, Shaar HaMiluim, 68). There is a discussion of this in the following responsa: Chasam Sofer, Orach Chaim 157; Maharam Schick, 289; Sdei Chemed, Pe'at HaSadeh, Asifat Dinim, Beis HaKnesses, 2, subsection 3; Tzafnat Paneach, Part 2, 31; Minchat Yitzchak, siman 65.

## 687

B"H, 3 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letters and the questions contained therein:

a) Sending a *shadar* (emissary) abroad: It seems I have already written several times that, in general, this is very correct. A definitive proof of this is that the vast majority of institutions in Eretz Yisrael *tichyeh* have been doing this for **many** years. However, as I have also written many times, it must be done in a way that does not cause confusion between one institution and another; rather, through cooperation and mutual understanding, they should easily coordinate all matters in a positive manner.

b) Regarding who should be the *shadar* and to which country: You must deliberate on this based on the individuals available and the suitability of the country. After all, in every country there are *anash*, especially in those countries where there is the greatest potential for success.

c) Regarding the time for laying the cornerstone, etc.: You must decide this on the spot, based on an assessment of which date in the near future is most auspicious. Furthermore—and this is the main point—there must be sufficient time for the necessary preparations.

d) When you have made a final decision regarding the date, inform me. *Bli neder*, I will write a general letter in connection with this. The matter has been delayed until now because, time and again, you have decided on a date for laying the cornerstone, only to have your decision canceled, etc.

e) In connection with what you write regarding the increase in the number of tourists in Eretz Yisrael *tichyeh*, especially in the coming months: I repeat once again what I have written to several Chabad institutions: to my astonishment, you are **completely** neglecting the matter of attracting tourists to visit the institutions in a way that would lead to a tangible contribution on their part. To my regret, this is a common denominator for all Chabad institutions in Eretz Yisrael *tichyeh*. Only in **extremely** rare cases have tourists been brought to visit their institutions, and even in those rare cases, the number of those whose visit led to actual action is **extremely** small. This is despite the fact that your institution has existed in Eretz Yisrael *tichyeh* for about ten years, and other Chabad institutions there have existed for even longer.

I do not know the details of the *Tomchei Temimim* schedule for the month of Nissan, but surely the committee will work out a detailed plan in due time, so that there will be no differences of opinion or confusion at the last minute.

With blessings for success in your holy work—for the establishment and development of the *Tomchei Temimim* under your administration—and may it be with true peace of mind.

**M. Schneerson**

## 601

B.H., 5 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and diligent, whose work is the work of Heaven,
R' Yosef, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

Following a long interval and silence, your two letters from the 3rd of Adar were received, along with the enclosures and the *pidyon nefesh*.

At an *eis ratzon*, I will mention you and all those you wrote about at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, each according to their specific needs as described in your letter. May it be the will of Hashem that very soon you will be able to share good news regarding the matters you wrote about.

I was especially pleased to read in your letter that although you find the matter difficult, you have promised to fulfill your commitment regarding the acquisition of the rooms soon. It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that when a Yid makes a pledge to *tzedakah* with a generous hand—meaning, it seems to him that it is beyond his means—if that is indeed the case, then at that very moment, the channels of *parnassah* are opened from Above so that he may fulfill his promise. One should add to the Rebbe’s words: since the Giver of the Torah and the Mitzvos commands us, "Serve Hashem with joy," and especially regarding the performance of *mitzvos*, it is clear that not only are the channels opened in a general sense, but the *parnassah* will be increased in a manner of joy. And we "bring about a merit through a meritorious person"—these days of the month of Adar, regarding which we are commanded to increase in joy. This will also increase the blessings of the *Ribono shel Olam* and your success in all the matters mentioned at the conclusion of *Midrash Esther Rabbah*—which are in abundance.

With blessings for good tidings regarding all the above, and also that you continue to utilize your talents specifically in the field of *chinuch* on the purity of holiness, and that your resolve to do so in the future remains firm. May it be the will of Hashem that in this, too, the saying will be fulfilled: "There is nothing that can stand before the will."

With blessings for a *Purim sameach*.

The *pidyon nefesh* was delivered to me by the *mashpia*, Rabbi Y.D. Groner, may he live—a gift of a photograph of a letter from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, dated 24 Teves 5743. Many thanks.

It is **most appropriate** that in your good camp, you should awaken each person—those whom you feel my father-in-law, the Rebbe, intended when he wrote "Anash" in his letter—regarding the content of this letter. You should suggest to each of them to take stock of the time that has passed since then (**fifteen years!** and in our era, as people say—the atomic age): what has been accomplished in the direction discussed in the letter, and what has been done in the opposite direction. Since you have merited to receive a letter that concerns the many—at the very least, the "poor of your city" are your responsibility. And the story of our Sages is well known (*Shabbos* 55a): if it is revealed before the *Ribono shel Olam* who did not accept the words, to whom is it revealed among people?

## 693

693

B”H, 6 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the Gemara shiur at the Tzemach Tzedek Nusach HaAri Synagogue, New York,
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings,

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the continuation of your communal Torah study, and that these days you are concluding Maseches Pesachim—a timely matter, thirty days before the Yom Tov.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in accordance with the conclusion of this Maseches, you merit the blessing of the Pesach and the blessing of the *zevach* (sacrifice) in the Mishnah, the blessing of *pidyon haben*, and the blessing of *Shehecheyanu* in the explanation of the Mishnah—which is the Gemara.

The offering of the Pesach and its significance are dependent upon *milah*, which is a prerequisite for them; therefore, they are of the same category, as the Mishnah states at the beginning of Maseches Kerisos. Their inner meaning is identical: the covenant (*kerisos bris*) between the Ribono shel Olam and Yisrael, which separates them from the nations (*milah*) and redeems the children of Yisrael from the *galus* (for all *galuyos* are called Mitzrayim). And the concept of the *zevach shelamim*—which brings peace into the world[a]—draws down spirituality into physicality; therefore, the meat is eaten by the Kohanim and also by the owners, an eating in the literal sense.

From this, we can understand the explanation in the Gemara and the relevance of *pidyon haben*, which is analogous to the aforementioned Pesach and *milah*: the redemption of the firstborn sons of Yisrael, together with the blessing of *Shehecheyanu*, which is recited specifically over good that is visible and revealed[b]. And the *halachah* is that the father of the son recites two blessings—He is our Father in Heaven.

May it be that speedily in our days, through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, He will redeem His firstborn son, Yisrael, from among the *galuyos*, and we will recite a new song before Him[c]—"This is our G-d"—as in the conclusion of Maseches Taanis, "Who has granted us life, sustained us, and brought us to this time."

With respect and blessings for good tidings,

P.S.
At a time of favor, I will mention all those whose names are listed in your letter at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

#### ***693***

**And the conclusion of this Maseches:** Regarding what follows, see also Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 11, p. 42 and onwards.

[a] Toras Kohanim to Vayikra 3:1.
[b] Tosafos, s.v. *Ha’oseh* (the second), Sukkah 46a.
[c] Tosafos, s.v. *Vene’emar*, Pesachim 116b.

## 694

[6 Adar 5718]

I received your letter in due time. Naturally, due to the distance, it is impossible for me to enter into the substance of the matter and the differences of opinion between you. It goes without saying that this situation has caused me great distress.

What is clear and imperative is that there must be peace among all those who are interested and involved in upholding and disseminating Yiddishkeit in your camp, and especially in the area of *chinuch* on *taharas hakodesh*. If they truly desire to bring hearts closer to one another so that peace may prevail among them, they will surely find the way to do so, for "as water reflects the face to the face, so is the heart of man to man." Then, Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted—He who is peace and makes peace in His high places, and who found no vessel that holds blessing other than peace—will grant His blessing of peace and will bestow blessing and success from on high, so that they may succeed in their *avodas hakodesh*, especially in the area of *chinuch hakasher*. Since this matter concerns the *chinuch* and the destiny of so many sons and daughters of Yisrael, every effort and endeavor in this regard is worthwhile.

Knowing that the esteemed and exalted *askan*, a man of stature with noble character traits who conducts his business with integrity, etc., etc., is currently in your camp and in your country, I am hopeful that through him, peace will sprout, grow, and increase in your camp, very soon.

## Vayikra

B"H, 7 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you ask how to conduct yourself according to Chabad customs.

Your question is not detailed enough, and the particulars of your environment are also missing. You should consult with the elders of Anash to whom you will present the aforementioned, and act according to their instruction.

2) You ask what the root of your soul is Above.

It is well known that our holy Torah teaches that Hashem did not create a single thing in His world in vain. This also applies to the knowledge a person requires: he must know the matters upon which his Torah and mitzvos depend, as well as the ways to fulfill them. But as for your question, what practical difference does it make? You have the Shulchan Aruch before you, which states everything you are required to do; what business do you have with hidden things?

3) You request assistance for studying Torah in both Nigleh and Nistar.

The statement of our Sages is well known: "If you have labored and not found, do not believe." Consequently, it depends on you to toil in Torah and be meticulous in the fulfillment of mitzvos, and then Hashem will grant you success.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 6,097

B"H, 7 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs,
R' Shmuel Elazar, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated 26 Shevat. At an auspicious time, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for each according to their needs, as appropriate to the content of your letter...

Regarding what you wrote concerning the agreement involving Israeli ships: while generally one should not express an opinion as long as there is no definitive information, it appears from a newspaper clipping that it is questionable whether this is a rectification or the opposite. For it is a clear matter that the journey itself—and not merely the docking—is forbidden, as it is bound up with work that is **d'oraisa** (prohibited by Torah law), etc. This constitutes a public desecration of Shabbos according to the Torah, which carries the implications regarding the wine and bread [of those involved], etc., as explained in the Shulchan Aruch. What, then, is the utility of a *mashgiach* in this? Furthermore, this leads to the result that, on the contrary, the approval of a *mashgiach* by a Rabbi is, etc. I will await clearer information.

May it be the will of Hashem that, in the end, they recognize that the name **"Holy"** Land—which has been affirmed and accepted even by the nations of the world—is not a reference to the past, similar to the claim of those days that "their G-d is old" (also in the sense of being aged and obsolete). Rather, these matters are eternal in daily life, and they stand in their **full power**. Therefore, in a place where the hand of Israel is strong, or at the very least in a place where the hand of the nations of the world is not strong, all matters of our holy Torah apply **with full force**. And if they have said that Shabbos is equivalent to the entire Torah (Yerushalmi, Nedarim 3:5), then this statement of our Sages is not to be taken out of its simple meaning, with all the consequences that this entails. It is distressing to speak of such alarming matters, and the alarm is all the greater because no one is setting their heart to do anything to rectify the situation, nor even to clearly state the *psak din* (halachic ruling). If they did so, there would at least be no room for deception, and the matters would be clarified and resolved—"Are you for us," etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that, just as in those days, so too in this time, when many of the peoples of the land are becoming Jewish, the results will now be seen: that our religion is different from every other nation—not merely in theoretical intellect or in hidden chambers, but in practical life and in the public eye.

With blessings.

## 698

698

B"H, 7 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter has been received (though it was difficult to decipher your name from your signature), in which you write regarding a certain woman whose husband lacks *koach gavra* (potency), and you ask my opinion as to whether she must divorce, etc.

First and foremost, it is necessary to clarify with expert physicians whether there is a remedy for the husband of the aforementioned woman, for in recent years, several new types of medical treatments have been added in this field, some of which are proven and successful, and it is possible that they could be utilized regarding the husband in question. Naturally, every effort and endeavor in this regard is worthwhile. If, *chas v'shalom*, the aforementioned treatments are not suitable in this specific case, a *shailas rav* (rabbinic inquiry) must be made. Since you do not mention the nature of the relationship between the husband and wife, I assume that if the matter were to lead to divorce, there would be no obstacles from the husband's side.

May it be His will that you are able to share good news.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 609

B"H, 7 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the avreich Maimon, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
Since you have already asked here this time, the answer is: The "foundation of fire" mentioned in Tanya, beginning of Chapter 19, is explained there itself as being located beneath the sphere of the moon, and not as you write in your letter, that it is in the moon itself. See also Midrash Bamidbar Rabbah, Chapter 14:12, near the end, that it surrounds the entire world and is above it. See also the Yad HaChazakah of the Rambam, Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah, end of Chapter 3.

2) Regarding the explanation of the verses: "And she called his name Reuven" (for several reasons, among them) "for she said, 'For He has seen...'"

However, regarding Shimon: "And she said, 'For He has heard' (and therefore) 'she called his name Shimon.'" With this, the question of Chazal (Berachos 7b) regarding the reason for the name Reuven is understood, whereas they did not ask this regarding the other tribes. Likewise, it is understood why Rashi brings this drashah in his commentary on the Torah — because it is necessary for the **peshat** of the verses. See the sefer Tzeror HaMor.

***609***

**Maimon:** Sabag, Kfar Chabad.

## 621

621

B”H, 8 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Shevat, in which you write:

1) Regarding your situation in the fulfillment of mitzvos, where it seems to you that you want to do teshuvah, but it is not helping.

It is a known ruling of our Torah, the Torah of life, that there is nothing that can stand before teshuvah. Certainly, what you feel as mentioned above is a temptation of the yetzer hara, which wants to influence you toward low spirits and despair, chas v’shalom, as you write. You should study in the holy Tanya in the places that explain how sadness is refuted, so that a person’s heart should not fall if he sees that he is in a battle with the yetzer. You should look in the index of topics at the end of the Kehot edition of Tanya.

2) Regarding your question on the matters of shidduchim, how to approach this, and how to know that this is the [correct] zivug.

The instruction of our holy Torah is known in this as well: that a person must engage in the natural way (and it is understood that this should be in a manner of modesty according to the Shulchan Aruch) in searching for a shidduch, and the Creator of the world, who watches over each and every one with hashgacha pratis, will guide him to find the zivug that is good for him.

It is my hope that you are not only meticulous yourself in the fulfillment of mitzvos, but that you also influence your friends in this, and not like those who make the terrible mistake that when one is in the army, it is impossible, chas v’shalom, to fulfill Torah and mitzvos. This, too, is one of the stratagems of the yetzer hara, which wants to trap a person in its net. Yet, the verse explicitly states that, on the contrary—a person who is in the army must increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos. Upon this depends the success of the individual, and furthermore, upon this depends the success of the many and the army as a whole. As it is said: "For Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp, to save you and to give your enemies before you; therefore your camp shall be holy, that He see no unseemly thing among you, and turn away from you" (Devarim 23:15). From this it is understood that salvation and the delivery of the enemy can occur **specifically** when "Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp," and if not, this causes, chas v’shalom, "and turn away from you," which leads to the opposite results, chas v’shalom. If you encounter any difficulties in matters of Torah and mitzvos, my strong hope is that when you turn to the military chaplain, the matter will certainly be arranged, especially since, as mentioned, this concerns the **entire** army, and there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 604

B"H, 10 Adar, 5718.
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Shevat (for "man is the tree of the field").

In it, you write regarding a proposal of marriage with a young woman who has found favor in your eyes, and surely your intention is that her fear of Hashem is as is fitting for a kosher daughter of Israel.

However, her name is the same as your mother’s name, and you conclude by noting that you are a student at Yeshivas Porat Yosef.

If, as mentioned above, her fear of Hashem is as it should be, and you both resolve with the necessary firmness to build a home in Israel upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, you should add a name to her. Naturally, you should establish this name during a *Mi Sheberach* blessing when a family member is called to the Torah, or the like. Then—all is well. Thirty days after the first time the additional name is established, you may conclude the matter, and may it be in a good and auspicious hour. You are surely aware of the response of the Tzemach Tzedek, which is based as well on the halachic ruling of his grandfather, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya (who rules in the hidden aspects of Torah) and the Shulchan Aruch (who rules in the revealed aspects of Torah), that when the names are not identical, there is no room for concern at all.

Furthermore, all that has been said applies even to Ashkenazim; but among the Sephardim, it is well known that many communities do not concern themselves at all with the names of a bride and her mother-in-law being the same.

You surely know of the three daily portions of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya; in any event, you should keep to them from here on.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 6105

B"H, 10 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, along with the *pidyon nefesh* that will be read at an auspicious time at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, in which you write the main points of your current activities in upholding and disseminating matters of Yiddishkeit, as well as the status of the organization you founded.

Regarding what you wrote—that you have not exerted much effort for the *bochurim* who have never studied in a *yeshivah*, seeing as even the *yeshivah* students themselves are in need of strengthening—it is not understood what the contradiction is between these two matters. On the contrary, we see tangibly that when one is tasked with the responsibility of upholding the love of Torah and *yiras shamayim* for others, this itself adds strength to the person himself, in the language of our Sages: "that he should be moist in order to moisten others."

And regarding what you wrote about the material state of the organization—that expenses exceed income—naturally, one should not be discouraged by this. For such is the way of Torah and proper *askanus*: one elevates in holiness and adds [to the work], rather than restricting the matters according to the state of the treasury.

Regarding what you wrote about covering the hair: I have already expressed my opinion on this many times. In our generation, may Hashem have mercy, a covering with a *mitpachat* (tichel) does not hold up, because **each and every time**, the woman faces a test—whether to cover every hair or only part of them, etc.—because she does not want to be embarrassed before those who mock (even if they are only in her imagination, or sometimes even in reality). This is not the case with wearing a *sheitel*; it is impossible to remove the *sheitel* when one is at a party or the like. Especially as you write that she will shave her hair and you both agree on this, this is the most correct path. As for walking with the *sheitel* uncovered, for several generations now, there has been no concern at all regarding this. Of course, the matter must be clarified in your location to ensure it does not constitute a *pirtzah*, *chas v'shalom*, but the matter itself is understood: the arrangement of shaving and wearing a *sheitel* is incomparably better than other methods.

Certainly, as you write in your letter, you have already begun teaching a *shiur* in *Tanya* and *Chassidus* in public; you should increase this, and the merit of the public will assist you.

In response to your notification regarding the condition of your wife, *tichyeh*:

May the *Ribono shel Olam* fulfill her days of pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child, at its proper time, properly and with ease.

With blessings for good tidings and a happy and active Purim.

## 6.

B"H, 11 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding your nature and that you do not know how to change it, because, as you phrase it in your letter, this matter is so deeply rooted in you, etc.,

The instruction of the Torah is well known: "A person should always occupy himself with Torah and mitzvos, even if not for their own sake (*shelo lishmah*), for from [doing them] not for their own sake, one comes to [doing them] for their own sake" [though, obviously, this is not at all a matter of *hiddur* (a superior level of service), and furthermore, there are many levels within *shelo lishmah*, and it is possible to fulfill the requirement of our Sages of blessed memory mentioned above, even at the most subtle of levels].

What is clear is that one must be persistent and diligent in his study, and likewise regarding the performance of mitzvos. As our Sages of blessed memory state, "A person should always occupy himself with Torah and mitzvos, even if not for their own sake," etc. Among the mitzvos, and the most essential of them, is the *avodah* of *tefillah*, which brings healing to all of a person’s affairs when he performs his *avodah* step by step, as it is written, "Little by little I will drive them out," as is also explained in *Tanya* in several places.

The conclusion from the above is that you must study with persistence and diligence—in the well-known expression, "study with ease"—both in *nigleh* and in *Chassidus*, and be meticulous in the performance of mitzvos. **It is simple** that all of this can be done without affecting your physical health (for this, too, is one of the temptations of the *yetzer hara*—to interfere with one’s health in order to subsequently weaken one’s *avodah*). For the time being, you should divert your attention from the matter about which you write, as sometimes the contemplation of this very subject also stems from an impure source, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 607

607

B"H, 11 Adar, 5718

Brooklyn.

...Regarding what you wrote concerning the well-known principle that "a prisoner cannot free himself," it must be that this does not apply to this matter, for our Sages have commanded us to search—specifically like a person seeking his lost object—that is to say, with the greatest possible energy. May it be His will that the commandment of the holy Torah regarding the month of Adar, to "increase in joy," be fulfilled in a tangible way. The intention here is for joy that is good in a revealed and manifest sense (as is explained regarding the distinction between Purim and Chanukah), and indeed, the entire miracle in this instance, though it occurred through nature, came about through a match and marriage.

## 608

B"H, 11 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing and distinguished, engaged in communal needs, R' Hillel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Yisro. It is understood that the beginning of your letter—which attempts to excuse the absence of a farbrengen on the bright day of 19 Kislev, the day of victory and redemption, by claiming that the Chabad shul here has been emptied of its elders, etc.—is not only insufficient to excuse the matter, but on the contrary, it only intensifies the difficulty.

For it is the duty of a true communal activist, and especially a Rav within his community, not only to speak to the "ears that hear" which were prepared by the activists and leaders who preceded him, but to influence the youth and the younger generation so that they, too, become "ears that hear" and follow in the footsteps of the elders. We see tangibly that in recent years, there has been a loosening in this work, as the youth and the younger generation have been shaken by events and the many upheavals. Therefore, there is no need to uproot something from its growth to plant it in a new place, for they have already been uprooted from their place regardless. And as the well-known expression of Chazal states, that he "confused the entire world"—this is not necessarily through physical relocation, but also through the emptying of a place and the shaking of its foundations from within. The youth and the younger generation, with their well-known ideals, have realized that what they previously considered a foundation is actually empty.

Regarding what you noted concerning the matter of a birthday, and that the proof from the Yerushalmi (Rosh Hashanah 3:6) does not appear to you to be relevant to the matter, and you substitute it with proofs from other places—I am puzzled on two points: 1) In the Yerushalmi, it is explicit that one’s *mazal* is stronger on that day; 2) In all the other places you noted, there is **no hint whatsoever** of this.

With blessings for a happy Purim and for good tidings regarding the above.

## 611

B"H, 13 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with great sorrow that I read your *pan* sent on the 10th of Adar. It is surely unnecessary to explain the reason for this sorrow, as you undoubtedly have a copy of the *pan* in which the lack of activity with others is highlighted and emphasized. No less distressing—and perhaps even more so—is the lack of activity regarding yourselves, which is highlighted by the opposite of *kiruv halevavos* (drawing hearts together).

Now, one does not cry over the past. May it be Hashem’s will that from here on, hearts will be drawn together as much as is necessary, and that you will increase your courage regarding yourselves and regarding others, in the manner explained in many places. Since it is known from the outset that "no one shall be cast away from Him," and it is inevitable that it must be accomplished in every single place—for the command of our Rebbeim, our *nesi'im*, regarding the *hafatzas hama'ayanos chutzah* (spreading the wellsprings outward) is a decree, and as our Sages of blessed memory said regarding the verse "G-d who completes for me," that Torah changes even the reality of nature—there is no benefit in delaying the matter from day to week, and from week to month, etc. Since, in the end, it will have to be done by a certain person, it is better that they do it as soon as possible, and specifically with joy and a good heart.

Especially since we are currently in days of *segulah* (spiritual auspiciousness), particularly for the aforementioned matters. For it is explained in the *sefarim* that one of the reasons for the mitzvah of Purim—through *mishloach manos*, etc.—is to increase the *kiruv halevavos* of all *Bnei Yisrael* toward one another, even to the *evyonim* (the destitute), which is even lower than a *ani* (poor person), and "there is no poor person except in knowledge." This is the concept of *hafatzas hama'ayanos chutzah*, and even to the "outside of the outside," and *kal v'chomer*. When you decide this with the strength of complete *da'as*, you will surely see success immediately. This is in line with what is explained regarding *nisyonos* (trials): when one does not pay attention to the trial, one sees that it was only a trial and not a reality, and only the benefit remains, as it is said, "For Hashem your G-d is testing you..."—which also means *menaseh* in the sense of *arim nesi* (raising a banner), meaning elevation and transcendence.

May it be Hashem’s will that from here on, the theme of "light, joy, gladness, and honor" will be the content of all the tidings that arrive from your camp.

With blessings for good tidings and a happy Purim holiday.

## 612

B"H, 13 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote, that you were offered to appear in various places in the name of Chabad, and you felt that you were not yet worthy of this, and that the matters you would be speaking about are too wondrous for you, etc.:

It is surely superfluous to explain that this is one of the temptations of the *yetzer*. It is similar to what is explained in the *Reshimot* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding Torah (and the same applies to our situation): even the greatest of the great cannot exhaust matters to their ultimate end, for "its measure is longer than the earth and broader than the sea" (*Iyov 11:9*). Even the simplest of the simple among the Jewish people has a portion in Torah, and consequently, an understanding of it as well. Especially since Divine Providence has placed you in a proper, holy upbringing, you have certainly been given the capabilities to fulfill the task. Although, of course, you are also included among the Jewish people, all of whom are commanded to go "from strength to strength" and to "increase in holiness"—which itself is proof that they have not yet reached the level of perfection and are lacking even in their service of Hashem compared to the state of yesterday versus tomorrow—provided that one's time is... a time of *avodah* for oneself and *avodah* with others.

There are those who justify their attitude toward their task by saying that their words will not be accepted since they are not worthy due to their feelings of the heart and the like. But it is well known that we must "accept the truth from whoever says it" (*Avos 4:1*), even if one is correct in his assessment of his own status. And this is doubtful—for a person is biased toward himself, and therefore he sometimes tilts the judgment to the right, but sometimes also to the left, and *kal v'chomer* (it is understood).

The central point in all such matters is that we are **workers of the day**, as the Tzemach Tzedek said, "to illuminate," and as it is written, "And G-d called the light Day" (*Bereishis 1:5*). It is like a laborer: when the employer assigns him to his work, he is certainly fit for this work. Furthermore, it is not the laborer's business to investigate and inquire why the employer did not choose a different laborer, etc.—and the analogy is understood.

With blessings for success in your holy work in all the above, and for good tidings regarding those you influence, and certainly regarding yourself.

With blessings for a happy Purim and for good tidings in this.

...Regarding your question as to why it is specifically through a "leap" (*dilug*) that the physical can be brought into being from the spiritual—the explanation is in the word itself: a **leap** over the "natural" order, over what is possible according to the *Seder Hishtalshelus*.

The reason is that just as a leap (in the literal sense) requires greater strength than walking from step to step, so it is with the aforementioned creation. And let this be known: there are levels in a leap—a leap, a jump, etc. See *Likutei Torah*, *Shir HaShirim* 15b.

## 613

613

B”H, 15 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter.

We bring merit through meritorious days—the days of the month of Adar, regarding which we were commanded in our holy Torah, the Torah of life, to increase in joy. This is especially true regarding the central point, the days of Purim (which we have just passed), when a person is obligated to become intoxicated until they do not know.

Just as with all times of *ratzon*, the matters of these days must be drawn down into the days and times that follow them, in such a way that their effect is recognizable in *b’po'al* (in practice), as the *Mishnah* states: The deed is the essential thing.

Since we have been commanded regarding this, and the *Ribono shel Olam* does not deal unjustly with His creatures, it is certain that from Above, everything necessary is being done to draw down revealed and manifest good (and certainly to remove all concealments and hiddenness), so that the joy during these days should be in abundance—"until they do not know"—and that its impression should be recognizable afterward, as mentioned above, and that they should draw down the blessings of *Hashem*: good in abundance, kindness in abundance, etc., as enumerated by our Sages in *Midrash Rabbah* at the conclusion of *Esther Rabbah*.

With blessings for good tidings.
