## 614

614

B”H, 17 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 15 Adar, Shushan Purim, in which you write regarding your situation in ruchniyus and ask for advice on the matter, etc.,

Surely you have the Sefer Tanya with you; you will find there an answer to all your questions. Certainly, you have the Tanya with the index of topics, which will make the searching easier.

Regarding what you ask—based on what is recounted in sefarim and also orally—about those who in their younger years were illuyim and gedolim b’Yisrael:

In general, what is the utility of asking questions as to why "their opinions are not equal"? Especially as explained in Tanya, beginning of Chapter 4, that the grasp of Torah is dependent upon one’s capacity for comprehension and the root of his neshamah Above. And as is also explained in Chapter 30 regarding the Mishnah, "Be humble of spirit before every person," that everyone has their own advantage relative to another. Likewise, it is mentioned in Iggeres HaKodesh, end of Siman 7, that the success of a specific person in a specific mitzvah is because "so it arose in His Will, may He be blessed."

I am surprised by your entire stance, for the purpose of a person is not to surpass and be greater than another, but as the Mishnah states, "I was created to serve my Maker." If HaKadosh Baruch Hu desires that one person should be great in the mitzvah of tzedakah and another in Torah, and the like, everyone must fulfill the intent of the Creator for which they were designated.

It is self-understood that this is said only regarding (Iggeres HaKodesh, ibid.) encouragement and preference, but all Yidden are obligated in all 613 mitzvos, and "Talmud Torah is equivalent to them all."

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S.
Surely you know of the three daily shiurim—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and in any case, you will observe them from now on, and also give a few cents to tzedakah every weekday morning before davening.

## 615

B"H, 17 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Reshet in the Holy Land, may it be built and established,
May Hashem keep them alive,

Peace and blessing!

In response to the letter written by the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing man, R' Yitzchak Ginsburgh, may he live, in which he transcribes a letter from Mr. ... may he live. Its content is that he is prepared to recommend handing over a school to the Chabad Reshet under three conditions: that the education be co-educational; that the teachers not engage in political matters; and that there be instructors from Chabad who will cooperate closely with the youth committee of the Tnuat HaMoshavim, etc. The Reshet administration asks for my opinion regarding the above.

Regarding all three points, the answer is **simple and absolute:**

a) Regarding the matter of co-education, we have spoken about this many times: this is the essence of **chinuch**. This is not only from a religious perspective, but also from a moral perspective. The recognition of this point is spreading even among non-Jews and non-religious people, as can be seen in the United States and several other countries, due to the tangible results seen from co-educational schooling. Even if one were to say that in an exceptional case, at a very young age and for a very short time, one could turn a blind eye to a certain place or a certain class, how can one agree when the matter of co-education is presented in the plan as a principled condition, contrary to the Shulchan Aruch?!

b) The same applies to point b. The Chabad approach is well-known: it has no involvement whatsoever with politics of any kind. It is also surprising that this is a condition on their part, since it is a condition on the part of Chabad that they will not involve themselves in any political matters whatsoever, whether from the right or from the left.

c) The same applies to point c, as it is in **complete** contradiction to what was stated in the previous point b. The youth committee of the Tnuat HaMoshavim has several political lines in its program, which is in absolute contradiction to point b, that Chabad does not involve itself in any matters of politics. Certainly, they will not change the program of the youth committee in those places where there will be a Chabad school to be an exception from the rest of the moshavim of the Tnuat HaMoshavim. It is obvious that the demand that Chabad include Chabad students in a national youth gathering organized by the Tnuat HaMoshavim—which has a **distinctly** political character, as is known from the past and present, and is part of their general work program—is unacceptable. The conclusion of the clause, that they will take into account the religious needs of the participants, does not rectify the matter at all, for it is possible to provide for religious needs one hundred percent while simultaneously being a politician for various parties; the program of the gathering and its results will bear a distinctly political stamp.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 616

B"H, 17 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Friday, in which you ask about the root of your soul Above, in connection with what is written in Tanya, Chapter 4:

I have already responded regarding such matters, that a person should exert himself in knowledge that assists and adds to the fulfillment of his role in the world, as the Mishnah states: "I was created to serve my Maker." This is not the case with the knowledge you mentioned—what practical difference does it make to him? Our focus in Torah study is explicitly detailed in the Laws of Torah Study regarding diligence and perseverance in learning. What is written in Tanya there is an explanation as to why the intellectual grasp of all Bnei Yisrael is not equal. Furthermore, even the grasp of Tzaddikim who serve Hashem all their days is also varied; the explanation for this is that they differ in their capacity for comprehension and the root of their soul Above.

I was pleased to hear of your participation in the Tanya shiur studied in a group, but it is understood simply that this is not sufficient at all. Certainly, in addition to what was mentioned, you should have shiurim for yourself every day, at the very least for a short duration according to your ability. May it be His will that in this, too, the commandment of the Torah to "increase in holiness" will be fulfilled, and "there is nothing that can stand before the will."

I trust you are keeping the three well-known daily shiurim of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, and in any case, you should keep them from here on out.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita

## 6117

B"H, 18 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you via the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, a man of many accomplishments, R' Shlomo Zalman Katzenelenbogen, along with your contribution. Since it was received during the days when we collect for *Maos Chittim*, your contribution was directed to the *Maos Chittim* fund, from which we assist the needy with *Kimcha D'Pischa*.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate on what is explicitly written in Scripture: "Is it not to share your bread with the hungry..." (Yeshayahu 58:7), and "do not hide yourself from your own flesh." My intention in this is as follows: Even though *tzedakah* is equivalent to all the *mitzvos* combined, every Jew is commanded to observe all 613 *mitzvos*—meaning 612 *mitzvos* in addition to the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah*. It is understood that the fulfillment of *mitzvos* is for the benefit of the person performing them, and he was given the powers from above to be able to fulfill them. If this applies to every single Jew, how much more so does it apply to those who have merited to study in the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim—which, as I have heard, includes you. In these yeshivos, our Rebbeim, our Nesi'im, drew down immense powers and a unique vitality into the education and its methods. And since they (I refer to our Nesi'im) were also, in the literal sense, excellent and experienced educators, it is certain that all of this was done in a manner that its impression would be recognizable and effective even many years after leaving the yeshiva. As our Sages of blessed memory summarized: "Throw a stick into the air, and it will land on its base."

It would please me to receive news from you from time to time regarding the above. It is understood that you may write in whichever language is easier for you, or convey information through others.

With blessings for health and for good tidings in all the above.

## 618

B"H, 19 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Sunday.

At a time of favor, I will mention you and your husband, *shichye*, at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya*, regarding the contents of your letter, and in particular for good health and the matter of the apartment.

It is surely unnecessary to point out that every person has important matters that come first, and less important matters that come in second or third place. Among the most important are *nachas* from children, *shichye*, and health. Even if these other, secondary or tertiary matters are not quite in order, one must not overlook the primary, important matters.

In your case, this is also true: Hashem Yisbarach has shown you—*bli ayin hara*—His great *chessed* with Yiddishe *nachas* from children and grandchildren, as well as in health. Especially when you compare this to the situation as it was previously, one must give praise and thanks to Hashem Yisbarach every day for His great *chassadim*. Furthermore, and even more importantly, you should strengthen your *bitachon* in Hashem Yisbarach even more, knowing that in the future as well, you will see the *brachos* of Hashem and His *hatzlacha* in what you require. Therefore, there is no reason to take the apartment problem to heart; it will certainly resolve itself in the best possible way, in truth, even if a person cannot always calculate how.

Therefore, as an answer to your question regarding the apartment, in my opinion, you should proceed in a normal fashion. Do not search for an apartment in a rush, but do not take it to heart. In any case, this is only relevant in practice for after Pesach. If a good opportunity arises before Pesach, it might be worthwhile, as you would then save yourself the work of making the old apartment *Pesach'dik*.

But the main thing, as mentioned above, is to strengthen yourself in *bitachon* in Hashem, and then you will see His *bracha* and *hatzlacha*.

With blessings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,
Secretary

P.S. Regarding what you wrote about paying off the debt, there is certainly no reason to take that to heart. When your *parnassah* becomes more comfortable, you will continue the payments.

## 619

619

B"H, 19 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write about several points regarding your life history, and conclude with the problem of your younger son, may he live, who has many fine qualities, but lacks the will and patience for learning, etc.

In such cases, one can only be assured of success when one is in an environment where *limudei kodesh* are studied with *hasmadah* and *shekidah* for the majority of the day. Therefore, it would be appropriate, if possible, that at least for a certain period of time, he should go to study in one of the yeshivos in Europe where they study *limudei kodesh* throughout the day (and surely you can influence him to do this, since it is only a matter of a certain period of time). Only after that can one see the effect of such an environment on him and come to a conclusion as to whether he truly lacks the will and desire, as you write, or whether the good environment and the yeshiva can change this for the better.

If it turns out that even this does not bring about learning with *hasmadah* and *shekidah*, it is well known what is explained in our holy Torah in several places: that among Jews there are different categories, even among those who are *shomrei Torah u'mitzvos*. There are those whose primary focus is being *talmidei chachamim*, who occupy themselves more with learning (even though they also fulfill all the *mitzvos*), and there are those who primarily dedicate themselves to fulfilling *mitzvos* (even though they also have fixed *shiurim* to study Torah every day). One can be a *gadol b'Yisrael* and bring benefit to oneself and to the *klal* in either of these two categories. May Hashem Yisbarach help you to have true *nachas* from him, which is Jewish *nachas* in all respects.

You should have the *tefillin* of your son checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home, to ensure that they are all *kosher* according to the *din*. And may Mrs. ... *tichyeh* maintain the good custom of *bnos Yisrael hakesheirois* to give *tzedakah* each time before lighting candles on *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*.

With blessings for good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 620

620

B”H, 20 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the chairmen, activists, and participants in the 16th annual campaign undertaking for Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal,
May Hashem protect them and may they live.

Shalom u’Bracha!

On the occasion of your annual dinner event, which is scheduled, G-d willing, for Thursday, 21 Adar, I extend my greetings to all the chairmen, activists, and guests, as well as to all the friends of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, may they live.

We are only one week past Purim, and for everyone, the lessons learned from Purim should still be fresh in memory, and this must have an impact on the daily life of the individual and the collective.

One of the wondrous accounts of the mesiras nefesh of the Jews during the time of Mordechai and Esther is that, despite the difficult experiences of that terrible decree, Mordechai gathered twenty-two thousand Jewish children and taught them Torah. And in that merit, the Ribono shel Olam helped so that the entire Jewish people were saved.

The Megillas Esther, like the entire Torah, is eternal. What is recounted there has significance in all places and at all times.

Therefore, these days should specifically remind each and every one of us how much we must dedicate ourselves with all our strength to provide the opportunity for all Jewish children to learn Torah al taharas hakodesh and to be raised to fulfill the mitzvos with mesiras nefesh.

I hope that all those present at the dinner will demonstrate their great awareness of this holy task, and will support Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal with the greatest generosity, thereby strengthening the existence of the Jewish community, may they live, in Montreal in particular, and in the entire world in general.

And may the merit of this stand for each and every one of you and your families, may they live, to be blessed by Hashem Yisbarach with everything needed, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

With blessings for all the best.

## 6,121

B"H, 20 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote about the matter of the ships (and surely you have received a copy of the questions in English), although you do not mention this, the situation is becoming more and more alarming. On one hand, it is becoming increasingly clear that there are additional prohibitions due to further types of work on the ships, which are not conducted automatically—even though, given current technology, it would have been possible to make them so. On the other hand, especially in connection with the current propaganda, the number of those inciting others to transgress this prohibition has grown, even in ways that cannot be justified even by those who seek leniency.

For example, they are organizing a special voyage for members of one of the "religious parties." That is to say, the overwhelming majority of the passengers on this ship will be traveling solely for pleasure, and specifically those who identify with a religious party and are traveling "only for the sake of Heaven." In this case, all arguments for leniency are null and void from the outset, even if it were a ship owned by non-Jews, operated by a non-Jewish crew, and departing on the first day of the week.

What is most alarming about this entire matter, beyond the actual conduct of public and wholesale Chilul Shabbos, is that there is no one who opens their mouth or chirps a protest. As one individual here, who carries the title of Rabbi (and, naturally, belongs to a "religious party"), explained regarding traveling on an Israeli ship: they are prepared to engage in mesiras nefesh for this matter, for they are G-d-fearing and tremble at His word, His Torah, and His holy land. I remarked, by way of sharp wit, that he is correct that this is indeed **true** mesiras nefesh. For mesiras nefesh in the conventional sense means that one sacrifices the **body** (so that the soul may be elevated through the sanctification of Hashem by fulfilling His Torah and mitzvos). In contrast, the conduct described here is a sacrifice of the soul—killing it through public Chilul Shabbos, the punishment for which is skilah—so that the body may "ascend" to a certain place in a certain manner...

May it be the will of Hashem that, just as many miracles were performed for our ancestors in those days at this time, there will at least be a miracle—that "it was turned around," and there will be "light"—this is Torah—shining in every matter and corner. For "the fear of the Jews fell upon them," as interpreted by the Rema—a decisor in Israel—in his book *Mechir Yayin*: that the fear which the Jews feel, i.e., the fear of Hashem, fell upon them.

With blessings for good tidings.

#### ***6,121***

**The ships:** See also above, Letter 5,898, and the references in the notes there.

## 6122

B"H, 20 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning the path of teshuvah, first and foremost I must preface a point regarding the concept of teshuvah from the teachings of Chassidus. One of its foundations is the matter of simcha and complete, absolute bitachon in the Creator of the world and its Guide.

The concept of teshuvah is not necessarily only for a sin; rather—and this is the central point in **all** types of teshuvah—it is the return to the source and the beginning of everything, to the Elokus that created us, through a way of life consistent with the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life. This is the common denominator in all forms of teshuvah, from the lightest of the light to the tzaddik of all tzaddikim, for all of whom there is an obligation of teshuvah.

When one does not know the specifics of what to repent for or in what manner to repent, the aforementioned is the path that encompasses everything. It is certainly superfluous to elaborate that a way of life according to the Torah is not limited to Rosh Hashanah, Yom Kippur, Shabbos, and Yom Tov, but rather applies to daily life in the literal sense. After all, the weekdays are greater in quantity than the days of Shabbos and Yom Tov, and they are the ones that require additional caution.

But as stated, all of this can be done—and must be done—out of simcha and bitachon. May it be His will that I hear good news in your upcoming letters regarding yourself and your household, and likewise from all the members of the family, shlita.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 6123

6123

B”H, 20 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregants of the Adas Yisroel Synagogue in Manchester,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive the news that your shul has settled into its new home in a good and auspicious hour. Since we are currently in the time between Purim and Pesach, the months of simcha and geulah, I wish you that your avodas Hashem be conducted with simcha—specifically the avodah of tefillah. For the concept of tefillah is also one of Yetzias Mitzrayim and geulah, as is explained in Toras HaChassidus. I hope that your beis knesses will also be a beis medrash for the study of Torah and Chassidus, not only on Shabbos and Yom Tov, but at least several times during the week as well, in order to bring holiness into the weekdays and all matters of daily life.

I especially wish to convey to you what was discussed this Purim regarding the verse, "And many of the people of the land became Jews" (*Esther 8:17*). Beyond the literal meaning, there is a deeper significance for every Yid. Since life is a neshamah within a guf, there are matters pertaining to the guf in which the concept of "people of the land" (*am ha'aretz*) is expressed—these are matters of eating and drinking, business, and the needs of the guf in general. The Torah demands that a Yid distinguish himself not only while studying Torah, davening, and performing mitzvos, but also during the time of business, eating, drinking, and so on. Business should be conducted according to Torah, with kashrus, without encroaching on others' livelihoods, without lashon hara about a competitor, and the like. Eating and drinking should also be according to Torah, in the proper measure and with the proper kavanah—in addition to kashrus, of course. This is the general concept of "In all your ways know Him" (*Mishlei 3:6*), as explained in the Rambam and Tur Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, siman 231.

A Yid’s day begins with davening—with the morning blessings at home and tefillah b’tzibur in the beis knesses. After tefillah comes a shiur in Torah, and only then do the matters of "in all your ways" begin (*Tur Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, siman 155, 156*). From this, it is understood that the beis knesses must be structured in such a way that its influence penetrates and illuminates one's conduct throughout the entire day.

May it be Hashem’s will that soon, from your new shul—which is a mikdash me'at—you will merit, together with all of Klal Yisroel, to go to the Third Beis Hamikdash, which will be built in the true and complete geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings for all the best,

**M. Schneerson**

## 624

B.H., 20 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Eliezer Steinman,

Greetings and blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your two books, *Yalkut Meshalim, etc., for the People and the Youth* and *Gan HaChassidus*. Thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending them here; I trust you will do the same with your future publications. I assume the books sent to you from here have arrived.

I read with interest your introduction to your book *Yalkut for the People and the Youth* regarding parables. I do not recall at this moment whether your books include the Chabad perspective on the role of parables in Torah and in Chassidic literature in general. This is, of course, a significant topic, as the Torah encompasses the Oral Torah until the end of all generations—everything that a veteran student is destined to innovate based on the foundations of the tradition that ascends in holiness up to Moshe Rabbeinu.

The concept of a parable in Torah is that it is impossible for a parable not to have a connection to the subject it illustrates, as it **descended** from it. For example, a parable involving a king of flesh and blood—how much more so regarding the King, the Ribono shel Olam. The validity of the parable exists because the sovereignty of the earth has its root in the sovereignty of the heavens. This is true for all parables and examples in Torah. This is also precise in the short aphorism in Tanya, beginning of Chapter 3, which discusses the human soul and explains that the *nefesh, ruach,* and *neshamah* are comprised of ten faculties corresponding to the ten supernal *Sefiros*, adding the reason: "that they descended from them." This is the way of all parables. This core idea is explained in several places; for example, in *Torah Or*, Parshas Mikeitz (42b, column 2), in the explanation of what is said about King Shlomo, "And he spoke three thousand parables"—that these are three thousand levels, one above the other, in that same subject itself. As the *Zohar* puts it, "this is the brain for that, and this is the peel for that," and in the words of *Torah Or* there: "The subject being illustrated is the spirituality of the lower level, and from it, the physicality of the higher level descended, etc."

When we analyze this, the explanation given regarding parables is necessarily based on the principle that there is no such thing as coincidence in the world. In *Elokus*, there is a reason for this creation in all its details and the details of its details. Therefore, it is impossible that one could draw a comparison from one subject to another by mere chance and without an internal connection.

Perhaps one can explain that this is why parables are so scarce in Chabad Chassidus. Its focus is the explanation of the doctrine of *Elokus* and how "there is nothing else besides Him." For this, the parable and example is "from my flesh I shall see [Hashem]," the body, and beyond that, the study of the soul in its details. Since *Elokus* is present in everything, and the goal of Chabad teaching is to reveal this, it is understood that one must find the example and parable within the study of the soul, its faculties, and its levels, and there is no need for parables of another kind.

With respect and blessing,

I will, in any case, add one specific note—or if you will, this is also a general matter. It concerns the section "From the Mouth of Chassidim" (in your *Yalkut*), page 300, regarding the story of a Chabad Chassid, a great merchant, who was doing his annual balance sheet and wrote at the bottom line: "Total: There is nothing else besides Him." Incidentally, it is passed down among Chassidim that this refers to a Chassid of the Alter Rebbe, R. Binyamin of Kletzk. The point of the matter, as emphasized by Chassidim, is that after he wrote the details of the account, without any calculation or deliberation, when he reached the "Total" line, he wrote "There is nothing else besides Him." That is to say, not through contemplation, etc., but simply, that the total of **any** matter whatsoever is—"there is nothing else besides Him." As a continuation of this, it is told about him that someone once asked him: How does the teaching of Chassidus mandate that in "all your ways"—even in matters of **and during** eating, drinking, and business—you should "know Him," as the concept of *Da'as* is explained in Chassidus as a deep understanding to the point of recognition and a feeling that permeates the entire person? He replied: We see tangibly that during *davening*, even at its central point—the beginning of the *Amidah*—thoughts arise regarding the fair in Leipzig. So why is it a wonder if, during the fair in Leipzig, thoughts arise regarding "there is nothing else besides Him"?

## 6129

B"H, 22 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

6131

It is also understood from Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 26, that "things which are well-known require no proof." This is especially true since you must acquire youth who are rich in talent and also in knowledge of Chassidus and Chabad in particular; any addition to the aforementioned will increase the success of this sublime endeavor.

Regarding what you wrote about the talks for the youth, we are writing about this to the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., Rabbi A. Paris.

It gave me particular pleasure to read what you wrote regarding the students of the evening yeshiva, your farbrengen with them, etc. Certainly, all those involved in this are striving to ensure that the results of the farbrengen are felt in practical terms—naturally, results appropriate for the students of the evening yeshiva. If so, it will certainly make an impression on their parents and their environment in general. As is known, the inner dimension of Torah is the analogy of oil, and the law of oil is that it permeates every place that is connected and attached to the point where the oil has penetrated. And the rest is understood.

It gave me pleasure to read in your letter that you have spoken with the Rosh Yeshiva and the teacher in pleasant ways, even though, naturally, without compromising on any essential point. We see tangibly that through ways of pleasantness and ways of peace, one accomplishes more than through other methods, in addition to the point that this is the way of Torah, whose "ways are ways of pleasantness," etc.

Regarding what you wrote concerning a specific student, as to how and where his studies should be in the future, it is understood that in this matter you must consult with the elders of Anash on the spot, for the matter depends on the minute details of the student, his home, his environment, etc.

At a time of favor, I will mention all those you wrote about at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May it be His will that you bring good news regarding both general and personal matters, in a way that is good, visible, and revealed.

In accordance with your request, the letter is being sent urgently, with an added note—though it is understood and simple—that the delay in the response from here is only due to the multitude of pressures here. Therefore, it is understood that we strive to answer first those individuals and those matters where there is a risk of a grave error, a grave breakdown, or where people might take offense. This is not the case for those who are "on the inside," who certainly will not take offense, nor will they err in a severe manner. Therefore, the response to their questions comes later [an example similar to the prayer of Solomon, where regarding Bnei Yisrael there were several conditions for the answer to the prayer, and the rest is understood].

With blessings for good tidings and for great success in all the above.

## 6,133

6,133

B”H, 25 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter from the end of Shevat, in which you write regarding the manner of your husband’s (shlita) activities since his return from here, and the resulting impact on the family, given that he is extremely busy, etc., and as you write, even within our own circles, people look upon this conduct with astonishment, etc.

First and foremost, I must dismiss this latter claim. The foundation and beginning of all four parts of the Shulchan Aruch is: "Do not be embarrassed by those who mock." This is especially true when one must question the reason for the mockery—whether it stems from jealousy or the like. If only it were "jealousy of scribes," which results in an increase of wisdom.

Regarding the substance of your claim, it is understood that, in general, you are correct: a husband and father must dedicate time to his wife and children, as it is absolutely simple that this is no less important than any other mitzvah of our holy Torah.

The words of the Rebbe (Rashab) are well known regarding this matter—that just as one must put on tefillin, so too [must one attend to these duties]. However, at the same time, it is the nature of any work in a new field that it is impossible to restrict and limit the time according to the clock if one wishes to establish the work in a way that is grounded and enduring. If this is true for any person, it is certainly true regarding your husband (sheyichyeh), whom you surely know is not one to adhere to the method of "the middle path." When he begins a task, he does so with total enthusiasm; if one were to restrict him in **any** way, he would not even begin to start.

However, based on my assessment—which is close to a certainty in my eyes—after the initial period of his work in these new fields passes, he will surely enter a steady rhythm. At that point, he will fulfill his holy obligation as a husband and father, as mentioned above, and this will not detract from the effectiveness of his work in these new fields. As is known from the example of this: even though Hashem gave many mitzvos to Yisrael, totaling 613, not only does one mitzvah not detract from or contradict another, but on the contrary, our Sages said, "One mitzvah leads to another."

As for what will be your portion: if only there were many more like you in Yisrael, whose husbands merit to engage in the chinuch of the children of Yisrael, drawing their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven. The reward for them, and for the entire family—especially the wife who assists him in this path—is beyond expression, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

It gave me pleasure to read at the end of your letter that you are seeing good fruit from your work in the school, in the progress of your class and the conduct of the students. May it be His will that you continue to see success and blessing in this as well, and that you bring good tidings regarding all the matters you touched upon in this letter.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach, and for good tidings regarding all that was mentioned, in good health.

## 6,136

6,136

B"H, 25 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Following up on what we discussed here, I hope these few lines will suffice to clarify the matters. It is very, very simple: there is no reason in what was said for discouragement or for a fall in spirit, chas v’shalom. I emphasize this especially, because I noticed that when he is told something that casts doubt on the correctness of his actions—whatever they may be—he immediately draws a *binyan av* (a precedent) for all his other activities. Through the intervention of the *kluginker* (the clever one) who begins to explain to him that, according to this, what is the use of his activities **etc.**, he begins to falter. Therefore, I repeat and reiterate: regarding the greatest in Israel, it is said that "a person does not grasp the words of Torah unless he has stumbled in them." On the contrary, past mistakes, when one overcomes them, add light and instruction for the future. Even if, for some reason, one finds a mistake not only at the beginning of one's *avodah* but even some time after starting, it is known what is brought down from the *Amora'im*, who said, "The things I said before you were a mistake on my part," even after they had led a *yeshivah* for many years and raised many students. The fact that this is told to us is not for the sake of historical narrative, chas v’shalom, but as an instruction on two points: a) that one must not conceal one's own mistakes, even though "love of self covers all transgressions," and b) that one must not fall in spirit, chas v’shalom, or cause a weakening in one's *avodah*. On the contrary—one must draw upon the powers of the *neshamah* in order to not only fulfill and complete the *avodah* of the past, but even to add to it many times over. As the well-known parable goes: in the place where a rope is torn and one ties a knot, the rope is double-strength there. *V'ka'le* (and it is understood).

With blessings for success in your holy *avodah*, the education of the holy *tzon kodashim* (holy flock), as is the desire of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *Nasi* of our generation—which will surely add blessing and success also in the personal matters of yourself, your wife, and your children, *shlita*. I look forward to hearing good news—not only that you received my letter well, but also that you are proceeding with joy and a good heart, increasing your *avodah* and bringing the hearts of the sons and daughters of Israel closer to our Father in Heaven.

With blessings for good news as mentioned above.

## 6137

B"H, 25 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter in which you write regarding those who pray in your shul, noting that those who wish to lead the davening are not always desired by the congregation for significant reasons, and you ask how to conduct yourself in this matter, etc.

Decisions in matters such as these depend on many details and minute particulars. Therefore, you should consult with the local Rav who is on-site and aware of all the details, and conduct yourself in accordance with his instruction.

What is surprising is your statement that they are wearing posul tefillin. If it is known that the tefillin are posul, why would they not give them to a sofer to be checked, so that he may repair them or replace them with kosher ones? It is worthwhile to dedicate funds, even from the communal treasury, for a matter such as this. After all, the entire Torah is compared to tefillin, and the kavanah of tefillin is well-known (that the kavanah of the mitzvah must correspond to the **action** of the mitzvah). This is as explained in Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim: to subjugate the heart and the brain, which are the kings and rulers **over all** the limbs of the body, as explained in the Tanya Kadisha, beginning of Chapter 41.

On this occasion, I would like to remind you regarding the observance of the three daily study portions—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—which we have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that they are appropriate for every soul and are a segulah for many matters.

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above.

## 6140

6140

B"H, 28 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi, a man of great deeds,
Rabbi Avraham Meir, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of Monday, in which you comment on the fact that people use the expression *zichrono livracha* (may his memory be for a blessing) — or, as you phrased it in your letter, *zichro yagen aleinu* (may his merit protect us) — only regarding Tzaddikim who are in the supernal treasuries, and not regarding Tzaddikim who are alive among us for long and good days.

In my opinion, the explanation for this is that for Tzaddikim who are alive among us in this world, with soul in body, the Tzaddik himself provides protection—through his prayer, etc.—as per the words of our Sages, which you also cite in your letter regarding the verse, "Their shadow has departed from them," whereas this is not the case for a Tzaddik who has passed on. Therefore, we then invoke his *zechus* (merit). This is in the sense of *zechus* as used in the Mishnah in Sotah (3:4). However, in the case at hand, it is also a *zechus* of a mitzvah. See there.

On this occasion, I am enclosing a *kuntres* that was published recently, which is in connection with *Shabbos Zachor* and the days of Purim that have passed. Surely you have fixed times for the study of *Pnimiyus HaTorah*. As is well known, the words of the Arizal, via his student R. Chaim Vital in his introduction to *Shaar HaHakdamos*, explain how in these generations it is a mitzvah to reveal this wisdom. The later Sages explained the necessity of this matter; see *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe (author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch), Epistle 26, and the *Kuntres Eitz Chaim* by his great-great-grandson, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, and others.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

Regarding the matter of *zichro yagen aleinu* (may his merit protect us), what requires further study is: what is its connection to the *zechus* (merit) of the Tzaddik, that it should protect him? After all, even a father does not grant merit to his son. And this is even according to the first answer in *Tosafos* (Sotah 10b, end of side b), that this applies specifically regarding the sin of idolatry. And this is even according to what the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, wrote in his will, *Chinuch LaNa'ar*. He writes: "And he who has eyes to see will understand that the intention behind the statement that a father does not save his son is that the father’s own deeds—which he performs for himself (i.e., not for the sake of his son)—do not benefit the son. This is not the case regarding the son saving the father; even what the son does for himself (not to grant merit to his father, but rather, if he performs good deeds and walks in the ways of Hashem as he was cautioned in our holy Torah, and adds strength to be meticulous in every matter, etc.)—through every good deed he performs, he saves his father from the judgment of Gehenom and brings him into Gan Eden, etc. And what is written in the text of the prayer, 'And He remembers the kindness of the fathers,' etc., refers to the fact that He remembers for us the covenant He made with our forefathers on our behalf, etc." End quote.

In any event, it requires the prayer of the father or his action on behalf of the son. And it is worth noting the concept of *zechus avos* (merit of the fathers) (Shabbos 55a; Vayikra Rabbah 36:6; Yerushalmi Sanhedrin 10:1; and elsewhere).

Based on this, the term *zichrono livracha* should be used for every Tzaddik (see *Sdei Chemed*, Vol. 6, entry *Tav*, and the references there). But *zichro yagen aleinu* (may his merit protect us) is used when speaking of Tzaddikim who are the guides of Israel or *mari d'oraysa* (masters of Torah), who teach Torah to the masses, and the speaker studies their Torah and follows their ways and instructions—concerning whom it is said, "Your children—these are the students."

This is easy to understand, but I will not elaborate further.

## 6101

B"H, 29 Adar, 5718
Brooklyn

To the Rabbis of the Beis Din Tzedek of the Eidah HaChareidis in Jerusalem, the Holy City—may it be built and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days—may they live:

Greetings and blessings,

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 11th of Adar, in which you write regarding the matter of the mixed swimming pools, Heaven forbid, etc. Surely you are already aware of the public reaction here regarding this matter.

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon there will be fulfilled in Jerusalem, our holy city, that which is written in our holy Torah: "A faithful city, full of justice, righteousness lodged in it," and it shall be called "the city of righteousness, a faithful city."

The inner dimension of these matters is explained by Rabbeinu HaZaken, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch: Jerusalem (*Yerushalayim*) represents the perfection of *yirah* (*yireh shalem*—the completeness of awe), and together with this, the Holy Mountain (*Har HaKodesh*) represents the perfection of *ahavah*—*ahavah elyonah* (supernal love). See this at length in *Likutei Torah*, *Devarim*, section 2.

The words of the *Sifrei* (*Devarim* 6:5) are well known: "There is no *ahavah* in the place of *yirah*, and no *yirah* in the place of *ahavah*, except in the attribute of the Holy One, blessed be He, alone."

With respect and blessings for good tidings regarding all the above, and for the perfection of goodness—good for Heaven and good for the creations (see *Kiddushin* 40a). We "roll" merit through those who are meritorious during the period between Purim and Pesach, linking redemption to redemption: the redemption of Purim—for we are still servants of Achashverosh—to the complete redemption, for "in Nissan they were redeemed and in Nissan they are destined to be redeemed" (as the law is settled regarding the dispute on this matter)—the true and complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, as it is written: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders."

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

P.S.
I am astonished, and I have been greatly pained, especially upon learning of certain individuals (though I have a strong hope that they are entirely the exception to the rule) who belong to the Chareidi community yet travel on Israeli ships (i.e., where the crew is Jewish, as are the owners). These ships travel on Shabbos as well. As explained at length elsewhere, it is beyond any doubt that this constitutes *chillul Shabbos* in public (*b'farhesia*), and involves *melachos* prohibited by Torah law, etc.

Can such a thing be told? This matter, in particular, pertains to Jerusalem, the Holy City. As the Sages said (*Shabbos* 119b), and also regarding our imminent redemption: if Israel were to keep two Shabbosos according to their law (or, according to the *Yerushalmi*, *Taanis* 1:1, even one Shabbos as it should be kept), the son of David would come immediately (see *Likutei Torah* by Rabbeinu HaZaken, *Vayikra* 41a). May it be His will that I receive good tidings regarding this as well, and may we merit speedily the day that is entirely Shabbos and rest for eternal life.

## 6144

[Adar 5718]

...Regarding your honor’s notes on the Iggeres HaKodesh at the end of the first section:

a) The expression "spies" (*meraglim*) — see Shmuel I 26:4; Likutei Torah, end of Parshas Shelach, and study it well there.

b) After all, testimony is only valid when given before a *beis din*. And furthermore.

c) After all, one should not push away with both hands. And furthermore, did our Sages not say (Berachos 28a) that it was only shown to him to settle his mind?

There are several distinctions to be made between the case in the Iggeres HaKodesh and the matters mentioned by our Sages. The primary one is that the conditions for testimony and the passage in Berachos concern a situation where the person **has already** performed an act and is behaving in a certain way—whereas here, it is a matter of establishing a fence, a warning for the future, and a safeguard for the Torah. This is all the more so *kal v’chomer* from the fact that we strike and punish, etc. (Sanhedrin 46a), even if they had not warned him beforehand.

#### ***6144***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 23, p. 360.

The letter is to R. Shmuel Yalov, and it was written on the margin of his letter dated 10 Adar 5718. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 9, p. 2796, and in the references noted there.

**Regarding his note:** In his letter: "In the Sefer HaTanya... to send spies to all the *minyanim*... and the word *meragel* (spy) denotes a person who spreads slander... and how can a person believe what another tells him... they must testify before him. And also, is it within his power to push away with both hands?"

## 6105

[Adar 5718]

Regarding your observation in *Torah Or*, in the *maamar* beginning with the words "Be-Chaf-Heh Be-Kislev," where it explains the opinion that the seven lamps of the Menorah were lit only at night (contrary to the opinion of the Rambam):

This is indeed the view of Rashi, Tosafos (Menachos 86b, end of side), the Ramban, the Raavad, the Rashba, and others. This is also evident from the text of the *avodah* of Yom Kippur composed by Yossi ben Yossi Kohen Gadol (*Pri Etz Chaim*, Shaar Yom Kippur, Chapter 4), which was established in the *siddur* of the Arizal and the *siddur* of our Rebbe.

As for what is written in *Zohar Chadash* (88b, 183a) that he would light [the lamps] at two times—

This is [the case] **according to all** opinions. As is also written in *Torah Or*, that he would light the seventh lamp (and the sixth lamp) in the morning. Thus, the difficulty raised by the *Nitzutzei Zohar* there is resolved.

At a time of favor, I will mention you at the *tziyun* for proper health.
